      \nEpisode II: Angels, Demons and Saints (Part 11)\n

      Charleston felt bitter and green with envy; he'd always hated and admired those who could create things successfully. Candace was enthralled. She could feel the greatness gathering around the young poet. She snapped her fingers and swayed with the crowd. Behind her, the man with the jug passed it to her. She took a swig.

      \n

      "Jack," he said, taking back the jug.

      \n

      "Candace."

      \n

      "That's my man Allen up there! Hey Neal, groove on this fine chick!"

      \n

      "Yes, yass, yes. You are from New York, aren't you. I can tell by the way you look, the direct stare of the New Yorker that cuts like a knife." Neal was the handsome man she'd noticed talking a mile a minute earlier. He turned to Temperance. "And who is this gone cat! Baby, you are a relief. You are all too much a muchly of much. You bring to mind certain Eastern philosophies I had the pleasure of reading once."

      \n

      "Any particular philosophies?" said Charleston.

      \n

      "Hey, dig. You know in a way, man, I envy you at this moment. Not to belittle what you carry\u2014being blind must be a heavy burden\u2014but to only be able to aurally appreciate what is going on, to feel those vibrations coursing through and the only conduit possible is the purest way to take in poetry! Unless you could find some way to just smash it through your veins on the ultimate kick! My name's Neal Cassady," he said, shaking Candace's hand warmly (and holding on to it a bit too long.)

      \n

      "You could just close your eyes. I can't open mine," said Charleston. "Unless they're already open."

      \n

      "Tell me, are you all poets?" asked Candace.

      \n

      Jack wrote poetry, he said, but he had written a novel\u2014The Town and the City\u2014that nobody had read, and had another one that nobody would publish. Candace commiserated and confidedthat she had written\xa0Homefront, which impressed Jack quite a bit. He'd loved it\u2014it wasn't his thing\u2014but he'd loved it.

      \n

      "Let me lay down on you how I wrote my book about me and Neal driving around. I taped typing paper together into one long scroll, and I just typed. I recommend it. Bill, our friend Burroughs, he wants to just cut up what he types and rearrange it at random."

      \n

      Temperance was dubious about the technique. "Of course, Bill does do a lot of heroin," said Jack.

      \n

      Allen rejoined them. "Well, I hope that went well." He looked wryly at Candace. "Are you here with Jack? Oh, hello Peter." A rather dandyish looking man walked up to him, and they kissed passionately. Temperance looked away.

      \n

      "How very European," said Candace.

      \n

      "That is a word for it. Well, Jack seems to like you so why not come with us to our favorite place, Langtry Lee's. It's a Chinese place, we can talk more and watch the show."

      \n

      "What kind of show?"

      \n

      "Um...a female impersonator show, actually. But it's a good bar for people of a certain bend to go to. Squares and straights come too."

      \n

      "Would you say of a certain predilection?" said Charleston, trying to leer.

      \n

      "Sure. Homosexuals, is what I'm saying. You would prefer I say\xa0artistic? But there are homosexuals who aren't artistic in the slightest."

      \n

      Charleston expressed his admiration for the poem; Ginsberg told him it had to come from the heart\u2014that too much of the country had been forced out of sight and he wanted to bring them into the light. It was why he and Jack called themselves\xa0subterraneans.

      \n

      "We're working in what Jung would call the gardens of the subconscious," said Ginsberg.

      \n

      "I would say perhaps you not below\u2014you're above. You see the whole picture," said Candace.

      \n

      "That's exactly right. I've been working on a section of\xa0Howl\xa0about a vision I had of Moloch here in San Francisco after ingesting some peyote."

      \n

      [Need I mention that, yup, this happened?]

      \n

      "What he say?" asked Charleston.

      \n

      It wasn't so much that Moloch had said anything, replied Allen, but that he existed at all: that the country had become machinery for Moloch, for greed...

      \n

      As he was winding down, an rather mousy redheaded woman of maybe twenty or twenty-two joined them. She had sashes of lavender silk tied around her wrists, and Ginsberg identified her as Helen Heck, Jack's friend. Charleston immediately was struck by a sense that something was\xa0wrong\xa0about the girl; without saying a word, he took her hand. He realized then why she had sashes tied around her wrists: she'd slit them both at some point, and hid the scars beneath the fabric.

      \n

      "I knew from the moment I saw you that you were something special," he said.

      \n

      "It's all like a dream to me here after all," she said, then looked sharply at him. There was an air of being\xa0out of place\xa0around her, he felt. He took her arm as they left the Gallery and wove through the foggy streets.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Langtry Lee's was done up like a Western saloon on the outside, all wagon wheels and hitching posts, save for the Chinese characters in red and gold painted under the sign. Inside it maintained the illusion, with silk wallpaper and brass cuspidors sprinkled around the floor. An elegant drag queen in a cheongsam came out to meet them.

      \n

      "Hello, I'm Langtry Lee and\u2014holy hell!" She ran up to Jimmy and embraced him tightly. For a second Jimmy saw a look of fear play over her face, but then she beamed at him. "Jimmy! I'm so glad to see you again."

      \n

      "Me too, Lily," he said.

      \n

      "Hey Jimmy, that the wife?" said Charleston.

      \n

      "No," he replied, and took her hand as they walked into the dining room.\xa0

      \n

      "Joyce!" shouted Lily. "Get these guys a bottle."

      \n

      From behind the bar came a very butch woman wearing a vest, black trousers, and a shirt with arm garters\u2014they height of men's fashion in the 1880s. "Holy hell," she whistled. "Jimmy Wright."

      \n

      "How do we keep running into each other, Joyce," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "No snakes allowed in here! We let dogs in."

      \n

      Betty wagged her tail. Joyce looked over at Charleston. "Oh my god, it's Charles\u2014wait, are you Charleston again?"

      \n

      "Who are you?" he said.

      \n

      "Remember when our plane crashed?" said Jimmy.

      \n

      "I need more."

      \n

      "In Venice? Joyce Summers?"

      \n

      "Don't ruin barkeeping," pleaded Joyce. "I liked planes and boats, so don't ruin running a saloon."

      \n

      "Then don't ruin it for us," said Charleston.

      \n

      She shook her head. "You all need to get seriously drunk."

      \nEpisode II: Angels, Demons and Saints (Part 12)\n

      Helen was a photographer. She felt bad that she couldn't show Charleston her work, but he asked her to describe them to her anyway. She was excited to hear he had lived for a long time in New York.

      \n

      "Then you know the old suicide chamber down on Washington Square, the one President Winthrop had built," she said.

      \n

      "I'm not familiar with\xa0that\xa0suicide chamber. Give me some details."

      \n

      She explained how the Winthrop administration had built a hotel-like suicide chamber during the 1920s. It had been shuttered in the 1930s, but she liked to go inside and explore and take pictures\u2014it was such an interesting, gloomy place. One time when she came out, she met Jack Kerouac, who she knew slightly from Columbia University, although he seemed somehow different. She had followed him out to San Francisco.

      \n

      "But of course this is all a dream," she said. "You had some guy named Warren Harding as your President in 1920. You had two wars with Germany but they never invaded New Jersey. This is all a dream."

      \n

      [Helen Heck is a character from the fine short story\xa0The Neurastheniac\xa0in the collection\xa0Cassilda's Daughters. In the story she was a minor Beat poet, never published in her life, who lived in a New York that must have been descended from Hildred de Castaigne's New York in "The Repairer of Reputations."]

      \n

      She was from Alabama originally, and attended Barnard, where the stress had driven her to make a suicide attempt. Her conviction that everything around her was some kind of a dream was unshakable. Charleston commiserated about her injuries, mentioning he had scars of his own. He asked for a list of the differences between their worlds; one of the ones she found most perplexing was two-pronged electric plugs\u2014four was so much more sensible.

      \n

      Charleston felt something odd whenever Lily came near him: some kind of strange\xa0aversion, something that twigged the ghosts of his\xa0other\xa0senses. He listened to her talk with Jimmy with half an ear.

      \n

      "Jimmy! we need to catch up! I heard you died in Peoria, Toronto, and Johannesburg."

      \n

      "I think there's at least a dozen other places I'm supposed to be dead," he said with a smile.

      \n

      "I missed you! You saved my life. Not like those Krauts didn't beat me up, put me in the hospital, but without you they'd have killed me and all my girls. Of course the bar closed down after that, but I ran into Joyce who had just come into some money and wanted to sell her barge\u2014so we came here, to the States! We have a little house over on Russian Hill. You should come stay!"

      \n

      [For this history, see Eternal Lies episodes IX and X.]

      \n

      "Are you sure? Bad things tend to happen."

      \n

      "Yes! And it's not like that. I just...want to talk to my old friend tonight."

      \n

      Jimmy felt that she was holding something back from him. "You okay?" he said.

      \n

      "Oh yes. Well, there's a few things...but I'll tell you later."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Temperance sat fidgeting in a chair. She didn't like Chinese food much. And the...lovely ladies serving it were a constant reminder that she now found herself in a world she never knew existed. It didn't help that Lily kept looking funny at her. Finally she snapped her fingers. "I do know you! You're Temperance, right? Ruby's kid? I knew your mother, back in Bangkok! I have to say, when we met she was a little bit of a mess. But I straightened her out."

      \n

      "How?" said Temperance, trying not to bug her eyes out.

      \n

      "Gave her a new hairstyle. Jimmy, she still with that really handsome Spanish guy?"

      \n

      "They're married now," he said with a smile.

      \n

      "Oh. Too bad."

      \n

      Bangkok? whispered Temperance at Jimmy.\xa0Long story, he whispered back.\xa0

      \n

      "Is that why there's a road flare available in every room?"

      \n

      "I'm very sure there were multiple things that led to why she keeps a road flare in every room," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "One day, Mr. Wright, we're gonna sit down to coffee and you're going to tell me your\xa0long stories."

      \n

      "You have a couple of years? Because I don't," said Jimmy. He got up as fast as he could and went to dance with Lily.

      \n

      \xa0

      \nEpisode II: Angels, Demons and Saints (Part 13)\n

      Candace sat amidst Jack Kerouac, Gary Snyder, and Allen Ginsberg, soaking up their talk about poetry. "We don't get too many gone chicks like you," said Kerouac.

      \n

      "Thank you. But I've been looking for someone I hoped would be here. Amadou?"

      \n

      "Wow, Amadou Lalin...Allen, you seen Amadou around?"

      \n

      "I think he's lying low somewhere in the city," said Allen. "Haven't seen him around for a while. I have something he wrote, actually; he crashed with me for a few nights out in Berkeley. I typed up a translation."

      \n

      "Translation?"

      \n

      "Amadou's first language is French." He handed her a piece of flimsy typing paper. On it in two columns were a poem in French and a line-by-line translation:

      \n
      \n

      Carcosa \u2013 br\xfble-t-elle?

      \n

      Kerouac said that Amadou was how he had met Helen; that one night he and Amadou had been sitting up late, bingeing on drinks and heroin, listening to bop, reciting each other's poetry...and when he woke up, Helen was there.

      \n

      "If you want to get a better lead on Amadou," said Allen, "you might want to talk to Neal...I think they were lovers for a while."

      \n

      "Hrm, Amadou Lalin," said Neal. "That cat vibrates on the higher frequencies, has a vision I can't understand because I'm not there yet. It's like...when you're driving on the highway for a long time late at night, fifteen hours straight and your mind is gone, you're just one with the machine? That's what these cats can't understand, how I can drive so well, but it's because I vibrate on those frequencies. It's like...it must come up\xa0through\xa0the car, and I can understand it, because me and cars are a thing. And Amadou is like that, but with poetry. And a good lay. But he's got this new boyfriend, a bit rough trade, and I don't like him. He goes to that Asylum party...I think his boyfriend, Coombs, Michael Coombs, he works for some occult bookstore up in Pacific Heights. I don't know. I'm welcome to all philosophies, we are all, all cosmic spirits ascending that latter to a glorious beginning and ending. Kundalini, man. It's a Brahma thing. A universal\xa0mind."

      \n

      [Okay, this is not the greatest Neal Cassady impression, but to be fair only Kerouac every really captured his voice, and I'm not Kerouac by any stretch of the imagination.]

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      "Back where I'm from," said Helen, watching the floor show, "this sort of thing is probably illegal. You been to Asylum yet? There's usually a sign down at Union Square in the afternoon. If you can't find it, let me know where you're staying and I'll come get you."

      \n

      "Instead of coming to get me later, I could show you my hotel room now," said Charleston.

      \n

      Helen laughed. "All right."

      \n

      "See you guys later," said Charleston. He was trying to do concentration of risk\u2014he was getting heebie-jeebies from multiple directions, but he liked Helen.

      \n

      As it turns out, she liked him as well.

      \nEpisode II: Angels, Demons and Saints (Part 14)\n

      Jimmy spent the night at Lily and Joyce's house, catching up on old times, talking about where they had all been in the intervening years. Lily was charming and effervescent, although still she seemed tinged with some sadness Jimmy couldn't place. Joyce kept up a constant stream of sniping and grousing in the background. They could be an old married couple, except for the fact that they weren't attracted to each other at all.

      \n

      Early in the morning, Lily took off her makeup and put on a little tweed suit. She looked smaller and bent; her age showed, and not just because she wasn't made up. Jimmy looked askance at her, and she sighed.

      \n

      "Once a week I go to a Buddhist temple to meditate," she began.

      \n

      "I can't even look at you when you're like that," said Joyce, emptying out a tea pot and shaking her head.

      \n

      "...they're very strict and so I have to go in drag," finished Lily with remarkable simplicity and \xe9lan. "Listen, Jimmy, can you meet me tonight in Chinatown? We can go over to the club and have a drink before you can go...I don't know, you're saving the world again, aren't you?"

      \n

      "I don't know yet," he said.\xa0

      \n

      "That's a yes, then. So meet me by the Dragon Gate tonight."

      \n

      "Why can't we talk now?"

      \n

      "Oh, I have so much to do, I have to go meditate, and open the club, and get a manicure..."

      \n

      "All right, I'll see you there."

      \n

      "I'll be wearing a red dress."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      A little bit later over breakfast at a greasy spoon near their hotel, Lisa talked with Jimmy about the previous night. She had no idea young people were like that now; she'd never been that young. She'd wanted to get out and see the world, of course, when she was a teenager; almost left for the big city once or twice. In the end, though, she decided to go to university instead. After all, she was from Manhattan, Kansas, home of Kansas State University.

      \n

      "You can always go see the world," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "I did a bit during the war. And Percy was a bit like those young people. Although they seemed joyous in a way he wasn't. And they're all drug addicts."

      \n

      "Yes. But a war isn't a way to see the world."

      \n

      "I trained as an anthropologist, I could do field work..."

      \n

      "Go."

      \n

      "Mostly I ended up working on other people's research. We can't all be Margaret Mead. Elizabeth Schicksal:\xa0Growing up in Ghana? I don't know."

      \n

      "I do. I've been to Africa."

      \n

      "That must have been really interesting."

      \n

      "I...it had its moments."

      \n

      "Do you think what we're finding out is dangerous?"

      \n

      "Absolutely."

      \n

      "Oh. What do you do? Call the authorities?"

      \n

      "No. It's like a slow poison. It worms its way in, and the more you share it the more it infects other people. So you have to have strength to deal with it."

      \n

      [Have I mentioned most of the dialogue is verbatim? This sure was. Bravo, JP.]

      \n

      "Prophylaxis. So...we're prophylactic?" she said with a smile. It was probably the first joke she had ever made to him. He chuckled and poured another cup of coffee.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Charleston took Helen out for breakfast around ten in the morning, and then she took him to some of her favorite places in the city. Over time, Charleston\u2014who was hyperaware of the sounds of footsteps around him, began to notice a consistent pattern following them. Whoever it was, he\u2014Charleston had gotten close enough to pick up his cologne\u2014was very good, frequently overwalking them when they stopped to avoid notice.

      \n

      "You don't have a boyfriend, do you?" he asked Helen.

      \n

      "No. Well, I sleep around with a lot of guys."

      \n

      "Any of them the jealous type?"

      \n

      "I don't sleep with any of them long enough to know."

      \n

      "Let me know when we get to a liquor store." A short while later she gripped his arm and led him through a doorway. He told her to pick up the cheapest bottle of wine available and buy it. Meanwhile he tapped his way to the back of the store and opened the rear door. The store owner began to shout at him in broken English, switching to Cantonese when he saw Charleston's face.

      \n

      "Hey, grandpa, help a guy out. I paid," Charleston said in the same language.

      \n

      "Stupid kids today! Just get out."

      \n

      At the end of the alley he had Helen hail a cab and they rode back to the hotel.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Candace had spent the night with Jack in her hotel room, finishing off a bottle of rye and making love. She dragged herself out of the room around noon and went for a long walk around the city, trying to clear her head and organize her thoughts.

      \n

      Somehow she found herself in Union Square. It was bustling with weekend crowds, homeless panhandlers, shrieking children, teenagers dancing to the sound of portable radios. She looked around for a long time, trying to catch sight of anything that might tell her where the Asylum party was going to be held. She had just about given up when a small sign on a movie poster caught her eye.

      \n

      She walked up to it. It looked like the symbol they'd seen in the complex in Nevada. It was painted in a fluorescent yellow that seemed to squirm in the sunlight. Chalked above it was an address in the industrial district of the city, and next Saturday's date.

      Temperance dreamed:

      \n

      She was standing on the shores of a foggy lake at sunset. Although rather disconcertingly, there seemed to be a\xa0second\xa0sun still in the sky. In front of her she saw Charlie, her dream companion, wearing a three-piece suit as he sometimes did in her dreams.

      \n

      "You white people have the stupidest clothes," he said.

      \n

      "I'm sorry, but you're the one wearing it," she said.

      \n

      \n

      \n

      \n

      \n

      \n

      \n

      \n

      \n

      \n

      "I've never heard of it."

      \n

      \n

      \n

      "Yes. Aldebaran's influence is rising."

      \n

      \n

      Charlie began laughing. He laughed for a good minute. "Sorry, I'm done...ho ho ho...done now. What do you think is going to happen? Not seeing the Yellow Sign is a good start. Have you seen the Yellow Sign?"

      \n

      "Yes."

      \n

      "Have you seen the Yellow Sign?"

      \n

      "In a facility in the desert."

      \n

      "Strange, it's usually near water."

      \n

      "There was an empty basin nearby."

      \n

      \n

      "No."

      \n

      \n

      \n

      \n

      "It's insipid."

      \n

      \n

      She woke up and discovered that as usual she'd recorded the details in her dream journal without realizing it.\xa0

      \n

      Later that day she headed out to City Lights and asked about\xa0Der Wanderer durch den See.

      \n

      "We don't have that," said Shig. "But I guess this Amadou guy is getting popular, everybody is asking about him lately."

      \n

      "Amadou Lalin?"

      \n

      "The same. He wrote a book based on that one. The title's the same, just in French:\xa0L'homme errant au bord du Lac. The wanderer on the shores of the lake. We've got a copy here somewhere..."

      \n

      She bought it and took it home; it seemed to be some kind of limited print run\u2014all the copies were hand-numbered. The book was unusual, starting with how it was divided into two acts. Quite a bit was in French, which fortunately she knew. Quite a bit was devoted to this figure Hastur or Kaiwan. There were dreams, and descriptions of dreams, and what could only be called prayers, especially the one at the end:

      \n
      \n

      Some would be disconcerted by the structure of this treatise, but it is for us to walk on the Earth in Carcosa: that is the Third Act. That passage may or may not be written.

      \nAidez-moi, Kaiwan; moi, le r\xeaveur, \xe0 trouver la rev\xe9lation de l\u2019Ald\xe9baran rouge et du Chali noir. Je fais le Signe.

      \n

      [My own translation of the original in Tatters of the King.

      \n

      Me: And you get a point of Cthulhu Mythos.

      TP: Ooooh. It begins.

      Me, as Temperance: \u201cMom? I understand now! Jimmy Wright is POISON.\u201d]

      \n

      Jimmy spent the day with Betty watching Vincent Tuck's office, but the private eye never showed his face. In the evening he sauntered over to the Dragon Gate, the entrance to Chinatown. It was that brief, magic hour in San Francisco when the fogbanks are still poised high on the slopes of the hills and the setting sun is still visible through the Golden Gate.

      \n

      As he approached it, he saw Lily wearing a red silk dress walking down the street on the sidewalk opposite him. He saw a little girl point at her, and Lily smile at her. Which is probably what distracted him.

      \n

      Someone bumped into Lily, a man wearing a longshoreman's cap pulled low over his face. As he stalked away from her, she slowly collapsed to the ground. Blood began to pool around her. As Jimmy fought his way across the crowd rapidly forming around Lily, he could hear the little girl screaming.

      \n

      [JP: Why! Whyyyy! Why must you take everyone from me!]

      \n

      "Call the cops," he shouted as he crouched by her side. Her eyes were closed, but as he knelt beside her and gently propped her up, they fluttered open. She smiled. "I knew this would happen," she whispered.

      \n

      "I'm going to get you to the hospital. Where's the nearest hospital!" he yelled at the nearest person.

      \n

      [CP: Just head this way for two minutes too late, you can't miss it!]

      \n

      "It's all right," she whispered again, and brushed his face with one bloody hand. Then her eyes closed for the last time.

      \n That prompts some notes on the death of NPCs.

      In the text, the NPC who dies is a psychiatrist whose job is basically to frustrate people.

      That is, he has quite a bit of info to dump but he doesn't give it on his first interview.

      Then he gets killed.

      Then a letter comes to the PCs explaining quite a few things.

      So how to map him in? And maybe make him a bit more important?

      I dithered for a while about making "Dean Moriarity" a character, or inventing a minor Beat who could serve this function.

      Now, all along I had planned to bring Lily back as a cameo, in exactly the fashion I ended up doing in the campaign: as the saloonkeeper of a drag bar the Beats haunted.

      One day, as I was walking from my desk to the kitchen, it suddenly hit me with chilling certainty: Lily was the one who had to die. And it was really sad; I liked Lily quite a bit, and all praise is due to JP for forcing me to create her. But of course she was perfect, backstory built in, on PC who actually was invested in her and three players who knew the character.

      So. Kill your darlings. I sometimes find it hard to totally do in NPCs I enjoy playing, an example is Noor in my Masks campaign, who I brought back as a ghost. I ended up making that work, I think. More notoriously I brought Jackson Elias back, something I dithered about for quite a while. I'm still not sure I made the right call, although again I made it work.

      I know, I know: rented car, always in crosshairs.

      \nEpisode II: Angels, Demons and Saints (Part 16)\n

      He stayed long enough to tell the cops what he saw, and to make sure they treated her with some dignity. It was all he could do to not slap one of the uniforms for making a lewd crack about her. They loaded her into an ambulance and took her to the morgue.

      \n

      He stumbled back through the dark and misty streets to his hotel. As he passed the front desk, the clerk handed him an envelope. His name was written in a scrawled printed hand.

      \n

      When he finally got to his room, he ripped it open and read:

      \n
      \n

      Dear Jimmy,

      \nI'm sorry I couldn't tell you more earlier, but you see it wasn't time yet. I know you don't understand that yet. But maybe I can explain.
      About six months ago Amadou started to come into my place late, right before closing. He was high all the time on something and rambling all the time. Sometimes he would read from his book. He left a copy and I tried to read it but it didn't make much sense. Some of it was in French and it's been a long time since I learned French from the sailors in Shanghai.
      The last time I saw him I tried to ask him about the book. He was really out of it but he repeated the passages I read out loud. And after a while I saw something I can't explain. The next thing I knew Joyce was shaking me awake. She said Amadou's boyfriend Michael came in and grabbed him.
      After that I kept my eyes open. A PI named Tuck came in one time asking questions about Amadou + some guy named Bacon. I found out later that this Bacon guy owns a creepy bookstore in Pacific Heights.
      Jimmy I know that Amadou is under the influence of this guy Bacon + Bacon is connected to those Neurotology people. And I think they are up to something ba. Like the stuff you and Joyce took care of in Bangkok...the things she doesn't talk about.
      I haven't told you about what I saw the last time I saw Amadou. I saw myself walking in Chinatown. It was like a technicolor movie. My dresses have never looked so good. But like a movie I couldn't change anything, just watch. It was near the Dragon Gate. I remember a little girl pointing at me and I smiled at her so I didn't see the man who came up to me and stabbed me. I saw myself fall to the sidewalk + the blood pour out of me.
      Of course I was frightened. It felt so\xa0real. It felt\xa0true, like something that is going to happen. I think it is going to happen and very soon. So I've been meditating, trying to get ready. But I'm not afraid. Because I saw that you were there. That my friend was there when I died. So I'm not afraid. And I won't be when it happens.
      All my love. Always.
      Lily\xa0\u767e\u5408
      \n

      He seized the lamp next to his bed and threw it at the wall, plunging the room into darkness.

      \n

      [JP: You know that dream in the beginning where Jimmy kills everyone? This is the shit it was referencing! Everybody dies!

      \n

      Me: You do know that you're a trenchcoat and a Cockney accent from being John Constantine. "Forget it, Temperance love, it was demonic activity. 'Appens to Jimmy Wright all the time."]

      \n

      And later he found himself sitting at the bar at Lilly Langtry's.

      \n

      "How could she let herself get killed like that?" groused Joyce Summers. "Didn't she learn any tradecraft? Stupid old woman."

      \n

      Jimmy poured her a drink.

      \n

      "Godamnit, Jimmy!" she said. "At least it wasn't a flying snake."

      \n

      Jimmy decided not to mention that it was near the Dragon Gate. "No, it was a dagger. I looked away...for a second..."

      \n

      "We're all on borrowed time. You, me, Lily. You have to deal with the heebie-jeebies, that's what happens."

      \n

      "Things that go bump in the night," he replied and drank. "I hope I never see you again, so that nothing bad happens to you."

      \n

      "Skoal."

      \n

      "Prost."

      \n

      They drank. Joyce slammed down her glass. "We have to give her a funeral, you know. The cops are just a bunch of homophobic assholes. If we let them bury her, they'll bury her in a suit or something."

      \n

      "I'll claim the body...and plan the funeral...or scrounge up funds for it."

      \n

      "We'll hold some kind of wake here tomorrow." She glowered for a second. "That old woman used to piss me off all the time! How many dresses can one human being own!"

      \n

      "I know. I'll miss her too."

      \n

      "I really loved her a lot."

      \n

      They finished the bottle together. They left the last shot for Lily.

      \n

      Jimmy spent another day fruitlessly running down the location of Vincent Tuck, the PI he'd hired to investigate things for him in San Francisco. In the afternoon he swung by Lily Langtry's to talk to Joyce about Lily's funeral.

      \n

      \n

      COMPTON\u2019S CAFETERIA

      \n

      [Compton's Cafeteria will be the site of a rather less-well known riot by trans people a few years before Stonewall; at this time it was still a hangout for gay and trans people since it was open all night.]

      "Hoo boy," he muttered. "She's gonna do something stupid." He went back to the hotel to talk to his friends.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Compton's was a clean enough cafeteria, part of a chain of places strung out across California. Jimmy had no trouble picking out Joyce's crowd; she was standing on a table surrounded by men in neat suits, women in neater suits, a couple of leather dykes, and two outrageous queens in full regalia. "Are you gonna stand for that?" she was shouting in her flat Tennessee twang. "Killing us on the streets? Hey, Jimmy." She hopped off and explained they were planning to have a service and concert/rally that weekend in Golden Gate Park; Van Carlyle was going to play.\xa0

      \n

      "We should find out who did this, because the cops don't care," she said. "Ain't you a private eye?"

      \n

      "It's been a long time since I was called that. I have a lead. Little girl in Chinatown saw the whole thing."

      \n

      "What are we getting involved in?" Charleston asked Jimmy.

      \n

      "Investigation. Whoever killed Lily was involved with some guy named Lawrence Bacon..."

      \n

      "No. What are you going to\xa0do\xa0when you find him?"

      \n

      Jimmy didn't say a word. But his face grew grim.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      The way you find someone in Chinatown, Charleston told them, especially among the immigrant community, is to find the big man. And since he was the only one even remotely conversant in Cantonese, it fell to him to do the negotiations. It took him a day or so, but he finally uncovered the guy he needed, a restaurant owner named Wu. "We're looking for a friend. We don't know their name, we don't know what they look like, and we don't know where they are. But they killed a lady the other night."

      \n

      "Oh yeah, the [slur] who got killed. I heard about that."

      \n

      \n

      "Wasn't my people. She paid up her protection money. Seems to me you want the girl who saw the knifer. I can send you to them. You're looking for the Chens over near Stockton. I hear you screwed with them, we're going to have a discussion."

      \n

      "I'm a harmless old man!"

      \n

      "I know old men, not all of them are harmless. Chiang Kai-shek wasn't harmless!"

      \n

      The Chen's apartment was a tenement populated by immigrants who only spoke Chinese languages. They walked up to the third floor, and Charleston knocked on the door. It opened a crack. "Who are you?" demanded a man's voice.

      What poor Mr. Chen heard and saw, however, was a blind, scary looking man with three Anglos behind him talking about their local protection racket chief, saying how there wasn't going to be any trouble, and talking about his daughter. Thoroughly shaken, he opened the door.

      \nEpisode III: You Want It Darker (Part 1)\n

      They returned to their hotel, walking past the room that Van had taken over with his trio. He waved wildly at Temperance as she walked past, hunching her shoulders. She came to her room.

      \n

      The door was ajar.

      \n

      "I've been told of things like this," she said to herself. She retreated to Jimmy's room and walked in without knocking.

      \n

      "Mr. Wright," she said, "it's happened."

      \n

      Jimmy looked askance.

      \n

      "My room's been tossed." She noticed the look of relief, worry, and resignation that tracked across his face in that order. "I think they are still in there. What do we do? I don't want to hurt anyone...I don't want to be hurt..."

      \n

      Jimmy sighed, went into the bathroom, and yanked the shower curtain rod free, letting the curtain cascade to the floor. He collapsed it down to about three feet, clubbed it like a truncheon, and walked with Temperance back to her room. They pushed it open.

      \n

      Two men in black suits were tossing the drawers of Temperance's dresser. They both stiffened and straightened up simultaneously as soon as the door opened. One reached smoothly into his coat pocket and pulled out a badge and ID card. "We're with Security," he said.

      \n

      "Whose Security?" said Jimmy.

      \n

      "That's not for you to know. You're not cleared for that...Mr. Wright."

      \n

      "Why are going through my room?" blurted Temperance.

      \n

      "That's not for you to know either," said the other suit.

      \n

      "It's my room! I pay taxes!"

      \n

      "It's not your concern."

      \n

      Jimmy narrowed his eyes. Their skin was very pale and they moved in a way that seemed...odd. For a second, he remembered the two agents who had tossed poor Mr. Jennings almost through the wall of his trailer back in Nevada...

      \n

      "I'm sure you don't want to be in trouble," said the first suit. "Mr. Lamp, are we done?" he said to the other suit.

      \n

      "We're done, Mr. Window," he replied. The two of them marched out of the room. Mr. Lamp bumped into Jimmy with his shoulder. "Be seeing you...Mr. Wright."

      \n

      "What do we do now?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "Look for something that's missing," said Jimmy. He left her to spend the rest of the evening in paranoia and rode the elevator down to the first floor. The clerk at first thought he was complaining about the noise, or the busted ice machine.

      \n

      "No, the guys in black suits," said Jimmy. "Called themselves security."

      \n

      Nobody came in but guests, the clerk told him. Jimmy asked about any other entrances, and with a sigh he told him where to find the fire door. Jimmy couldn't find any sign of tampering.

      \n

      [JP: Hey, I guess I\xa0could\xa0be a building inspector.

      \n

      Me: For all we know, that was one of your odd jobs you had, until you found out the super living in the basement had a kid in hock to the Mob and then you had to fix that and finally walk off to the sound of sad piano music...hey, I wanna see that webseries.

      \n

      This was 1 point of Stability loss to Jimmy, and 2 for Temperance, since the \u201cagents\u201d had their weird paws all over her stuff. I had been looking forward to bringing in my somewhat idiosyncratic ideas about the Men in Black to the game.]

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Thoroughly unnerved, Temperance spent a couple of days running down the story Sol Molinari had told them in Savannah. There was indeed a Brotherhood of the Yellow Sign, with some shadowy connection to the Vatican, although it seemed to be dormant. Likewise, Drakmar was a real place, an unusual rock formation of striated rocks that had Buddhist shrines nearby. The other members of the expedition were all real people, and all listed as dead.\xa0

      \n

      \n

      She decided that it might be worth paying a visit to the San Francisco Neurotology office.

      \n

      [TP was fishing for Stability here. This was Occult and Research, mostly; a 2 point Outdoorsman spend would have gotten her a connection to the sherpas on the '29 expedition!]

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Candace appointed herself the task of finding the occult bookstore owned by Lawrence Bacon.       \n

      \n

      \n

      CP: ...weird New Jersey!]

      \n

      "The Dark Mare," said Shig. "It's really more of an occult store--antiquities, curiosities, that sort of thing. Not all that great, kind of out of the way." He wrote down the address on the back of a business card for them.

      \n

      The store, such as it was, was actually a house on a pleasant Italian neighborhood. Candace and Charleston walked up and rang the bell. \xa0Several times. Finally a man opened the door a crack.

      \n

      "Yes?" he said. He wore an elegant Imperial beard and mustache that was mostly grey.

      \n

      "May we enter?" said Candace.

      \n

      "Do you have an invitation?"

      \n

      "I didn't know--" But the door slammed in her face.

      \n

      Charleston rattled the door. It opened up a crack. "I think I might have heard of you, sir,\u201d said the man through the door. \u201cIf you are who I've heard of, there's no way I'm letting you in." He slammed the door again.

      \n

      Charleston tapped on the door with his cane for several minutes, using all his considerable powers of annoyance (and they were\xa0considerable; he'd once managed to annoy an Outer God.) Finally he gave up and asked Candace about the buildings on either side; they were San Francisco Victorian houses.

      \n

      "Should we do a stake out?" she asked.

      \n

      "I'm not much use on those," said Charleston. "But I have a certain set of skills. If we can't get past\xa0this\xa0door, we can see about getting access to one of the houses on the either side...and then get in through the upper floor of this house."

      \n

      "You want to break in?"

      \n

      "No, I want\xa0us\xa0to break in."

      \n

      Candace wasn't sanguine about their chances, with her inexperience and Charleston's disability. What do you think will happen? she wondered.

      \n

      Something interesting, said Charleston, but she remained unconvinced about the break-in. Finally she suggested talking to the neighbors before moving on to felonies.

      \n

      [Me: The problem is that Charleston doesn't have an angel and a devil on his shoulders, he has a devil and a Cthulhu.]

      \nEpisode III: You Want It Darker (Part 2)\n

      Jimmy and Temperance decided to pay a visit to the Neurotology office in San Francisco. This was a modest store front in an expensive neighborhood in the financial district. Inside it looked like the waiting room for a doctor's office. "My name is Delia. How may I help you?" asked the receptionist, a pretty woman in her 20s.

      \n

      "My name is Candace," said Temperance, internally wincing at telling a lie. "I was at a soiree the other night and I heard people talking about the wonders of Neurotology..."

      \n

      "Oh, it's a wonderful way to improve your memory, and your physical capabilities--kicks psychotherapy into a cocked hat as far as I'm concerned."

      \n

      Jimmy let them talk while he cased the place. Hanging on the wall was a photograph of an intense man with curly hair and a thin mustache--N. Quincy Lund, he assumed.

      \n

      [My picture for him was of Orson Welles in\xa0The Stranger.]

      \n

      Temperance told Delia she wanted to get a general feel for Neurotology. Delia told her to buy the book,\xa0Diametrics; Temperance bought two, one for her "uncle" Jimmy. Together they cost $10, which was outrageous. Delia offered to have her husband come down to talk to them; Temperance tried to beg off, saying she had a gallery opening, but Delia told her they had so many interesting people who came in, poets, artists, poets who were also artists...

      \n

      "Have you ever heard of Amadou Lalin?" said Delia.

      \n

      "Ye--no," said Temperance, changing her answer when Jimmy kicked her.

      \n

      Delia, flattered, told them about the very\xa0artistic\xa0Mr. Lalin and also mentioned that there was a prominent doctor--a psychologist--who was also a member. Temperance pressed her for a name...Delia resisted for a moment but eventually said it was Dr. Edwina Montague.

      \n

      "What's your names, so I can tell my husband you're here?" said Delia.

      \n

      "Edward McCoy," said Jimmy. "What's involved in meeting him?"

      \n

      "We have a process called Debriefing. We get you talk about past traumas and we use very sensitive electronic equipment to monitor your responses to see when your traumas fade. It's part of our program, the Drama of Thought--where we use Diametrically Opposed Therapy to treat each stage. We call it 'following the DOTs'."

      \n

      A man came into the office, shrugging into a suit jacket. "Didn't know anyone was here," he said, "Especially such a lovely young lady. Peter Morrison." He picked up the clipboard. "Mr. McCoy? Why don't you two come back to my office."

      \n

      His office was a professional looking wood-paneled space, with bookcases full of what Jimmy suspected were fake books. He sat them down and began his hard pitch, going over the levels or "Acts" of DOT: starting with the Audience, DOT 1, moving--provided you attended the classes and paid for the materials--to DOT 2, also known as Act One. And then--

      \n

      "Well, there's levels beyond that, but you need to be in the program," he concluded smugly.

      \n

      "I have some questions," said Jimmy, and then proceeded to aggressively challenge Peter on every point. Soon they were screaming at each other.

      \n

      "You're not ready to pierce the Waves of Mist at DOT 4 and move on to Act Three! Because then you'd have Gone Quiet. Then you'd be a Silent! And there are only a few, and I've met them all! I've met Dr. Montague! I've met Mr. Bacon! They are so far\xa0beyond\xa0you. Their powers are superhuman."

      \n

      "Magic," smirked Jimmy.

      \n

      "Science," said Peter with gritted teeth. "You'll have mental powers that are inconceivable for you, since you're not even DOT 1."

      \n

      Jimmy demanded proof. Peter demanded a reading, and fifty bucks. Jimmy persisted in his skepticism, so Peter unceremoniously chased them out.

      \n

      [This was an Interrogation spend by JP.]

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Charleston and Candace knocked on the door of the house on the right of the Dark Mare bookstore. A pleasant young Italian-American woman opened the door. "Can I help ya? You guys lost or something? Oh, I already got a laundry."

      \n

      "My boss Mr. Jefferson does the best in the city," said Charleston, rolling with it. "We're looking for a bookstore--"

      \n

      "Right next door. The creep. Lorenzo...Lawrence, I mean. He speaks wonderful Italian. Says he's from England...I think sometimes he sounds a little Milanese. Maybe it's because I don't like Milanese; my dad was from Abruzzo."

      \n

      She explained that he mostly kept to himself except to shop at the local Italian groceries. According to Bacon, he'd learned Italian while studying in Florence. She also talked down about Michael, Bacon's shifty looking handyman. Candace kept her chatting long enough to match his description to what Julie Chen had told them.

      \n

      [Reassurance spend by CP, because poking too hard in a close-knit Italian neighborhood needed a spend to get anything other than a slammed door in the face.]

      \n

      They tried the house on the left-hand side, but the woman in it had three kids and no time.

      \n

      \xa0

      \nEpisode III: You Want It Darker (Part 3)\n

      Jimmy dropped by Tuck's building and buzzed the door. To his surprise, he heard the door unlatch. He trudged up the stairs to the office and shoved his way inside. Tuck, a harassed-looking balding man closing on fifty looked up from behind his desk. "Oh,\xa0you," he said with a sigh.

      \n

      "Yeah. I want to know what you found out. What you paid to find out."

      \n

      "Well, the thing is--" he began. They both heard the sound of a board creak out in the hall. The blood drained from Tuck's face and he turned with wild eyes on Jimmy. "You brought them here! You're with them!"

      \n

      "No I am not," said Jimmy. At that moment two men in black suits suddenly appeared by the stairwell. They looked uncannily exactly like the two men he'd seen in the hotel. "I'm Mr. MacAdam," said one. "This is Mr. Asphalt. We're with Security."

      \n

      "How good are you at jumping out of windows?" said Jimmy to Tuck.

      \n

      "Not!"

      \n

      "That's unfortunate," said Jimmy, grabbing him by the arm and plunging through the window.

      \n

      They fell hard, but the office was only on the second floor and even with his advanced years Jimmy still knew how to take a fall. He came up bleeding and with something grating in his shoulder. Tuck was rolling on the sidewalk. "I think I broke my leg," he moaned.

      \n

      Mr. Macadam--or was it Mr. Asphalt?--looked down on them from the window, his face a waxen mask totally devoid of emotion. Jimmy pulled Tuck to his feet and they hobbled over to the curb and hailed a cab.

      \n

      They took refuge in a bar. "What did you do to me?" groused Tuck into his rye whisky. "I mean, I was at Guadalcanal, I saw some stuff...but this thing..."

      \n

      He ran down the points. Lalin was shacked up with some creepy guy in Pacific Heights. (Tuck was not happy about having had to troll the area gay bars.) He'd seen Michael Coombs there too a lot.

      \n

      "By the way, you could have mentioned that this might be a\xa0government project\xa0you set me on," continued Tuck. "Now I got these creepy agents after me! This kid Lalin worked for the Feds on some secret project, testing bombs, who knows what this TAROT was..."

      \n

      He'd managed to track down Carl Simon, Lalin's colleague at TAROT who now wrote a weird newsletter. He showed Jimmy a letter Simon had sent him:

      \n

      \xa0

      \n
      \n

      Dear Sir,

      \n\xa0I received your letter with great interest. \xa0It seems you have begun to unravel some of the mysteries surrounding my past activities.
      \xa0About them I can only say at this stage of our correspondence that I regret some things but others were wondrous. \xa0A new world was revealed to me and I have been awed and cowed by its revelations.\xa0
      As far as your current investigations go, I can provide this information: \xa0there is a man in the city of San Francisco who goes by Lawrence Bacon but I have it on good authority that he is in fact Lorenzo Pancetti, a member of the 1929 Italian expedition to Nepal. \xa0I am sure you have heard of it by now. \xa0Do not be fooled by his current appearance, I am definite that he is the same man. \xa0He owns a small bookstore in Pacific Heights called the Dark Mare. \xa0
      \xa0Be careful around "Bacon". \xa0He is accompanied by a man named Michael Coombs, a man of vicious and brutal nature. \xa0If you seek to confront Bacon, I suggest neutralizing Coombs by distracting him. \xa0He is an alcoholic and while he struggles to control himself he remains susceptible to the lure of the bottle.
      \xa0Be wary of Bacon. \xa0He long ago gave himself up to madness and his abilities are not to be taken lightly. \xa0
      \xa0After that . . . well, I'm sure you will figure it out. \xa0You'll see the connections. \xa0When you want to talk again, post a classified in the Rocky Mountain News and then watch for a reply. \xa0It will have contact instructions.
      \xa0Good luck and I hope to speak to you again soon.
      CS
      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Tuck then began a rambling discourse on how he'd trailed Lalin and Coombs whenever he could. ("You're Jimmy Wright, ain't ya? What happened to you, I heard you were dead.") One night Lalin met with a couple of other people: a curly headed middle-aged man with a mustache, Coombs, and a red-headed lady who had some kind of accent, Irish or Scottish. Lalin liked her for some reason.

      \n

      Tuck began to sweat so Jimmy ordered another round of doubles. One night, said Tuck in fits and starts, he'd followed Bacon out of his house. He'd gone down to the docks on a foggy night, hanging around until he found a wino passed out in a doorway. Bacon did some weird movements with his hands while saying words in some foreign language.

      \n

      "That wino, he just\xa0died," said Tuck. "Not like dropped dead either, like he aged fifty years in a second. And when I saw Bacon walk by, he looked younger somehow! How is that possible!"

      \n

      [Me: What did you get me into! I don't have PC levels of Sanity!]

      \n

      Jimmy advised him to take another long fishing trip and paid him off.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Charleston was very interested in hearing about Bacon's ability to drain vitality. "Nosferatu?" he asked.

      \n

      "Had coffee with one in Vienna after the war. No, I think he did some magic," said Jimmy.

      \n

      Charleston knew the spell; it haunted his thoughts. "You shouldn't believe a word of it," he said, coughing a little bit in a futile attempt to get Jimmy off the subject in front of Temperance.

      \n

      [Cthulhu Mythos use here by CP.]

      \n

      "One thing is clear," he continued. "This Coombs living at Bacon's house? Amadou's boyfriend? He's the one that killed your friend Lily."

      \n

      Jimmy pondered this for a while, then slipped out to a local Army-Navy store. "I'm looking for something in a knife. Something big," he said.

      \n

      "Got a Japanese sword bayonet," said the clerk. "GIs bought a ton of these back from the Pacific. Need anything else?"

      \n

      Jimmy decided to cover up his purchase by picking up a bunch of surplus equipment--a sleeping back, some rope, K-Rations, and a medical kit.

      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n
      Episode III: You Want It Darker (Part 4)\n

      Saturday was another beautiful day in San Francisco: mild temperatures, and after the fog lifted, a cloudless sky. Lily's memorial service was being held near the Japanese Tea Garden.

      \n

      [In fact, it's where the AIDS Memorial Grove will one day be.]

      \n

      The size of the crowd took Jimmy by surprise; either Lily had been more popular than he knew, or Joyce was good at organizing protests. Probably both. They'd set up a temporary stage and Van and his bandmates were there, alternating between bop takes of spirituals and genuine gospel songs. Joyce had brought along some of her very butchest friends to run security. "Be easier if we had motorcycles," she mused in Jimmy's earshot. "Maybe we could form some kind of club..."

      \n

      Lily's ashes were inside a lovely Chinese urn on a pedestal on the stage. "You wanna say something?" asked Joyce. "People are saying things, if they want."

      \n

      "I'm no good at it," Jimmy said, tight-lipped. He kept scanning the edge of the crowd to see if Coombs, like so many murderers, would be looking in on his victim.

      \n

      There! At the edge of the crowd, under the cover of some trees, he picked him out. He didn't look unhappy. Coombs looked up and caught his eyes. For a long moment they stared at each other. Then Coombs turned and ran.

      \n

      Jimmy cursed and hopped off the stage, running for the woods. Temperance came aside of him, panting to keep up. "You need my help to find him," she said. Jimmy swore silently, but she was right: he'd already lost the trail.\xa0

      \n

      [Jimmy has no Surveillance, but Temperance does.]

      \n

      "Where is he?" he said.

      \n

      "You are only going to detain him, right?"

      \n

      "I will detain him."\xa0I'm going to immobilize him. By nailing him to a tree with this bayonet...

      \n

      "I'm trusting you," she said miserably, and then led Jimmy around the edge of the woods; she'd already spied his escape routes and took the best choice.

      \n

      But they were just a bit too slow: they saw him dash out from under the trees and out to the street, where he hoped on a bus that had just pulled up.

      \n

      "Oh," said Temperance.

      \n

      Jimmy screamed and punched a tree. "I just found out something," he said, eyes tearing up. "I\u2019m almost sixty." He moaned with pain and cradled his hand in the crook of his arm.

      \n

      "Not going after him?" said Charleston, huffing up. "Look at you, bawling your eyes out, gripping your bayonet. Find Coombs.\xa0End this."

      \n

      "I have a duty," said Jimmy. "And I'm going to go do that."

      \n

      "You have two duties. One of them's getting a memorial right now. We'll help you out.\xa0I'll\xa0help you out."

      \n

      [I gave Jimmy 2 points of Stability because CP gave him a hard driver.]

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      That night they got ready for their trip to the Asylum.\xa0

      \n

      [JP: I do their makeup!

      \n

      Me: Obi-Lily has taught you well.

      \n

      TP: Noooooo....]

      \n

      Temperance wore her good outfit: it was the same outfit she was wearing anyway, a full skirt, white blouse, and dark grey cardigan. She was putting on her high heels when she saw Candace come in, wearing a slinky black cardigan, black cigarette pants, and ballet flats. A trim beret set off her look.

      \n

      Jimmy was wearing a suit jacket with extra-large armholes to make it easier to draw the long bayonet he had strapped under his armpit. He thought about putting on a tie, but then gave up on the idea.

      \n

      Charleston let Helen dress him; he couldn't see any point about worrying about it.

      \n

      And Temperance strapped a small automatic pistol to her bra strap under her shoulder blades, just the way her mother had taught her.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n
      \nEpisode III: You Want It Darker (Part 5)\n

      They headed out around ten o'clock, through the dark and foggy streets of the Industrial district. Temperance opined that it looked like the set of a film noir movie.

      \n

      "That's because they're filming a movie," said Jimmy, pointing to a bunch of guys setting up a shot. "Hey, you, want to be an extra?" one them shouted at him.\xa0

      \n

      They pushed on until they found a large warehouse. It loomed over them, black and silent, and it had that air of emptiness and wariness only abandoned buildings have. They filed inside. There was nothing they could see--no glimmer of light other than the scatter from the lone streetlamp outside--but after a moment they could hear the faint sound of music coming up from the basement. They walked down a dingy concrete staircase until they came to a heavy steel door. A Judas window opened in it. "You here for the Asylum?"

      \n

      "Yeah, man," said Candace, with a wink. The door opened up. A dubious looking man with a scraggly beard and a black vest looked her over and whistled, and then frowned. "Who's the squares?" he said, nodding his head at Lisa and Temperance.

      \n

      "They're cool, man," said Candace.

      \n

      "All right, all right, and your blind friend is our kind of weird. Come on in, the water's fine."

      \n

      [Counterculture was the governing factor here: you need Counterculture 2+ to get in, but you could spend (at 1 point per person) to bring in people with Counterculture 0, and Counterculture 1 Investigators could spend to "piggyback." Also, given the weird nature of the place, Cthulhu Mythos 2+ got in for free.]

      \n

      Inside the basement had been transformed into a large cabaret-style nightclub. There were little tables gathered around a couple of different performing areas; a wooden bar set up in the center of the room; and some quiet nooks for canoodling. The walls were covered with tapestries and old movie posters. A band was playing the hardest bop jazz with a driving rhythm.

      \n

      Candace was hopping with excitement. "Wait \u2018til I tell Vlad about this." Temperance stared around with a frown. "A lot of disreputable people here."

      \n

      [2-point Stability loss here for Temperance; basically I charged 2-Counterculture to everyone.]

      \n

      The focus of the room was a large stage with some elaborate cardboard sets being rigged up on it. A movie screen hung behind it, and there was a space for a small orchestra to play. It clearly looked like where the evening's main event was going to take place.

      \n

      "Wow, I can totally tell you're an artist, ain't you?" a man wearing a rather unusual assortment of clothes--velvet smoking jacket, khaki fatigue pants, and a too-small trilby said to Candace. "Let me see\u2026poetry...no...prose. You're a novelist."

      \n

      "Wonderful powers of detection," said Candace.

      \n

      "Not me," said the man, holding up a little vial. "It's the Yellow. I'm Nick."

      \n

      "What is that?"

      \n

      "It's the Yellow...if you're creative, it inspires your\xa0true\xa0art. We got a whole room set up," he said, guiding Candace toward the back, where she could see a large studio with easels and desks with typewriters. Several people were working furiously inside it, with looks of intense concentration. From what she could see of the paintings, they looked very good.

      \n

      "Everybody here has some Yellow. Here, have some. I don't know how you take your kicks, but injecting gives you the longest one. Snorting gives you a sharp kick but it slacks off suddenly..." Nick led her to a table near one of the performance stages.

      \n

      Jimmy was following her with his eyes when someone plopped down next to him at the bar. He was wearing longshoreman's clothes\u2014pea coat, watch cap, and tar covered dungarees. "You're an artist, I can tell," he said without preamble. "Your art is your\xa0life. Have some Yellow." He slapped a little envelope on the countertop and walked away.

      \n

      Everyone avoided Temperance; she was far too square. She felt a little tinge of envy; she was actually a skilled restorer of paintings, but had never felt that she had any\xa0real\xa0creativity.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Charleston was tapping his way through the crowd. His cane smacked into someone's ankle. "Sorry, excuse me..."

      \n

      "Teach us, guru," said the man.

      \n

      "Oh no, not you guys!"

      \n

      "We can tell what you are. Teach us. Tell us about the King. Take our Yellow. Bless it for us. Let your artistry escape."

      \n

      Soon there was a small but tight-knit knot of people around Charleston. He tried to ignore them and insult them, but they seemed to think that he was being gnomic. "Who's coming tonight?" he asked one.

      \n

      "Amadou's coming...but there's a bunch of other poets first. Helen Heck is going to read." Whoever he was talking to slipped him a little vial of Yellow. With a sigh, he tapped out a little on the back of his hand and then rubbed it on his gums.

      \n

      At first, he felt the lassitude of an opium high. He sank into a padded armchair, and sighed contentedly. He felt marvelously at\xa0peace\xa0for the first time in a long time. And gradually, through the fog and mists, the room swam into focus, filtered through his now-open Third Eye. Reality quivered around him. For a second he felt that he could step through it and into dreams...but something pulled him back. A surge of creativity. A strong desire--a compulsion, really--to make\xa0art.

      \n

      [Here are the effects of The Yellow:

      \n

      The primary effect of Yellow is to make the user fall first into a listless, relaxed state that gradually makes them completely insensible to their surroundings. During this time, fantastic dreams and visions occur. These generally are a\xa02-point Stability loss. However, if a user makes a spend of\xa0Art,\xa0Pharmacy,\xa0Chemistry, or\xa0Occult\xa0after taking their first dose of Yellow, they may increase their\xa0Cthulhu Mythos\xa0score by +1 (one time only).

      \n

      \xa0After this phase (which lasts from 30 minutes to two hours), the user will suddenly find them plunged into a period of manic creativity.

      \n

      \xa0The mechanical effects of Yellow are as follows:

      \n

      \xa0Users receive a dedicated Art pool equal to 1d6 -3, minimum 1.

      \n

      Users receive an urge to create Art, at least one point a day, with an appropriate amount of time spent, until the pool is exhausted.

      \n

      Resisting this urge is a\xa0Stability Test against a Difficulty of 4. Failure results in the spend of an Art point on pointless parodies of art: hypergraphia, painting endless series of monochrome canvases, singing the same uninteresting twelve tone row over and over again, etc.

      \n

      A user may spend a point of\xa0Sanity\xa0to fully refresh their\xa0Stability\xa0and two other Investigative skills. If they do so, they\xa0must\xa0rewrite one statement.

      \n

      A user with\xa0Cthulhu Mythos\xa0may make\xa0a Test with a difficulty of 5\xa0to enter the Dreamlands, or their 1950s periphery: the Interzone, the Raketen-Stadt, the Socialist Utopia, Main Street USA, etc. The user may spend\xa0Cthulhu Mythos\xa0or\xa0Stability\xa0on this test.

      \n

      ...and of course there are side effects, but we'll get to that in a bit. Charleston was at -1 Stability, so CP took the "spend Sanity for full refresh" option.]

      Unsure -- the thing is, it has to have a nasty mythos side, and art as a driver's not enough.
      \nIt could if it's a Mythos driver of sorts--that is, they drop below 1 Stability then it hits Sanity. (Of course, larger issue is I want to get rid of Sanity entirely, but that's different.)

      \n
      Episode III: You Want It Darker (Part 6)\n

      Temperance had found an unoccupied stool at the bar which she perched on, as forlorn as a lighthouse keeper\u2019s widow. Around her the revels swirled, but she was at a loss on how to join in, or if she even wanted too.

      \n

      Another woman sat next to her. She was wearing a fashionable, if slightly tight, grey skirtsuit. She had blonde hair and was wearing a pair of black patent leather spiked heels. "This your first time?" she asked, placing a hand on Temperance's arm.

      \n

      "I've been to other...meetings before."

      \n

      "This is nothing like any other party. I'm Susan."

      \n

      "Temperance."

      \n

      "That seems appropriate. You want a drink?"

      \n

      "Water...or...I should loosen up a bit. Champagne, or maybe a nice white zinfandel..."

      \n

      "Two whisky sodas," Susan said to the bartender. "Temperance, you're at the Asylum. You're gonna need to..." she reached up and pulled out the comb holding Temperance's hair in a bun. "...loosen up." She slid a little vial full of yellow powder across the bar at her.

      \n

      "I can see it in your eyes," said Susan, staring intently at Temperance. "You've never let yourself really go and let your creativity flow. But I can see you have depths...you have amazing eyes, by the way. And the Yellow will help."

      \n

      "What is it?"

      \n

      "It's a drug. When you take it, it will break the shackles that hold your creative mind back."

      \n

      "Is it like...reefer? I saw a movie about that, and it didn't look good..."

      \n

      "No, this works best if you inject it."

      \n

      "Is it an opiate?"

      \n

      "I don't know what it is. But I'm on it now. Look, if you really don't like needles, you can ingest it. The Edwardians over there--" Susan nodded to a table with men dressed up in the height of velvet-bowed foppery--"like to mix it with absinthe or laudanum, for maximum antique authenticity."

      \n

      [A bit of an anachronism, but there really was an Edwardian fashion moment in San Francisco during the early '60s.]

      \n

      "They serve\xa0absinthe\xa0here?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "Charlie, get me an absinthe," said Susan. The bartender got out his works--flame, spoon, sugar cube, ice--and began making the drink.

      \n

      "What is it you do?" asked Temperance. "Are you a poet? An actress?"

      \n

      "I'm an actor, yes. Not in movies yet. I do a lot of performance art."

      \n

      "You have the face to be in movies."

      \n

      "That's so sweet of you, especially coming from such a beautiful girl." She smiled wide.

      \n

      "Such friendly people here!" muttered Temperance.

      \n

      The bartender passed over the absinthe. "Let me help you with this," said Susan. She dumped the Yellow into the pale green drink and took a long sip. Then she kissed Temperance full on the mouth.

      \n

      Temperance slapped her. "Worth it," said Susan, rubbing her jaw, as Temperance fled into the crowd looking for Jimmy.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      "So when are you going to tell me what you're\xa0really\xa0about," said Helen to Charleston.

      \n

      "Where are you from, Helen?"

      \n

      "I told you, I'm from the real world."

      \n

      "You miss it?"

      \n

      "It was up and down. Your world is up and down. Our world never pulled of anything as destructive as the two wars you pulled off. But you have jet planes. And...there's something wrong with my world, I think. A shadow on it."

      \n

      "I...I'm really fired up to do something I haven't in years," said Charleston breaking into a sweat.

      \n

      Charleston stretched out his arms, and then swept her up and laid her on top of the bar. "Here? All right," said Helen, reaching up to unhook her bra.

      \n

      Charleston ripped her dress open from throat to navel. He smashed a glass on the bar, then took a shard and cut his hand open. With the blood flowing from his wound, he began to trace weird symbols on Helen's skin. "I used to dabble a bit in art myself," he said to the crowd that had gathered around them. "I made something once. Something really beautiful...it got away from me a little bit. But I can't get these symbols out my mind..."

      \n

      Charleston was so intent on what he was doing that he didn't notice that he had started to\xa0levitate\xa0next to the bar. He was busy tracing out horoscopes on Helen's flesh: two separate horoscopes that merged together at one point. He reached out to open her mind: if this worked he'd be able to connect it with her own world, let her communicate...

      \n

      [I pulled out the magic "rules" I had used for Millicent Lowell in the Eternal Lies campaign, so this was a General Test that you could spend Cthulhu Mythos on; CP spent 3 and rolled a 5. But the Difficulty was 6...which provoked a 3-point Stability loss...]

      \n

      Helen began to scream, scream like her head was being crushed. Jimmy came pushing through the crowd and took it all in one sweep: the naked woman, the hieroglyphics, the\xa0levitating man.

      \n

      "Levitation. Again," said Jimmy with a grimace. He cold-cocked Charleston, who suddenly came to himself. He crashed to the floor and pulled himself up, smearing a bloody handprint on Helen's stomach. "Oh, that's not good," he muttered.\xa0

      \n

      Helen kept screaming. Temperance, who had just arrived, grabbed someone's beer and splashed it on Helen, erasing even more of the bloody symbols. Helen began to convulse.

      \n

      "I need something to get her out of this!" said Temperance.

      \n

      "Here's some heroin!" said a woman, shoving her works at Temperance. She took them limply, with a look of shock on her face.

      \n

      Jimmy grabbed them out her hands, and expertly tied off a vein in Helen's arm and injected her with the smack. She began to calm down and fell into a slumber. Some men helped Jimmy take her to a quiet room with some other people who needed to come down a bit.

      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n Also, poor Temperance.

      \nEpisode III: You Want It Darker (Part 7)\n

      Candace was having a blast over in her corner, so engaged in conversation that she didn't even notice the commotion by the bar. Her new friends were trying to get her to take some Yellow, but she protested: hers was a solitary art, after all.

      \n

      "You don't write poetry?" said Nick.

      \n

      "I do, but I'm mostly a novelist." A blonde woman in a grey skirtsuit slumped down next to Candace. "Struck out again," said Susan.

      \n

      "I'm sure you'll do better next time, dear," said Candace.

      \n

      "She was really pretty too. Hello, Allen."

      \n

      Allen Ginsberg sat down next to them. "Candace, right? Jack's new friend? So glad you found the party. It reaches out to you, through the universal cosmic oversoul."

      \n

      "I found it. Well, it found me."

      \n

      "Exactly. Hey Nick, give me some Yellow. I'm interested in many chemicals," he said with a glance at Candace, "but this has proven to be very effective for my art."

      \n

      "Is Jack coming?"

      \n

      "He doesn't usually come to these things. He came a few times, but he was so inebriated that he passed out before the show began. He did tell me about you, he said he enjoyed your company very much and that you were a gone chick and really with it."

      \n

      "Very kind of him."

      \n

      Ginsberg waved somebody over. "Amadou! Come here and meet our friends."

      \n

      A thin, slight man, elegantly dressed in a chalk stripe suit with a foulard scarf wrapped around his neck, approached the banquette they were sitting on. He had a cafe au lait complexion, and his long hair was pulled back into a ponytail. His eyes were dark and sensual and looked almost as if they were rimmed with kohl. But there was something absent about them, something far away, something seeking but never finding. He moved gracefully and had an ethereal quality, and a soft, lilting voice.

      \n

      [I used Jaye Davidson as the portrait for Amadou.]

      \n

      "Hello...I am Amadou...Lalin."

      \n

      "Candace Heartbrooke. I'm an author."

      \n

      "I write poems...and plays. And sometimes I paint."

      \n

      "I read one of your poems. It was wonderful."

      \n

      "I haven't published any of them, how did you read it?"

      \n

      "Allen gave it to me."

      \n

      "Oh, Allen, you've been naughty again. What was it about?"

      \n

      "A place..."

      \n

      "Carcosa? I write about it a lot.\xa0Parlez-vous francais?"

      \n

      "Un peu."

      \n

      "Have you seen Carcosa?"

      \n

      "No."

      \n

      "Are you staying for my show? Then you'll have a chance...oh, Michael." Amadou waved languidly to a man standing near the stage. He had the desperate strut of a wounded gamecock, and he looked around him with a sneer that seemed etched into his face. "That's my friend Michael," said Amadou. "He's not a very nice man but I like him." He lightly touched Candace's face. "You're an artist but something is holding you back...you haven't accomplished what you want to accomplish. I felt that way too...for a long time. I met a man who helped. A great man, a good man. I think he's dead now. His name was Percy. I loved him in my own way. He showed me Carcosa. And then I understood how to fulfill my art. Soon I will fulfill it. Soon, very soon, I will walk the streets again."

      \n

      "You're working on a masterpiece?"

      \n

      "To say the least. It's not quite ready yet. Soon, very soon. I will do it for my friends who want me to do it. And I will stay where I want to be. Not this poor world, but a better world, a more beautiful world. I'd love to show it to you one day. Perhaps you see it tonight. If you wish, take the Yellow while you watch it. Most people find it a very engaging experience like that. I have to go now."

      \n

      [I was channeling some Andy Warhol here.]

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Temperance sat glowering at the bar. "I had to give it to her to calm her down," Jimmy said.

      \n

      "Heroin!"

      \n

      "Did you have anything better?"

      \n

      "I splashed her with beer to wake her up! Don't they have a first aid kit? Look, they've got a fire extinguisher...oh wait that that's conceptual art."

      \n

      "Didn't you learn anything from Murphy about being ready for things?"

      \n

      "Mostly the Colonel taught me about containing the collateral damage." She sighed. "Look, there's a string quartet...with a singer...I think the show is going to start soon."

      \n

      [In fact, I played the Schonberg 2nd String Quartet here; it was the opening act, and I started it at the line "I feel the air of another planet..."]

      \n

      They made their way to the main stage area. Candace had grabbed them some seats and she waved them over to her. There was a furious circle of activity going on at the stage: a guy was loading a projector, some men were putting on costumes (mostly togas, it seemed), and some women in dance tights were stretching out.

      \n

      "I want to\xa0see\xa0this performance," said Candace to Ginsberg.

      \n

      "Of course, we all come here for it. The performance is usually amazing. I'm really not sure where Amadou is going, but it gets more elaborate every time. The film is very interesting. Shame he never got a chance to show it the way he wanted to before."

      \n

      Amadou suddenly strode onto the the stage. He stood in the spotlight, swaying a little, as the string quartet continued to play softly. He ran his hand over his forehead, leaned on the microphone stand, and without looking up began to recite. "Cassie...oh Cassie I can't see you anymore but I know you're out there somewhere. I'm waiting to see you again and I'll see you soon. Being locked here is so inconvenient. It means I can't finish my work yet. I can't go to where I want to go. I have to write honestly. I have to show you honestly what I'm doing. You have to open your mind and your eyes to see what is\xa0out there. A bigger world, a greater world, beyond the Pallid Mask, beyond the Lake and its beauty..."

      \n

      He swayed forward for a second and righted himself. "Edie said I can only work with her but I'm going to go beyond\xa0everything. Oh...is Barbara still out there? Is she still calling for the King? Has she brought him here yet? I can't sense it. Have you seen it? The Yellow Sign? Have you seen it yet? Edie and I will soon be done. I will walk my streets again. Yes. Maybe you'll see it too. Maybe you'll find it."

      \n

      He collapsed and the lights went out. And then the film started...

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
