      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode III: You Want It Darker (Part 8)\n

      Later, when they talked about what they had seen, they felt that the movie was much better than the small portion they had seen from it before: Temperance (disdainfully) and Candace (excitedly) recognized the heavy influence of German Expressionism on the sets and lighting design. But there was also something else, a bit of the\xa0fin de si\xe8cle\xa0melancholy of the Decadents mixed in--a strange but thrilling combination of doom and anticipation.

      \n

      The film had been shot in black and white, but in places the frames had been hand colored to bring out different moods. Candace, who had snorted some Yellow right before the film began, was deeply inspired by the artistry of the movie. It was clear to here that all the effects had been done "in camera" which bewildered her because some seemed impossible to achieve. Jimmy was convinced that the film was an elaborate attempt at steganography, although what the message being hidden was he could not say.

      \n

      [Photography for the effects, Cryptography to pick up the steganography.]

      \n

      The plot was hard to follow, or at least hard to keep in their heads, and at one point their recollections of the film diverged wildly. Lisa made a point of compiling their versions of what they had seen and typed them up for the notes she was keeping:

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Act One\xa0

      \n

      In the first act, a young poet encountered a woman wandering in the desert. He took her with him to a large building that she referred to as a castle. There she was introduced to the others, whom she invariably gave royal titles. Most of the other characters seemed to think she was mad, but the poet had clearly fallen in love with her.

      \n

      In Scene 2, the woman, who is addressed as \u201cCassie\u201d, sang a lovely song about a strange realm called Carcosa. Excited, the poet decided to use her stories as the theme for a masked ball that evening. As the ball began, a strange man in a white mask appeared; no one seemed to know him, but Cassie and a young woman from the \u201ccastle\u201d tried to speak with him. Their confusion suggested they thought he was the poet, but much to their surprise he suddenly appeared as the clock approaches midnight. \u201cWho are you, really?\u201d he asked Cassie, but she turned away, distracted, as the Stranger approached.

      \n

      Midnight struck. Everyone unmasked but the Stranger. Cassie and the other woman, Camilla, demanded that he follow suit. He claimed not to be wearing a mask, which terrified Camilla; then he raised his arms, and the Yellow Sign blazoned on his robes was fully visible. The screen went black for a long time, over a minute; because of persistence of vision, the Yellow Sign seemed to linger in the air long after the screen had gone dark.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Act Two

      \n

      Cassie\u2014or Queen Cassilda, as the poet had taken to calling her, identifying her with one of the characters in her stories, fled the \u201ccastle\u201d and headed for a city. The location shots are of an unidentified American city that seemed cut out of a thick block of Film Noir: shadowy alleyways filled with fog, flickering neon, strangers with hidden faces pursuing them through the night. They went to a nightclub. The poet tried to kiss Cassilda, but she gently and distractedly put him off. Suddenly they realized that the music has stopped and the other patrons were no longer talking; instead, they were looking expectantly at the door to the nightclub. Slowly they turned their gaze to Cassie and the poet; except now they were suddenly all wearing masks.

      \n

      The door opened. There was a glare of light. A figure stepped into the nightclub. He was surrounded by a harsh nimbus of light that made it difficult to see any details other than he was very tall\u2026

      \n

      They each had different recollections of what happened next:

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Temperance's Impression of Act Two, Scene 3

      \n

      The Stranger walked in. The poet did not notice him at all. The Stranger took the hand of Cassilda, who was frozen in fear and shock, and silently handed her a pair of masks. Gently, lovingly, she placed one of them on the poet\u2019s face, and then covered her own face with the other. In an extreme closeup, viewers saw tears welling out from the eyeholes of the mask\u2026but the eyes behind them were harsh and somehow not human\u2026

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Candace's Impression of Act Two, Scene 3

      \n

      The Stranger appeared and walked right past Cassilda, who seemed not to notice him. He helped up the poet, who had fallen to his knees, and they both turned toward the figure in the doorway. The Stranger whispered, \u201cThe King!\u201d and the poet nodded mutely. The music rose to a triumphant, religious tone as the King extended a long-fingered hand at the poet, who wept tears of joy\u2026

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Charleston's Impression of Act Two, Scene 3

      \n

      The poet fell convulsing to the floor. The Stranger appeared, grabbed a shrieking Cassilda by the neck, and threw her down at the feet of the figure in the doorway. She rose to her knees. \u201cWhy, O King?\u201d she moaned.\xa0

      \n

      \u201cWe have sent thee the Yellow Sign. And it calleth thou home.\u201d

      \n

      \u201cI will never return to Carcosa,\u201d she said with desperate intensity.

      \n

      \u201cThinkest thou that thou hast left? Look thou out upon our realm of Carcosa. Thou mayest never leave her until we shall step down from red Aldebaran and the Hyades shall give up their secret.\u201d

      \n

      Cassilda shrieked, and with a final lunge she pushed through the doorway and into the streets. The King\u2019s mocking voice followed her as she dashed from corner to corner.

      \n

      \u201cThou canst never leave. We shall give no leave to do that which is forbidden to ourselves. Upon thee shall fall the same fate as us. Forever.\u201d

      \n

      \u201cNot upon us, O King!\u201d Cassilda wailed.

      \n

      \u201cForever.\u201d

      \n

      \u201cNot upon us!\u201d

      \n

      Forever.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Jimmy's Impression of Act Two, Scene 3

      \n

      The figure raised one bony hand. Both the poet and Cassilda fell to the ground, shrieking and convulsing. The Stranger appeared. Slowly he removed his mask. The face behind it was inhuman, unspeakable, and blasts itself from the memory of anyone who saw it; it was impossible not to turn away in horror. The next time the viewer looked at the screen, Cassilda and the poet, both wearing masks and dressed in white robes, were being carried in biers by people wearing vaguely medieval costumes. The music was low and funereal; this was clearly a cortege of some kind. They approached a cemetery in the twilight. The procession paused in front of a massive marble tomb and waited as the light slowly grew stronger.

      \n

      There was a cut away to the sun rising over a misty lake. As its rays touched the masked face of Cassilda, the Stranger appeared. He took her hand and she stepped down from the bier. She led the cortege down from the tomb as the poet stumbled off his own bier and fled in the opposite direction\u2026

      \n

      \xa0

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nFebruary 2017 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n Episode III: You Want It Darker (Part 9)\n

      The Final Sequence

      \n

      The poet was pursuing Cassilda along a sandy beach. Both were naked. Shreds of mist washed over them. The poet caught up to Cassilda and tackled her. They rolled around on the ground, fighting and scratching, until he locked his hands around her throat. He crouched over her, choking the life out of her, until at almost the last possible moment he released her and rolled away, weeping. She slowly lifted herself into a crouch, too exhausted to try to flee.

      \n

      Still lying on his back, not even looking at her, the poet once again gasped out, \u201cWho are, you, really?\u201d

      \n

      \u201cWho am I, really,\u201d she repeated to herself. \u201cReally, who am I. Am I? Who? Am I\u2026real\u2026\u201d\xa0

      \n

      She stopped and gazed out at the camera. Something sparkled out of the frame, casting a play of light across her face.

      \n

      The camera pulled back and both characters look out at the same object, slowly revealed by the camera\u2019s motion: a battered diadem or crown, washed up in the waves lapping the shoreline. The poet and Cassilda slowly stood and held hands, looking out across the water as the sun rose, washing everything with a bright glare. The film began to be tinted yellow as the camera panned up to reveal a\xa0second\xa0sun hanging angrily in the sky above the one rising over the horizon. The yellow tint got more and more intense until the entire frame was a pulsating, sickly chromium yellow. The film abruptly cut to black and the soundtrack stopped.

      \n

      There were no credits.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      They all sat stunned as the lights came back up. Their minds reeled from the burning symbol--the Yellow Sign--that seemed to hang lack an afterimage in the air before their eyes. Candace and Temperance both felt that it was the finest work of art they had ever seen in their lives. They had cried during the movie without even noticing.

      \n

      [2 points of Stability loss for seeing the Yellow Sign; the opinion of the film's quality is likewise a side effect.]

      \n

      Charleston recovered first. Still high on the Yellow, he didn't even notice that he was able to see around him (after his own fashion). With a sudden shock he realized that there was no way for either the King or the Stranger to speak with all their masks and prosthetics on, yet their lines--which hadn't been wildtracked in--were articulated clearly.

      \n

      Temperance stood up and gave a solo standing ovation. Around her, the crowd began to stagger away in pairs or larger groups for the quieter areas of the room. They room pulsed with musky desire.

      \n

      Helen leaned on Charleston's shoulder. "Oh, you saw it?"

      \n

      "Yes. Not sure how."

      \n

      "You want to have sex?"

      \n

      "Yes, I think that's for the best."\xa0

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Susan walked up to Temperance, still standing alone, and hugged her. "Are we feeling better?"

      \n

      Temperance clutched her crucifix. "I'm fine." There was finality in the air.

      \n

      Susan sighed, and turned to Candace. "Well, how about you, toots?"

      \n

      Candace looked at her steadily. "Sure, why not. Jack's not here."

      \n

      Temperance spluttered. "That doesn't mean you go with Jill!" she shouted as Susan led Candace away by the hand.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Lisa was sitting in stunned silence. Jimmy moved over next to her. "Mr. Wright," she stammered. "I...don't know why but I feel like you should know what to do. It was so beautiful..." He took her elbow and maneuvered her to the bar, where he ordered a couple of stiff drinks...and then another couple after that.

      \n

      "This is what came of TAROT," he said.

      \n

      "Was Percy involved?"

      \n

      "I don't know, but it resulted in this."

      \n

      "But it was so beautiful..."

      \n

      "Beauty is only skin deep."

      \n

      "You mean like in Rilke? \xa0'Beauty is only the beginning of terror.'"

      \n

      Jimmy shrugged. "Whatever made it wasn't beautiful," he said.

      \n

      "Anthropologically it was an interesting document...but I'm just a girl from Kansas, I don't know about this kind of thing."

      \n

      "I don't know what to do most of the time. But I just\xa0do. I move. I try. And eventually things get clearer."

      \n

      "That sounds like an interesting life. When I was a little girl I used to think about doing stuff like that. I was going to be an adventurer, like in the film reels. Am I doing that now, Mr. Wright? You tell me, you're the boss."

      \n

      Jimmy clenched the letter in his pocket. "No I'm not," he said softly.

      \n

      "Where are you from, Mr. Wright?"

      \n

      "New York."

      \n

      "I like New York. I worked there for a little bit during the war. It's kind of ironic, actually, you being from New York, because of where I'm from. A college town in Kansas called Manhattan."

      \n

      "Small world. We should probably get back, get some rest. Don't worry about the others," he said, casting his gaze around, "they'll be fine."

      \n

      He helped her put on her coat. Out of the corner of his eye he saw Amadou get corralled by Michael Coombs and a couple of guys in bad suits. They were pushing him toward the back door, but it was taking them a while.

      \n

      Jimmy didn't even think. He raced over to the front door, ran through it, and then took the stairs two at a time back to the ground level. He skidded across the dusty concrete floor of the warehouse to the back entrance, dashed through it, and stopped in the middle off the alleyway behind the warehouse, facing the basement service entrance. He heard the door slam behind him and Lisa and Temperance clattered down the stairs. He motioned them into the shadows.

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

    • \n

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode III: You Want It Darker (Part 10)\n

      The service door burst open, and a knot of men shuffled through it. Jimmy edged forward into the glare of the streetlight. A light rain was falling, and tendrils of mist curled around his feet. Amadou lolled in the grasp of the two men in suits; Coombs looked up and barked at Jimmy, "What the fuck do you want?"

      \n

      Jimmy stared.

      \n

      "I don't have time for this," said Coombs. He and the others began to drag Amadou up the ramp from the basement door and into the alleyway. Jimmy didn't move a muscle. Coombs stopped short and caught Jimmy's gaze. The ghost of a sneer flitted across his face. "Boys," he said. The goons pulled out snub nosed revolvers.\xa0

      \n

      "We don't want any trouble," said Coombs. "You don't want any trouble. What are you gonna do?"

      \n

      "You killed her," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "Killed who? I killed a lot of people in the war."

      \n

      "You made one mistake. You killed my friend. Lily."

      \n

      "Who, the homo?"

      \n

      Jimmy growled. He braced off his back foot and lunged at Coombs, who was already drawing his rather nasty looking commando knife. Jimmy cracked his forearm against Coombs' wrist; there was a sharp crack as the scabbard of the bayonet he'd concealed up his sleeve smashed into hard bone. Coombs screamed and dropped his knife.

      \n

      One of the goons fired his pistol. Jimmy danced back and the bullet smashed into the brick wall behind him.

      \n

      [Quick analysis: this was an Athletics test to get in range before Coombs could cut Jimmy (he's an experienced knife fighter and letting his opponent attack first is one of his tricks.) JP got a total of 8, which let Jimmy claim an extra benefit in my house rules; that was how the disarm happened. The goon fired back and hit Jimmy, but as long as the target\u2019s Health stays above zero I usually treat damage like that as near misses.]

      \n

      Temperance pulled out the little gun from under her shoulder blades and fired two shots in the air. Everyone froze. The icy rain ran down her neck and she shivered. One goon dropped into a shooter's stance and shot back at her. She slipped up against the wall, breathing heavily.

      \n

      [Good idea by TP, until I asked if Temperance had any Intimidate; she doesn't. So in this case even though the gun was scary, I ruled that without Intimidate the goons would realize she didn't want to kill them and they started shooting back. This is a nice example, I think, of making abilities count even in their absence.]

      \n

      Coombs lunged for his knife. Jimmy danced toward him but then saw the goons taking a bead on Temperance. He turned on them and growled like a Burmese tiger: "I have no business with you. Go!"

      \n

      They took one look at him and began running up the alley, dragging Amadou with them. Temperance waited until they passed her, and then sped off in pursuit.

      \n

      [2-point Intimidate spend by JP. I gave Jimmy back 2 points of Stability because staying to fight Coombs was hitting his Duty drive.]

      \n

      Coombs swept up his knife and stepped back, whipping it in front of him. "This how you want to go out? Dying for that [slur]? Fine. I'll kill you too."

      \n

      Jimmy screamed and lunged in, bringing the knife down in an overhand feint before flipping it over in his hands and ducking under Coombs' block. He slashed through his jacket, coming within a hair's breadth of impaling him.

      \n

      Coombs grabbed Jimmy's arm and spun him away, slashing out with his knife as he did. Jimmy felt it tear into his side just below his floating ribs and grimaced in pain. He backed up and felt the wound. His hand came away very bloody.

      \n

      "Who the FUCK ARE YOU!" shouted Coombs.

      \n

      "Your worst nightmare!"

      \n

      "Who says things like that? We can drop this right now. We don't have to do this anymore, none of us is too banged up."

      \n

      Jimmy narrowed his eyes and bulled in, stabbing wildly, but even in his winded state the younger Coombs was able to dodge. He stabbed Jimmy under the ribs again. Jimmy stumbled and slid to the ground. Coombs kicked him in the back. "I'll kill you like I killed that bitch!" he said as Jimmy struggled to get up. He sank to his knees, staring dead-eyed ahead of him.

      \n

      Coombs circled around behind him. He smirked as he walked up to grab Jimmy by the hair and cut his throat. Jimmy kept staring forward. As Coombs wrapped his knife hand around his neck, Jimmy's left hand flashed out and grabbed him by the wrist. He pulled Coomb's arm down and forward, yanking him off balance while his right hand jammed his knife backwards into Coombs' torso. He felt the point, which he had spent all afternoon filling to needle sharpness, strike home. Coombs stumbled back, pulling the knife out of Jimmy's hand.

      \n

      [And JP challenges Jimmy's Duty Statement "Ugh, here I go again!" by breaking his promise to Temperance. The Health and Weapons refresh was enough to do Terrible Harm on Coombs.]

      \n

      Jimmy slowly stood up. One sleeve of his jacket had been ripped off the shoulder. He walked over to Coombs. He grabbed the handle of his bayonet, still stuck in Coombs' chest, and gave him a sharp kick to pull it free. Blood spurted from the wound, and he could hear the sucking sound of air rushing in. Jimmy looked around for a moment, then scooped up Coombs' knife and slipped it under his coat. He grabbed Lisa, who was pressed up against the wall of the alley with her face twisted with shock, and they began running as the first police sirens could be heard in the distance.

      \n

      A later installment makes it clear Coombs died.

      \n
      \nEpisode III: You Want It Darker (Part 11)\n

      Temperance huffed down the dark streets of the Industrial district. Up ahead was Market Street; she reached it just in time to see the two suits pile themselves and Amadou into a cab and speed off.

      \n

      She froze in frustration for a moment, until another cab rolled up. "Hey, toots, need a ride?" asked the cabbie.

      \n

      "Yeah," she said, climbing in. "Follow that car!"

      \n

      "I always wanted somebody to ask that," said the cabbie, turning on the meter and gunning the engine. "You do this kind of thing a lot?"

      \n

      "No, just been a hell of a night," moaned Temperance. "No judgments, but you wouldn't happen to have a flask on you?" The cabbie grinned and slipped her a pint of bourbon.

      \n

      They followed Amadou's cab up Market and then along Broadway. It soon was clear they were headed to Pacific Heights. Finally the cab stopped outside a rather dismal looking house. Temperance hadn't seen it before, or the man who came out to the car, but she knew where she must be: the Dark Mare bookstore. The man must be Lawrence Bacon. She stopped the cab a few blocks away and then hurried back to the house, keeping in the shadows on the other side of the street.

      \n

      Bacon helped the goons carry Amadou into the house. Edie Montague came out onto the porch, wrapped in her cardigan. "Ah, Amadou," she muttered. "Take him upstairs, I'll be up in a minute." Bacon closed the door behind her and she stood for a while in the misty night, smoking.

      \n

      "All right, lassie," she finally said, flicking her cigarette into the street. "Come out into the light and let me see you."

      \n

      Temperance froze as Edie walked down from the porch and stood under a streetlight. Then she \xa0stepped out herself into the light of another streetlight, a few lampposts away from Edie.

      \n

      "What are you here for?" asked Edie.

      \n

      "Curiosity, mostly," said Temperance.

      \n

      "Ah, curiosity? Let me show you something curious then." Edie pulled a straight razor out from under her sweater, where it hung from a cord. She flicked it open, and then made a clean cut down the back of her forearm, a broad slice like peeling an apple. She shook the flap of skin off her arm and it fell to the street. Blood glistened black under the yellow glare of the streetlight. Temperance could see the skin already begin to reknit on Edie's arm.

      \n

      "Come here and let me show you how I did that," said Edie.

      \n

      Temperance backed up slowly. Edie put her head down and ran at her. Temperance watched her blink in and out of sight as she raced through the circles of light cast by the lamps. She drew her gun and dropped into shooter's stance, waiting...waiting...and firing as Edie dashed through the last circle of light. It struck the Scotswoman center mass and\xa0she didn't stop running\xa0and Temperance turned to run and Edie kicked her leg out from under her and the razor flashed down and carved a square of skin off the back of her hand...

      \n

      Edie stopped. She looked at the back of her own hand. She flicked out the razor again and sliced an identical patch of skin from it. Temperance remembered through her shock how when Miss Yates had died, there had been enough blood for two bodies; now she knew why.

      \n

      "I always found the fascia of the hand interesting in anatomy class," said Edie. "That was a guid hit you gave me there, girlie. I almost felt it." Temperance could see the blood staining Edie's blouse.

      \n

      She kicked off her heels and jumped up, running for her life. She could hear Edie following close behind.\xa0Maybe regeneration causes the lactic acid to not build up as fast\xa0thought Temperance, somewhat hysterically, as she ran. She ran and ran, down the quiet streets, always hearing the other woman close behind.

      \n

      Suddenly she saw a cab up ahead. She ran up and yanked the door open. It was the same cab as before; he'd been circling to find another fare. "Hey, toots--holy hell!" he said when he saw Temperance's bleeding hand.

      \n

      "Drive! Drive!" gasped Temperance. The cabbie looked up and saw Edie running down the street. "Does she have a razor?" he said. Then he threw the car into gear.

      \n

      Sam--that was his name--drove Temperance to the hospital, and then stayed there waiting for her to come out of the examining room. A big patch of gauze covered the stitches the doctor had put in. He offered her a cigarette, which she took gratefully. "Gosh, I'm sorry ma'am. Let me take you back to the hotel." She smiled blankly.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Jimmy and Lisa raced through the streets. He grabbed her to slow her down. A police car, sirens blaring and lights flashing, sped past them.

      \n

      "Mr. Wright--you did that--for your friend--I..." She grabbed him and kissed him on the mouth.

      \n

      "I'm sorry," she said as he pulled gently away. "I mean...is this what it's like...my goodness, you're bleeding! You need to get to a hospital."

      \n

      "No hospital," he panted. "Just go back to the hotel." She nodded and went to flag down a cab.

      \n

      As it turned out, she'd learned some emergency medicine when she'd been overseas; that was how she\u2019d met Percy, helping victims at the site of a V-2 strike. When they got back to the hotel she dug around the military surplus Jimmy had bought and came out with the first aid kit. She stitched up Jimmy\u2019s wounds in his room. They weren't as serious as she feared, although she wished she could do more than give him some sulfa and slap a compression bandage over the stitches.

      \n

      "I'm going to go wash all the blood off my hands," Lisa said.

      \n


      "It does come out," said Charleston as he stepped out of his room. He was wearing a dressing gown, adding an incongruous touch of class to his weathered frame.

      \n

      "Mr. Chiu, can I ask you a question?" said Lisa.

      \n

      "I'll allow it."

      \n

      "You seemed to respond to the film as if you were watching it."

      \n

      "Is this really the time for that question?"

      \n

      "I'm covered in Mr. Wright's blood, so maybe."\xa0

      \n

      It was of course at this moment that Temperance arrived, leaning on Sam the cabbie's shoulder. "Holy cow," he said when he saw Lisa. "What are you people\xa0up to? Serves me right for pulling an extra shift in my brother-in-law's cab." A groan and a howl came from Jimmy's room, unnerving Sam, although it was only Betty jumping up on his stomach.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Temperance collapsed into her bed, the whisky sloshing unpleasantly in her stomach. She was unconscious almost as soon as her head hit the pillow. And she dreamed:

      \n

      She was back on the street in front of Lawrence Bacon's house. Edie was frozen in place behind her, razor blade out, trailing drops of blood that hung uncannily in the air. Standing next to her was Charlie, smoking a cigarette.

      \n

      "I have only one question," she asked him. "Am I going to have to kill someone?"

      \n

      "You don't\xa0have\xa0to kill anyone."

      \n

      "Can I do this? Will doing this help other people survive?"

      \n

      "Maybe. Little Miss, you've never killed anyone. I have. Interesting. That looks like an Unspeakable Possessor you've got here. Tough draw for your first. Enjoy yourself...but not too much."

      \n

      "I don't like some of the things I've found out about..." said Temperance. She turned around and saw Susan standing there. She shrieked and woke up with a start.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Charleston walked into Jimmy's room, sniffing. "Smell of blood...the sound of Jimmy chugging whisky...did you get him?"

      \n

      "Yes," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "Fine work. I'm sure your friend, wherever she is, probably doesn't give a damn. But it helps put a bookend on things for you."

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n\nLisa Padol \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nFebruary 2017 \n

      \n
      \n
      \n Hey, Millicent will be glad Jimmy got the thug. It'll save her from considering whether to ask her sister if she wants to have the kind of fun Millicent generally tries to stop her from having. (Him? Okay, yes, you can turn him inside out or through the eighth dimension.)
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n

      \n
      \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nFebruary 2017 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode III: You Want It Darker (Part 12)\n

      In the morning, Charleston woke up with an enormous craving for the Yellow. His hands shook, but he tried to shrug it off. For a while he drew endless looping doodles on a notepad, until finally his head cleared.

      \n

      [When a Yellow user's Art pool--the temporary pool granted by the Yellow and her own Art pool if any--is exhausted, then it's a Difficulty 4 Stability Test to avoid taking it. So it's a manageable addiction--but the trap is that an artist must permanently forgo some of her talent to avoid addiction. CP added a secondary Drive here, "Addicted to the Yellow."]

      \n

      Candace, on the other hand, woke up inspired. As if her head had cleared overnight, she suddenly had her next novel in her head--like all she needed to do was type it out...

      \n

      Throughout the day the only thing anyone heard from her room was the sound of rapid-fire typing.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      She took a break in the afternoon to go with Temperance to see if they could dig anything up on Bacon from her writer friends. They found Neal Cassady and Kerouac in a bar near City Lights. Jack was already three sheets to the wind, and it was still early in the afternoon.

      \n

      "Ah, the fair Temperance and the fair Candace: two names that rhyme, there's an assonance and dissonance of consonants and vowels..."

      \n

      "Yes, yes," said Temperance. "Listen, we had an inspired evening, Amadou is a genius. We want to see it again."

      \n

      That could be a problem, Neal said. Around dawn the cops had found a body in the alleyway behind the warehouse the party had been held at--some cat named Coombs, Amadou's boyfriend, had been brutally murdered. The cops had raided the party and arrested a lot of people; Amadou wasn't one of them, but nobody knew where he was.

      \n

      He asked Candace how her work was going, and was happy to hear that she had started her novel. "Inspired by Jack, or by Amadou?"

      \n

      "By all of you," she said.

      \n

      Neal was happy to hear that. Some people, he said, only had one great work in them; some, like himself perhaps, had none. But Amadou had\xa0two\xa0works in him, he thought. "He's definitely a cat who is somewhere other than else," he concluded sadly.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      When Temperance came back to the hotel, she went to Jimmy's room to change his dressings. He looked at her warily as she put her Bible down on the nightstand. He grimaced as she stripped off the bandage and cleaned the suture site--although in truth she was very gentle. She finished re-bandaging him, and then put a hand on his shoulder.

      \n

      "I think there are enough monsters in the world," she said. "We don't need any more."

      \n

      She left without waiting for a reply. Without taking her Bible with her.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Helen dropped back in on Charleston. "What did you do?" she demanded.

      \n

      He lit a cigarette. "I had a selfish thought."

      \n

      "What a surprise."

      \n

      "I thought I could solve your problems by giving you the ability to do things that I knew how to do. But if I'm being honest,\xa0I\xa0just wanted to do the things I knew how to do. I wanted you to be able to hear from where you're from."

      \n

      "The real world."

      \n

      "Let's put that aside and just say you're not from around here...what you need is what I always wanted, a little bit of agency over your life. But I think I messed it up."

      \n

      Probably, she said. She'd heard strange piping and danced for a while around some kind of swirling chaos. Then she'd met someone, an Arabic-looking girl with thick glasses. The girl had told her that Charleston was doing his best but not doing things well. That he had stopped asking for help...and that she knew Charleston and was going to see him again soon. "She did tell me something," finished Helen. "She told me how to do what you were trying to do. And that you were probably regretting a lot of things that you did because you hadn't listened to her."

      \n

      Charleston lit another cigarette. "I guess it's true about good intentions. There's a saying about that. Wish I could remember it."

      \n

      "So you want to do it again sober?"

      \n

      He sputtered. "You want to try that\xa0here?"

      \n

      "Not the magic! I didn't come here for no reason."

      \n

      He grinned. "Let's take it from the top."

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n

      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode III: You Want It Darker (Part 13)\n

      Temperance went up to Pacific Heights; she wasn't the most friendly person in the world, but if she could talk to the parish priest, she might be able to dig up some facts about Lawrence Bacon. Father Vic, the priest, one of those bright-eyed young men, was happy to talk with her after mass, although he had a different idea about why this serious and apparently devout woman wanted to talk to him.

      \n

      "Are you considering a vocation in the church?" he asked after the pleasantries were over.\xa0

      \n

      "I actually work with the church," said Temperance. "I've thought about becoming a nun, but I'm not sure I'm interested in secluding myself."

      \n

      Not all orders were cloistered nowadays, Father Vic gently reminded her, and they broke into a discussion of the neighborhood: the excellent Italian food, the fresh fish caught by the boats that still plied the harbor. Temperance, remembering going grenade fishing with Colonel Murphy, smiled and merely said she liked fresh fish.

      \n

      Temperance brought up Mr. Bacon. "He's a great connoisseur of Italian food, I can tell you that much. Not a member of my flock."

      \n

      "I hear he...dabbles in the occult."

      \n

      "The Church is modernizing, we don't have to attribute all these...tools of ignorance to Satan. You know, I was just talking to Alphonse down at the grocery and he mentioned he hadn't seen Mr. Bacon for a while. He called in a large delivery order but hasn't come in since, and normally he buys fresh vegetables for his dinner every night. Very European."

      \n

      There was one other odd thing, it turned out that Father Vic had heard, second hand from a widow who lived on Bacon's street. Last night some cars had pulled up to Bacon's house and taken out a young man of color from it. There was a curly-haired man with a mustache who had seemed to be in charge.

      \n

      "My informant likes to think she's on\xa0Dragnet. You're not in pictures, are you? Because I have this interesting idea for a TV show about a handsome young priest..."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Lisa found Jimmy in his room. He was feeling much better after a couple of days of bed rest but trying to stay grumpy to keep people from bothering him. She sat down on a chair across from the bed. "Mr. Wright? I suppose we should...talk about that kiss. Are you sorry I kissed you? You didn't seem to want..."

      \n

      "I was bleeding after all."

      \n

      "I was caught up in the moment. Like some silly TV character."

      \n

      "It's okay. There's nothing wrong with that."

      \n

      "I didn't say there was anything wrong with kissing you!"

      \n

      "I'm not good with people anymore," said Jimmy as gruffly as he could.

      \n

      "You could be, I think, if you wanted to. It seems to me that you're fighting who you are, that you're really a good person who protects the people in his life."

      \n

      "I have failed...so many people that I tried to protect."

      \n

      "Did you succeed with any of them?"

      \n

      Jimmy fingered the engagement ring in his pocket. "I did. But I can't see her anymore. I hurt the people I am close to."

      \n

      "I let Percy go off and do this madness. I should have protected him. I knew what kind of person he was. I don't know. I guess I keep looking for older men to protect me."

      \n

      "You know what I believe? That you can protect yourself."

      \n

      "Elizabeth Schicksal can protect herself, eh? I mean, I knew how to shoot a little when I was growing up. But I don't know anything about all this! I'm not some kind of brassy film noir dame! I'm just a farmgirl with a PhD."

      \n

      "I knew a farmgirl. She was...extremely brave. Loved comic books. She never let anything get her down."

      \n

      "She sounds remarkable."

      \n

      "And she didn't even have a PhD."

      \n

      "What was her name?"

      \n

      He paused. "Betty."

      \n

      "Like the dog?" She grinned. "I don't let anyone call me Betty. Percy called me Elise...you know, French. He thought it sounded more European or something."

      \n

      "You can be anything you put your mind to. Most people who went through what we went through last night wouldn't have handled it so well."

      \n

      "It\xa0was\xa0pretty thrilling. I mean, up until when you brutally murdered that man. But he was a bad man, right? He killed your friend?"

      \n

      "And many other people, and he would probably have killed many more."

      \n

      "Then I think he got what he deserved. I mean, if you can do that--if you can be a force of justice...then I want to help you. I guess what I want to know is...if I do that, will you help teach me to be more than I am now?"

      \n

      Jimmy's face contorted with warring emotions. "I will show you how to protect yourself. What you do with that is up to you. And when I'm done, you need to stay far, far away from me. For your own good."

      \n

      She sat back and pushed her glasses up her nose a little defiantly. "I won't make that promise. But I'll understand if that's the way you feel. Good night, Mr. Wright."

      \n

      \nEpisode III: You Want It Darker (Part 14)\n

      On her way out of Jimmy's room, Lisa bumped into Temperance, who was coming back from buying a sketchbook and some charcoal pencils at an art store. Lisa shook her head as Temperance surreptitiously hid her purchases in her purse. "He's a very strange man, don't you think?" said Lisa.

      \n

      "Yes," said Temperance forcefully.

      \n

      "I guess you know what happened..."

      \n

      "Which part?"

      \n

      "With that Michael."

      \n

      "Yes. We had a discussion about it."

      \n

      "I don't know...I mean he really cared for his friend. I don't understand how that worked..."

      \n

      [Me: Nobody knows how that worked! Jimmy's taking that one to his grave!]

      \n

      They walked into the sitting room of their suite. "He's staying on this whole thing about Percy," continued Lisa. "Even though he's risking the gas chamber. But he was a really bad guy, that Michael!"

      \n

      "We're definitely in a minefield here."

      \n

      "I think we need to find the people who actually have some understanding of what needs to be done. And it can't be Charleston!"

      \n

      "...he can hear you, you know."

      \n

      "I don't care!" said Lisa, but she looked over her shoulder. "I'm just saying, Percy might have put us all in danger. And if what Percy did threatens not just you and me but...everybody? And we don't even know what he was doing! I saw the movie! That King was really scary! Why is everyone wearing masks all of a sudden! What does that mean? Do I have to drop my mask? Do you?"

      \n

      "I don't think that was the metaphor they were going for..."

      \n

      "I mean, what are we underneath? Who are you, under your mask, Temperance?"

      \n

      "I don't wear a mask!"

      \n

      "I saw that girl kiss you."

      \n

      "And I didn't like it!"

      \n

      "That's deeply disturbing," said Charleston, walking into the room and flopping down in an armchair. "She gave you a sign of affection and you hated it?"

      \n

      "I didn't like it. It made me uncomfortable. It was unsolicited. And I'm a good Catholic girl," said Temperance coldly.

      \n

      "We all pretend a little bit to be people we're not," said Lisa. "You went out to find information today, Temperance. Can you say you didn't lie to anyone?"

      \n

      "I didn't tell everyone the truth, but that doesn't mean I bore false witness."

      \n

      "No, it means you were concealing something. Like you were wearing a mask."

      \n

      "You're reaching for a metaphor."

      \n

      "Maybe I am. I'm not an artist like Candace. You don't understand because you haven't been married yet. Everything changes. Now you're some man's husband, not who you used to be. You can't have your own money--it's all your husband's. You think it's an accident you put on a veil when you get married? I'm not some crazy women's libber type, but the symbolism is important! You lose your name! Another name drops down on top of it. I wasn't always Elizabeth Schicksal."

      \n

      "There is an issue of identity, yes," said Temperance soothingly. "I don't mean to downplay that."

      \n

      "I could have kept my maiden name professionally, but I didn't feel like it," mused Lisa. "I liked Percy. I thought he was a good man. He just got crazier as he got older. I mean, you know, that's how men are." She sat down in a glower and lit a cigarette. "All I know is that movie\xa0shook\xa0me. I feel...unmoored."

      \n

      "I may not be an artist," said Temperance, "but I understand the artistic world. Your husband had an obsession. He's chasing the horizon."

      \n

      "He's not my husband any more. I only use the name because, fuck it--" Temperance raised her eyebrow: she'd never heard Lisa swear before.

      \n

      "Almost every artist I know is the same way," said Temperance. "They can paint the most perfect painting, type the most perfect words, but it will never be good enough. That was a masterpiece we saw at Asylum!"

      \n

      They could hear the sound of furious typing coming from Candace's room.

      \n

      \nEpisode III: You Want It Darker (Part 15)\n

      "That was Amadou," said Lisa. "And now we're all mixed up in this. Do you know anyone who has been mixed up in something like this? Other than Mr. Wright."

      \n

      "I do know some people. They're wounded," said Temperance.

      \n

      "So was it worth it? Should we stop?"

      \n

      "They say it was worth what they went through, yes."

      \n

      "If we keep going, we're not going to stay the same. Everything is going to get stripped away from us. I'm an anthropologist, I know how these myths work."

      \n

      "We are dealing with the mythological, yes, as bizarre as that may seem."

      \n

      "But whose myths? I've seen echoes of these things before, but nothing like all of this at once."

      \n

      "Lisa, you do hit a nail on the head. We should be trying to chase that down. We're not so good at hitting the streets--"

      \n

      "--the brutal murders in alleyways--"

      \n

      "--that's not our expertise, no."

      \n

      "Maybe it could be though. I was raised on a farm, it's not like I haven't seen things die. Thanksgiving doesn't just\xa0happen."

      \n

      "Of course, but you could be in a room, walking off a stomach wound or hopped up on some kind of a drug, writing a novel..."

      \n

      "Is this the smell of an existential crisis I detect?" said Charleston, leaning back. He was wearing a smoking jacket and slippers, and was high on Yellow, of course.

      \n

      "Can you smell those?" said Lisa sarcastically. "I mean, you watched the movie and you're blind. And then there was the levitation."

      \n

      "Parlor tricks."

      \n

      "I've seen that, true, in a magic show. Not in real life."

      \n

      "I tell you how it works, and you're angry?" said Charleston. "What do you want out of life, to start fights for no reason?"

      \n

      "Temperance is pretty feisty."

      \n

      "I'm\xa0feisty?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "Ladies, if you have something you don't like, and somebody offers you a way out, you take it! Honesty isn't worth all that much!\xa0Trust me. Trust me."

      \n

      "Well what about you, Mr. Chiu? What's lurking behind your mask?"

      \n

      "My mask? I'm an open book! What would you like to know?"

      \n

      "Have you seen stuff--sorry, poor choice of words--have things like this happened to you before?"

      \n

      Charleston chuckled bitterly. "From time to time. I've done stuff like this to others."

      \n

      "What were you like before it all happened?"

      \n

      "I would say a lifetime of experiences have really opened my eyes. It seems a little odd at first, I'd imagine, when you initially encounter the fact that people can do things you never thought possible. But really, when it comes down to it, who you are and what you want never really changes. Just because you get the access and the ability to do things other people can't doesn't mean that you're going to turn into a better a person\xa0or\xa0a worse person. What it means is that the ability to embrace a power that nobody else can stop is in you, that's when you find out who you truly are. When no one can stop you, when no one can tell you what to do, when you can embrace all your true desires, what you see come out at that time is really who you are at your core."

      \n

      "That sounds like godlike power," said Lisa defiantly. "Humans can't have power like that."

      \n

      "It's not necessarily godlike power, but it sure is a godlike feeling. The best part of finding out who you are is that if you find out you don't like it, from that point onwards you can try to change it."

      \n

      "That's easy for you to say, you don't have to change your name back."

      \n

      "Why not change your name back if you want," said Temperance. "Come up with a new last name."

      \n

      "My old last name was kind of stupid anyway," said Lisa.

      \n

      "This is all about a\xa0label?" said Charleston. "Hyphenate!"

      \n

      "That seems too European. It was a city, my old last name. I should pick a different city, maybe. What's a good city name?"

      \n

      "It's not a city, but how about\xa0Queens?"

      \n

      "That would be appropriate. Lisa Queens?"

      \n

      "How about Elizabeth Queen?"

      \n

      "It's got a ring to it," said Temperance with a smile.

      \n

      "Yeah...but maybe not Elizabeth. Simpler. Beth."\xa0

      \n

      "Gives a name to your aspirations," said Charleston. "Let's people know who you are, who you want to be."

      \n

      "I do kinda like that," said Beth. "Sounds better than Auckland at least. That was a hard name to use."

      \n

      [And Jimmy wasn't there to hear this big reveal! Which was\xa0even better\xa0than it would ever have been if he was there--this way, all the players know, but of the three\xa0characters\xa0who know, the name Betty Auckland doesn't mean anything, and the one character who it would mean something to doesn't know.

      \n

      CP: Hey, Jimmy, you should put some points in Stevedore for all the baggage you're carrying!]

      \n

      Charleston retreated to his room for a moment and came back with a bottle of absinthe. He whipped up a couple of drinks and held his glass aloft in salutation: "A toast...to Miss Queen."

      \n

      "Wait!" said Beth. "That's\xa0Doctor\xa0Queen." She took a drink. "What the hell is that stuff?" she spluttered.

      \n

      "Your reaction was an exaggeration, right?" said Temperance. She took a drink. Her eyes got very far away. "I have to go to the bathroom now."

      \n

      "I can't decide which is worse," mused Beth. "Being like Charleston, or being like Jimmy. I can't end up like Temperance--I've had sex."

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 1)\n
      \n

      I came so far for beauty

      \nI left so much behind
      My patience and my family
      My masterpiece unsigned
      \u2014Leonard Cohen
      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      It happened again.

      \n

      Candace had been writing\u2014she wrote for hours a day now\u2014and she felt a presence in the room; like someone was standing in the room, gradually getting closer and closer. Like how Andy, her husband, had done before going away to war. And she felt...a movement in the air, a prickling of the skin on the back of her neck, as if someone was almost,\xa0almost\xa0touching her...

      \n

      It was gone. She sighed, pulled the cover over her typewriter, and rolled into her hard hotel bed. She was asleep almost instantly.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      "You know how to shoot, right?" Beth asked Temperance over breakfast the next morning.

      \n

      "Yes, a little."

      \n

      "I was wondering if you would like to go to the gun range with me. I grew up on a farm, I know how to shoot."

      \n

      "Is this because of all the\xa0excitement\xa0lately?"

      \n

      "Well, I saw Mr. Wright do something...and if that kind of thing keeps happening, I want to make sure I'm prepared."

      \n

      They found a place in Alameda County that didn't mind some ladies up from San Francisco doing some target shooting. They shot off an entire clip each from the .32 automatic pistols Colonel Murphy had helpfully put in their camper's gun rack. Nothing too good for his little girl, after all.

      \n

      The targets scooted back to them on their wires. Temperance's hits were mostly aimed to be non-lethal if possible: tight groupings in the shoulders and a couple of hits center mass. Beth's...well, Beth...

      \n

      "I guess I'm still a little rusty," she said, and bit her lip. She'd missed the target entirely with every round. "Maybe shooting isn't my thing anymore."

      \n

      Temperance tried to do what she could with some tips, but it soon became apparent that Beth couldn't hit the broad side of a barn even if she was standing inside it.

      \n

      "Are you perhaps a lefty?" asked Temperance.

      \n

      "Maybe I'm more near-sighted now than I remember. I guess this isn't my...m\xe9tier."

      \n

      "There's something that my mother learned that you might find very useful, and you can probably find a teacher around here: the ancient art of\xa0karate..."

      \n

      A day later Beth sat down in Temperance's room, her arm in a sling. "Nope," she said.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Jimmy reviewed their options while shaving. Lawrence Bacon was holed up in his house. Amadou Lalin had been shipped off by the Neurotologists to an unknown location. He'd been staking out Bacon's house for a while and he was sure nobody had come in or out for several days.\xa0

      \n

      And each of them had seen something different when they watched the film of\xa0The Unanswered Question.

      \n

      "Maybe we should go down and check out the Neurotologists," suggested Temperance over breakfast.

      \n

      "Maybe their records," murmured Jimmy. "I was able to pull the building plans for Bacon's house. He doesn't have any bunker or anything there. Tuck said he comes out to feed on derelicts ever two to six weeks, so sooner or later that will probably happen."

      \n

      [Bureaucracy spend by JP.]

      \n

      "Jimmy, don't even think about it," said Temperance. "I know it would be easy for you to look like a homeless person."

      \n

      Jimmy sighed. "Then maybe the office."

      \n

      "One target: their files. We don't stay long."

      \n

      "We do it quick and quietly, agreed."

      \n

      "This is really alarming coming from you, Temperance," said Candace.

      \n

      "It's the least violent thing we can do, and there isn't anything in the Bible about breaking into a house to\xa0not\xa0steal anything. And don't you two start casting stones at me!"

      \n

      "I'm not the one who presents herself as holier-than-thou."

      \n

      "I never! Oh, I'm sorry when someone hit on me at a crazy party. And I'm not comfortable when a woman did it to me. I didn't make it my problem that you went off with that lady!"

      \n

      Why,\xa0thought Jimmy,\xa0have I spent most of my life surrounded by crazy women?\xa0"What the hell happened to Beth, by the way?" he said out loud.

      \n

      "Don't give her a gun, first," said Temperance. "Have you ever heard of\xa0karate? She wasn't very good at it."

      \n

      "Your mom wasn't any good at it!"

      \n

      "Did my mother ever dislocate her own arm?"

      \n

      Jimmy frowned. "I can't remember. She lost two of them, however."

      \n

      "I am willing to go on this excursion. I'm not proud of myself for doing it, but I guess things just must get done.

      \n

      "If you keep on this general path you're going to do a lot of things that you're not comfortable with."

      \n

      "You don't have to tell me that, Mr. Wright!"

      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n
      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 2)\n

      Peter and Delia Morrison lived in an apartment over the storefront of the San Francisco Neurotology office. Jimmy cased it for a while during the day, then brought the others over to it late that night. He noted that Temperance was dressed sensibly in black with gloves and Candace was wearing an expensive black sweater. He shook his head and led them down the back alley to the rear door of the office.

      \n

      He must be rusty; it took him a long time to pick the lock. Maybe it was the arthritis. But after ten sweaty minutes he felt the lock click and he swung through the door into a utility room. Peter's office wasn't far beyond it.

      \n

      He rested in the corner while Temperance got to work on the file cabinets. She rifled through the files, noting they had files on herself and Jimmy under their aliases. The file on Amadou Lalin had been emptied out. The files on local Neurotologists were thick and detailed; they had the transcripts of their "Debriefing" sessions. She figured there was a small fortune in blackmail there. She grabbed a bunch of random files, Peter Morrison's own file, and her own file.

      \n

      They heard somebody come down the stairs. They all hid in the corners as Peter Morrison walked by and went into the kitchen. Peter opened the fridge, took out a beer, and pulled off the tab. He closed the door, revealing Jimmy Wright standing behind him.

      \n

      Jimmy cold-cocked him with a sock full of ball bearings. Peter staggered back. "You!" he said. He pulled out a whistle from under his shirt and began to blow on it. Jimmy didn't hear any sound, so he smashed him again with the sap.

      \n

      Peter fell into the corner, bleeding, the fight all out of him. Jimmy noticed however that he had a rather smarmy grin on his face.

      \n

      "If I were you," said Peter, "I'd\xa0run."

      \n

      Jimmy turned around and ran back to the rear door, followed by Temperance and Candace. They sped out into the alley. Fog rolled down it from the street. A shadow suddenly seemed to fall across the exit.

      \n

      And then there were two men in bad black suits standing there. One held out a badge. "We're with Security," he said. They had the same waxen features of the other black-suited agents they had seen before.

      \n

      Temperance faded into the side of the alley as the two agents walked down the alley. "Mr. Wright, we want to have a word with you," one said.

      \n

      "No thanks."

      \n

      "Hit him, Mr. Stapler." The other agent smacked him with his open hand. Jimmy winced with the pain\u2014he'd been\xa0cut, like with claws.

      \n

      Candace smashed her crowbar into the agent's knee, as hard as she could. There was a crunching noise, and for a moment she thought she'd crippled him. Then the agent\xa0hissed\xa0at her; he'd felt the blow, but it hadn't slowed him much.

      \n

      Temperance shot out from the shadows and smashed her heavy sack of equipment into the same leg. Something splattered out of the wound. It wasn't blood. The agent collapsed to the ground and began to\xa0dissolve.

      \n

      She ran. Jimmy was right behind her, and Candace just a little way ahead. The other agent slashed at her as she came by, rending her sweater, tearing into the flesh of her side. She could feel blood pouring out of the wounds and she staggered, but Jimmy threw his shoulder under hers and dragged her to their car.

      \n

      When they got back to the hotel, Beth threw up her hands. "What the hell is wrong with you people! Mr. Wright! Look how inflamed that wound is!"

      \n

      "I feel terrible," said Temperance. Beth sighed and began to clean the wounds. Jimmy handed her a broad-spectrum antibiotic from their medical kit, and then helped her put in a few stitches.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Jimmy sorted through the files they'd stolen while Temperance tossed in uneasy dreams. There was one thing he thought they might be able to use: two tickets to a fundraiser in Los Angeles for Neurotology. The accompanying flier said that N. Quincy Lund himself would be in attendance. He kept flipping through the papers.

      \n

      "Charleston," he said, "I've got Bacon's number in here."

      \n

      "What would I say?" asked Charleston.

      \n

      "Just be yourself."

      \n

      Charleston shrugged and dialed the phone. After a few rings, someone answered. "Yes," he said, panting. "Who is this?"

      \n

      "I\u2019m looking for a Mah Jong partner. I hear Mr. Bacon can accommodate."

      \n

      "Mr. Chiu." Bacon's voice had changed; it was hoarser and he panted out each word as if he was having trouble breathing.

      \n

      "The one and only. Well, as far as I know."

      \n

      "Interesting. That you. Should call. Perhaps I am. Ready. To have that Interview. Come to. The House. Whenever. You wish."

      \n

      "Can I bring the whole gang? It sounds like quite a party.

      \n

      "It won't. Matter." Bacon hung up.

      \n

      "I've got good news, and really good news," said Charleston to the others. "The good news is, I think I made a friend. The better news is that he invited everyone to come to his place."

      \n

      ...oh, wait, she may have dealt with him in the Other Place. She may already have done so...

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 3)\n

      The next day was Thanksgiving. They drove from their hotel down to Pacific Heights. All around them families, dressed in their best, were traveling to their families or dropping in on friends' houses.

      \n

      [There was a brief visit to the hospital by Jimmy\u2014after all, he's a veteran\u2014to get healed up.

      \n

      That it's now Thanksgiving makes a complete hash of the timeline! But that's okay; I did it intentionally, wondering if anyone would notice. There was some discussion of bringing a turkey, possibly concealing a weapon inside.

      \n

      Me: When did this turn into the\xa0Boondock Saints?]

      \n

      Bacon's house looked even grimmer than before, if that was possible. Everyone window had the blinds pulled down, and there was a subtle feeling around it, as if it had already been abandoned. Charleston went to knock on the door but it creaked open as soon as he touched it.

      \n

      Charleston took a swig from the flask he had of rum mixed with Yellow. His third eye opened up and he stepped over the threshold into the house. The rest followed him. The house was dark and gloomy. They could see someone sitting in an armchair in the deepest shadows of the room.

      \n

      To Charleston's mystic sight, he was glowing like the sun. "Mr. Bacon, I presume," he said.

      \n

      "I'm not sure. I still can claim. That name. I'm not sure. That I have a name. I made an Oath long ago. For knowledge. And that promise. Has come due." He stood up and stepped into the dim light from the open door. His skin was scaly and hardening, and his body was becoming somehow amorphous or amphibian-like.

      \n

      "For," said Bacon. "He is coming."

      \n

      "You sound so fatalistic. It seems to me you are moving on to wonderful things."

      \n

      "I understand now why so many sorcerers wanted to kill you."

      \n

      Charleston uncomfortably denied knowing what he was talking about. Bacon retreated to his chair and gestured around the room. Jimmy, Candace and Temperance began to look around as their shock dissipated. There was a copy of the\xa0Turner Codex\xa0that Jimmy uncovered. Candace found a copy of\xa0L'homme errant au bord du lac. It was the same text as Temperance's copy of that book, but this one had extensive notes in Bacon's handwriting. Temperance found his daily planner which meticulously detailed his activities; she noticed he had called a number in Los Angeles several times over the last few days. Jimmy found a piece of paper:

      \n

      \xa0

      \n
      \n

      PROJECT TAROT PRINCIPALS (1951-1953)

      \nPercy [Percival Schicksal]
      Carl [Simon]
      Juliet [M- ?]
      Barbara [?]
      Solomon Molinari
      N. Quincy Lund
      Cassie\xa0(this last was scrawled in pencil)
      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      "Mr. Bacon," said Charleston.

      \n

      "Mr. Chiu."

      \n

      "Who did you make what promise to?"

      \n

      "I think you know. The King in Tatters."

      \n

      "Why is he so popular?"

      \n

      "It is the cycle of Aldebaran."

      \n

      "And where are we in that cycle?"

      \n

      "At the advent. And also. Mr. Lund intends to repeat Mr. Schicksal's experiment."

      \n

      "That worked really well for him. He seemed pleased with the results..."

      \n

      "Lalin is the key. He will summon the city. It will be easier to bring the Presence into the world that way."

      \n

      "That sounds fabulous. Could we see him?"

      \n

      Bacon explained that Amadou had been taken by Lund, along with Dr. Montague. "One day she will be more like me," he rasped.

      \n

      "Perhaps we all will be."

      \n

      "I very much hope not. For all your sakes. I think perhaps now would be a good time for you all to leave. While I can. Contain. Myself."

      \n

      Temperance noticed that the arms of the chair Bacon was sitting in had been crushed almost to powder under his grasp. She nodded at the rest and they backed quickly down the hall.

      \n

      "You can't escape him Mr. Chiu! He will come for you!" shouted Bacon as they darted down the porch.

      \n

      "Happy Thanksgiving, Mr. Bacon!" shouted Charleston as nonchalantly as possible.

      \n

      Before they got in the car, he finished his flask of Yellow and then smashed it. He slit his hand with the shards and then wrote some symbols in blood next to the door to Bacon's house. If it worked, it would keep any innocents from entering the house, by shifting them to a slightly out of phase time.

      \n

      [That was CP's Yellow-mandated Art spend. And was quite interesting, considering my own ideas about the Yellow Mythos...]

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Back at the hotel they reviewed the books. Candace found Bacon's criticism quite insightful\u2014she had that moment so uncomfortable for an author when they realize the critic seems to have understood the work better than the creator. Everything led to an unusual conclusion: that Lalin's work was the key to a powerful summoning, and that there were elements of that summoning that Lalin was not aware of himself.

      \n

      Jimmy and Candace ran down the numbers in Bacon's diary. Most were to the Neurotology Headquarters in Los Angeles (just outside Santa Monica), but a couple of exchanges were for somewhere out in the San Fernando Valley.

      \n

      Candace went down to one of the few bars open on Thanksgiving where Kerouac and Neal Cassady were drinking. "The fair Candace," said Neal. Behind him Kerouac shouted something and slipped off his stool. "I'm always willing to hear what you are laying down."

      \n

      "My friends and I are thinking that the scene here in San Francisco is over, and want to go check out LA. So how's a road trip sound to you?"

      \n

      Neal wanted to know what conveyance, chariot, vehicle they had brought, and Candace told him about the RV. Neal then wanted to know just how much he could push the RV on the trip.

      \n

      "Whatever it takes," said Candace.

      \n

      "'Whatever it takes' are my two favorite words in the English language."

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 4)\n

      And so they flew down the PCH, the RV packed with everyone and sundry: Neal at the wheel with Candace sitting next to him, watching him weave deftly through the Thanksgiving traffic; Jack in the main cabin listening to Van and his trio lay down Bop riffs. Temperance hid in her bedroom. Jimmy took a nap.

      \n

      [It cost a point of Stability to sit up front with Neal; he was a demon on the road.]

      \n

      Temperance, as their dedicated square was the natural choice to go to the Neurotology party. And to accompany her, Jimmy had rented a tuxedo and was slowly trying to put himself back into presentable shape. It used to be easier.

      \n

      [JP used a point of XP to buy a point of High Society in order to fit in at the party; you can imagine the montage of Jimmy gradually turning from derelict into something presentable. Quoth JP, "That's what XP are for\u2014to fill in those gaps." I should mention it also nicely makes sense\u2014Jimmy had once been a big shot in LA, so it's natural that he would be able to grudgingly return to his old form.]

      \n

      Candace called Vladimir from their hotel\u2014once they had found one that would look the other way at hosting a jazz band\u2014to see if he had received the first draft of her novel she'd sent him. Nabokov wasn't sure he could follow it; he wondered if Candace had been under the influence of anything while writing it.

      \n

      "Only the influence of Art," she said.

      \n

      "I have to think about it all. The writing is fine, I'm not sure I follow the actual story. I do note something quite interesting: you are aware that you are writing the novel in blank verse. If I put the line breaks in, it flows quite naturally. Almost as if you were writing a Shakespearean play. I can only assume this was your intention."

      \n

      "Yes\u2014I mean...I met some poets out here..."

      \n

      "Well, I suppose if it was good enough for\xa0Melville, then that's all right...I guess..."

      \n

      She hung up the phone. "Jack, Neal, want to hit some bars?"

      \n

      It turns out that the two of them knew all the best dive bars in Los Angeles, and took her to all of them. And Neal, it developed, was quite a tender lover.\xa0

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      The party was at a tony Beverly Hills hotel. There was a sedate mambo band in one corner, and the usual glittering array of society dames surrounded by their escorts in black tie. Temperance saw a man holding court in one corner of the room. He was in his late forties but had a robust charm that made him look younger; his hair was curly and he sported a thin mustache. She knew him from his pictures, especially the one on the dust jacket of\xa0Diametrics: Nathan Quincy Lund, the founder of Neurotology.

      \n

      Jimmy saw Temperance skating over to talk to Lund. He wanted to keep a close eye on her in case anyone made them. Which is why he didn't see the woman who bumped into him from behind. "Oh my goodness, I'm sorry\u2014Jimmy?"

      \n

      It was Janet Winston Rogers. Of course. "What on earth are you doing? What are you wearing? I suppose a tux is magic\u2014when you wear one, I see you," she said. But she smiled.

      \n

      "I heard about this event," he started.

      \n

      "What's that you have around your neck?" she said. Jimmy tucked the engagement ring he had given her once and now wore as a necklace back under his shirt. "What's wrong with you? You look pale, like you've seen a ghost. Am I that frightening to you?"

      \n

      "Absolutely not. You just...caught me off guard."

      \n

      "Jimmy, what happened to you?" She put a hand on his arm.

      \n

      "War, death, homelessness."

      \n

      "You didn't have to be homeless, you know."

      \n

      "I think I did."

      \n

      "Have a drink with me, at least."

      \n

      "Why not two?"

      \n

      She smiled again. "I think you're going to need more than just a double."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      "There I was," said Lund. "Standing in the middle of a desert. And that's how I found the way to write this book. The old Tibetan guru had given me the idea, and I made it come to life." Temperance slid up next to him.

      \n

      "Hello my dear," he said to her. "I don't think I've ever seen you at one of these before."

      \n

      "I only show up on random occasions."

      \n

      "You look a little familiar, can't place you..."

      \n

      "My last name is Murphy."

      \n

      "Not the same as that ridiculous man with the campers...you are? I bought one of those from him. It was actually useful for me, I bought some land up in the Valley a few years ago and while we were building the development it was useful for me to go out and keep an eye on the workers. Was able to get a good price on the land. Strange area."

      \n

      "I've only been up there once or twice."

      \n

      "You remember that blackout back in '26? I suppose you weren't born yet. Old-timers like me...anyway, the place I bought was where the transformer that blew and started the blackout was located. And some crazy religious cult burned down a building there."

      \n

      "A religious cult? Imagine!"

      \n

      "All sorts of weird things in California. N. Quincy Lund," he said shaking her hand. "This is my shindig."

      \n

      Temperance studied him. He had the air of...the cat who had eaten the canary. She could tell that he was a smug bastard most of the time, but something made it even more pronounced right now.

      \n

      [Mostly High Society and BS Detector to ping this; I think I wrote the clue to actually work for Psychology, but it was harmless enough to give out for the other skill.]

      \n

      "You should come out and take a look at it," he said. "While there's still space available. I'm putting up a housing development. Everything new and wonderful. Incorporating the place as a town, calling it Chambersburg." He lit a pipe, and then looked up. "Clark! Wonderful to see you!"

      \n

      While Lund talked to Clark Gable, Temperance quietly slipped off into the crowd.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      "Jimmy, you keep running into me after coming out of the cold for the first time in fifteen years," said Janet, as they started their second round of drinks.

      \n

      "I'm doing a favor for Bradley. Sort of strongarmed me out of the cold, I guess you could say."

      \n

      "You really shouldn't be a stranger, Jimmy. I know things have been hard between us. If I had known where to find you...I would have apologized."

      \n

      "You...you don't need to\u2014"

      \n

      "I was very rude to you."

      \n

      "I am pretty sure I could have handled the situation better," Jimmy started.

      \n

      "You mean how you broke my heart? Yes, I suppose that could have been\xa0better handled." She finished her drink and waved to the bartender. "There hasn't been anyone serious since you."

      \n

      "There's...not been anyone at all. Wandering around the desert..."

      \n

      "Jimmy, you always were a sentimental old fool. Now I suppose we're just old fools together."

      \n

      "Cheers."\xa0

      \n

      The next morning they slept in together, the Los Angeles sunlight streaming through the curtains of her Hollywood bungalow, illuminating her hand running over his chest, fingering the ring he wore around his neck.
