      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 5)\n

      Janet dropped him off back at the hotel. Betty the dog came padding out to him, saw Janet, and howled. Beth followed her out of the room. "Was that an old friend of yours?" she said, trying to keep the hurt out of her voice.

      \n

      "Where did you go last night?" demanded Temperance from inside.

      \n

      At that moment Candace came gliding down the hallway in a dishevelled cocktail dress. "Morning everyone," she said.

      \n

      Charleston didn't yell at him; he and Helen had slept in the RV that night. Charleston had been sweeping the emergency channel on the CB listening for reports of people being murdered by having their skin cut off.

      \n

      "Well, I found out some information, at least," huffed Temperance. "Mr. Lund has some property in the San Fernando Valley. A town called Chambersburg."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      As soon as everyone was more or less presentable they tumbled into the RV and drove up to the Valley, following the 101 through Hollywood and into the rapidly-surburbanizing neighborhoods where once oranges had blossomed. It took a few hours, but they finally happened upon Chambersburg, a pleasant, smallish housing development arranged in a broad semicircle around an artificial lake. Straight roads ran radially from the center of town, connecting curving cul-de-sacs lined with identical California split-level houses. A broad village green jutted like a tongue through the town; a Christmas tree had been erected in the center of it. At the end of the green, on the shore of the lake, was a half-ruined building with an amphitheater looking over the water. One wing of the building had been abandoned, the other currently housed the town hall and the high school.

      \n

      Jimmy reached into his pocket and tightly gripped the engagement ring. He recognized the building, the "New Temple of Joy" that had been the site of certain unpleasant events in his life back in 1937. Temperance stared at him. "You only do this when you see something that could harm us," she began.

      \n

      "Nothing. Old history."

      \n

      "Old history that could come back to bite us on the...ass?"

      \n

      "I don't know the future. I don't know. I only know the past."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      The people of the town looked like they could have filled out a casting call for a sitcom set in Anytown, USA. Children played on the sidewalks, watched over by their mothers, who had their hair tied up neatly under scarves. They passed a soda shop named Doc's, and a bar. They grabbed some lunch at Flo's diner and tried to get the lay of the land.

      \n

      Flo wanted to know if they were in town for the Shriner's convention being held "up the road a piece." Candace allowed that they might be interested in buying some property in the area. "We got lots of lots to sell," said Flo. "But I should warn you, we have some\xa0pretty stringent requirements."

      \n

      She told them that there was a hotel just outside town, the El Rey, although with the convention they might not have any rooms. Temperance half-listened to the conversation. She'd noticed something odd: she hadn't seen a church, even a storefront Pentecostal place, anywhere in town. Which seemed out of character for the kind of town they were claiming to be.

      \n

      [Anthropology use by TP.]

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Neal Cassady drove Candace up to the motel, a rather typical example of its type: long rows of identical windows and doors, a semicircular drive and a porte cochere in front of the rental office. "I only have two rooms," the desk clerk said. Candace paid anyway, and took the keys from the clerk. He handed her a couple of matchbooks. She saw the full name of the motel written on them: El Rey de los Jirones. It took her a while to find someone who could translate that for her: the King of Tatters.

      \n

      Jimmy went down to Sam's Bar off the green. It was a pleasant Californy-type place: clean leatherette booths, high stools with green leather seats, a smooth wooden bar with brass finishings. Behind it was a man wearing a white jacket and a bow tie. "My name's Sam," he said. "What can I get you?"

      \n

      "James."

      \n

      "You a Shriner, James?"

      \n

      "Yes."

      \n

      "Good, we have a discount for Shriners; half-price beers." Jimmy bought one and got a dish of water for Betty. He sat down at the bar next to a rather nervous-looking little man. He was bald, with thick round spectacles. "So you're a\xa0Shriner\xa0too," he said. "Henry Lister. I'm with the San Francisco chapter. Pleased to meet you. I bet you're very excited about the convention."

      \n

      "I may not look it, but I am excited." Jimmy could see a copy of\xa0Diametrics\xa0tucked into his jacket pocket. "You read\xa0Diametrics?"

      \n

      "Of course. We're both\xa0Shriners."

      \n

      "I was at the charity event."

      \n

      "You saw Mr. Lund? How lucky! I think he's going to try and do a repeat of the '53 Summoning."

      \n

      "Too bad what happened the first time."

      \n

      "There was interference. If it hadn't been for that busybody...I don't know what you know, so I don't want to get too far into it. What a charming dog. Do they allow dogs on the other side?"

      \n

      "We're certainly going to find out. An exciting experiment."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Temperance went down to Debbie's Dos, a hair salon on the other side of the green from Sam's Bar. (Flo had intimated that Debbie and Sam had a\xa0thing.) Debbie was a middle-aged brassy blonde with a pencil stuck behind one ear. "What are you here for, darlin'? Permanent, manicure? Maybe do something about those brows I think..."

      \n

      "My brows...oh, no. I have an important event tonight\u2014"

      \n

      "You're going caroling?"

      \n

      "Yes. I was invited to go and want to look my best."

      \n

      "It's supposed to be quite an event. Don't know what to expect, but it should be very\xa0entertaining. Sure been practicing those new songs a lot."

      \n

      "I don't know too much. I was invited by an old school friend."

      \n

      Temperance sat down for a set and a permanent. While she was under the hairdryer, she noticed another woman glancing over from time to time. She was a youngish woman, with blonde hair done up in curlers. She introduced herself as Joy, Mrs. Joy Harris that is. "You're not from around here, are you? Are you here for the caroling? An old friend? Are you Midwest Chapter?"

      \n

      "Signed up in Los Angeles."

      \n

      "They sure sent you up here quickly."

      \n

      Temperance spun up a tale about going through a rapid induction process. "Don't worry," said Joy. "We're all Neurotologists here. I'm...a little worried about the ceremony. I'm frightened for my kids. I don't know what's going on, and you're not from around here, so maybe you can look out for them? Little Jack Junior, and Jenny, and Ray is only 8 months old..."\xa0

      \n

      Temperance cooed (she hoped) over the pictures Joy showed her. "You can put them in our vehicle."

      \n

      "There seemed to be some disreputable people there...I think I saw...a..."

      \n

      Temperance grimaced. "Mencius is very nice and helps out with the...cleaning."

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 6)\n

      "How can you drink this stuff?" said Charleston as Helen sucked down another chocolate malted. He hated ice cream.

      \n

      Helen smiled and kept inhaling the thick cold liquid.

      \n

      Charleston tried to order a whisky, but then remembered he was in a soda shop. "This used to be America," he groused. "You could get booze wherever you wanted."

      \n

      "Listen, pally," said Doc by the cash register. "Back in the war we kept your kind in the camps."

      \n

      "My kind of\xa0what?" muttered Charleston. A bunch of teenagers came in gathered around the juke box. Charleston held up a roll of quarters. "Help a guy out who can't see. Why don't you play some of the new stuff you kids like."

      \n

      "You would like...Little Richard?" smirked one of the clean-cut youth of America.

      \n

      "You met him? He's a\xa0crazy\xa0cat."

      \n

      "I do like him, don't understand why he sings like a girl."

      \n

      "Doesn't come through right on the record. But you get a chance, go see him, no matter what it takes."

      \n

      "You're clearly pulling my leg, but I'll put him on anyway." He snatched the roll of quarters, dropped one into the jukebox, and chose a three-song set: "Tutti Frutti", "Maybellene", and of course "Rock Around the Clock."

      \n

      "Should we dance or something?" said Helen. Charleston shrugged and they swayed together for a while. "What else do you like here?" said Charleston.

      \n

      "We like Pat Boone," said one fresh-scrubbed young platinum blonde girl. "Or Perry Como. And Frank Sinatra is pretty good, even if he is a little old."

      \n

      "I met him once," muttered Charleston as the girls punched up some Pat Boone. "This is better than what we have to sing tonight," said Platinum to Charleston. "I don't know why we can't just sing regular carols like everyone else."

      \n

      "Making music is a wonderful thing," said Charleston. "What even is this?"

      \n

      "Something out on the green. We're singing some kind of new songs."

      \n

      "They're like all in\xa0French," said another girl.

      \n

      "French! What's happening to our country!"\xa0

      \n

      "It's all for our parents. They're so impressed Mr. Lund is coming tonight. I think they're all crazy. They're all in that church, that Neurotology thing."

      \n

      Helen elbowed Charleston. "Doc is looking at us," she hissed.

      \n

      The girls had noticed Doc's interest. "I think we have some homework," they said and began picking their books up.

      \n

      "Maybe I'll see you tonight," said Charleston.

      \n

      "I doubt it," said some smart-aleck, and the kids laughed as they left.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      As evening began to fall, the population of the town gathered on the green. The Christmas tree blazed with yellow lights. It was a cold and clear evening; as the sun sank, the first stars came out. High above the apex of the tree Jimmy could see Aldebaran blazing an intense, angry red. It was brighter than he'd ever seen it before.

      \n

      Temperance stood next to Joy; she'd already secured her children inside the RV, where Beth, Van, and the band were keeping watch and trying to entertain them. The crowd started to softly sing Christmas carols\u2014some so old that Temperance didn't recognize them; a few were in other languages, mostly French and German. In between they chanted slow ritual phrases. With a start she realized that the chants were the "songs" from\xa0L'homme errant au bord du lac, Amadou Lalin's strange book of dreams and poems.

      \n

      As the sun set, a fleet of limousines drove through town. To Jimmy's expert eye, they were clearly armored, with heavy bulletproof glass in the windows. Candace got a fleeting glimpse of Amadou Lalin huddled in the back of one of them, wrapped in a blanket and a muffler. The temperature was dropping fast now that the sun was below the horizon; it was colder than any of them, even Temperance, had ever known California to get in December.

      \n

      The cars drove to the other end of Lake Till, as the huge ornamental pool was called, and stopped. A sound system turned on with a whine of feedback. Amadou's thin, weak voice began to be broadcast, singing a strange song that was not from his book but very much in its style. As he sang, his voice got stronger, deeper, richer, and the words struck their listeners to the core. If Rilke had written music, it would sound like this; if Wallace Stevens had written lyrics, they would be like these.

      \n

      Mist rose over the surface of the lake, quickly becoming opaque in the twilight. It seemed to hump itself up as something thrashed in the water, then swept in toward the town, breaking like a wave over the green. Something was moving in the fog, a large\xa0flock\xa0of some kind. There was an insectile chattering as\xa0things\xa0flew over them. Then just as suddenly as they had arrived, they swept back over the water. Through the mist a multitude of small lights gradually became visible.

      \n

      At the far end of Lake Till was the skyline of an enormous city, with towering skyscrapers blazing against the black sky.

      \n

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 7)\n

      The mist sprang up again. The crowd seemed to vanish around Temperance; she couldn't see any of her friends either. (Had she known it, each of them was similarly alone.) Ahead of her, the only thing she could make out in the thick fog was...a turnstile. It sat, completely incongruous in this featureless netherland, an ordinary mass-transit turnstile that would have been at home in any of the great metropolises of the world.\xa0

      \n

      She trembled, more in fear and shock than because of the clammy air. She pushed forward, into the gate, and heard the oddly comforting and oddly ominous grumbling as the bars clicked forward. Then she was through...

      \n

      For an instant she had a glimpse of a vast train station, a crystal ceiling at least a hundred feet above her, marble fixtures and an enormous departures board. Then a crowd of people rushed into her, pushing and pulling her along with them.\xa0Just like rush hour in New York, she thought in a flash as she was swept into a waiting train car.

      \n

      The doors slid shut behind her and she grabbed onto a nearby pole. There was a lurch and the train began to move forward, shooting out of the darkness through a tunnel and then out \xa0onto a broad, elevated track. Around her people were chattering in what at first was an unfamiliar language; but soon, with the logic of dreams, it became comprehensible.

      \n

      They looked like people. They looked like the people she might see on an elevated train anywhere in America, except that she saw every shade of skin possible (and a few she didn\u2019t think were possible) in the crowd around her. The men were wearing suits and hats that looked very much like fedoras, the women dresses or skirt suits. All of their outfits had something a little antique, a little outre, a little out-of-place: the chalkstripe suit of one man was purple, not black or grey; one woman had an enormous toucan pin perched on her shoulder, looking for all the world like an actual bird was sitting there. And they all wore masks.

      \n

      The masks had enormous variety, although most were of the type called\xa0columbina: porcelain or metal, covering the eyes, cheek and nose. Here and there she saw a few masks that covered the entire face, and a few people wearing only a petite domino. Several people gave her a dirty look; she was the only unmasked person in the car.

      \n

      Over the PA system came a voice she assumed was the conductor's: "This is the Orange Line to Palace Terminal,\xa0stopping at Uoht, Noatalba, Aldones, Aldones Plaza, Demhe Banks, and Palace Terminal. Uoht will be the next station stop. Uoht."

      \n

      She looked around in a daze. The train seemed very modern to her, much like the subway cars in New York City. Strange advertisements were held in the molding between the windows and the ceiling; the script resembled no characters she recognized, but much as the chatter around her had, they soon resolved in her mind to a readable state. The pictures were of products she recognized\u2014a coffee pot, a beauty cream, some kind of movie\u2014but the names were strange or completely nonsensical.

      \n

      Below her a twilight metropolis unfolded. To her right was a vast lake, so large that it went to the horizon. She could see a large suspension bridge to a rocky island that had some kind of large building complex on it; the lights were just turning on along the cables and towers of the bridge. The sun was somehow oranger than she thought the sun should be, and perched half-submerged at the rim of the world; above it was another sun, a glowing red coal that was also sinking to the horizon. Against the bright orange and yellow sky she saw dark pinpoints of\xa0unlight, like black stars caught in the firmament. To her left, the sky was already dark; brilliant stars were becoming visible, especially a bright red one, brighter by far than any star she'd ever seen, that seemed to hang from the zenith.

      \n

      A great city curled in a vast semicircle around one end of the lake. She could see broad avenues\u2014and narrow cobblestone streets\u2014vast parks purpling in the gloom\u2014broad plazas\u2014great towering skyscrapers in the center\u2014small dark tenements\u2014throngs moving down the boulevards\u2014children playing in the alleys...a great amalgam of every city she had known, full of the energy and vitality only an American metropolis seemed to have.

      \n

      And yet...the people in the car had a strange air about them, something more than just their alien clothes and habits. A suppressed anxiety and tension, as if tonight was important somehow. She craned her head around to look at the back of a tabloid a man was reading. Half of it, as she expected, was devoted to a sporting event although what it was she couldn't guess\u2014the headline, "Laht takes 7 chukka while saving a nelson in an all-outer"\u2014was gibberish. The front page, however, showed a blurry photograph of a figure in white robes hurrying down a street; the headline blared "PHANTOM OF TRUTH?" while the subhead assured everyone that the royal family was doing everything it could to protect the city.

      \n

      The name of the paper was the\xa0Carcosa Evening Standard.

      \n

      [BS Detector pegged the mood of the train, Notice got the headlines on the paper.]

      \n

      The train swept down its elevated course, heading straight at a large building that crouched over the right-of-way; they shot\xa0through\xa0it like a tunnel, the lights flickering. For a second she had a vision of ordinary life in Carcosa: a secretary packing up her purse and getting ready to leave, a man wearing a sad-eyed mask staring out of his office window and smoking a cigarette...the lights flickered on and off. And each time they came back on there were fewer people in the car.

      \n

      Suddenly there were two men wearing black suits at the end of the car. "Mr. Cable," said one to the other.

      \n

      "Mr. Lamp," said the other. "There's the intruder."

      \n

      Temperance stuck out her hand. "Take me to your leader," she said as confidently as she could manage.

      \n

      "We don't have orders to take you in," said \u2018Mr. Cable\u2019. "We have orders to stop you."

      \n

      "Oh..." said Temperance. The lights kept flickering...and each time the men were a little closer.

      \n

      "Demhe Banks coming up," said the conductor. Temperance turned and ran, banging open the door to the adjoining car and running through it. A little boy tugged at his mother's sleeve. "She's not wearing a mask!" he said. Temperance paused, then swept the mask off of his mother. She gasped and covered her face as Temperance sprinted to the next door.

      \n

      The lights flickered again. When they came back on, the car was empty. The two strange men were standing at the opposite end. Above the windows, all the advertisements had been replaced by the glowing, twisting Yellow Sign. "Stop," said one of the men.

      \n

      The train suddenly began to skid to halt. Temperance burst into the next car as the train shuddered to a halt and the doors slid open. "Demhe Banks," said the PA. She sprinted through the doors as they snapped shut behind her. As the train pulled away, she saw the two men pressed up against the windows of the doors.

      \n

      She sighed, and tied on her mask. She was standing on an open air platform, covered by a tiled roof. A set of stairs spiraled down from the platform. With a start she realized she was much closer to the lake now. In the fading light, what she took to be large seabirds were circling above the water.

      \n

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 8)\n

      Charleston pushed through the turnstile without hesitating. He could see it. He could see everything...

      \n

      ...he was swept through the great train station and then with dream logic found himself standing on the sandy shore of the lake, looking almost directly into the sunset. He spun around slowly. A moon was rising behind him, in front of the city. Mist rose over the lake, sometimes rearing up like a wave. A long boardwalk curved to either side of him; boarded up kiosks and little shops lined it. Everything was a bit forlorn, dripping with moisture.

      \n

      When he turned back to face the suns, a figure was standing there. She was wearing rich robes out of some medieval pageant; her hair was bound up in a headdress like a crown. The whole effect was rather Chines; perhaps it was the red silk robes she was wearing. Her mask was ornate, faced in gold and lapis lazuli. But even so, he recognized her. Noor. Noor al-Buraki, his erstwhile friend and assistant, thirty years dead.

      \n

      Suddenly he realized this was the place he had dreamed of before.

      \n

      "Hello Charleston," she said in her familiar Egyptian accent.

      \n

      "Hello," he said, distracted. "Sorry, getting over the multiple suns."

      \n

      "It has been a long time."

      \n

      "It hasn't."

      \n

      "Why do you say that?"

      \n

      "I just had this dream a few months ago."

      \n

      "That's true, but it has been a long time since we saw each other."

      \n

      "Maybe for you. You...pop into my head a lot. From time to time."

      \n

      "Well, you\xa0were\xa0crazy for a long time."

      \n

      "Not something you get rid of so easy."

      \n

      "Back in the day you thought crazy was the thing to do, as I recall."

      \n

      "Didn't think it was really crazy."

      \n

      "We did so much good work together, don't you think?" Noor walked toward him and sat down on the edge of the boardwalk. He moved a little closer but remained standing.

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nMarch 2017 \n edited March 2017
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 8 cont'd)\n

      "I don't think it worked out all that well," he said.

      \n

      "No, not for me," she replied with an ambiguous smile. "I mean, I'm dead."

      \n

      "I went crazy, you went dead. Didn't seem to help either of us in the end. Helped some other people go crazy. Possibly crazier than me."

      \n

      "You did stop the Dark Lord, after all."

      \n

      "As much as I enjoyed that\u2014and to be honest, I really enjoyed that\u2014I don't think it really made much of a difference in the grand scheme. I'm sure he's still scurrying about somewhere."

      \n

      "I'm sure. But you stopped that plan, and that plan was very dangerous."

      \n

      "Wasn't much of a plan, either."

      \n

      "I suppose that's what the Dark Lord wanted people to think."

      \n

      "So this was all part of his plan?"

      \n

      "Who can say?"

      \n

      "Can I ask you a question? Where the hell am I?"

      \n

      "This is the city of Carcosa."

      \n

      "I don't know what that is, but it sounds familiar."

      \n

      "I'm sure we read about it. And, as is always the case when one arrives in Carcosa, we are here at the night the King in Yellow enters the city."

      \n

      "Isn't that every night?"

      \n

      "Yes, it is. But we are together for the first time so long." She reached out and took his hand into hers. He started back. "That's new!" he sputtered.

      \n

      "Of course I have physical form here. Don't be afraid. I am warm and alive...well, close enough for sorcerer's business."

      \n

      He tentatively reached out his hand and stroked her cheek. He slowly lifted the mask from her face, exposing the simple, open features of the Bedouin girl he had known so long ago. She blinked and took out a pair of thick horn-rimmed spectacles. She put them on, then took off her headdress.

      \n

      "This is so much more...this is better," he said.

      \n

      "You sound almost as if you missed me."

      \n

      "I thought if I did see you again, you would hate my guts. Because it's my fault you got turned inside out."

      \n

      "I think I had some say in that, didn't I?"

      \n

      "It's tough for me to remember that period of my life and think anyone was in charge except for me."

      \n

      "No, you were not always as much in charge as you thought you were."

      \n

      "I don't think I was\xa0ever\xa0in charge, in reality. But reality is a very soft thing."

      \n

      "Strange that you learned wisdom."

      \n

      "Got to break a few eggs to make an omelet."

      \n

      "I do want to know one thing, Charleston," she said, beaming and drawing him closer to her. "Why in all this time haven't you detected my bullshit?"

      \n

      The knife was in her hand as quick as thought. He felt it stabbing into his gut and chest as her other hand clenched like a vice with an inhuman strength around his wrist, holding him immobile. Finally she let go and he fell to the sand, bleeding profusely from many, many wounds. He was still clutching her mask in one hand.

      \n

      Noor had vanished. Instead, towering above him was a man in a tuxedo. The tie was undone and hung slackly around his neck. His face was indescribable. It contained cruelty and cold amusement and an infinite, infinite contempt. It seemed to gaze down from some incredible height, beyond understanding or sympathy. The man lit a cigarette and smiled.

      \n

      "Ah, Chuckles, it's been such a long time," said Nyarlathotep. "Do you know how hard it is to get into this place?"

      \n

      "For me it was easy," said Charleston, coughing. "Must have something you don't...besides a bunch of stab wounds."

      \n

      Nyarlathotep gazed out over the lake. "You know," he said almost wistfully, "for a long time I thought you and I would really have something together. Now you have about fifteen minutes before you bleed out. You see, I finally figured out something about you. I thought you were saying\xa0no\xa0to me because you were that strangest of all monkeys, the kind of monkey that could stand up on his hind legs and say 'No!' like Don Giovanni...ah, opera is lost on you. But now I understand that what you are, what you really are, is a goddamned coward."

      \n

      "You came all this way to tell me that?"

      \n

      "No, I came all this way to torture you." The Dark Lord threw his cigarette into the lake where it hissed. Something began to thrash the water in the place it fell, and he reached over, without moving, into the water and pulled some kind of gelatinous mass out of it. Charleston couldn't see what it was from his angle; he was flat on his back and in intense pain.

      \n

      "You ever wonder when you had your little gun, what those things were, where they came from?" said Nyarlathotep, quite casually. "Or ever let one grow up a little?"

      \n

      He stood above Charleston now, legs straddling his head, holding a squirming mass of tentacles, some kind of arachnid\xa0thing. "Open wide," he said with a malicious grin, and shoved the creature down Charleston's throat.\xa0

      \n

      He felt it crawl down into him sickeningly. Pain thrilled down every nerve; his stomach felt like it was erupting as tendrils burst through it and began to knit themselves to his bones, his muscles, his blood vessels...

      \n

      "Good news, bad news," said Mr. N, lighting another cigarette. "This thing can heal you. Bad news is, when it does, it will leak a little bit of itself into you."

      \n

      "Is it possible a little of me will leak into it?" Charleston coughed up a tentacle, and what looked like part of his liver.

      \n

      "Not really."

      \n

      "Are you just bitter because I stabbed you?"

      \n

      "Could be," sneered the man in the tux.\xa0

      \n

      "All these times I looked over my shoulder, you were never there," said Charleston. Black ichor leaked out of his mouth.

      \n

      "That was what made it fun. Speaking of which, I don't want to get in the way of tonight's entertainment. Quite the program."

      \n

      "You always think\xa0you're\xa0the program."

      \n

      "I\xa0am\xa0the program, Chuckles. Always have been. Ask your friend Jimmy about that."

      \n

      "He's not my friend!"

      \n

      "You're righter than you know about that. You'll find out. Spoilers. See you around, kid." The Dark Lord snatched a newspaper out of the thin air and threw it over Charleston's face. Of course it landed open to the funny papers; right in front of his nose was an amusing little strip where a comically drawn Chinese man was stabbed to death.

      \n

      He swept it off of his face and dragged himself up onto the boardwalk. There was no one else there.

      \n

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 9)\n

      Candace pushed through the turnstile...

      \n

      ...She was on a city street. Around her towered office buildings with fancy stores on the ground level. The sky was purple-black, and directly overhead burned an angry red star. In front of her was an enormous long, low building. It had a columned portico that swept in two wings along its vast facade. A broad set of stairs led up to the enormous bronze doors of the place; flanking these stairs were two huge recumbent statues of griffins holding bowls filled with fire in their front paws. The effect was almost like the New York Public Library built to the scale of St. Peter's Basilica.\xa0

      \n

      Above the door, carved in weird characters that quickly became comprehensible to her, was written: Royal Library of Carcosa.

      \n

      She climbed the steps in a dreamlike state. The doors proved easy to push open; they must have been counterweighted. Beyond them was a cavernous entry hall. Chandeliers of brass lamps hung forty or fifty feet in the air above her. She stared, open-mouthed, at the wonders of the place, until she heard a polite cough behind her.

      \n

      She turned and saw a young woman wearing a plain blue mask and a navy uniform of some kind. The woman started when she saw Candace's face. "You're...you're not wearing a mask."

      \n

      "Why would I be wearing a mask?" demanded Candace.

      \n

      The woman shook her head and opened a drawer in her desk. She handed Candace a simple black domino mask. "We keep a loaner here in case people lose theirs," she said apologetically. As soon as Candace had fastened it to her face, the woman's face lit up. "Oh! I didn't recognize you before! You must be here for your exhibit." She held up a flyer which advertised the Candace Heartbrooke room at the Royal Library.

      \n

      Still in a dreamlike daze, Candace followed the woman up a long central staircase to a beautifully decorated reading room. The walls held floor-to-ceiling bookcases. The woman indicated a button to Candace. "Ring the bell if you need anything," she said and backed out of the room.

      \n

      Candace examined some of the books. Her picture was on the back of them. She didn't recognize the title of the book, but it seemed to be written by her. She opened one of them to a random page:

      \n

      \xa0

      \n
      \n

      She stood in the library, looking around at all the books, her books, books she had yet to write, books she had yet to even\xa0conceive. And all in such a place of high honor! She couldn\u2019t help but feel a little giddy.

      \nAs she stood in the room, she seemed to sense the presence of someone else\u2014dimly at first, but then stronger and stronger. She looked around, but there was no one there. And yet\u2026she couldn\u2019t help but feel that there\xa0was\xa0someone there, unseen, always behind her. It seemed to be getting closer and closer. She held her breath, but she could hear nothing. But there was a faint tickle at the back of her neck\u2026as if the hairs were standing on end and being disturbed by a faint breeze, or the breath of a loved one. She tensed herself, expectantly, waiting for the familiar touch\u2026
      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      She looked up. She could feel something in the room. Something behind her. Something that reached out and gave her shoulder the gentlest of caresses, a touch both familiar and faintly sinister. And yet, she found herself thrilling to an awakening of her art, as if inspiration itself were touching her...

      \n

      There was a loud bang. The spell seemed to break. She looked up and saw a figure in a white robe flying out of the room. She ran through the door right behind it, pursuing the figure up and down long staircases and through dark, narrow passages. Always ahead of her she could hear the heavy tread of booted feet, even though she had long since lost sight of the figure. She pushed through some doors and came into a wide-open space...

      \n

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 10)\n

      Jimmy pushed through the turnstile...

      \n

      ...he and Betty were standing on a dark city street made up of dilapidated tenements and tired-looking storefronts. He saw a diner on the corner, filled with people wearing workaday clothes...and masks. He glanced down the street and saw a man walking a dog; both the dog and he were wearing a mask. Betty looked Jimmy askance.

      \n

      He began to stroll down the street. He noticed that the few people out and about would scurry away when they saw he wasn't wearing a mask.\xa0

      \n

      The sky bothered him. He'd always been interested in astronomy and years of living rough had made him familiar with the night sky. So the blazing red star at the zenith...that could only be Aldebaran...was far, far too close. He tried to remember the configuration of the stars above in case he ever got back to Earth and could access a celestial atlas.

      \n

      [Astronomy use here by JP.]

      \n

      He turned a corner and saw, halfway down the street, a neon sign hanging from the side of a building. It depicted a large eye that sometimes blinked; below, in the weird characters of Carcosa, it said "Private Investigations."

      \n

      "Might as well," he said to Betty. He went into the building and climbed the disheveled stairs, pushing through the office door on the second floor marked simply "P.I." Beyond it was a tired looking office, with the usual receptionist's desk and usual faded carpet and ratty chairs.

      \n

      A woman was sitting behind the desk filing her nails. She looked up at Jimmy as he walked in, and behind her mask her eyes registered surprise. She pressed a button on the intercom and said, "Boss? It's...him..."

      \n

      A wooden door with a pebbled glass window in it opened up and out stepped a man in a neat grey suit. He undid his mask, and Jimmy saw his own smiling face staring back. It seemed younger somehow or...no, that wasn't it: less weathered. Whoever this was, they hadn't had nearly as rough a time over the last twenty years.

      \n

      [2 point Stability loss here.]

      \n

      "Let me explain," said the man. "First, you should probably call me J. W. It will be much easier. See, the name I used to use kind of doesn't apply in this situation...old friend."

      \n

      Jimmy's jaw dropped.

      \n

      "I know what you're thinking," continued J. W. "Time was altered, lots of things were made to\xa0never have been, including the version of the Yithian Kakakatak that you used know. Think of me as an echo, placed here in Carcosa, a world outside of time..."

      \n

      Jimmy wrapped him up in a hug. "I know, I know," said J. W. "I feel the same way, pal. How you been?"

      \n

      "Lotta mileage."

      \n

      "I've been the same. Things are always the same here. Well, it's complicated. Carcosa doesn't exist in time the same way as your reality. We kind of stand...next to it. Whenever you come to Carcosa, it's always the same time: the evening of this day. What might actually happen can be different; but this night will always end with...Him arriving. Don't worry, if everything breaks right you should be able to get out ahead of that. Lots to do; we have to go to a museum."

      \n

      "So like old times."

      \n

      "I'm...not sure. I don't know what branch Kakakatak Prime sorted out. True or false: Ruby Fitzgibbons is the President of the United States of America?"

      \n

      "Horribly false."

      \n

      "Whew. Boy, you dodged a bullet there. Japan win or lose World War II?"

      \n

      "Lost."

      \n

      "Nuclear weapons?"

      \n

      "Yah."

      \n

      "No spoilers. Long-term, you're screwed. Anyway, my car is outside."

      \n

      "Is it armored?"

      \n

      "You kidding? We live in a bad neighborhood but it\u2019s not that bad. Like the dog, what's its name?"

      \n

      "Betty."

      \n

      "That's terrible. And funny. By the way you haven't met...the real Betty, have you?"

      \n

      "No."

      \n

      "That's good." They clomped down the stairs and walked over to J. W.'s car, a sleek thing that looked poured out of a science-fiction magazine from the 1930s. "We have a lot to catch up on," said J. W. as they climbed in. "But gotta go now. We'll never beat the Palace traffic otherwise."

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 11)

      p>Temperance sprinted down the stairs from the elevated train station and ran through the streets. Ahead of her she saw a sandy beach and the vast sheet of water and mist that was Lake Hali. The larger of the two suns was setting, and the sky getting darker.\n

      She saw a person crawling in the sand, and she approached him cautiously. "Charleston, is that you?" she said when she drew near.

      \n

      "Stay the hell away from me!"

      \n

      "That's Charleston. It's me, Temperance. Actual Temperance," she added as an afterthought.

      \n

      Charleston motioned her down and then reached up to feel her face. She pushed him back down and stared as his rent clothes and the stains of blood and ichor. She tried to probe the wounds but Charleston swept her hands away and stood up.

      \n

      "Charleston, you have eyes," she said. "Can you see?"

      \n

      "No," he replied, distracted. He swept up the shiny gold mask "Noor" had been wearing.

      \n

      "What happened to you?"

      \n

      "Nothing. What happened to you?"

      \n

      "Nothing happened to me, I'm not the one covered in...you can explain later..."

      \n

      "Let's get the hell out of here." This struck them as a good idea; something was bubbling out of the misty waves. It seemed to have tentacles.

      \n

      They limped up to the boardwalk, making sure they did not look back at whatever was coming up on the beach. Charleston looked at the city, lit up against the black sky in the west, with both his new eyes and his Third Eye. He only saw the visible forms with both; this vaguely relieved him, as he was sure the entire experience was being mediated somehow and the actual Carcosa was far more inhospitable to the human mind.

      \n

      [Cthulhu Mythos use here.]

      \n

      "You've been in the city?" he asked Temperance as they began to stagger down the boardwalk.

      \n

      "I was on a train, then I was attacked by those strange men in suits, then here."

      \n

      "I don't know what that means, but we're supposed to be in a city."

      \n

      "We are, it comes right up here."

      \n

      "Right up where?"

      \n

      "Oh dear. I think one of us is losing their minds."

      \n

      "I think we both are."

      \n

      "If you told me you can't see the city I would believe you because, A, you're blind, and B, this is not a normal place."

      \n

      "This isn't a normal place even for abnormal places."

      \n

      "Charleston, I need to know...is this what it's like to use a hallucinogen? I've never experimented like the others. Can you share a hallucination? Could we be the victims of some kind of drug attack, and we're still in that field?"

      \n

      "Of course, that's probably the most likely explanation," said Charleston in a way he thought was reassuring.

      \n

      "So it's not true then."

      \n

      "Temperance...human beings don't just grow eyes back. The only reasonable explanation is hallucinogens. Whenever you see anything you can't explain, that's the reason. I stake my reputation on this."

      \n

      Temperance looked askance. "I'm just eliminating possibilities. I can accept this as bizarre and strange if that is what it is; I just don't want to waste time chiseling out some weird sign in a wall if we're in fact in a field somewhere. Wasting time is wasting time."

      \n

      [TP, after Charleston's speech: Yeah, I have BS Detector.

      \n

      Me: TILT! TILT!]

      \n

      "I don't know what to tell you, Temperance. You're arguing with one of your hallucinations then."

      \n

      "I will throw you in the water with that\xa0thing," began Temperance.

      \n

      "Don't acknowledge the thing! Let's finish this argument inside the city."

      \n

      They made their way along the boardwalk. Out over the surface of the lake huge banks of mist would gather and rush toward shore, breaking like waves against the beach. The kiosks lining the boardwalk were all closed and locked up, forlorn in the gloom and covered in glistening droplets of condensation.

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 12)\n

      As they rounded a curve, they saw a woman sitting at the end of a little pier that jutted out into the lake. She was wearing beautiful, well-made but antique clothes: a white silk dress trimmed in gold, ropes of thick gold chains around her neck, and a mask of porcelain and silver. Her hair was done up in an elaborate series of braids. Temperance thought it looked like a theatrical costume of some kind.

      \n

      [Art pegged that clue.]

      \n

      As they approached, the woman sang in a lovely soprano:

      \n
      \n

      Along the shore, the cloud waves break,

      \nThe twin suns sink behind the lake,\xa0
      The shadows lengthen\xa0
      in Carcosa...
      \n

      She stopped when she saw them. "Who are you?" she demanded. "Neither of those masks belong to you!"

      \n

      "None of your business," muttered Charleston. "People have to wear the mask they have."

      \n

      "You really are strangers," said the woman, surprised.

      \n

      "We think the same of you."

      \n

      "You don't know who I am?"

      \n

      "No."

      \n

      Temperance tried to say something, but the woman cut her off. "My name is Yolanda Lareine," she said. "I don't know who you are."

      \n

      "We're fans of a play," said Temperance. "We've come to Carcosa to watch it."

      \n

      "Oh! In that case you'll be wanting to go to the Palace." She smiled to herself and reached into her robe and took out several oblong pieces of stiff paper. "Sorry, didn't realize you were fans. Take these passes for tonight's performance. And since you're strangers in town and don't know your way around...Noss!"

      \n

      A man came down a flight of stairs, wearing a chauffeur's uniform. "Yes ma'am," he said, then stopped when he saw Charleston and Temperance.

      \n

      "We're new," said Temperance drily.

      \n

      "Clearly! So first stop is a mask shop, then we'll head to the Palace. Gotta stop at the Museum on the way to pick someone up." He led them up the stairs to a parking lot; the only car in it was a rather odd-looking long vehicle, evidently a limousine of some kind. It had a certain old-fashioned look about it, although it was sleek and futuristic in some ways; Temperance decided it was the kind of thing you might have seen on the cover of Amazing Stories back in the 1930s.

      \n

      [Carcosa is very retro-future. TP and I had a brief description of masks in Carcosa; it was evident to Temperance that the masks contained complex markers of class and faction, as well as revealing certain aspects of the wearer's personality. And of course, Carcosans couldn't recognize each other without their masks. "Carcosans as a people are given to rather heavy-handed metaphor," I said.]

      \n

      "You don't have to call me Mr. Noss or anything," said Noss as he opened the car. "It's just plain old Bill. I'll drive you done to Techarn's, he usually has a good selection. Probably really busy, it's a big night."

      \n

      "When was the last time you had a night this big?" asked Charleston.

      \n

      "Well, I work for Yolanda, everything is big with her."

      \n

      [I grinned at CP. "Good luck."]

      \n

      "Can you give us some help finding a mask...we don't want to look any more\u2014" began Temperance.

      \n

      "Ridiculous?" snorted Noss. "Hard to look more ridiculous than you do now. Like you're a dairy processor fourth class, lady."

      \n

      "What should we expect tonight? I don't want to do anything rude..."

      \n

      "Apparently there's a special guest at the performance, so who knows."

      \n

      "Big surprise at the end?"

      \n

      "We do like our spectacle. Tonight we're doing a play called\xa0The Unanswered Question."

      \n

      "What was the last play you did?" said Charleston.

      \n

      "Does\xa0East Side Story\xa0sound familiar?"

      \n

      "Vaguely."

      \n

      They drove through the rapidly fading light, past the storefronts that poured golden light out onto the streets. Most were closing up for the evening, and the sidewalks were packed with throngs of people. Both Temperance and Charleston were picking up on a strange, electric sensation in the air; like the tenseness in the atmosphere before a summer thunderstorm.

      \n

      When they reached the mask store, the clerk had just put his hand to the "Closed" sign. He sighed, an in an accent that was surprisingly close to that of New York City, asked them what they wanted.

      \n

      "Busy day today?" said Charleston.

      \n

      "Every day's busy."

      \n

      [Me: Keep trying, man.]

      \n

      "We need masks," said Temperance.

      \n

      "Do you have the paperwork? Of course not, you're strangers. Going to the Palace? Of course you are, strangers always go to the Palace. Have you see that Phantom of Truth? Nobody knows who that is." He handed Temperance a mask and turned to consider Charleston. "Your eyes weren't always green, were they?"

      \n

      "Of course they were," said Charleston dismissively.

      \n

      The clerk handed Charleston a harlequin mask. Temperance considered her own mask; it somehow resembled\u2014in some subtle fashion she couldn't quite divine\u2014a painting of Mary Magdalene that she had admired a great deal when she had studied in Europe.

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 13)\n

      J.W. slammed on the brakes and they came to an abrupt stop in front of a gigantic cube-shaped building that took up an entire city block. Chiseled above the undecorated entrance was the legend, in the weird characters of the city, "Museum of Carcosa".

      \n

      "Come on, come on, you're meeting someone I think," said J.W., tugging Jimmy out of the vehicle. They dashed through the entrance. Inside, the museum proved to contain wonders to delight and frighten...

      \n

      The entry hall was lined by massive statues that resembled, vaguely, the WPA style of the late 1930s: stylized, Art Decoish representations of the Queens of Carcosa. Their consorts were on the other side of the hallway in various poses. They heard a door bang and Jimmy saw Candace walk in.

      \n

      "Candace," he said, waving her over. "This is J.W."

      \n

      Candace stared somewhat agape.

      \n

      "I know what you're thinking," said J.W. "I'm better looking."

      \n

      "I think the only thing better looking than me is a baboon's ass, and it's a close call," muttered Jimmy.

      \n

      Candace noticed that between the statues there were paintings of people that looked like they could come from Earth; at least, they weren't wearing masks. As she approached, she saw they had little plaques and birth and death dates noted as "E.D." which she took to mean "Earth dating."

      \n
      \n

      Robert W. Chambers 1865-1933 ED

      \nHildred de Castaigne 1891-1920 ED
      Janet W. Rogers 1905-1975 ED
      Candace Heartbrooke 1924-1956 ED
      \n

      "They all wrote about the King in Yellow," said J.W. "C'mon, we gotta get to the North Wing." The Museum didn't have the large, straight hallways linking exhibition halls they were used to back on Earth; instead, twisting and narrow passageways opened up from time to time into larger rooms. They were never sure of what to expect next: a grove of trees erupting out of the marble flooring, a room full of glass vitrines filled with seemingly-identical carvings of a goldfish out of marble, and everywhere bookcases, bookcases, bookcases. And the details of the exhibits themselves were strange: a suit of armor powered by steam, looming twelve feet high; a ship sailing across a desert under three suns; a room full of marionettes reenacting a ballet very similar to\xa0The Rites of Spring.\xa0

      \n

      And strangely enough there seemed to be some kind of afterhours party going on; they often passed little cabaret tables lit by candles or small lamps, surrounded by little knots of people in evening clothes, wearing their fanciest masks. There was an odd sounding music in the air\u2014something a little like atonal French jazz played by a Latin swing band. And everyone had that nervous, chattery despair that people get during moments of great national stress: Jimmy recognized it from people he saw in London during the Blitz.

      \n

      J.W. led them to the Hall of Weapons. It was filled with polearms, armor with spikes in unusual and anatomically dangerous areas (and armor for people with more limbs than customary in humans), unusual muskets with bizarre carvings.

      \n

      Jimmy lifted a polearm inquisitively. "Put that back!" barked J.W. "We don't have much time left. This is what we came for."

      \n

      He pointed to a long case lined with red velvet. Lying unsheathed in the case was a long single-edged sword: a scimitar of some kind. It took Jimmy a moment to recognize it: the Sword of Akmallah.

      \n

      "James," said J.W., "you know what that sword is, don't you?"

      \n

      "Extremely sharp," said Jimmy, staring at the blade.

      \n

      "You saw Freddie carry it. You saw Geronimo carry it. Don't you think...it's time for\xa0you\xa0to carry it?"

      \n

      Jimmy put his hand on the haft. "It fell outside of time," said J.W. softly, "and so it came to Carcosa, the world outside time."

      \n

      "I'm worried about the things I might do with it," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "The sword cuts both ways. Who do you think is better to carry it than you?"

      \n

      Jimmy lifted up the sword. Its blade flowed like water, flashing in the dim light, resolving into a well-balanced longsword with a simple crosshilt.

      \n

      "Now put that pigsticker away," said J.W., handing Jimmy the scabbard.\xa0

      \n
      \n

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 14)\n

      Candace had wandered away from the boys and their toys some time before. She followed a narrow corridor until it suddenly opened onto the largest open space she had seen so far in the museum.

      \n

      It must have been a conservatory of some kind. A glass dome towered overhead, bigger than any she had ever seen, on the scale of St. Paul's or the Pantheon or the U.S. Capitol. She craned her neck back. Directly overhead was the angry red glare of Aldebaran, bright enough to cast faint shadows from the vegetation around her. It was almost night now; the stars were coming out, a spectacular scattering of light far denser than any nighttime sky she had seen on Earth; had Jimmy been there, he might have speculated that perhaps they were close to a star cluster, such as the Hyades. The moons were rising in front of the city. Somehow overhead she sensed the malevolence of the black stars, invisible now against the sky, circling warily.

      \n

      The air was heavy, steamy, and chokingly scented with a wild melange of tropical perfumes. Strange and exotic plants were everywhere she turned, many with night flowers that opened and displayed a sickly radiance. They were unusual colors, deep purples trimmed with gold, bright, bright blues, reds the color of innocent blood. She walked along the winding path until she reached the center of the room. She stopped short. A man was standing in front of her, holding a leatherbound book; he seemed to be gazing through the dome at the illuminated skyscrapers in the center of the city.

      \n

      He turned around and she realized it was Amadou Lalin. "Candace Heartbrooke," he said with a smile, holding out his hand. "We met at Asylum, back on Earth."

      \n

      "Yes, we did." She stared at his mask, which was made of leather dyed midnight black and outlined with a faint tracery of white or silver. He noticed her gaze and smiled again. "You should really get a better mask if you're going to stay her for a long time."

      \n

      She paused. Amadou seemed a different man in Carcosa: in control, present, alert. Whatever had been missing from his psyche, his\xa0soul\xa0on Earth was returned here.

      \n

      "I actually know some lovely places," he continued. "We can go after the play is done. Are you here for the play? Or to stay?"

      \n

      "For the play. Is it the play we saw at Asylum?"

      \n

      "Everything's the play. But there will be a performance to come. We all have a role. And they recur."

      \n

      "I'm not quite sure what mine is."

      \n

      "There's a certain amount of latitude that every performer has, don't you think? I've seen many different Lady Macbeths. Each one slightly changed. I've known many people who I hope will one day play my small part in this production. So it's not always easy to tell what your role is, that's true; but I think you have a place in this play. Yes. Most definitely."

      \n

      They sat down on a cast iron bench nestled under trees that bore a strange yellow fruit. "Did you see your book?" said Amadou. "You're held in great renown in Carcosa. Possibly because I liked you so much when I met you. Are you here with your friends?"

      \n

      "I'm not sure. I saw one just now."

      \n

      "Mr. Wright. And J.W., that scamp. Yithians are such funny people, when you get to know them. Most people don't know that about them. Wonderful sense of humor, not like the mi-go at all."

      \n

      "Yes," said Candace, mystified.

      \n

      "I think...your friends will be arriving soon. Perhaps we should go find Mr. Wright." He held out his book to her. "I like reading this book. It's the poems I haven't written yet. I guess I'm slightly sad about one thing: I won't write them now...not on Earth."

      \n

      "I guess if you don't return..."

      \n

      "I don't mean to return. What's on Earth for me? I missed my chance once before, I let Percy go. And I loved Percy very much; but I was too afraid then. Cowardice is not a good look. But now I am here, and have built all this."

      \n

      "You seem at home."

      \n

      "Yes, I do. How wonderful."

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 15)\n

      Bill Noss had driven Charleston and Temperance to the Museum, then swiftly led them through the winding passageways; so quickly, in fact, that they barely had any chance to register an impression of the place. They came across Jimmy, holding a sword in a scabbard, walking out of a room full of obscure and bizarre weapons.

      \n

      "Hey, Mr. Wright," said Noss. "J.W."

      \n

      "Hiya Bill."

      \n

      "Who's that?" said Jimmy, alarmed.

      \n

      "That's just Bill Noss."

      \n

      "Mr. Wright," said Temperance, looking at both Jimmy and J.W.

      \n

      "I know, he's not wearing a mask, it's disgusting ain't it?" stage whispered Noss.

      \n

      "Keep talking and I'll take off your mask," said Jimmy darkly.

      \n

      "C'mon Mr. Wright, I can't afford too many masks on my salary. I'm just a working guy!"

      \n

      "Sorry," said Jimmy gruffly.

      \n

      "You probably need a drink. Let's go pick up Amadou."

      \n

      Noss led them to the Conservatory. Amadou looked up as they came into view. "Hello, everyone. Lovely night, isn't it?"

      \n

      "No," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "Mr. Wright, why don't you like Carcosa? It's my heart's delight."

      \n

      "Well currently you and I have different hearts."

      \n

      "I haven't had a chance to sound out your heart yet, Mr. Wright. I suppose I could ask J.W...."

      \n

      "Nope," said J.W. firmly. "That would be cheating. Gotcha back, Jimmy." He glanced over at Charleston. "Oh, you brought\xa0Chuckles? Somebody was looking for you. He find you?"

      \n

      "Yeah. We had a rendez-vous."

      \n

      "Who was it?" said Jimmy

      \n

      "Nobody important."

      \n

      "We should get out of here."

      \n

      "Did Edie bring you? Or Nathan?" asked Amadou.

      \n

      "Lund, yeah."

      \n

      "I'm worried about Nathan. I think he's making a mistake. I warned him many times, but Quincy is...have you met him?"

      \n

      "Once," said Temperance.

      \n

      "What was your impression of him?"

      \n

      "Amiable, but a little full of himself."

      \n

      "So accurate, then. I think he has made a very dangerous error. I think he thinks Hastur and the King are the same thing."

      \n

      "Are they not?"

      \n

      "Do you know your Rilke?"

      \n

      "Not really."

      \n

      "It's all in the\xa0Duino Elegies. Here:

      \n
      \n

      \u2026Denn das Sch\xf6ne ist nichts

      \nals des Schrecklichen Anfang, den wir noch gerade ertragen,
      und wir bewundern es so, weil es gelassen verschm\xe4ht,
      uns zu zerst\xf6ren\u2026
      \xa0
      For beauty is nothing but the beginning of terror
      which we are barely able to endure and are awed
      because it serenely disdains to annihilate us.
      \n

      "That's Hastur: the terror behind beauty. Death in the bloom. Nature red in tooth and claw. Something raw, beyond understanding. As Rilke says elsewhere in that poem:\xa0Ein jeder Engel ist schrecklich: every angel is terrifying. That is how it must be; the terror of Hastur is inseperable from the angelic nature of the King. But at the same time they are separate..."

      \n

      He turned to Candace. "You've been touched by him," he said. "You know the inspiration brought by the King. But Hastur is also in that. The wild part, the unknowable. When you stand outside at night and look at the stars and are awed, you stand in the shadow of the King. When you look up into the heavens and are terrified by the empty void behind them, you stand in the shadow of Hastur. If you try to bring Hastur but expect the King...you have lost wisdom."

      \n

      He looked at them with sad resignation. "You did not know any of this, did you? Why then are you in my city?"

      \n

      "We got dragged along for the ride," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "We were looking for you," said Temperance.\xa0

      \n

      "We were hoping to find you before you got to the city," added Jimmy.

      \n

      "You were the girl who fought Edie!" said Amadou, eyes lighting up as he looked at Temperance.\xa0

      \n

      "Is the Palace a way out?" demanded Jimmy.

      \n

      "There's no way out of Carcosa except through it...but...yes, the Palace would lead the way."

      \n

      "Is this what you and the others at TAROT were trying to do?"

      \n

      "You know about TAROT...Percy stumbled into these things accidentally. But when he came through, and led us here\u2014of course, it was Percy's city and a very different place...he didn't know what to expect. It's why we researched these things, how we learned the spells to summon Hastur, like he did. That did not work very well. We also didn't expect the bomb that night."

      \n

      "Somewhere near Vegas in '53?" asked Charleston.

      \n

      "Indeed. The bomb...I don't want to say it interfered, but it came at a very inopportune moment. We only brought Hastur into the world for a very brief time. But I think he may have escaped our control. You need monoliths arranged in a V-shape when you summon Him."

      \n

      "I saw some of those," said Temperance. "At Chambersburg. Back on Earth."

      \n

      [Preparedness spend by TP.]

      \n

      "If Quincy is summoning Hastur into your world, but doesn't realize who he is bringing...he won't take the right precautions. You should try and stop him here, if you want to stop him that is. Bill, you should take us to the Palace."

      \n

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 16)\n

      Noss whisked them in his limousine through the dark and empty streets of the city. The twilight was rapidly fading. There was no one out on the sidewalks; the few lights left on in the buildings were even more forlorn because clearly they had been left on by mistake.\xa0

      \n

      The city was deserted. Everyone must now come to the Palace.

      \n

      They raced over the suspension bridge. Beneath them the dark waters of the Lake of Hali were thrashing in agitation; above the dark stars beat down their malevolence. Candace remembered her Milton:

      \n
      \n

      As one great Furnace flam'd, yet from those flames

      \nNo light, but rather darkness visible
      Serv'd only to discover sights of woe\u2026
      \n

      They skidded down the ramp from the bridge and approached the Palace: a wedding cake confection of flying buttresses and towers, but even at this distance it was obvious that it was an enormous theater: Radio City Music Hall, built on the scale of the Louvre. Above the entrance a towering marquee rose into the night:

      \n
      \n

      ONE NIGHT ONLY

      \nTHE UNANSWERED QUESTION
      OR, THE STRANGER AND THE QUEEN
      BY AMADOU LALIN
      AND N.Q. LUND
      SPECIAL APPEARANCE BY
      EDIE MONTAGUE
      AND THE TATTERDEMALION KING
      \n

      Noss screeched to a stop below the marquee and pushed them quickly inside. There was a bored usherette standing at the other end of the lobby; velvet covered ropes had been strung from stands to block off the other entrances into the main auditorium. She threw her cigarette to the floor and ground it out as they approached.

      \n

      "Royal Box," she said, taking their passes. "Right up that way." She nodded to a sweeping curved staircase behind her, and they quickly moved up it. Candace threw a last glance back at the lobby before she reached the top of the stairs. The usherette was smoking again; but from underneath her mask, a single tear was rolling down her cheek.

      \n

      They followed a plushly carpeted hallway for what felt like miles until they came to their box. To their surprise, they found a few people already sitting in it that they recognized: Joy and John Harris from Chambersburg were there, without their children; a pompous college professor type Candace vaguely remembered seeing at the hotel; and Henry Lister, who was peering nervously around. He smiled at Jimmy. Joy looked over to Temperance and silently mouthed\xa0Thank You\xa0at her.

      \n

      "Quentin Spencer," said the professorial man, shaking Jimmy's hand vigorously. He stopped when he saw J.W. "Are you twins?"

      \n

      "I'm the older," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "Clearly."

      \n

      "He's the alien remnant of an entity I wiped out of time," said Jimmy, hoping it would end the conversation. He looked out at the stage. Below, a performance of\xa0The Unanswered Question\xa0was taking place; but at a scale appropriate to Carcosa. The movie screen was bigger than a couple of football fields; the sets were built to a grandeur impossible to attain in any stage production on Broadway. In the pit a huge orchestra was playing symphonic music that was plain but engraved with deep lines of sorrow and misery. A woman with a prodigious soprano voice was singing a lament; Temperance and Charleston recognized her as Yolanda.

      \n

      [I listened quite often to Gorecki's Third Symphony "Sorrowful Songs" while writing my notes for this session; at this point I was playing an excerpt from Colin Stetson's fascinating reworking of the piece called "Sorrow".]

      \n

      The auditorium was gigantic. A sea of faces looked up at them. It seemed impossible that the entire city's population could fit inside a single building but that was the impression conveyed by this immense dim cavern of a room. The inhabitants of Carcosa, in their finery both familiar and strange, their masks and feathers, tiny children and aged grandparents, all, all, had the expression of shock and the gradual realization that something they had long dreaded but never believed to be actually possible was now somehow coming to pass. Something terrible, and unavoidable.

      \n

      [Psychology picked this up; it was Candace who got the clue. "We here on Earth know nothing about how\xa0that\xa0feels like.\u201d Have I mentioned that this session took place on the first Saturday after the 2016 US Presidential election?]

      \n

      From her seat, Candace could see a little into the wings of the theater. She say N. Quincy Lund standing there, wearing a really theatrical costume of yellow robes and a tinsel crown. He was pacing back and forth, smoking a cigar, giving the appearance of someone desperately trying to remember their lines.

      \n

      Charleston looked up into the darkness. Hanging somewhere up in the dark gloom that hid the ceiling were...things...somehow insectile, somehow human, chittering and hissing in the blackness. They reminded him of the things that had swarmed in the fog at Chambersburg. They reminded him of the agents that Jimmy had encountered in San Francisco.

      \n

      The music died down. Yolanda and another woman stood near the center of the stage. And Edie Montague, wearing long white robes, stood next to them. Somewhere deep offstage, a gong boomed.

      \n

      And everyone took off their masks.

      \n

      All of them; the actors and the musicians; the shopkeepers and soldiers; the children and their parents; young and old; rich and poor; the frightened, the humble, the sick, the lame, the strong, the weak, the blessed, the cursed. They stood blinking and naked in the dim lights of the auditorium, almost pathetic, almost wretched.

      \n

      Yolanda turned to Edie. "Come, sir, you should unmask."

      \n

      "Indeed?" said Edie. She took out something that glittered from underneath her robe and held it tightly in one hand.

      \n

      "Indeed. We have all laid aside disguise except for you."

      \n

      Edie took a deep breath before replying. "I wear no mask," she said, and unfolded the straight razor she held in her hand. She placed it along her ulnar bone, and then sliced deeply into it, a long cut parallel to the bone that she worked gradually up her arm, to her bicep, up over onto her shoulder..."I wear no mask," she said, gritting her jaw with pain. "I wear no mask," she repeated, working the razor around her neck, changing hands and then working it down her other arm, her sides, slicing down one leg and then the other...blood gushed from the wounds in sickening bursts, pooling blackly around her feet.

      \n

      "No mask?" said the woman standing next to Yolanda. "No mask!" Her voice was strangely familiar.

      \n

      "NO MASK!" shouted Edie, and stepped forward.

      \n

      The skin parted off of her body like a bathrobe. It curled up at her feet as she stood in the klieg lights screaming, "NO MASK! NO MASK!"

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 17)\n

      As the audience gasped in shock, Jimmy saw Quincy Lund striding onto the stage. \xa0Charleston motioned up at the ceiling. "Don't forget about the second audience."

      \n

      "J.W., what's hanging from the ceiling?" said Jimmy.

      \n

      "The Byakhee. They're servants of Hastur."

      \n

      "Do we have to worry about them?\u201d

      \n

      "Yeah, yeah, definitely."

      \n

      "Do they kill people?"

      \n

      "If you're lucky they kill you first. Sometimes they fly people off to other parts of the universe."

      \n

      "I think I met those guys; called themselves 'Mr. Stapler' and 'Mr. Lamp' or something."

      \n

      "Oh, they're doing that one. That's fun."

      \n

      "They hit like a truck."

      \n

      "That's them."

      \n

      "We have to stop this," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "What are you going to do, swing down there like Errol Flynn?" said Charleston.

      \n

      J.W. looked at him. "Actually, I figured that was exactly what he was going to do."

      \n

      Temperance pulled out her pistol and fired down at Lund, smashing a bullet into the stage right in front of his feet. Everyone on the stage stopped what they were doing. Lund looked up, scanning for the source of the shot.

      \n

      Jimmy jumped from the box, grabbed the curtains and swung down onto the stage. The sword was in his hand even without his thinking of drawing it. He aimed a vicious cut at Lund's head; he raised his arm to block without thinking and Jimmy's blow sliced off his hand.

      \n

      [JP, who was reading the house rules sidebar on his sheet, turned the extra benefit he got from his roll of 10 on the Athletics check to get to the stage into an attack, and then used his Maneuver pool to do terrible harm.]

      \n

      Lund fell to the ground, bleeding everywhere. The tinsel crown he was wearing rolled of his head. The Byakhee dropped like a swarm of insects from the ceiling.

      \n

      "It's the end of Carcosa!" shouted J.W. "It's always the end of Carcosa\u2014"

      \n

      The building went away.

      \n

      They were standing in the open, on a rocky promontory on the shore of Lake Hali. The waters, black in the starlight, were clashing and swirling. Suddenly, the lake seemed to hump itself up, like a whale diving or a gigantic man getting out of bed. It formed into a gigantic standing wave, moving toward the city.

      \n

      There were eyes in it.

      \n

      Suddenly, without any of them ever exactly clear how, Yolanda was with them. "The subway, you fools! Run!"

      \n

      They ran. The wave followed, swept ahead, towered against the sky, now completely black. Aldebaran glowed red and violent and refracted through the translucent waters of the wave, of the old one, of Hastur the Unknowable and Unattainable and Unspeakable. Its eyes darted around, glancing, rolling, lurching without any sign of intelligence or understanding and yet brimming with an utter malignant indifference.

      \n

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 18)\n

      Temperance stared into the watery depths and saw two eyes lock hers in their gaze. And she knew at that moment, as she stood in the presence of a monstrous deity, that everything she had once thought was true about religion was a hollow joke. For some reason a Bible verse kept running in her mind, over and over again: "It is a fearful thing to fall into the hands of the Living God..."

      \n

      [Temperance challenges her "God's words will put me back on the path Statement; this kept her Stability positive, but still cost 2 Sanity...]

      \n

      Jimmy looked up and saw the eyes of Hastur, a wave of destruction and malignance and was struck, once again, by the utter insignificance he held in the sight of the Outer Beings: that only the ritual had caused the incomprehensible intelligence of this entity to notice him even for a fraction of a moment. And he knew that the dangers they were facing were graver than he had dared let himself realize, that if Carcosa was intruding into their world that no one would ever be safe again, not even Janet who he had done everything to protect. He recalled that when Sol Molinari had told him about his experiments with Hastur that the world had convulsed, one step toward liberation, one step toward annihilation. Betty began barking and barking, dragging him by his pants cuff until he lowered his gaze and began to back into the city. The last he saw of Betty she was standing in the gloom cast by the immense column of water, barking furiously at him as if pleading for him to go...

      \n

      [Jimmy challenged his Drive (At least Janet is safe) and his Solace (Betty is always there for me when I need her). I told JP I might have some bad news about Betty...]

      \n

      Charleston shattered.

      \n

      He felt the fragile construct of his personality break apart and reassemble itself again. He thought about Noor, not the imitation the Dark Lord had used to fool him, but the goofy, brilliant girl who had shared his passion for...well, this: the universal. His third eye violently opened, even without Yellow in his system, and he felt again the strange currents of the universe that he had once read like a sailor read the winds, carry him up again. How could he have ever thought he was a\xa0normal person? Hastur the Unspeakable had reached into his mind and rearranged it. And he knew, he\xa0knew\xa0that none of this had been chance: that as Amadou had said, he was playing a role in a work written by a greater playwright. His connections to the world, his way of hiding himself in the cracks of a humanity he no longer felt, crumbled apart like damp cardboard in his hands. Oddly, at this moment, he thought of Helen: realizing, maybe, that she was the one \xa0person in the world who would understand him...

      \n

      [CP challenged every statement on his sheet, but of course Sanity went down by 2...]

      \n

      Candace ran. Her fountain pen, the only present her husband Andy had given her, fall out of her pocket and before she could pick it up, it was crushed by someone in the fleeing throng that was suddenly all around them. What was death, and life, compared to this horrid thing? And yet...here she was in Carcosa, the city Art had created, and she knew somehow that art would be her salvation...

      \n

      [HP challenged Candace's Solace statement. You guessed it, 2 points of Sanity; this was the minimum seeing Hastur cost the characters.

      \n

      At this point I again saw how the Statements rules really worked effectively\u2014rather than just losing Sanity or maybe going insane, all the PCs were\xa0changed, permanently altered by this encounter. I've wanted for a while to use them to remove Sanity as a stat, but haven't had the time to write up a set of rules to test.]

      \n
