      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 19)\n

      Yolanda was pushing and dragging them. "This way, come on!" she kept shouting, until they all shook themselves out of their stupor and saw a few blocks away a set of stairs leading beneath the sidewalk. Behind them, the spell broke and the eyes went out and the wave collapsed. Dirty water flooded into the streets, rapidly rising to ankle level.

      \n

      As they fought through the current in this eternal final night of Carcosa, they all began to feel\xa0pursued, of something dreadful following them. Temperance thought she saw the flash a piece of yellow cloth, silk perhaps, dragged suddenly around a corner, and the crushing sense of something\xa0watching\xa0with cold amusement as they fled increased.

      \n

      Night had fallen. The King of Tatters was coming to claim his own.

      \n

      They slipped and stumbled down the water that rushed in a cascade down the subway steps. Yolanda was in the front, craning her neck behind her to plead in gasps with them. "You're taking me with you, right? Carcosa is a trap, you understand? It's a trap!"

      \n

      They reached the platform and leaped into the flooded trackway, pushing through the knee-deep waters down the dark tunnel. Charleston laughed as he gathered the eldritch energies all around them. "I've done this before, don't you see! Except this time we're the bullets!"

      \n

      Jimmy shoved his way forward. He caught up with Yolanda and dragged her behind him, followed by Candace who was pushing forward with grim determination. Temperance kept turning around to see if anything was following them. The water had risen up to her waist. She saw something crest out of the water for a second.

      \n

      The Byakhee were swimming behind them. Two jumped out of the water and grabbed with their rear claws onto a metal beam that supported the roof. In the dimness she thought she saw great wings unfold.

      \n

      Jimmy was wading up behind her, the Sword already in his hand. He slashed blindly out at them, trying to push it back into its companion...

      \n

      And that was when Charleston's spell went off.

      \n

      [I asked for tests/spends here; JP and HP did Athletics, CP Cthulhu Mythos, and since TP was out of Athletics, the spend was Notice. Jimmy's attack on the Byakhee got him a benefit, so JP chose "Suppress" to keep them from attacking.]

      \n

      It was like being squeezed through some ever contracting tube of muscle, so tight that it crushed the air out of them. Before their ribs splintered, they felt a sudden release and then felt cold air moving over them.\xa0

      \n

      They were on the shore of Lake Till. There was a crowd of the people of Chambersburg around them. And it was snowing.

      \n

      Behind them the water of the lake humped up for a second...

      \n

      ...and then collapsed. A cold mist rolled over them. For a second they could see yellow flashes around the eyes of some of the people around them. Then the mist dissipated. In the heavens, the fiery glow of Aldebaran faded and then was hidden behind a cloud.

      \n

      Jimmy heard it first: the sound of heavy equipment moving toward the town. He thought of halftracks on Normandy beaches and began to shout for everyone to scatter. Not long after, the first gunshots rang out.

      \n

      They followed. Temperance got glimpses of men wearing military uniforms without any insignia she could see moving through the town, barking orders and yelling. They turned a corner and saw a young soldier holding a M-14 rifle.

      \n

      "Hold it right there!" he yelled nervously. "All of you! Nobody move!"

      \n

      "Stand down, soldier!" barked Jimmy, hoping to bluff him.

      \n

      "Just down on your knees!" Two other soldiers were closing in now that they could see him trying to apprehend people.

      \n

      Charleston saw the young soldier glance at them and struck out quicker than anyone could have thought possible. He pulled the rifle out of his hands, spun it, and then clocked the kid in the forehead with the butt. He yanked the magazine out and threw it away, then sped toward the RV. Temperance grabbed Charleston before he turned the last corner. Then she peeked around it.

      \n

      Two soldiers were standing guard next to the RV. Beyond them they could see most of the population of the town being herded onto the town green.

      \n

      Temperance pushed Jimmy to the ground and grabbed him by the shoulders and dragged him toward the the RV. "Help! Help! His pills are in the RV!"

      \n

      "You're under arrest, ma'am!" shouted one of the soldiers, leveling his rifle. "You too, hobo. Why are you wearing a mask, lady?"

      \n

      "I'm a veteran," gasped Jimmy.

      \n

      "Look, mac, nobody's in trouble. We just need to sort this out...is that a sword? We don't want any trouble\u2014"

      \n

      Suddenly he went ramrod straight.\xa0

      \n

      "James," someone\u2014a woman with a clipped English accent\u2014from behind him.

      \n
      \n
      \n

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 20)\n

      Jimmy closed his eyes and sighed, then stood up. "Hello, Mina," he said.

      \n

      The woman was fashionably dressed in business attire\u2014a severe black skirt suit with an expensive silk blouse under her jacket. A long red scarf was wrapped tightly around her throat, and a pair of pince-nez hung from a chain worn over the scarf. She looked him over severely, then sighed herself.\xa0

      \n

      "You know the Directrix?" boggled the soldier.

      \n

      "You remember Freddie's aunt, who made our lives a living hell?" said Jimmy to Charleston.

      \n

      "That can't be Freddie's aunt, it's been thirty years\u2014ohh..." said Charleston.

      \n

      "Did you bring\xa0Charleston\xa0in on this, James?" said Mina incredulously.

      \n

      "Wasn't my idea," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "Are you...completely\xa0mental\xa0after all these years?"

      \n

      "Lady, I'm right here," said Charleston, miffed.\xa0

      \n

      "I wish I could help that, but I can't," said Mina.

      \n

      "But I helped!" said Charleston. "I helped!" He looked at Jimmy, pleading.

      \n

      "Come along, ladies and gents, let me buy you all a cup of tea," said Mina.

      \n

      "Have any brandy?" groused Jimmy.

      \n

      Mina looked at him, and then at Temperance. "My God...is that..."

      \n

      "Yeah, but she doesn't really know much\u2014"

      \n

      "Temperance Murphy? Don't you remember me from the Christmas parties? Auntie Mina? I worked with your mother?"

      \n

      "Until she stole the company," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "We did that for your own good."

      \n

      "Keep telling yourself that. Not that I cared, I was out of it by then."

      \n

      "Let's not agitate the men with the guns," said Temperance. "Tea would be lovely."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Directrix Murray's command post was a tent set up on the end of the green, as far as possible from the shores of the lake. A nervous orderly poured them tea from a thermos.

      \n

      "Beastly stuff," said Mina. "Dreadful once it's been in the thermos for half an hour. Candace Heartbrooke, isn't it? Don't worry, my dear, you're not in any worse trouble than you are from hanging around James."

      \n

      "Ow," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "James, James, James," said Mina. "The world isn't the way it used to be. We can't have\xa0cowboys\xa0running around taking care of things on their own. The Russians have nuclear weapons. Do you care to imagine what would happen if they had mystic powers? Or signed a treaty with the Mi-Go?"

      \n

      "You think I'm running around giving them things like that?"

      \n

      "Do you think there's not a single Russian sorcerer out there?" said Charleston.

      \n

      "I happen to know there are at least fourteen. Happily, five of them are in prison."

      \n

      "Thirteen," said Charleston. "You're welcome."

      \n

      "I suppose you are good for something then. Well done. There are also all the German sorcerers they took at the end of the war...well, don't trouble about that; it's all classified."

      \n

      "You don't make it easy to contact you," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "Of course not! I'm the head of a secret government organization!"

      \n

      "Am I just to scream in the air?"

      \n

      "The existence of Majestic-12 is a Top Secret. Still we have our feelers out\u2014"

      \n

      "Literal feelers?" said Charleston.

      \n

      "Every the droll one, Mr. Chiu."

      \n

      "Let's not lose sight of what is important! Irony! Irony! And a good sense of humor\u2014"

      \n

      "How is he seeing?" said Mina to Jimmy. "If he can see again that's probably very bad."

      \n

      "It's variable."

      \n

      "Well. I will remind Mr. Chiu of something I said in an earlier encounter: you've done well, in that nobody very important is dead. I take it Mr. Lund did not come back with you?"

      \n

      "No," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "And Mr. Lalin?"

      \n

      "He's where he wanted to be."

      \n

      \xa0

      \nEpisode IV: Came So Far For Beauty (Part 21)\n

      They were all confined to the tent, but made as comfortable as the situation allowed. The soldiers and some agents in civilian clothes were interviewing the townsfolk. Temperance saw Joy standing in line on the green, clutching her children to her. The snowfall had stopped, although it was still much colder than normal.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Mina sat down next to Temperance. "I know your mother doesn't think very highly of me anymore," she began without preamble. "Understand that we had to do what we had to do, and quite honestly there was nobody more qualified than me for the job. I do intend to look for ambitious and able young women for my organization; it's still a man's world, whatever darkness leaks in. The President always wants us to take on another FBI agent or a lunkhead from the Marines. This is my card. I think we could use someone like you."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      The next day the Majestic-12 agents dumped them in the middle of Los Angeles. "It would be my suggestion," said Mina in absence of farewell, "that you don't stay around much longer."

      \n

      "That's always your suggestion," muttered Jimmy. He went to a soda shop to call Governor Grey.

      \n

      "How is it going?" he barked when the call went through.

      \n

      "Technically good because we succeeded," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "Really? I've got some weirdo Fed organization going over every scrap of paper in Sacramento."

      \n

      "Don't mind them. We stopped something terrible from coming into the world."

      \n

      "Do you think its over?"

      \n

      "No."

      \n

      "That's what I thought. I have a letter for you. Let me know where to send it."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      "I'm so sorry you lost your dog, Mr. Wright...should I call you Jimmy?" said Beth when he got back to the RV.

      \n

      "Most people do.

      \n

      "We haven't talked about that kiss yet. It's...all right if you don't find me attractive." She straightened her sweater nervously.

      \n

      "Look, you're a very attractive woman," Jimmy began. He saw Beth wince.

      \n

      "It's all right, Jimmy. I saw you with Janet. I like her books. I think one of the characters is based on you. I just...if I can help you I want to do so. I don't think what Percy started is over. I don't know anything about this life, so...if you can use a gal Friday I can do that."

      \n

      "You're going to get yourself into something you regret."

      \n

      "I already have. Good night, Mr. J."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      The next day he got the letter the Governor had mentioned:

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Cher James,

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      I know it has been a very long time. I have not tried to contact you\u2026because I know you have needed to be alone. I of course can understand, mon cher; there have been times I too have sought solitude\u2026

      \n

      I think by now you must be very tired. May I offer the hospitality of my home for the holidays? Francis is out of the country for a few months, and I am staying in our place in New Orleans. I would love to see you and catch up. Please bring anyone you like; the house is large, and of course we have no children to fill it. Perhaps your old friend Janet (and if you see her do let her know I enjoy her books!)

      \n

      Please come. It has been far too long. Those of us who faced the fire thirty years ago are slowly slipping from the Earth. I dearly wish to see you again, and to usher in the New Year with someone who was kind to me.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Yours very affectionately,

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Isabelle O\u2019Donnell.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      The truck was one of those vehicles that looked old the day they were made. It rumbled through the darkness, splashing mud as it wallowed in the dirt road. Rain fell in great sheets, and lightning flashed on the distant hills.\xa0

      \n

      In the cab, the driver petted his old basset hound and hummed a song he'd heard on the radio the other day; one of those new jazz pieces that had gotten so popular since the doughboys came home. He took another swig of Canadian whisky from his flask.

      \n

      Somebody walked out into the road in front of him.

      \n

      He slammed on the brakes, frantically downshifting as she stood senseless of her danger in the glare of the headlights. The truck skidded and shook to a stop less than a foot from what he saw now was a woman. She was wearing a white gown of some kind, with heavy ropes of chains and pendants hanging from her neck. Her back was to him, and he saw her reach up and unfasten something from her face.\xa0

      \n

      He rolled down the window. "Are you all right, miss? You better come inside and get dry."

      \n

      She stumbled in a daze to the other side of the truck and after a moment yanked open the door and climbed inside. "Don't mind ol' Jim there," said the man. "He's just an old coon dog." Jim bayed softly.

      \n

      The woman slowly turned to look at him, eyes blank and expressionless. "...dog..." she said.

      \n

      "Yeah, dog." The woman switched her empty gaze to him and he shuddered for some reason. "I don't know what your problem is, ma'am, but you're not the only one with troubles tonght. There's a big blackout in Los Angeles, power's down all over the area. Everything's all messed up. Hell of a way to start 1926, you ask me, two weeks in and we have this. Them's all messed up in that town."

      \n

      She blinked again, and then smiled. Her face seemed to change, become warmer, more open, more recognizable. "Like she pulled on a mask or something," he told his wife later, and shuddered when he did; the change was so sudden and severe.

      \n

      The strange woman leaned forward and petted Jim. "I thank you so kindly for the help," she said, in a voice with the same flat Oklahoma twang he had. "My head was just not here yet. Y'all can call me Cassie."

      \n
      \n And I'm back! Long delay on getting the transcript for Episode 5 done. (To be fair, I'm also behind on Episode 6, alas.) This mostly has to do with real life, prep for the two final sessions...and, well, some of these episodes aren't all that satisfying to me, personally. They went over fine, folks had a good time; but the middle act just didn't gel all that well in my eyes. There were also some creative clashes that resulted in one PC leaving the campaign.

      But onward. Starting in Episode 8 I largely began writing my own scenarios, using some elements from published adventures (most especially Graham Walmsey's fine The Final Revelation) and things...improved a bit, although they remained somewhat railroady. This is a problem with the campaign as a design and my own GMing style in it; and it gave me some grief, which is another reason the middle sessions weren't quite up to my own standards, with the exception of the rollicking Episode 7.

      All that said, everyone is enjoying the game quite a bit and I feel like we've earned its incredibly grim potential denouement.

      Episode V is based on Oscar Rios' neat little New Orleans confection "Song and Dance" with some influence from "Tell Me, Have You Seen the Yellow Sign" by Kevin Ross.

      \n
      \nAct II: Lonesome Traveler (December 1955--October 1956)


      Episode V: A Singer Must Die (Part 1)\n
      \n

      Then read me the list of the crimes that are mine

      \nI will ask for the mercy that you love to decline\u2026
      \u2014Leonard Cohen
      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      The townhouse of Isabelle O'Donnell was in the French Quarter of New Orleans: an old brick building with a balcony running around the second floor. It was decorated in a tasteful mixture of old Louisianan and modern French styles. Local wags liked to insinuate that it had once been a bordello, but in truth it was nothing more romantic than a repurposed warehouse.

      \n

      Jimmy and his friends had arrived in the middle of the month, with Temperance\u2019s two half-siblings, Rodolfo and Charlotte (everyone called them Rudy and Charlie) in tow; they had been inflicted on her by her mother, who needed some time off. Typical.

      \n

      It was a warm Christmas, but that seemed restful after the unseasonable (and alien) cold they had encountered in California. Mrs. O'Donnell was a charming hostess, with a small but dedicated staff of servants, and they made sure to give the best a Southern Christmas could offer to Jimmy and his friends. As a present, Candace gave Temperance an invisible ink pen.

      \n

      "A girl has secrets," she said.

      \n

      The day after Boxing Day, Jimmy found himself drinking coffee with Isabelle in the parlor. She preferred her coffee strong enough to chip paint off a battleship; she apologized to him about it, noting that her condition only allowed her to taste the strongest flavors.

      \n

      "Actually, I was going to ask for a bigger cup," said Jimmy. "No need to explain. Seems you're doing well."

      \n

      "Francis is away from home more than I would like. Do you remember Seamus and Sean, who worked for that Irish newspaper in Paris? They're both here as well; Seamus has a small farm outside the city, and Sean lives in town. They both married lovely American girls and have families...of course, they have to deal with their own condition, but the children did not inherit it."

      \n

      "It's a full moon tomorrow, right?"

      \n

      "Don't worry about it. Are you working on something? I've heard rumors."

      \n

      "Bradley dragged me into something."

      \n

      "Should I be worried?"

      \n

      "It involves the King in Yellow."

      \n

      "Oh dear. I read that play once. Very boring."

      \n

      "In the course of events we found ourselves in Carcosa. We escaped..."

      \n

      "I hope you did. Carcosa is a city that tries to hold onto its secrets. Ah, well. If you would like help with your costumes for the ball tomorrow, I have a wonderful woman who can make them for you and your friends. They are such charming people. Beth reminds me of someone, but I don't know who...ah, Freddy's friend. Sheila. Abigail. Audrey..."

      \n

      "I hope she doesn't follow her into attempted murder..."

      \n

      "If we are fair, she only attempted to murder Freddie," said Isabelle with a grin.

      \n

      "I hope not to be Freddie in this. By the way, do you know Etienne Laurent de Marigny?"

      \n

      "Etienne? Oh, yes. He's mostly retired these days...well, I suppose as retired as you. I would be happy to make an introduction. He is very knowledgeable about things...such as what you are looking into."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Temperance was at Mass that morning. Of course she was. Beyond her ordinary devotion, she wanted to be around people who were quiet, respectful, and sane.

      \n

      She went to weekday Mass a lot.

      \n

      She was listening the offertory music\u2014one of the reasons she liked this church was the beautiful organ music they played\u2014but today she couldn't help notice that the music sounded strangely...discordant. She glanced around her. She seemed to be the only person who had noticed.

      \n

      The music stopped and she felt as if someone was watching her. She turned and saw the organist descending from his loft. He was tall, thin, and extremely pale, with a bald head that gleamed in the light. She caught his gaze and was astonished by the look of pure hate he shot at her. She watched as he swept in his black cassock to a side door and vanished.

      \n

      After the benediction, she pushed her way through the crowd. She saw the organist following her, so she walked quickly to a bench at a bus stop. She sat down next to an empty space as an invitation.

      \n

      A bus drove by, blocking her view of the opposite side of the street. When it drove away, she suddenly saw the organist staring at her with that same venomous look.

      \n

      [This was an actual Stability Test here, a somewhat rare mechanic in my games. This encounter is of course based on the Chambers short stor \u201cThe Court of the Dragon\u201d]

      \n

      She jumped up and began to cross the street. The man turned away and began walking rapidly up the street. She tailed him as close as she dared, and she saw him turn down an alley.

      \n

      She followed. The alley was blind, with no exit; but she didn't see him anywhere as she walked down it. She turned around.

      \n

      The man was standing at the entrance of the alley. He began to move toward her.

      \n

      "Who are you and what do you want?" she demanded.

      \n

      He kept moving forward in silence. She pulled out her gun. "I won't fire a warning shot!" she said.

      \n

      He kept moving, silently, toward her. He raised his arms as he got near.

      \n

      She shot him through the heart. He kept moving, wrapping his hands around her throat with shocking strength. As she dropped her gun and saw blackness coming in from the edges of her vision, the man whispered in a horrible voice edged with malice and full of the subsonics of despair, "It is a frightful thing to fall into the hands of the Living God..."

      \n

      She awoke with a start. She was sitting in her pew; she had dropped her missalette. The elderly Creole woman next to her was giving her a disapproving stare for having fallen asleep during Mass.

      \n

      \nEpisode V: A Singer Must Die (Part 2)\n

      Charleston had been spending the holiday trying to worm his way into the local occult community. As expected, it was large in New Orleans, but very clannish and fractured. The intricacies of the Southern racial castes also threw him; he wasn't familiar with the differences between Creoles, whites, and blacks. But his work had uncovered two young scions of black Creole families who were expected at Isabelle's ball: Collette Lamar and Nicole Savoy.

      \n

      The balls! They were going to be his best bet to meet the occult society of the city, for the last four days of the year were filled with four of them, on successive nights, the Bals d'Indulgences: the Bal des Innocents tomorrow night, where young occult New Orleansians made their debut; the Bal des Debauches, where anything might and often did happen; the Bal des Mortes, a rather sedate black tie affair mostly dedicated to planning for the next year; and finally the Bal des Monstres on New Year's Eve, the only one attended by "normal" citizens of the Crescent City.

      \n

      They sounded like quite a party...on any number of levels.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Candace spent much of her time with Jack Kerouac and Neal Cassady, who had helped drive out from California. They took her on a whirlwind tour of the dives and low areas of the city, introducing her to other writers and getting her howlingly drunk and high on life and chemicals. One of the writers she met was their friend Bill Burroughs, a dour-faced tall man who was an obvious hophead. They talked shop.

      \n

      "My current novel is something very different from my first book," said Candace. "I feel I've really evolved."

      \n

      "I'm working on something very big," said Burroughs. "I'll probably have to cut it down for publication...if it is even publishable."

      \n

      "Oh, it should be published in its full form."

      \n

      "It would be too long and nobody would understand it."

      \n

      "Does anyone really understand the heart of a writer?"

      \n

      "How perceptive. You should maybe visit me in Morocco sometime."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Sam had returned to them somewhat unexpectedly, showing up without preamble just before they'd left California. Now he was working on digging up some information on the members of Project TAROT; he'd been in Paperclip, and hoped he might uncover some stuff, especially about Barbara Miller, who seemed to have been Percy's number two. He invited Jimmy to have a drink with him and talk over what they knew.

      \n

      "We should check out that place that the second ball is going to be at," said Sam. "This Caf\xe9 Hippolyte."

      \n

      Jimmy winced. "I don't trust places with names like that. It's probably just a coincidence. Let's just go someplace close." Sam shrugged and they walked over to a corner bar.

      \n

      "I want to talk about Percy," said Sam when they had gotten settled. "Been a while since we talked about him."

      \n

      "Yes, what with him no longer being human."

      \n

      "A lot has happened since we were in Vegas. I've been working...on various projects."

      \n

      "I think he was trying to find a way into Carcosa."

      \n

      "Why would anyone want to find a way there?"

      \n

      "I am not one of those people, so I can't explain."

      \n

      "There are a lot of realms it might be beneficial to visit," said Sam with visible longing in his eyes, "but I don't think Carcosa is one of them."

      \n

      "Carcosa...shapes itself to whoever creates it. I don't know exactly how that works, whether or not there are multiple phases of it..."

      \n

      "Does that mean that if you or I create Carcosa it would be our own?"

      \n

      "It would be different. Amadou stayed there and his was different than Percy's."

      \n

      "Is it possible to create multiple Carcosas? Or is there only one at a time?"

      \n

      "My grasp on physics has been passed by theory."

      \n

      "What I am saying is that maybe we could create a better Carcosa of our own..."

      \n

      "We are talking about eldritch beings. I doubt there is a better Carcosa. Maybe a less bad one. Amadou wrote a book about it, The Wanderer on the Lake I think. Temperance has a copy. But you'll have to deal with the god Hastur if you try this; he always comes at the end of the night."

      \n

      "What if we could create our own Carcosas, in our own image? Maybe we could avoid these mistakes."

      \n

      Jimmy looked at him a bit incredulously, and finished his drink quickly.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Temperance came awake quickly to the sound of muffled screams. She flipped on the light and looked across the room to the other bed. Beth was rolling in an agitated fashion under the covers; suddenly she sat bolt upright and said, "No!" in a loud voice. She blinked painfully in the light. Without her glasses she looked far away and lost.

      \n

      "Sorry," she said. "I was having a bad dream. People were trying to kill me. There was this horrible man. He had something wrong with his face...no...wait...he wasn't bad." She shook her head. "I don't remember."

      \n

      "I had a terrible dream last, uh, night," said Temperance, hurrying past the lie.

      \n

      "Didn't those actors say they had bad dreams after they made the movie? Is that happening to us?"

      \n

      "Maybe it's just nerves. It has been quite an ordeal."

      \n

      "What are you going to wear to the ball tomorrow?"

      \n

      "I went out with Rudy and Charlie today," said Temperance, referring to her half-siblings who were visiting from California. "I picked us all out something special."

      \n

      "Can't wait to see it," said Beth drowsily.

      \n
      \n
      \n

      \nEpisode V: A Singer Must Die (Part 3)\n

      The next night the first Ball was held at Isabelle's house. Candace came dressed as Calliope, Muse of Epic Poetry: a long white chiton and a crown of tinsel leaves. Temperance was dressed as Wonder Woman. Rudy was dressed as Batman and Charlie as Robin.

      \n

      "We always thought of you as a bit of prude," said Charlie approvingly. "No fun...pious...it's really strange that you're not Geronimo's daughter, actually."

      \n

      [TP: Two Sanity points ago Temperance wouldn't dress like that. But now she's okay with showing some skin around you deviants!]

      \n

      Jimmy was dressed in a tuxedo and an incredibly detailed mask of a rabbit. "Private joke," he said to Beth. Who was dressed as Alice in Wonderland.

      \n

      "Why is one hand bandaged?"

      \n

      "I'm the rest of rabbit."

      \n

      Sam came out in a white lab coat and a thick German accent. "Von Braun!" exclaimed Beth with a cackle. "Oh, that's great! He's such an asshole!"

      \n

      Charleston came dressed as the 1930s serial version of Buck Rogers. "Deep cut," he explained to anyone who asked, and then got annoyed when so few people asked.

      \n

      Isabelle O'Donnell was dressed as the Bride of Frankenstein, which caused Jimmy to chuckle. "Private joke," he explained again to Beth. Her two associates Seamus and Sean arrived wearing puppy dog masks\u2014another private joke.

      \n

      "How'ye doin', yeh old bastid?" said Seamus. "I heard you died."

      \n

      "Heard that too," said Sean. "In Kilkenny."

      \n

      "I heard Cork," said Seamus.

      \n

      "I'm still kicking," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "Thought the Germans would have blown you up, or the Japanese."

      \n

      "Or the Americans, ta be fair," put in Sean.

      \n

      "There were always a bit of explosions nearby, but I managed to keep out of the blast radius."

      \n

      "I see ye brought crazypants," said Seamus, pointing at Charleston.

      \n

      "He's a little...less unhinged."

      \n

      "That still leaves a lot of room between him and sane. He doesn't still think he's a preacher man a' color anymore, do he?"

      \n

      "The less said about that the better. I hear you're both family men now?"

      \n

      "Aye, they're all wonderful. Here are the gals now. They know about our condition, but American girls, they're acceptin' of most anything."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Isabelle, who was at core a Frenchwoman of the 1920s, had a small jazz band playing in the corner and was steadfastly ignoring how Charlie had spiked the punch. Candace saw two young black Creoles come in dressed as muses.

      \n

      "Which one are you," said one of them to her.

      \n

      "Calliope."

      \n

      "Oh, good. I'm Euterpe and this is Terpsichore. Or Collette Lamar and Nicole Savoy, if you prefer." Their costumes were immaculate, gorgeous white gowns, their black curls piled high into an elaborate hairstyle that included small masks as part of the effect. "You're not from here originally, are you?"

      \n

      "Boston," said Candace, suddenly self-conscious about her accent.

      \n

      "We're hoping to win the contest tonight. If we do we get to set the costume theme for our krewe this year, the Krewe Janus. What do you do?"

      \n

      "I'm a writer."

      \n

      "How appropriate!" The girls exchanged a knowing glance that Candace could read: we're pulling this off better than you.

      \n

      Helen picked Charleston's sleeve. "Over there," she hissed. "Them two girls you were interested in. Why don't you use those eyes of yours, now that you've got them again?"

      \n

      "It's our secret, my dear," he replied, looking at her over his dark glasses. They're only for you."

      \n

      "I do like you in green."

      \n

      Charleston ambled over, clutching the "ray gun" he'd made out of an old coffee can. "Hello, ladies."

      \n

      "Wow," said Nicole. "I haven't seen anyone do Flash Gordon in a long time."

      \n

      "Flash...yes. well, nothing like the classics. Everything old is new again."

      \n

      Nicole noticed his glasses for the first time and was a bit abashed, but Charleston waved it off with a smile. "Well, I'm the Muse of Song, so you only need to hear me," she said, smiling.

      \n

      Indeed, said Charleston, he'd come to New Orleans for the music; he'd heard it was amazing. "Sans doute," said Nicole. Charleston asked if it was true that music could have profound effects.

      \n

      "Only if you listen to the right song," said Nicole. "I think everyone is going to be listening to us tonight, and we're going to win the contest."

      \n

      "I still think you should have gone as John Carter," said Helen to Charleston. "Where I'm from, he's huge. Half the kids dress up as him at Halloween."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Jimmy cruised the edges of the crowd. He saw Rudy trying to leave out the backdoor. He collared the kid.

      \n

      "Leggo, old man," said Rudy. He did a double-take. "Wait...are you that Jimmy? If you are, I heard you used to be a lot more interesting. And that you died in Topeka."

      \n

      "I've died in a lot of places, kid," said Jimmy, pulling Rudy back into the ballroom. It was almost midnight. He could see Nicole and Collette standing in the middle of the room, trying to get everyone's attention. They pulled their masks down over their faces...

      \n

      ...and collapsed in a dead faint. The music crashed to a halt. One of the musicians let his clarinet slip from lifeless fingers. "I can't play," he said in bewildered horror. "I got...nothing..."

      \n

      Candace felt as if some dark fog was washing in a horrid tide over her mind. The lights seemed to dim. She felt horrible, bereft: because all her inspiration seemed to have vanished in a moment, crushing her spirits under a vast weight. She saw Temperance stagger; clearly she'd felt the same thing happening.

      \n

      "I tasted it," she muttered. "Now it's gone. Ashes, ashes, my book is ashes..."

      \n

      Helen was weeping. She collapsed onto Charleston. "It's over, over, all gone...you wouldn't understand..."

      \n

      [This was a 3 point Stability loss to anyone with Art 1+]

      \n

      Sam was examining the girls. "Pulse weak and thready," he said to Charleston. "Fixed pupils. I probably have something for this."

      \n

      "I'm sure you do," muttered Charleston. He pulled off Collette's mask, but it had no effect.

      \n

      "Should we take them to the hospital?" said Isabelle.

      \n

      "We don't know what is wrong. You should get them someplace to lie down."

      \n

      "Absolutement." She waved at some servants, who carried the girls upstairs. "What do you think happened?"

      \n

      "Partying too hard? Too much excitement?"

      \n

      "I've lived here close to thirty years. I have seen partying. It doesn't usually end like this!"

      \n

      "So you want to start a panic?"

      \n

      "No! Of course not! You know how many people died the last time you started doing things like that?"

      \n

      "I don't have a number..."

      \n
      \n

      \nEpisode V: A Singer Must Die (Part 4)\n

      Temperance called around for a doctor\u2014Isabelle had one who was extremely discreet. He took several hours to arrive. "It has been quite a night young miss," he said when he finally arrived: a pleasant sounding man with silver hair. "Many calls came in quite suddenly. I've had two suicide attempts this evening."

      \n

      He examined the girls. "If I had to hazard a guess, I'd say they'd had a stroke."

      \n

      "Simultaneously?"

      \n

      "Perhaps they ingested some substance." Sam edged toward the door.

      \n

      Jimmy slipped behind Charleston. "I think these girls bit off more than they can chew. Can you see any...you know...woo-woo-woo stuff?"

      \n

      "Decades after decades of this stuff and its still woowoowoo stuff, eh?" Charleston opened his Third Eye. The room practically glowed with power: tendrils wrapped the two girls and spread out across the city.

      \n

      Jimmy studied his face. "So they did something stupid."

      \n

      "We may have an...unexpected guest." The girls had summoned something. But nothing that he was familiar with... "If I were to hazard a guess, they summoned a spirit to possess themselves or someone else. A loa, perhaps."

      \n

      "And this spirit came from where?" asked Sam.

      \n

      "Lots of places possible," muttered Jimmy.

      \n

      "I see two paths," said Charleston. "We can try to follow the trail back to what they summoned, or we can try to break the spell and release them. Unfortunately I don't know how to do either."

      \n

      They argued for a while about what to do, pointing out that they had put on masks...was that important? Or was it the time? Charleston left the amateurs and went to find Helen.

      \n

      He found her in her room. She had shot up all her supply of Yellow. And all his. He shook her awake.

      \n

      "It did nothing...nothing..." she croaked, and then passed out.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      The next day the newspapers were full of stories of the unexpected suicides of many local artists, and notices that every live act in the city was cancelled. The girls remained comatose.

      \n

      "We will have to play recorded music at the ball tonight," grumbled Isabelle over coffee, while the rest of them resumed their argument over what to do. Sam wanted to get some Yellow, so he and Charleston headed out to find some.

      \n

      They turned up a dealer by the levee. "Ain't none to sell you," he told them. "I got smack if you want that, but every grain of Yellow's been bought up. Can't find a gram of it anywhere in the city. Didn't seem to help them; they kept coming back for more."

      \n

      Back at the townhouse, Beth pointed out that things were a) terrible b) the kind of thing that Percy would have been interested in and c) a chance to do a very interesting natural experiment. Jimmy shook his head and he and Charleston went to talk to the Lamar and Savoy families, who were sitting nervously in the parlor.

      \n

      Jimmy raised the question of searching the girls' rooms back at their homes.

      \n

      Mrs. Lamar was indignant. These girls were not common musicians; there could be no reason for them to be affected in the same way as those misfits. And if they had taken something, it would certainly not be in her room, would it?

      \n

      "There are people who are dying and if I have to tear apart your house I will do it," he growled back.

      \n

      [Intimidate spend by JP.]

      \n

      Everyone trooped over to the Lamar and Savoy houses. It was soon apparent to Candace that the families were voodoo aristocracy of New Orleans. Jimmy found Nicole's diary in the very clever spot nobody would ever look, in the closet. There wasn't much there; just that both girls were very excited to come to the ball...and they had been spending a great deal of time at the Caf\xe9 Hippolyte.

      \n

      [Occult for Candace\u2019s clue, Notice for Jimmy\u2019s.]

      \n

      Charleston had somewhat better luck; he confirmed that they had done some kind of summoning; as near as he could figure, they were using a modification of a loa spell to channel the essence of the Grecian muses.

      \n

      "Good thing we're going to the Caf\xe9 Hippolyte tonight," he said brightly to Jimmy, who shuddered.

      \n

      \nEpisode V: A Singer Must Die (Part 5)\n

      The Caf\xe9 was a clean, glowing space in the French Quarter, lacking pretension but full of atmosphere. Cabaret tables were strewn around the room; there was a wet bar and a coffee bar. And on the stage was a woman who was singing.

      \n

      She had a caf\xe9 au lait complexion and was wearing a sparkling champagne-colored evening gown, singing blues standards without any accompaniment. She was probably the only performer in New Orleans this evening, Temperance thought to herself. It was difficult to track her musical style since she was singing a cappella, but she was sure that the singer wasn't always using normal Western tonality.

      \n

      [Art History.]

      \n

      Candace dropped heavily onto a barstool. The saloonkeeper, a youngish looking woman with her hair in a flapper's bob, drifted over. "What can I get you, honey?"

      \n

      Candace sighed. "What's the specialty of the house?" she said without any enthusiasm.

      \n

      "Depends. You want to feel awake, or good?"

      \n

      "Good. I want to feel good."

      \n

      "Then hurricanes all around. My name's Hypatia; I run this place."

      \n

      "Beautiful name."

      \n

      "Certainly a storied one. What do you do?"

      \n

      Candace indicated she was a writer, and mentioned the new book she was working on. "Probably not going too well today," said Hypatia.

      \n

      "Taking a break."

      \n

      "You and everyone else in the city, except for Queenie here. She's...unusual."

      \n

      "Her music sounds experimental."

      \n

      "You could say that. Seems to me that someone has their eye on you\u2014nobody here. You're missing someone, aren't you?"

      \n

      "My husband. But it hasn't bothered me for a while."

      \n

      "Men, right? But it's somebody else. Don't worry. You'll be fine."

      \n

      "I can handle it."

      \n

      "I said the exact same thing once," said Hypatia, lighting a cigarette in a long ivory holder. "Different party than the one you're dealing with. And you know what? I was right."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Charleston ordered some coffee\u2014dark as night, plenty of cream and sugar\u2014and sat down to watch Queenie singing. With his second sight, he could tell that she wasn't affected by whatever was plaguing the city; it was as if she could draw inspiration from another source. He sipped his coffee meditatively and gave a standing ovation when she finished her set.

      \n

      Jimmy was asking the waitresses about Nicole and Colette; they had both been regulars, often talking to the boss: "She's a great supporter of young women," one said breathlessly.

      \n

      Sam was chatting up the drug dealers. "Yellow is impossible to get," they told him. It wasn't lack of will; it was just that every poet, dancer, singer and musician in the city had tried to score. "I'd charge you a hundred bucks a hit if I could," one said. "And I would. But there's none to be had."

      \n

      "Surely you have more coming in," said Sam.

      \n

      The supply chain was very chaotic, it seemed; the dealers were contacted by their source, never the other way around. But they didn't care, since the markup was so high.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Temperance was sitting at the coffee bar. A woman in a bob haircut came by to freshen her cup. "Hypatia Masters," she said.

      \n

      [Yup, the same from Masks of Nyarlathotep. As I am not a fan of her fate in that campaign, when I ran it I made into some kind of powerful figure, having made a deal with Nyarlathotep\u2026somehow.]

      \n

      "Temperance."

      \n

      "Well-named. But don't you ever want to just let go? When I was your age, I used to hit every jazz club in New York."

      \n

      "I can understand. I've been to several clubs recently. Jazz is becoming a hobby for me."

      \n

      "A hobby? Listen, I understand you want to do things temperately if you will, but jazz is not something you can do by half-measures. You either got to give yourself to it or not bother."

      \n

      "I've heard a lot of artists say that, but I don't know what they mean."

      \n

      "You don't know...have you ever cared about anything in your life?"

      \n

      "Of course. I love the arts..."

      \n

      "I know, I know. You go into a museum and stare at paintings. But do you paint yourself?"

      \n

      "Once or twice. I have a sketchbook..."

      \n

      "Art isn't all inspiration. Leonardo worked his ass off, and I would know."

      \n

      "Are you a...fan of his?" asked Temperance, twigging to the last part of what Hypatia had said.

      \n

      "Very much. I don't think he was a fan of me. A homosexual is what I mean."

      \n

      "I've met some of them recently too."

      \n

      "Just met? Quelle dommage. Oh, sweetheart. No half-measures! I mean, I know you go to church, but are you going to church because you really believe, or because you're Catholic and works not faith and all."

      \n

      "How do you know I go to..."

      \n

      "It's all over your face. I can smell the incense coming off of you. It's not a good look. Haven't you ever danced? Haven't you ever kissed someone? Haven't you\u2014oh my God, you haven't! I didn't think they still made 24 year old virgins. I can help you. I will help you! I said I wouldn't do this anymore but..." She touched Temperance on the lips with one finger. "Say no more."

      \n

      \nEpisode V: A Singer Must Die (Part 6)\n

      While he was clapping, Charleston felt Hypatia loom up behind him. "Oh Chuckles," she said. "You're so naked."

      \n

      "Trying to appreciate this."

      \n

      "Which part are you trying to appreciate?"

      \n

      "That she can still perform at all. Tremendous. Tremendous!"

      \n

      "What are you doing in my club? You know I throw people like you out."

      \n

      "You're acting like it was my fault that your place in Paris got blown up."

      \n

      "No, that was Eddie."

      \n

      "He got his."

      \n

      "I know. I keep track of these things. But you hung up your sorcerer's license when you came in here."

      \n

      "Hung it up long ago."

      \n

      "If you want to talk to Queenie, you have five minutes."

      \n

      "I see the relationship here."

      \n

      Hypatia frowned. "She needed a place to sing, I let her sing here. I look out for ladies, somebody has to."

      \n

      "I could actually use your advice about\u2014" began Charleston.

      \n

      "Your little extradimensional friend?" She nodded at Helen.

      \n

      "Yeah. She's not doing so well, and my backup plan...well, that wasn't going to work either."

      \n

      "I have ideas...but I'm having trouble getting past the part where you're helping people." She shook her head. "Never understood what the Boss saw in you. Look, whatever is happening now, it's probably not permanent. If you really care about this girl\u2014which is again blowing my mind\u2014then you should prepare for crisis management when this wears off. Unless you want to send her back. You know who you have to ask for that."

      \n

      "I don't want to send her anywhere. She's in a bad spot, I want to see her through it. Isn't there a pill? A song I could sing? That's like our bag. You telling me we can't do anything with this crap?"

      \n

      Hypatia looked at her watch. "Not yet."

      \n

      "When?"

      \n

      "A couple of hours."

      \n

      "And then everything is going to be better?"

      \n

      "Remember who I work for. Nothing is ever going to stay the same. But how it goes is up to you. I'm not in charge of this trip."

      \n

      Charleston wandered backstage, muttering to himself, and stepped into Queenie's dressing room. She was taking off her makeup. Her wig hung on a nail beside the large illuminated mirror she was sitting in front of. "Can I help you?" she said.

      \n

      "You already have," enthused Charleston. "That was absolutely lovely, on a day when I needed to hear a song."

      \n

      "Yeah, lots of people needed to hear a song," said Queenie absently.

      \n

      "Is that a Kansas City sound I heard? Reminded me when I was a kid in the Twenties. Those were very special days to me. I met a lot of people who were important in my life while in jazz clubs. The music might be different, but I got the same feeling listening to you. Especially with everyone down in the dumps. I think you might be the only one singing in the entire city. If I may be so bold, how could others find inspiration?"

      \n

      "Everyone's inspiration is personal to them. Mine is...well, I ran away from home. So it's to keep running. And I like being around young people, play a lot of college towns."

      \n

      Charleston asked how long she had been in New Orleans. Not long, and probably not staying long either. She was supposed to sing tomorrow though, at the same place. Hypatia had been very good to her, had protected her.

      \n

      "From what you're running from? Forgive me, that was gauche. You ever record?"

      \n

      Her sound wasn't commercial enough to record, she said. "If you're trying to pick me up, it's probably not going to work."

      \n

      "I wasn't even thinking that way."

      \n

      "Generally men who come in my room talking about recording\u2014"

      \n

      "Just wanted to know if you had anything I could buy to listen to. I have a friend who is really down and I'm not sure how to give her back her inspiration."

      \n

      "She a runaway too? Yes? Probably you should just try to support her. Now if you don't mind, I need to change."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      At midnight, the party was barely limping along. Even with recorded music, most people weren't interested in dancing. If it wasn't for the orgy, it would have been a very boring party indeed. Bored and embarrassed, Temperance decided to accept Hypatia's offer to read her cards for her.

      \n

      Of course when Hypatia cut the deck, she showed the major Arcana card Temperance. This did not impress Miss Murphy, who knew how to stack a deck cold.

      \n

      "What do you want to know: what's gonna happen, who you are, or what you're gonna be?" said Hypatia, shuffling the cards rapidly.

      \n

      "Who I'll be," said Temperance lazily.

      \n

      [The possibilities were to gain a point of Cthulhu Mythos, rewrite one statement, or have a vision.]

      \n

      Nicole and Collette suddenly walked into the Caf\xe9. They were still wearing their Grecian dresses. Collette began to sing:

      \n
      \n

      Strange is the night when the black stars rise

      \nAnd strange moons circle in the skies
      But stranger still
      Is lost Carcosa...
      \n

      They were none of them exactly sure what happened next. Time passed. They danced. They all danced, with abandon, with joy, with ecstasy. Outside bands wandered the street, playing music, followed by long lines of singing and swaying people.

      \n

      Candace came to her senses first. She felt flooded with inspiration and ran out the door, racing for the townhouse and the typewriter.

      \n

      Jimmy paused in mid-step. He was standing on the bar next to Beth. "I don't know how to shuffle off to Buffalo," he muttered. He leapt down gracefully and helped her to the floor.

      \n

      "Were we just doing something from a Gene Kelly flick?" she said. Jimmy shrugged.

      \n

      Charleston was dancing with Helen, doing, of course, the Charleston. He thought he had left her back at Isabelle's. "How are you feeling?" he asked.

      \n

      "Great. I wrote a poem. I wrote three poems, actually. Wait a minute. Four. I wrote one on your back."

      \n

      "I was wondering why I wasn't wearing a shirt or pants."

      \n

      "Maybe we should not let that go to waste," she leered.

      \n

      Crisis management, thought Charleston.

      \n

      [So everyone with any points in Art suddenly got a bonus pool that refilled daily...but they also had a strong urge to make art immediately and constantly...]

      \n

      Temperance flagged down a barmaid, who was humming loudly to herself. "Where did Nicole and Collette go?" she asked her.

      \n

      "Hrm," she said. "They're not backstage...wait, I know! I think they left when that impromptu parade started. Or maybe they began it. Anyway, I've been singing all night."

      \n

      "That's great." She raced over to Hypatia. "You see Nicole and Collette\u2014"

      \n

      "Yes. And since you're going to ask, I don't know where they went. Down Bourbon Street, followed by a lot of people. You all right? Your pencil hand keeps twitching."

      \n

      "Yes, yes it does." She tried to push the urge to draw out of her head. She sped away to Jimmy. "Mr. Wright!"

      \n

      "Hello, Temperance."

      \n

      "I have a job for you. Follow the crowd. Find the girls. Keep Sam away from them, he wants to put them in a cage. Something involving chicken wire."

      \n

      "A Faraday cage?"

      \n

      "Whatever. I have something important to do." She turned and practically skipped out the door.

      \n

      When she got back to the townhouse, she found Van playing remarkably beautiful music on the piano in the parlor. She sat down on the couch with her sketchbook, drawing while he played.

      \n

    The Unanswered Question (a Tatters of the King remix) [Trail of Cthulhu]

    \n
    \xab12345\xbb

    Comments

      \n
    • \n
      \n

      \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJune 2017 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode V: A Singer Must Die (Part 7)\n

      If the previous day had been one of a dolorous lack of joy in New Orleans, today was the day when there were literally people singing on the street. Candace and Helen were both busy at their typewriters; neither had stopped since they had come home, and neither came down to have breakfast with Jimmy and Isabelle.

      \n

      "I tried to get Van to stop playing. He threatened me. With a knife," sighed Isabelle. "I took it from him, but maybe it's best to let him play. And Temperance will need a new sketchbook soon. If you want to talk to Etienne, I spoke to him and he'd be happy to meet you."

      \n

      "I would definitely like that," said Jimmy. "I'll take Sam and Charleston. They seem the least affected."

      \n

      Isabelle shook her head. "Who would have thought?"

      \n

      Etienne Laurent de Marigny lived not far away in the Quarter. They walked over, and let the aged African-American butler take their coats. He led them into a drawing room that was wall to wall bookshelves, stuffed with obscure items, charts, vials, bottled specimens, and a hundred other things they couldn't recognize.

      \n

      Etienne was sitting behind a desk covered with high stacks of paper. He was somewhere in his seventies, an elegant white-haired man, portly, with sweeping mustaches in the French style. "Mr. Wright, please forgive me for not having introduced myself earlier," he said. "I believe we are both in a similar field. I am aware of many of your accomplishments. Dr. Acererak, I am familiar with your questing. My son and his friend Titus are more in that line. I wish you well. A friend of mine attempted to get into that realm. Perhaps you know him: Randolph Carter?"

      \n

      "Honored, I think," said Sam.

      \n

      "Mr. Chiu," continued de Marigny. He paused. "The less said the better."

      \n

      "I feel people treat me as a lot less approachable than I am," groused Charleston.

      \n

      "Your reputation from the Twenties and Thirties does tend to prejudice people, I think."

      \n

      "There certainly was less prejudice back then."

      \n

      "Touch\xe9. So, gentlemen, you have been in touch with my friend Carl Simon. And I have corresponded with Mr. Bacon in San Francisco, although my letters are being returned now. Probably for the best. Mr. Bacon is closer to what people think Mr. Chiu is like than Mr. Chiu. He was interested in the King in Yellow\u2014not just the play, but other manifestations of that entity..."

      \n

      "Such as?" said Charleston.

      \n

      "If one were to consult the Seven Cryptical Books of Hsan (of which I happen to be a translator) one would find many references to the Yellow Emperor of Chinese legend, enough that the King and Emperor may be the same. Certainly history shows the rising and falling influence of Aldebaran on the affairs of this planet."

      \n

      "We managed to stop a ritual about that," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "You are to be commended. The release of Hastur upon this world...well, I shudder to think about the effects it might have on our society. We already teeter on the edge of paranoia; the influence of the King tends to push things in that direction."

      \n

      "Is what's happening now part of that influence?"

      \n

      "I'm not sure. I think our young ladies may have made an...error. We may reliably conjecture that they dabbled with Yellow."

      \n

      "So did every artist in this city," said Sam.

      \n

      "It has a potent effect on the artistic. It allows the spirit to wander."

      \n

      "But how is it that these ladies were able to experience this phenomenon when everyone else is bereft of inspiration?"

      \n

      "We are under the influence of Aldebaran. My friend Carl has his own theories...but for our purposes, I propose that if one's spirit wanders under such circumstances, it runs the risk of being forced into the pattern. The pattern of the play."

      \n

      "So they have entered Carcosa?"

      \n

      "They may be re-enacting roles. There are always two ladies. There is always the King. And always a Stranger. However, I think there may have been a stronger influence here: some personage that might be closely connected to Carcosa?"

      \n

      "I know that some people in this room have been there," said Sam. Etienne paled visibly.

      \n

      "I was doing my best to avoid saying anything about that," growled Jimmy.

      \n

      "I'm sorry, I didn't get the memo."

      \n

      "Would you be interested in seeing an artifact of Carcosa?" said Charleston. He held out the mask, Noor's mask, that he had taken from the city.

      \n

      "I don't know what that is," said Etienne, puzzled. "It doesn't look like anything to me."

      \n

      [Fine, fine, I stole it from Westworld. But it's a good line.]

      \n

      "Part of its charm, I suppose," said Charleston suspiciously.

      \n

      "Well. You escaped from Carcosa, you say? Did you bring anyone with you?"

      \n

      "Of course not," said Charleston quickly.

      \n

      "Well. There may still be Carcosans on Earth. I have my own agents looking into that," said Etienne, patting a thick envelope, "when I have more answers I will let you know."

      \n

      "The King is the ruler of Carcosa?" said Sam.

      \n

      "That question is somewhat complicated."

      \n

      "But the person who creates Carcosa controls it. So maybe if we could make Carcosa, we could become the King."

      \n

      "You cannot become the King. He is not human. He is beyond human comprehension. The form we see him in is only the way our poor minds grasp him. You don't create Carcosa, sir. You can make it appear in your own image, but it is still Carcosa. It will still always be the same day."

      \n

      "We should stop talking about making it," said Jimmy. "We should be trying to reduce its influence on us."

      \n

      "But this is the time when we could become so much more! Why should we limit ourselves? Once we understand this, we could become\u2014"

      \n

      [TP: I want to thank you for being a Resident Evil villain.]

      \n

      "Gentlemen, I have my agents working on this problem," said Etienne, standing up and gently pushing them toward the door. Jimmy noticed he had a letter lying on the desk that was signed, unbelievably enough, Millicent Lowell. "There are many influences in New Orleans, from long before any white man saw this land. I think the ladies may have found a way to tap them. I would expect some incident at Mrs. O'Donnell's ball tonight."

      \n

      [Millicent was a PC in my run of Eternal Lies, which also included Jimmy of course.]

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n

      \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n

      \n\nJune 2017 \n
