      \n
      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode V: A Singer Must Die (Part 8)\n

      Temperance was curled up on the davenport, still sketching, when Van abruptly stopped playing piano. "I don't wanna stop," he mused, "but my hands can't take it anymore. Your hands look kinda clenched, I knew a cat like that. Drummer, his wrists got so bad he couldn't play. Anyway, I just did the entire Well Tempered Clavier and I'm out of ideas."

      \n

      "Yes," said Temperance, looking at her hands. "I ran out of ink a while ago, the only pen I have is this one Candace gave me."

      \n

      "That pen doesn't write, man."

      \n

      "Invisible ink."

      \n

      "Wow. That's brilliant, man. How would that work? Would the audience have some way of making it appear? That's ephemeral."

      \n

      "You can use black light on it. She gave it to me to write secrets in. But I don't have any."

      \n

      "Everyone's got some secrets."

      \n

      "You want to hear my life story?"

      \n

      "I'd love to hear it. Lay it on me."

      \n

      "Here's the pamphlet: left in an orphanage when I was little, my pa got me when I was 5, he kept up my education and the church. Most of my time has been spent with nuns or him. I like baseball and comic books, got educated a little in Europe, and through the Carlyles\u2014family friends\u2014I met the infamous Jimmy Wright."

      \n

      "Oh man, you should see the files my father keeps on that cat. I only read one, it was about an inch thick and labeled 1929-1930." He closed the piano lid and sat down on the couch next to her. "You probably know my story: born in California, my mom wanted to name me after my crazy dead uncle..."

      \n

      "Really?"

      \n

      "You never heard the story of Roger Vane Carlyle the First? Well. My family is very rich, armaments and chemicals. My grandparents died in a car accident, and even though Mom was the older sibling, times being what they was it all went to her brother Roger. Now, he was many things, including not very likely to produce an heir if you understand me. But he was not a good businessman. What he liked to do instead of that\u2014and maybe this is how I really am like him\u2014is run around to jazz clubs and bars, drinking and having a good time. He was just a kid, and running the company into the ground. Then he took up with some crazy people and got those heebie-jeebie visions. Next thing people know, he's lighting out for Egypt to be an archaeologist, like that cat Carter, him and all these crazies, Penhew, some kinda British noble, this cat Jack Brady, an ex-marine my uncle was close to, and this chick Hypatia. She was his beard, I think. So they go to Egypt and then Africa and they got themselves killed there."

      \n

      "Hypatia?" said Temperance sharply.

      \n

      "Yeah, Hypatia Masters. Anyway, that's the story of how my uncle went off his rocker and got eaten by wild animals."

      \n

      [That's the backstory, of course, for Masks of Nyarlathotep, with my own additions to the corpus (mostly the relationship between Roger and Jack, and Erica being cheated of her inheritance.) Fortunately Temperance doesn't know who "Vanessa Brady" is in our continuity...]

      \n

      "Actually, I can identify with parts of that..."

      \n

      "I met your mom. She's a little..."

      \n

      "Off her nutter."

      \n

      "Yeah. I sometimes worry I got a little more of my uncle in me than I think. I had a breakdown while I was in conservatory. After I got better I just ran off to Europe. Played a lot of gigs in Europe. Good training."

      \n

      "Maybe I should do something like that. Let my hair down."

      \n

      "Can you sing?"

      \n

      "Hymns. My father once said, Temperance, you're a great many things, but when it comes to singing you sound like a cat caught in a garbage compactor."

      \n

      "Well that don't seem fair. If you can sing, we could put you in the band."

      \n

      "I hear what the guys call me behind my back." She made a square shape with her hands.

      \n

      "You're not that square. Not with your mom for family."

      \n

      "I have my moments. I mean, I could fleece you all at cards if I wanted."

      \n

      "Hold it a moment," he said, and got up and dashed upstairs. He came back holding an album, an old 78. "This is Duke Ellington," he said. "Listen to a little of this. It will...wait what am I doing."

      \n

      He sat back down at the piano and played "Sophisticated Lady" to an entranced Temperance.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      It happened while Candace was typing, that feeling that some presence was gathering in her room: that feeling that someone was standing right behind her, like when she had been writing too long and Andy would come up behind her and put his hands on her shoulders. So close. So close, almost touching.

      \n

      Like always, her writing became much better during these events.

      \n

      Eventually it faded. She stretched and felt her stomach groan. She was out of cigarettes. She was almost out of Yellow. She took the last hit of it she had.

      \n

      She felt a hand run up and down her back.

      \n

      She turned back to her novel. It was an epic story in a modern setting, an autobiographical story of a woman coming into herself. She bent over the keyboard in a frenzy and hammered out the best sex scene she had ever written. At least Beth was impressed when she showed it to her.

      \n

      "That's..." she stammered, as her glasses fogged. "That's really...wow. You have to tell me who taught you that...so I can meet him."

      \n

      Candace grinned. "It's been like five years," muttered Beth to herself, reflecting on how long she had been separated from Percy. "And not like there's any likely candidates in the current crew. Well, maybe one, but I have a thing for older men."

      \n

      "I'm sure Neal and Jack would love to meet you."

      \n

      "I thought Neal was..."

      \n

      "That doesn't hold him back."

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJune 2017 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode V: A Singer Must Die (Part 9)\n

      The Bal des Mortes was a staid affair, black tie for the men, evening gowns for the ladies. As the guests filed in, Rudy and Charlie confronted Temperance. "We've been in the city for like a week and we haven't seen anything," said Charlie.

      \n

      "You've been to the balls..."

      \n

      "They're all weirdos. It's New Orleans. We want New Orleans weird. No more boring old people music. Some Bill Haley or good R&B?"

      \n

      "Who's Bill Haley?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "That cat can't play for shit," said Van. Mencius, warming up his bass, just looked over and nodded. "True."

      \n

      "Are there going to be any young people around here," said Rudy, "or are we stuck with you?"

      \n

      "I will take you out on the town tomorrow. No, not to a museum. NO, you may ABSOLUTELY not go with Sam."

      \n

      Candace came down in a gorgeous purple gown. "Jesus Mary and Joseph," said Seamus. "That would make a bishop kick through a stained glass window." His wife smacked him.

      \n

      Most of the evening was taken up with a rather boring meeting where Isabelle and the other principals worked out their fundraising goals for the next year, where they would donate their charitable givings, and where they wanted to do the balls next year. Helen, lounging near Charleston, stifled a yawn. "Whoever knew monsters could be so dull?" she said.

      \n

      Candace found herself near the bar next to an elegantly-dressed older woman who had bronzed , Mediterranean good looks. She gave Candace a once over and said, "Dior?"

      \n

      "Givenchy."

      \n

      "Aren't we fancy. Haven't seen you here before. Yolanda Giacoma."

      \n

      "Candace Heartbrooke."

      \n

      "Are you moving here?"

      \n

      "I don't plan to put down roots anywhere."

      \n

      "Oh, one of those jazz people. Jazz used to be so much more interesting when I was younger, in the 1920s. Who are those charming children?" she asked, pointing to Rudy and Charlie, who were in the middle of a fight. As usual.

      \n

      Candace glanced around for Temperance. "Not really my responsibility."

      \n

      "I think I will go make their acquaintance."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Temperance was getting a cup of punch. She turned around and almost bumped into a red-headed woman in a white dress. "Pray forgive me," she said.

      \n

      "Think nothing of it," said Edie Montague.

      \n

      Temperance gaped for rather longer than would be considered ladylike. "What brings you here," she finally said.

      \n

      "It's a party, innit?" She gave a wolfish grin. "Where else would I be?"

      \n

      "Why are you here?"

      \n

      "I'm single, in a strange city. These people are accepting I here, especially yon revenant lady running things." She nodded at Isabelle. "Would ye care to have a Sco\u2014a cuppa tea with me?"

      \n

      "I'll have Scotch with you."

      \n

      "Yer health then," said Edie as they sat at a small table. "Don't be alarmed lassie. I don't bear ye any ill will. Why would I? I weren't in my right head back when I saw you last. I took off my mask, d'ye see? Of course, I put it back on tonight, for appearances sake."

      \n

      "What have you been doing?"

      \n

      "Errands. Verra busy. In fact I must be goin'. But we'll see each other soon."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Jimmy and Beth were looking around for Rudy and Charlie. "I don't see why we have to chaperone," grumbled Beth. "I don't even like children. You think I wanted to have children with Percy? They'd have come out all weird, with tails or something."

      \n

      Jimmy grunted. "Why should we bother?" continued Beth. "Mr. Wright, do you know the foxtrot?"

      \n

      "Now is not the time for the foxtrot!" panted Temperance, running up.

      \n

      "When is it ever the right time?"

      \n

      "What's wrong?" said Jimmy.

      \n

      "She's here. Edie. And she's being creepily polite and cryptic."

      \n

      "That's never good. Where's my sword?"

      \n

      Sam was trying to spike the punch when he noticed several people coming into the townhouse. They were elegantly dressed, although the style was a bit out of date. Not that it meant much; he suspected there was a reason some of the guests had asked Van to play music from the 18th century: probably revisiting the hits of their youth. Still, he ambled over to Jimmy, Beth and Temperance. "We may have a problem."

      \n

      And at that moment Terpsichore and Euterpe showed up. I mean, of course, Nicole and Collette.

      \n

      Jimmy found himself foxtrotting with Beth. In the corner Van was pounding out some new theme with countless variations. People were singing and dancing all around him, all but a knot of men in tails and women dressed as flappers. And they were closing in on Rudy and Charlie.

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nJune 2017 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode V: A Singer Must Die (Part 10)\n

      Yolanda grabbed Nicole and Collette and pushed them toward the door. All four of the strange men in tails surrounded Rudy and Charlie; their three flapper companions began moving toward Temperance and Jimmy.

      \n

      [Sense Trouble checks here to act for J & T.]

      \n

      As Temperance tried to jog up, two of the girls slashed at her with claws that burst from their fingertips. Her dress was slashed to ribbons and she fell back.

      \n

      [10 points of damage here.]

      \n

      Jimmy fished into the piano and pulled out his sword and a pistol. "That's why that B was flat?" said Van, without missing a note. Jimmy tossed Temperance the pistol and ran for the door, trying to cut off the kidnappers. He slid in front of them, drawing the sword, and slashing one of the men.

      \n

      [Preparedness by JP to have this stuff in position, then Athletics; the Athletics roll netted an extra benefit, which was to take an attack, and THAT netted an extra benefit, Terrible Harm in this case.]

      \n

      He had just time to note that the wounds weren't bleeding much when Yolanda seized his wrist. "Mr. Wright, you don't want to get in our way. Oh BOYS!" she shouted.

      \n

      From the street, Jimmy heard a sound he hadn't heard for quite a while\u2014but you never forget the deep-throated bark of a Thompson submachine gun. He slammed to the deck as bullets shattered the front windows. Glass fragments flew through the air. The other people in the room were screaming, in perfect harmony as it happens. A couple of bullets struck some of Yolanda's party boys, but they didn't slow down as they dragged the kids outside.

      \n

      Temperance slid into a slight crouch, the shooter's stance her stepfather preferred, and fired off several rounds. The good-time girls took the bullets and slid back toward the door. Right into Jimmy's sword. He damn near cut one of their feet off.

      \n

      [Shooting test got TP a benefit, which was Suppress.]

      \n

      Jimmy pushed out the door behind the girls. He saw two men standing on the running board of an old Packard, holding Thompsons. They fired off some bursts as the car sped away. He picked himself up and came back inside.

      \n

      "In my house!," Isabelle was ranting. "That bitch. Yolanda Giacona! Her father Iggy was a mobster back in the Twenties and Thirties. He and his son died rather mysteriously in 1937 and she took over the Family."

      \n

      "Does anyone in our circle die normally?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "Yes...well, sometimes. But it doesn't always stick," said Isabelle. "They were more than mobsters. They were cultists of a certain god. Haven't heard anything from that particular group in almost twenty years, though."

      \n

      "Where's Francis' armory?" said Jimmy.

      \n

      "What makes you think Francis would have a...oh, all right. It's not here in the house, but I'll get the key. We have some time, if they kidnapped them they want them for something. I can't help but notice they took them the night before the Bal des Monstres and the end of the year...and that they took Nicole and Collette."

      \n

      "Maybe they were trying to meet a quota before the New Year," said Charleston.

      \n

      "Sometimes I think I have missed you. Then you say things like that and I stop."

      \n

      "When I cut them they barely bled," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "That is entertainingly interesting. And they had claws."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Francis' armory was in a stoutly locked cinderblock shed just outside the city. Isabelle had to do a long series of checks to make sure she had disabled all the traps. "Help yourself," she said, waving around.

      \n

      "Where did you get this?" said Sam, grabbing an automatic weapon from the wall.

      \n

      "Oh, the Russian weapon? Somewhere on the Soviet border, I think." Sam cradled the AK-47 to his chest. Jimmy shrugged and selected a shotgun and some other small arms.

      \n

      "Hey Jimmy, try this on," said Charleston. He handed him a bulletproof vest.

      \n

      Meanwhile, Candace talked to Isabelle's friends, especially the ones who spanned both the occult and criminal worlds. She found out the Giaconas had been part of a cult that had a reputation for being somewhat...dark and twisted. They had a fearsome reputation, but in the last couple of decades the Giaconas had lost their grip of terror on the underworld and were actually in decline.

      \n

      She took Beth with her to help do interviews; her anthropological training could fill in the gaps of her own knowledge. They trolled some waterfront bars for a while. Yolanda had managed to ably run the family since her death of her brother and father. They found out something else interesting: back in the Twenties, the Giaconas had owned a paddlewheel steamer that they kept on Lake Pontchartrain. They only took special guests there...and sometimes they didn't come back.

      \n

      [Beth gives the Investigators a 2-point Interpersonal pool because of her field training. This was mostly Oral History and High Society.]

      \n

      When they got back they found the boys and Temperance loading weapons. "Mr. Wright, were you ever in the army?" said Beth, taken aback, when she saw Jimmy cleaning his shotgun and laying out his armor.

      \n

      "Something like that. You should stay here with Isabelle."

      \n

      A little while later they drove up to the Lake. Francis kept a boat there for fishing. Unsurprisingly, it had a sonar set in it, along with a note from Francis telling Jimmy to not touch his stuff. The pilot Isabelle had arranged waited until they were all onboard and then cast off.

      \n

      "Guy Rondeau," he said by way of introduction. He swung them into a search pattern over the fog-shrouded water.

      \n

      [It turns out nobody had Pilot.

      \n

      TP: Couldn't Isabelle hire someone?

      \n

      Me: Sure.

      \n

      TP: Some rando guy.

      \n

      Me: It's pronounced "Guy Rondeau" and he's Cajun.]

      \n

      After a couple of hours, they finally got a sonar echo that looked likely. They approached carefully, and had Guy cut the engine as they came within rifleshot.

      \n

      "Gonna be guys with guns for sure," muttered Jimmy.

      \n

      "Actually, not," said Charleston, keeping a weather eye. They glided up along the paddlewheeler and jumped to the deck.

      \n

      "Here's why," said Jimmy, pointing to the bodies of some Giacona soldiers. They had all had their necks cleanly slit by a very sharp blade.

      \n

      "Edie," said Temperance.

      \n

      "This is pretty recent," said Charleston. "Within the last couple of hours."

      \n

      [Me: You don't have Medical, so you're not sure how long...

      \n

      CP: I base it on my years of experience as a murderer.

      \n

      Me: Fair enough.]

      \nEpisode V: A Singer Must Die (Part 11)\n

      Temperance made her way down the promenade deck. She found a large room that was padded and had many restraints along the walls and on tables. She spun around at the sound of something rustling.

      \n

      She turned around. A small figure was toddling out of the shadows. It was a baby.

      \n

      With no eyes. Not even sockets.

      \n

      She screamed. The baby opened its mouth. It was filled with sharp teeth. As it raised its hands, she saw strange scars on the palms...they looked almost like little mouths with teeth...but they were healing over, like they were wounds of some kind.

      \n

      She kicked it against the wall like she was making a field goal. It smashed apart, and slid down in a slimy, bloody mess just as the rest of them came up. They stalked down the stairs to the lower deck.

      \n

      At the foot of the stairs, they saw more of the "babies" come running up, six of them. Jimmy backhanded one with the sword, but it ducked under the blade. Two of them bit savagely into his ankles, drawing blood.

      \n

      The rest of the, well, demonic children were crawling toward the stairs. Temperance reared back and kicked the head off of one them, but missed her second kick. Candace retreated back a few steps. Charleston was trying to push past her when Sam stepped up.

      \n

      He thumbed the fire selector on his AK-47 to "Full Auto" and sprayed the hallway with gunfire until the magazine ran out. Ricochets whinged around; splinters of wood flew back at them. Even with the cordite rounds the assault rifle used, the hallway was filled with thin, acrid smoke.

      \n

      Jimmy swept up the two things clutching on his ankle and bashed their heads against the wall, killing them.

      \n

      They filed down the companionway. They saw the remains of the Party Boys and Good Time girls in one stateroom; they were riddled with Sam's bullets, but looked like they had been rotting away even before he fired. They found another staircase leading down and followed it to a large stateroom below the waterline.

      \n

      This was a plush room\u2014literally, given the extensive velvet coverings. A brick wall had been inset into one of the bulkheads; chained up to it were Rudy and Charlie, both gagged. Standing near a sumptuously upholstered banquette was Yolanda Giaconda, wearing an opulent red velvet gown with a cape that swept over her shoulders and ran down onto the floor for quite some distance behind her.

      \n

      Temperance noticed, however, that despite her normal dans un certain age appearance, Yolanda seemed wan, drawn, and tired. She also noticed that something seemed to be moving under her dress.

      \n

      [1-point Notice spend.]

      \n

      "You're here for the children," said Yolanda without preamble. "Of course. You have to understand, the family religion\u2014when the Mouths started talking again...I had to make a try, didn't I? But it turns out we were just actors in a play. The wrong play. I took your siblings because the God was very well acquainted with your mother..."

      \n

      Temperance realized with a sharp shock that Yolanda kept wiping her mouth because when she didn't, it seemed to heal shut...she fired off a couple of quick rounds, striking her center mass. She slowly walked over to where Yolanda had fallen upon the floor.

      \n

      Jimmy watched intently. He hadn't liked the drift of this conversation at all...

      \n

      Temperance bent down. Yolanda was bleeding out, but she already seemed sapped, drained of vitality. Her mouth continued to film over as she gasped out her final words. "No more...lies. I wasted too much time...on the dead! Listen! The exile does not wish you harm...but...she is caught in...a...trap...and wishes you to take...hr...plce..."

      \n

      Her mouth was sealed shut, covered over with skin as if it had never been open. Charleston was swinging around behind her to shoot her if, as so often was the case, the sorcerer's first death wasn\u2019t permanent. He saw something crawl out from under Yolanda's dress.

      \n

      In a lifetime spent walking the boundaries of the strange, few things after his first horrific encounters were capable of startling him; but this...this...

      \n

      It was long and tubular, like some great pallid worm dug up from the Stygian depths of the sea. On the ventral side was a mouth, a horrid lipless thing like a slash across flesh, with snaggled and broken teeth jutting out at all angles. A black and forked tongue flashed out almost lasciviously, and a honey-colored slime drooled out from the edges of the mouth. It muttered in a wordless ululating language. But perhaps the true horror was that this thing the Mouth grew on had been a human arm once; withered and wasted, but clearly a woman's arm. It seemed to have lost all its bones and it writhed sickeningly as it inched across the floor, pulling itself with boneless fingers.

      \n

      [4 point Stability loss for Chuckles here.]

      \n

      Jimmy ran to the kids. "Uncle Jimmy, we've seen some things," moaned Rudy.

      \n

      "Close your eyes," he said. He strode over to the arm. The Mouth hissed at him as he unsheathed his sword. He raised it slowly, then lowered it, sighting along the blade. The Mouth chuckled evilly; it clearly recognized him. Then he slammed the blade into it, with such force that he felt the blade bite clean through the hull. The orange slime sprayed everywhere. He felt dizzy. For a moment, he saw vast ranks of himself arrayed on either side, like an infinity mirror; then it faded and he felt cold water pooling around his feet. He paid it no mind and helped Temperance take the kids out of the room.

      \n

      Had he been paying closer attention, he might have noticed that some of the slime had soaked his pants leg. And was rubbing up against the open wounds on his ankle.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      They pulled away from the paddlewheeler. Somebody had come on the boat and killed everyone, Rudy stammered out. Someone wearing a white mask. Whoever they were, they had taken the Muses with them. Charlie, who had kept a clearer head, told them some of what she had overheard from Yolanda: how her cult had stolen the Last Mouth from some facility out west; how suddenly two days ago it had started to talk again; that Yolanda had kidnapped them because of "something in their blood."

      \n

      "I'm going to take care of all this," said Temperance.

      \n

      "They thought they were going to the ball tonight," said Rudy. "The Muses."

      \n

      "That's our next stop. We'll handle this."

      \n

      "I'd be more confident since Mr. Wright is here, but he's scaring me right now," said Charlie.

      \n

      "He's just seasick," said Charleston.

      \n

      "Seasick makes you murderous?"

      \n

      "Now you'll know to never get seasick."

      \n

      \nEpisode V: A Singer Must Die (Part 12)\n

      They dropped the children off at Isabelle's house. Seamus and Sean were there to watch over things. "Don't worry, things may get a bit hairy," said Sean, winking at Jimmy. "But we'll watch over the bairns."

      \n

      They moved on to the Bal des Monstres, at the recently-refurbished Hotel Palais Royal\u2014no expense had been spared to make it look 200 years old. The Ball itself was in the parqueted main ballroom, a room dizzy with mirrors that would not have looked out of place in Versailles. This Ball, the last of the occult balls, was the only one attended by the non-occult denizens of the city; several notable local politicos were there, mixing it up on the dance floor in a fine New Orleans style.

      \n

      As they entered, they could see Nicole and Collette standing as still as caryatid columns next to a gilded throne; it was the custom of the Ball to elect a King of the Revels at the end of the night. Candace pulled down her mask, the one she had been given in Carcosa; Jimmy pushed his shotgun a little higher on its sling.

      \n

      They fanned out into the crowd; around them swirled the masked revelers. Suddenly Candace saw Edie\u2014she wasn't sure how it was that she got there, or how it was that she knew it was Edie\u2014striding through the room, wearing white robes. Her mask was a smooth, almost featureless porcelain affair that covered her whole face with just slits for the eyes and mouth.

      \n

      "Hello, Candace," the...Stranger...said.

      \n

      "Hello...Edie?"

      \n

      "Not really. I took off my mask for the Ball. What do you intend to do, Candace? Which Court do you belong to?"

      \n

      "Whichever one suits me best," said Candace. She didn't see any change on the mask, but she felt Edie was smiling.

      \n

      "Verra good. You will help me? I wish no harm to these girls. But it is almost time for them to unmask."

      \n

      "What help do you need?"

      \n

      "Just stand at my side." She stroked Candace's face. For a moment, she felt that same shiver of feeling she had felt earlier, when she had been touched by the Presence that invaded her writing.

      \n

      Edie turned and moved through the crowd. Someone tried to grab her, but he pulled back his hand as if burned. Temperance could see blood spurting from his eyes. Midnight began to strike. The crowd began to remove their masks, even including Nicole and Collette. Edie hopped up on the stage and stood next to the throne.

      \n

      Nicole turned to her with blank eyes. She said in a monotone, "You should unmask."

      \n

      "Indeed?" said Edie.

      \n

      "Yes, we have all laid aside disguise but you," said Collette in the same monotone.

      \n

      "I wear no mask," said Edie. She sat down on the throne, crossed one leg over the other, and relaxed back into the chair. "Don't be afraid. We come as viceroy, not as King."

      \n

      "Welcome, viceroy," said Charleston with a tone just above a sneer.

      \n

      "It is not for you to welcome Us, nor to hinder the coming and going of the King. For His time will come when it is His time to come. And you cannot change that."

      \n

      "When is he coming?" said Sam.

      \n

      "First let us discuss the matter of the Exile. Where is she, you ask? That is an interesting question. But since you are responsible for her escape, you shall be responsible for her return. For that is Our Royal Will."

      \n

      "Capture a person from Carcosa? Sounds intriguing," said Sam.

      \n

      "It is an affair of your mortal world, and you will settle it. Or we will settle it for you. Deliver her to Us, or We will not be merciful." Nicole and Collette began to bleed from the eyes. "Shall We not hold them hostage for the vouchsafing?"

      \n

      Temperance and Jimmy glared at Edie. At the Stranger.

      \n

      "We can afford to be merciful," said the Stranger. And then she made the Yellow Sign.

      \n

      She made it in the air, moving her fist rapidly, leaving a glowing sickly yellow afterimage that hung there horrifically, burning and beating even against closed eyes. People shrieked in the crowd, or broke down weeping, all but Jimmy, Charleston, Temperance and Candace, the veterans of Carcosa.

      \n

      The room went black for a moment. When the emergency lights came back on, they saw the two girls, the former Muses, collapsed on the stage, but breathing gently, caught in a deep sleep.

      \n

      \nEpisode V: A Singer Must Die (Part 13)\n

      There were some loose ends to tie up:

      \n

      Charleston concluded that the girls, by trying to connect the loas to the ancient Greek muses, had accidentally tied themselves into the ascendant power of the King in Yellow. Which might have happened no matter what, but with Aldebaran's influence growing, it was an unfortunate mistake. They had been caught up into the Play, the only play, taking on the roles of Camilla and Cassilda. He speculated that the temporal distortions that seemed to accompany anything to do with Carcosa had allowed the brief revival of the god Jimmy would only call the Liar.

      \n

      The girls only had dim, dreamlike memories of wandering the dark streets of an endless city that seemed like New Orleans except older and vaster, and with two suns that were constantly setting into a vast lake they guessed was and was not Lake Pontchartrain. They were stalked by some figure they never caught sight of but was always there; the soft hiss of his silken robes haunted them and they were incredibly jumpy around everyone. It was the whispers, said Nicole in a low whisper. He offered us so much, and it was so tempting\u2026to achieve true art, to live forever, and all we had to do was agree to be His\u2026

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Etienne Laurent de Marigny had been assaulted in his home. Using his skills after a lifetime of dodging the law, Charleston managed to talk his way past the cops to look in on the study. He found a picture of a jazz singer from the 1930s, in front of a Kansas City nightclub called the Dapper and Brown. The singer's name was Cassandra Lezhone; Etienne had circled her face and written, in French: Les yeux! On peut y toujours voir la verit\xe9, m\xeame si toutes des autres caract\xe9ristiques de son visage ont chang\xe9.

      \n

      [In English: The eyes! We can always see the truth there, even if all the other features of her face have changed.]

      \n

      There was also a record of Etienne's trying to call someone named Millicent Lowell with no success; there was a letter from her that he showed Jimmy later. It naturally caused him much concern:

      \n
      \n

      Dear Mr. de Marigny,

      \n\xa0
      After sending you my last letter, I made some further inquiries at Miskatonic University. I have been able to find out a few things thanks to our friends there.
      \xa0
      First, the woman you asked about seems to have been in the city more than once in the last 15 years although not matching the description you gave me. From what you have said, I expected as much.
      \xa0
      Second, the box was definitely brought back to Miskatonic University sometime in 1939 or 1940. I am trying to get access to the Orne Library, but since Professor Armitage\u2019s death it is harder to visit the special collections.
      \xa0
      Third, I have found some very interesting phenomena in this building. I don\u2019t want to say more until all the evidence is in (as a good friend taught me when I was younger) but I have taken a room here to try and observe them first hand. I am not sure but I was able to determine that Miss C lived here at least twice in the last twenty years.
      \xa0
      I look forward to writing to you soon with what I have uncovered. As always, if anything should happen to me please forward the sealed letters I gave you to their addressees.
      \xa0
      \xa0
      Your friend,
      \xa0
      \xa0
      \xa0
      Millicent Lowell
      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      "How do you handle these things?" Rudy asked Temperance when they were alone.

      \n

      "I have my faith, and I have my training. I've been doing this for a while, and there's someone very special who is helping me."

      \n

      "Should I talk to the Colonel? Dad never teaches me about fighting, he just wants me to study engineering."

      \n

      "Talking to my father is probably not a good idea," she said with a wince. "Geronimo is a good man. But you should go far away from this."

      \n

      "I'm going to go to college and be good. Maybe be a doctor like Dad wants."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Jimmy found Charlie waiting for him late one night when he went down to the kitchen for a drink.

      \n

      "Okay, spill," she said. "James."

      \n

      She said it just like her mother. Before he could make that observation, she soldiered on, just like her mother:

      \n

      "Don't pretend I haven't heard Mom talk about you. She didn't lose her arm in a car accident, did she?"

      \n

      "No. She meddled in something I told her not to meddle with, and lost her arm in the process."

      \n

      "Can I help?"

      \n

      "No. Go back and leave this alone."

      \n

      "But I can help. You're bringing Beth, and she's an old lady."

      \n

      Jimmy shook his head. "Go home before you end up like your mother."

      \n

      "A famous adventuress?"

      \n

      "Go home. Go home before you become like that lady on the boat. Before you become a corpse."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      For Candace, the whole thing just spurred her onto even more and better writing; but then again, just about anything did that for her nowadays. Sometimes she took walks for relaxation and inspiration. Around town, she saw the graffiti:

      \n

      Il arrive qu'il arrive.

      \n

      The King! (or Le Roi)

      \n

      The world will have a new spirit, the Stranger says

      \n

      And a few times, twisting in the shadows, the Yellow Sign. Those walks always refreshed her; and after them, as she banged away on the typewriter, she could feel the Presence stalking ever closer, urging her on, supporting her, filling her, inspiring her.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      "What the hell is going on, Charleston?" said Helen, one day when they were both at the tail-end of a Yellow high.

      \n

      "How's your poetry going?" he replied evasively.

      \n

      Excellent, she said. She had been writing about the photographs she had taken of the "real world", the New York City she was from. A lot were of the abandoned Suicide Center in Washington Square. "It was closed up in the 1930s. Liberal administration took over."

      \n

      "Wait a second. Suicide Center?"

      \n

      "Yeah. You could show up and get yourself killed if you really wanted to. Not going to say no one got purged ever."

      \n

      "Sounds like a very political situation."

      \n

      "Well, we have our own Cold War, you know."

      \n

      "Really? Between who and who?"

      \n

      "The US and the USSR, of course," she said, but gave him a slantwise look as if she were hiding something.

      \n

      \n
      \nEpisode VI: Broken Night (Part 1)\n

      Give me back my broken night

      \n

      my mirrored room, my secret life

      \n

      it's lonely here,

      \n

      there's no one left to torture\u2026

      \n

      \u2014Leonard Cohen, \u201cThe Future\u201d

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Armed with the letter from Millicent, Jimmy convinced the rest of them that their best chance of finding Cassie's trail was to head to Arkham and see what Millicent had been investigating. They began to make preparations for the long drive north, aided by Isabelle O'Donnell and her collection of amiable monsters. Temperance's mother, Ruby Fitzgibbons Cuevas, flew out from California (in her own plane; she was still quite a pilot) to collect Rudy and Charlie. It was a surprise visit; she still knew how to make an entrance.

      \n

      [TP requested this scene; in our Eternal Lies campaign they had played Ruby. I tried to do my best by the old girl\u2014she was one of my favorite characters in all the games I've GMed.]

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      "James," Ruby drawled as she came into the parlor. Jimmy jumped up, twenty year old reflexes snapping back into action. "So good to see you again. I didn't know you were back in business. Hello, Temperance. Give me a cigarette, won't you?"

      \n

      "I\u2014you\u2014what\u2014" stuttered Temperance, lighting the cigarette she placed in her mother's elegant ivory holder.

      \n

      "Well, I\u2014" said Jimmy, and he beat a hasty retreat without an intelligible word.

      \n

      Ruby followed him with her eyes. Unnervingly, she held her cigarette holder in her artificial arm. "I'm here to pick up my children. I got a strange call from Rudy. He was crying on the phone, I'll never hear the end of it from Geronimo."

      \n

      "My stepfather can be a bit protective. They're fine."

      \n

      [We had a brief aside at this point about how Ruby and Geronimo must contemplate suing Lucy and Ricky Ricardo; and pondering what a rebooted I Love Ruby would be like\u2014Ruby no doubt whining and scheming to join Geronimo's mercenary company off to fight with the Socialists somewhere in Latin America.]

      \n

      "They don't look fine, Temperance." Ruby sighed. "I suppose it's all my fault. I haven't always been there for you."

      \n

      "Can I talk to you frankly?" Temperance went to the bar and made them a pair of martinis, extra dry. The room was quiet and filled with unsaid tension.

      \n

      Temperance handed her mother the drink. "Was it because of all this?" she said in a low voice. "The reason you left me in Mexico? Was it because of...all this. Ever since I joined Mr. Wright on his adventures I've seen things. Things that before would only have been the worries of nuns or priests. But I found them to be real."

      \n

      "James does have that effect on people."

      \n

      "All these things I thought were made up stories turned out to be true. And so I can understand if that's why you wanted me out of harm's way, and left me in Mexico."

      \n

      "Oh darling, I wish that were the case. Perhaps if I had known more, I would have made sure you stayed there when we got back from India.\u201d Ruby paused. \u201cNo, dear, it was that my parents couldn't stand the thought of what I had done\u2014the trouble I had gotten into. And your father and I were...well, we were a little combustible."

      \n

      "He's told me stories. Not all of them are flattering. To either of you."

      \n

      "I do...love you. Just because I have Rudy and Charlie doesn't mean I don't care for you."

      \n

      "But you left me in Mexico."

      \n

      "Well, I had you."

      \n

      "If that's any consolation."

      \n

      "I left you with your father, in the end. Somehow you turned out to be a much better person than Captain Murphy ever was."

      \n

      "Did he ever tell you what he did with the ship? He burned it. He got drunk on the beach and he burned it. Because he didn't have time to go to sea anymore, he told me. That he had a daughter to raise. But he cried while it burned. And then he took me clothes shopping."

      \n

      "Ashley was always a very dramatic person."

      \n

      "You seem to share that trait."

      \n

      "That's why we were combustible. To be honest, Temperance, and I don't know how you managed to pull this off, but you could really be Geronimo's daughter: upright, good, devout...like he is."

      \n

      "Geronimo did a good job of making me feel included. He's a good man, I respect him."

      \n

      "And now you hang around with Jimmy."

      \n

      "He's quite a character," said Temperance resignedly. "He's old, and he's tired, but he won't stop walking they beat."

      \n

      "He's the most interesting man I ever met. And it's a shame to see what he's become," said Ruby.

      \n

      "Does it really eat you alive, all of this?"

      \n

      "No...not as long as I stay in the light. You'll find, I think\u2014darling\u2014that when you fight in the shadows, you fight with your shadow-self as well. My shadow-self is...rather shady."

      \n

      "You don't say."

      \n

      "And I had a thing in the Thirties. It was a different era. FDR, the Japanese, it was all crazy!"

      \n

      "Things seem to have toned down now."

      \n

      "That's true, we could all die at any moment. A feeling I got quite used to during 1937." Ruby glanced slyly at Temperance. "I don't suppose you've come across any...substance...honey-colored, maybe?"

      \n

      "Once."

      \n

      "Really? Where?"

      \n

      "In a bunker in Nevada."

      \n

      "Nevada, you say."

      \n

      "I think it was like that yellowish substance all the bohemians take..."

      \n

      "Oh, Yellow? Not the same at all. Not that it matters. I'm clean now."

      \n

      "I think you should take Rudy and Charlie now."

      \n

      "Yes. Yes. I don't want them on the line of fire. Frankly, if I had known that you were working with Jimmy, I probably wouldn't have sent them out."

      \n

      "I didn't realize things were complicated between you two."

      \n

      "Just make sure you take better care of yourself than he did."

      \n

      "Have fun, Ruby."

      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n
      \nEpisode VI: Broken Night (Part 2)\n

      "Mr. Wright, who was that beautiful lady?" asked Beth. She had found Jimmy in the closet he had retreated to. He was cleaning their guns. Rather tensely.

      \n

      "A walking disaster," he said morosely.

      \n

      "But she was so elegant! And she seemed so nice! She said that she liked my dress and found it very unusual."

      \n

      "She's mellowed out a bit, but I don't think..."

      \n

      "Oh. Oh! Oh." Beth's face fell.

      \n

      "That's the posh for you," said Jimmy, and he pulled the door closed. Beth went upstairs and sat down in Candace's room. She was sorting through the stacks of typescript on her desk, and dresser, and nightstand, and by the bed, and on the bed, and on the windowsill...

      \n

      "Candace?\u201d said Beth. \u201cI can't ask Temperance about this for reasons that will become extremely evident. This whole...half-dead spinster academic thing I've been doing, I don't want that to be me anymore...I'm still young. I can look different."

      \n

      "Oh honey, I've been in your situation before," said Candace.

      \n

      "Should I get a...permanent?" She looked up at Candace with her large eyes, blurry behind their glasses.

      \n

      "Well, why not. Have fun! You should be having fun!"

      \n

      "I don't follow Vogue or anything like that..."

      \n

      "I can take you to the hairdresser. Nothing like a fresh change."

      \n

      "I asked Mrs. O'Donnell, but her clothes are so old-fashioned. It's like she died in the Twenties or something."

      \n

      "Just give me five minutes."

      \n

      An hour later, after she had run out of typewriter ribbons, Candace remembered her promise and ran downstairs to find Beth.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Neal and Jack left them in New Orleans, heading back out on the road, to coin a term. The rest of them drove the RV north. It was big enough for all of them to sleep in it, which was appreciated by Mencius until they were well clear of the Mason-Dixon line.

      \n

      Candace was driving late one night, on the approaches to New Jersey. She had one of the wildcat radio stations from over the Mexican border on\u2014a 100,000 watt clear channel transmission that could probably be tuned in up by Lake Erie. The program was bop jazz, hosted by a woman calling herself Isis.

      \n

      "This goes out to all the Lonesome Travelers out there," she purred through the speakers. "If you're out there all alone, and you feel that presence coming up behind you, just a reminder: embrace it. Here's a dedication, a King Creole cut. To Candace, somewhere in America."

      \n

      It wasn't until long after that Candace realized the voice had been familiar to her: the saloonkeeper in New Orleans. Hypatia Masters.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      They stopped in New York. It was the first time back to his old home for Jimmy since he had passed through in 1945 while getting demobbed.

      \n

      Candace had a crash in Greenwich Village, a very artistic couple of young men that were so solicitous of Temperance that for whole minutes at a time she forgot to be uncomfortable. They took an evening to head up to Birdland in the West 50s and troll the hard drinking musicians' bars around it.

      \n

      "I don't get it. I try to get it, but I don't get it," muttered Temperance during a particularly abstract solo by Dizzy Gillespie.

      \n

      "It's all right, others see more meaning, but you don't have to. Just try to enjoy it," said Candace.

      \n

      "I am enjoying it."

      \n

      \xa0"Would you like a drink?"

      \n

      "Yes. Many."

      \n

      "I think I get it," said Beth brightly. "You have to hear what they're not playing."

      \n

      "That's so asinine!" said Temperance.

      \n

      "When you drink something other than a Shirley Temple, you can get back to me," said Beth with remarkable brio.

      \n

      "I'm drinking scotch and soda."

      \n

      "That's a very manly drink," said a barfly, with a bit of a leer.

      \n

      "What are you drinking?"

      \n

      "Martini."

      \n

      "Is it any good?"

      \n

      "Very."

      \n

      "I'll have a martini."

      \n

      "I'll get it for you, doll,\u201d said the barfly.

      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n
      \nEpisode VI: Broken Night (Part 3)\n

      Sam dropped by one of the chem labs at Columbia. He knew a guy there.

      \n

      "Oh, no. No, no no!" said his guy when he opened the door.

      \n

      "Yes yes yes!" said Sam. "You still owe me."

      \n

      "You still owe me! We put LSD in the punch!"

      \n

      "That was hilarious and you know it."

      \n

      "I nearly got fired!"

      \n

      "They couldn't prove it though."

      \n

      "What do you want? Meth? Give me some time to cook it up and then get out."

      \n

      "I can do that on my own. I have something better now."

      \n

      "I'm clean," muttered his friend, but he took the vial of Yellow Sam gave him. "That's new. What is it, alkaloid?"

      \n

      "Don't know. All the tests I've been running have not been conclusive\u2014"

      \n

      "How do you take it?"

      \n

      "Injection, mostly."

      \n

      Ten minutes and one syringe later, his guy leaned back with a satisfied grin. "Oooh."

      \n

      "Interesting, isn't it?"

      \n

      "I'll tell you when you stop speaking Latin."

      \n

      "Apparently all the artists are taking it."

      \n

      "Artists are all crazy."

      \n

      "Like us!"

      \n

      "Nah, they take things like mescaline."

      \n

      But after 72 very entertaining hours, they were still no closer to knowing just what the hell it was, or how to synthesize it.

      \n

      [Pharmacy is baffled by Yellow; just what it is forms a plot point for Episode X.]

      \n

      And Sam had a dream.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      He found himself in a city floating in an endless sky, no land below, just endless clouds in a permanent sunset. The city was made of graceful spires and elegant bridges that connected floating platforms. From time to time beautiful, wasp-waisted rocket ships lifted from some edge of the city and threw themselves into the void.

      \n

      He watched them with pleasure for a few moments. When he lowered his eyes, he saw Percival Schicksal standing in front of him\u2014not the twisted creature he had encountered underneath the Nevada desert, but Percy as he remembered him, a trim figure in a grey suit with curling black hair and smiling eyes.

      \n

      "Sam! Glad to see you finally made it!" said Percy.

      \n

      "You look better than the last time I saw you," said Sam.

      \n

      "That was just my physical form."

      \n

      "You have more than one?"

      \n

      "I float between many worlds now."

      \n

      "Am I back here permanently?"

      \n

      "Probably not. You only took a little of the Yellow."

      \n

      "Is that how you got here?"

      \n

      "No. I made a Promise."

      \n

      "To whom?"

      \n

      "Hastur."

      \n

      "Operating on the whims of external beings is not going to be good for science."

      \n

      "Probably. Welcome to the Raketen-Stadt: Rocket City," said Percy, waving his arms around.

      \n

      "Is this a German city?"

      \n

      "Let's just say that a lot of people dream of escape and find it represented here. There's a rocket that will take you to Hlanith or whatever it was called. I don't want to go there, too Currier and Ives for me. Or we can go further on. Have you...seen the Yellow Sign?"

      \n

      "No, but I'm interested."

      \n

      "Haven't been to Carcosa, eh? Let's not go there right away. You'll have a chance to go there soon enough."

      \n

      "I take it you've been there."

      \n

      "Oh yes," said Percy softly.

      \n

      "What sustains it?"

      \n

      "Interesting question."

      \n

      "We're scientists."

      \n

      "Carcosa sustains itself. It is a world outside of time. Very hard to get in...or out."

      \n

      "I hear it destroys itself and renews itself constantly."

      \n

      "I wouldn't say that. It's in a perpetual state of unchanging. And yet it changes: details, though, just the details."

      \n

      "I want to make this in our own image."

      \n

      "You might not like the result."

      \n

      "Look at the world we live in now. We've unlocked the atom only to try to use it to kill ourselves. We need to evolve."

      \n

      "I'm not sure Carcosa is the answer to that."

      \n

      "I don't think we should overlook any opportunity."

      \n

      "Well, I'll pass that along."

      \n

      "To who?"

      \n

      "Top men. The men in charge. You'll get to meet them soon, and I'm sure then you'll sign on with the program. But now you got to go back."

      \n

      "I don't want to leave! This is where I belong!"

      \n

      "Not yet....not yet..." And everything faded away.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Jimmy had stayed with the RV, which was parked at Idlewild airport. He didn't mind the immediate squalor; at his age (or more accurately, with his mileage) he didn't need the excitement of the Big Apple anymore. Plus he had been feeling vaguely off somehow ever since that terrible night on the paddlewheeler in New Orleans: vaguely discontented and angry. Twitchy.

      \n

      He had made a dismal if serviceable dinner from a can of beans and some bread and was sipping a whisky next to the big bay window on the left side of the RV. Out on the edge of the lot he could see the local working girls plying their trade. As he watched, he saw a man dragging a woman out amidst the cars. He threw her up against the side of one of them. "Bitch, I'm not paying you for what you did," screamed the man.

      \n

      Jimmy sighed, got up, and rummaged in the weapons locker\u2014the one with "Sporting Equipment" painted in day-glo letters on the hatch, in a weak attempt at subterfuge. He pulled out a baseball bat, slung it over his shoulder, and stepped out onto the asphalt.

      \n

      As he sauntered up to them, he could hear the woman crying. "You should really learn some manners," he said, loud enough to make the john pause with one fist raised to strike the woman.

      \n

      "Who the fuck are you?" said the john.

      \n

      "The guy who is going hurt you very badly if you don't mind your manners," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "Go to hell, old man," said the john. He turned back to the girl.

      \n

      Jimmy sighed, and let his shoulders droop. Then he spun, sliding the bat off his shoulder and jabbing it forward. The man turned around and took the bat right in the solar plexus. He sat down hard, blood dripping from his mouth.

      \n

      [JP used Jimmy's Maneuver reserve to pick up an extra benefit on the roll: here, it was "No Traces" so this guy took one where it won't show.]

      \n

      Jimmy raised the bat again. Suddenly he was in a blinding, violent rage. He wanted to smash this guy's skull in. He wanted to see the blood flowing under the sulphur lights.

      \n

      [Sudden two point Driver to do violence! I wonder why...]

      \n

      The john looked up and caught the glimmer of murderous rage in Jimmy's eyes. He coughed, rolled up into a crouching run, and got away as fast as he could. Jimmy helped the girl up to her feet. "Thanks, mister," she sniffed. Jimmy's ankle itched as he helped her to the RV. He poured her a glass of water and gave her a washcloth to clean up with.

      \n

      With her makeup off, she wasn't bad looking. Quite good looking, as a matter of fact. He felt a strange urge that took him a moment to process: lust. He hadn't wanted someone this badly in a long time.

      \n

      What the hell is going on? he thought. He reached for his wallet. "You better get going," he said to her, handing her a sawback. "Go. Make better life choices. Get the hell out!" He practically shoved her out the door, and slammed it behind her.

      \n

      His hands shook as he made himself the stiffest drink he dared. What happened? he thought again. I was acting like I was on Nectar...oh no. He felt the burning itching on his ankle, near where his leg had been slashed open: where the last drops of a dying god's essence had flowed into his veins...

      \n

      Fortunately the wet bar on the RV was very well stocked.

      \n

      [Yup, this was the Dark Bargain I eventually made for Jimmy having taken out the last remaining vestige of the Liar in the previous episode. We didn't make that much of it in every episode going forward, but it's definitely emerged a couple of times.]

      \nEpisode VI: Broken Night (Part 4)\n

      They took the highway up to witch-haunted Arkham. Past the Howard Johnson's on the interstate, down the low hills with a few patches of snow under the pine trees, and into the sleepy Boston exurb that was home to Miskatonic University.

      \n

      There were new housing developments on the north side of the river, but downtown still had a carefully-manicured colonial charm. Temperance smiled, remembering the fresh boys that had come down to the bars near Wellesley when she had been there. Very grabby, she remembered. Like they had tentacles for arms.

      \n

      They parked at a garage and walked down to the Macallister building on Pickman Street, Millicent Lowell's last known address. It was an average looking three-story building, except for the castle motif: gargoyles and fake crenulations, even a mock portcullis. Much to no one's surprise, Millicent didn't answer her buzzer. But when Jimmy tried ringing all the other bells, no one answered them.

      \n

      "She went to Miskatonic," said Candace. "We could check the alumni association."

      \n

      "You wearing a different perfume, Beth?" said Jimmy in a low voice.

      \n

      "Yes, I am. I'm surprised you noticed," said Beth, beaming. "Surprised you noticed anything given how drunk you are," she muttered to herself.

      \n

      They walked down to Miskatonic and Candace ingratiated herself with the staff. Down at the alumni association, they found a bright young lady named Jill. "Oh, Miss Lowell...yes, she came by...it was always so interesting to see Millicent. She really hasn't changed at all since college. She was teaching high school down in Boston."

      \n

      "When was the last time she came by?"

      \n

      "December, seems like. She met President Peaslee, that's...odd."

      \n

      "Perhaps they knew each other. Is the Professor in?"

      \n

      Jill gave them a look. "He might be. Is that Miss Temperance Murphy over there? Her father has contributed a lot to the school....let me see what I can do..."

      \n

      [To meet the president, you needed both High Society and a Counterculture UNDER 2. President Peaslee doesn't meet any riff-raff.]

      \n

      And an hour later Temperance, Jimmy, Sam and Candace were shown into the office of Wingate Peaslee, member of a Miskatonic dynasty. "I knew Miss Lowell very well," he said after the formalities were over. He was in his sixties, one of that specimen of New Englander that gets worn down to a hard, rounded nub as they get older: he had white hair combed in the style of the 1920s, and wore a three-piece suit with a watch on a chain. "She was quite a gifted student. Bit of a strange girl, but we don't hold that against anyone here. She came into town and decided to stay a while. This was back in December, before the break."

      \n

      "How was she strange?" asked Sam.

      \n

      "Was she different than usual?" broke in Jimmy.

      \n

      "No, she was exactly as she used to be. A bit crazy-eyed...well, you seem to know her."

      \n

      "President Peaslee, I'm sure a man of your education in these things could help us," said Sam, laying it on thick; he'd learned how to do that from budget meetings at his school.

      \n

      [Flattery use.]

      \n

      "Well, since you're friends of hers...she was looking for a woman, for some friend of hers in New Orleans. She took a room here in town. I don't know much more, she spent most of her time on campus talking to Professor Wilmarth. The building she was staying at is a bit interesting...it was built on the site of one of our most haunted buildings."

      \n

      "I always find stories like that amusing. What was this one?"

      \n

      "It was the old Keziah Mason house. She was a witch, burnt by Judge Hathorne back in the 17th century. Sad times back then. In the 1930s one of our students here was living there. Had a bit of a breakdown, I guess; claimed he saw Mason coming out of the corner of his room. Said he saw a black man who made him sign the Book of Satan or something. There was also some unpleasantness with an immigrant family as well. In any case they tore it down and built an apartment building on the lot."

      \n

      [That's the plot of Lovecraft's Dreams of the Witch House.

      \n

      TP: Some unpleasantness? That is a white people answer for sure.]

      \n

      Peaslee leaned back in his chair. "I tell you what," he said, as if he had reached a sudden decision. "I can send you over to Professor Wilmarth. He's having his office hour today. He's an emeritus professor now, but he does try to drop by once a week."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Professor Wilmarth was every inch what a retired New England professor of English should be: avuncular, with thick horn-rimmed glasses framed by a halo of unruly white hair, and a tweedy jacket still coated in chalk dust. "Millicent Lowell," he said when they arrived. "I remember her well; one of my best students. Liked to talk about D.H. Lawrence a lot. You're here from her friend in New Orleans, I take it? Well. She was searching for some woman; she found a building that she was supposed to have lived in multiple times. To me the pictures looked like different people, but she made some connection. The Artlife association on the north side of the river runs the Macallister as a kind of artist's colony. And Millicent was looking for the Box."

      \n

      [There was a running gag in Eternal Lies about Millicent reading Lawrence for the "dirty" parts.]

      \n

      "The Box?" said Temperance and Jimmy.

      \n

      It was an interesting artifact, said Professor Wilmarth. Back in 1938 they University had, somewhat unbelievably, sent a botanical expedition to the Pyrenees, despite the Civil War in Spain; supposedly it had the support of the French and British. (The professor implied heavily that espionage was involved in the British interest.) It was led by Professor Francis Morgan, who had fallen under the spell of a young coed named Cordelia Gelbpfluchtig. Morgan was a good friend of Professor Armitage, though, and that rolled over any objections. Sadly, the expedition was massacred by Carlist militias.

      \n

      "We thought everyone died," said Wilmarth. "But in 1940 a girl from it turned up in Toulouse, by the name of Milla DeVille. Half out of her wits; we had to commit her. She never really explained what she saw other than to say things like 'The Horror from the Hills' and 'the Idol moved!'"

      \n

      But she had brought the Box back with her. It was carved of teak, maybe Indian or Chinese. Professor Armitage examined it, and then sent it to the Orne Library Special Collections. And only people with the permission of the Select Committee were allowed to examine the collection.

      \n

      "Did Millicent get permission?" asked Sam.

      \n

      Professor Wilmarth admitted he was on the Committee, and had indeed granted Millicent permission. Sam asked for the same privilege, and after some hemming and hawing, the Professor gave in.

      \n

      [Flattery spend by SP.]

      \n
      \n

      \n
      \nEpisode VI: Broken Night (Part 5)\n

      Charleston and Helen decided to take a tour of the town to get the lay of the land. "We have a Miskatonic where I'm from," said Helen. "Big research school."

      \n

      "I hear the same about this one," said Charleston. He ambled up to a gangly looking senior. "Say, man, where's the fun places around here?"

      \n

      "There are some coffee houses around. They play folk music there mostly," he replied.

      \n

      "I don't mean fun like that. I mean, this place has a reputation that's a bit haunted\u2014"

      \n

      "That's overblown, old-timer. I didn't come here for any mumbo-jumbo. My dad came here, and I'm going to end up with a good job in Boston."

      \n

      "Waste of my time," Charleston muttered darkly. He and Helen went to the campus bookstore and bought a Fighting Squids pennant.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Sam spent the rest of the day combing through the archives. A surprising amount of things had been donated by a Freddie Blakely, by the name didn't mean anything to him. Finally he located the boxes that should have had anything from the Pyrenees expedition, but they were empty.

      \n

      He spent some more time trying to find the right box, but eventually had to go back to the grad student who had been left in charge to try and run through the history of people who had requested the Pyrenees artifacts, guessing one of them had removed the Box. He narrowed it down to a coed named Yolanda Vierge, who had studied for a single semester in 1947. It seemed, according to campus scuttlebutt, that she had been very close to Professor Wilmarth.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Candace, Temperance and Jimmy dropped in on Artlife. "We're an artists' collective," the nice middle-aged lady explained to them. They offered reduced rent to working artists in their building.

      \n

      "I'm very interested in staying there," said Candace. "I'm working on finishing my new novel and could use some isolation."

      \n

      "Oh, you're that Candace Heartbrooke! I loved your novel! Great, great, very good..." While she worked on getting the paperwork, Temperance struck up a conversation with her. It seemed that one of the reasons she was so happy to hear that Candace was interested in the building was that nobody there had paid their rent in some time.

      \n

      [Negotiate use by TP.]

      \n

      "Artists not paying their rent, eh? How surprising," said Temperance.

      \n

      "A family friend was supposed to be living there," said Jimmy. "Millicent."

      \n

      "Miss Lowell? She hasn't paid her rent either, though of course we have the deposit..."

      \n

      "I'd be more than happy to cover her rent," said Candace. "So she won't be evicted."

      \n

      [TP and JP then shot rock paper scissors to decide who made the Negotiate spend to loosen up the Artlife lady.]

      \n

      After that, asking casually if they might get Millicent's spare key so they could check on her was easy enough. Lease in hand, they headed out to the Macallister building.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Millicent's apartment was #1FE. It was kept meticulously neat, except for a few romance novels and a couple of crime novels by J.R. Stolt. In the closet there was almost no clothing at all, just a nice suit, and a cocktail dress hanging forlornly and alone.

      \n

      "No suitcase," said Candace. "She packed up, these aren't everyday clothes."

      \n

      Jimmy pulled a note out of the mirror frame it had been wedged in. "Just says to contact Erica Grey in Sacramento if she isn't back by February," he said.

      \n

      Temperance pulled open the desk drawer and found a sketch map of the building...she thought. There were scrawled notes on it: "Roses." "Bread and Butter." Along the edge of the map doors had been drawn in pencil.

      \n

      Charleston flopped down on the bed, pulled open the nightstand drawer, and came up with a pile of typewritten pages. They seemed to form a screenplay of some kind. The beginning and end seemed to be missing, but as he flipped through it he kept track of the names of the characters: Thomas Manuel, Roger Carom, Louise Post. All of them had been listed on the building directory in the lobby.

      \n

      "Helen, run through this script with me," he said.

      \n

      "What kind of ridiculous thing is this?' she mutter. "But all right\u2026

      DOG: Woof, woof."

      "Uh...Line?" said Charleston.

      \nEpisode VI: Broken Night (Part 6)\n

      They went to the apartment opposite Millicent's and knocked on the door. The man who opened it was wearing an artist's smock, streaked with various shades of paint. Temperance asked if he knew the woman across the hall.

      \n

      "Lily?" the man said. "Yeah, I knew her."

      \n

      "What?" said Jimmy. "Lily?"

      \n

      "Sure, her name was Millicent but I called her Lily. Tom Manuel," the man said, holding out his hand.

      \n

      "Do you know when she'll be back?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "Oh, she's probably left Arkham. She was a free spirit. Come on in."

      \n

      They filed past him. "I like your work," said Candace, who had seen a few of his paintings in Cambridge galleries. "Candace Heartbrooke. Novelist. Homefront?" she trailed off.

      \n

      "I don't read a lot of women's literature."

      \n

      [Counterculture 2+ snagged the name & reputation of Manuel.]

      \n

      The room was austere and bare: no books, no record player, no radio. There was not even an easel; the only thing interesting that Jimmy saw was a large reel-to-reel recorder.

      \n

      "The manager lets me paint downstairs," said Manuel, noticing Candace's surprised look.

      \n

      "Do you have to share the space with anyone?"

      \n

      Michelle and Roger were writers, Manuel said, and Louise was an illustrator. So he was the only serious artist, and the only painter. Jimmy asked about the tape recorder; Manuel said he should probably get rid of it, like he had done with his books and music, but it was a gift from his parents. Still, it was just a distraction, like the other things. He should probably get rid of it.

      \n

      Temperance frowned. Manuel's body language indicated that he was lying; but his eyes didn't show the signs of fabrication. Could it be that he didn't know he was lying?

      \n

      [BS Detector 1-point spend.]

      \n

      Jimmy flipped on the tape player. He didn't hear anything from the speakers, just the low hiss of tape speeding past the magnetic heads. "Hey!" said Manuel. "Stop screwing with my stuff! Coming into my house when it's almost dark..."

      \n

      "You afraid of the dark?" said Charleston.

      \n

      "No. Of course not. Just...it's almost dark...look, I don't know what happened to that girl. Why don't you go ask Michelle or Roger, or creepy Louise on the top floor."

      \n

      \u201cSorry about the player,\u201d said Temperance. \u201cCome along, father,\u201d she said to Jimmy.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      The grad student Sam had been berating offered to give him a ride. "That's good," said Sam. "I'm really high on meth."

      \n

      "Why do people always tell me when they're high!" the poor kid moaned. "Where do you want to go?"

      \n

      "Interesting question," began Sam, but then hurried on when he got a withering glance from the kid. "That artists' colony building."

      \n

      "The MacAllister? They're all weirdos in there. I used to see one of them around, Louise Post. She's an illustrator, does a lot of science fiction magazines. Met her at a convention once. Robert Heinlein was there!"

      \n

      [In the original text of Tatters of the King there's a possibility to have Aleister Crowley make a cameo; when casting around for the 1950s equivalent, I pondered using RAH, but never was able to get him in.]

      \n

      "That's great," said Sam. "You have any keggers around here?"

      \n

      "Yeah, of course. I don't know where they are, I'm a grad student. Don't have time anymore. I used to see Louise around, bought her a cup of coffee. Trying to make her, to be honest. Guess the last time was before Halloween. Columbus Day, that neighborhood has a lot of immigrants, so it's a big deal."

      \n

      He dropped Sam off as the shadows were growing long in the street. He buzzed the door. "Let me in, I'm coming down," he told Jimmy, who answered the buzz.

      \n

      "Doesn't he mean coming up?" said Temperance. Jimmy shook his head.

      \n

      They split up. Jimmy and Temperance went up a flight and knocked on Michelle Vanfitz's door. It opened with a jerk. Ms. Vanfitz was a shortish woman with even shorter hair, an assertive jut to her jaw, and eyes that showed appreciation for Temperance's charms. She was wearing a sleeveless tee shirt and men's dungarees. "Well hello," she purred at Temperance. "You from the building?"

      \n

      "We're looking for Millicent."

      \n

      "Oh, her. Come on in." She waved Temperance through but tried to close the door in Jimmy's face. "So sorry. Didn't see you there," she smirked.

      \n

      The room was wall-to-wall bookshelves, with a small couch in one corner. The books were all of philosophy and feminist criticism; Le deuxi\xe8me sexe was displayed prominently, and the few pieces of art were mostly paintings of Sappho. Well, of Sapphic themes, in any case. "Can I get you a drink?\u201d asked Michelle. \u201cIt's five o'clock."

      \n

      "Water is fine," said Temperance, clenching her jaw. "Did you know Millicent?"

      \n

      "Yeah, I would see her in the hallway. Creepy looking girl."

      \n

      "We\u2019re friends of hers, just in the neighborhood, on our way to...Maine. You have a lovely home. I like your books..."

      \n

      "Do you know them? De Beauvoir is an amazing writer. One is not born a woman, one becomes one, because in the eyes of society, women aren't human..."

      \n

      While she ranted, Jimmy cast a discerning eye around the room. The only thing unusual he noted was a copy of The King in Yellow\u2014the 1947 Penguin Classics edition, of course. He tried to point it out to Temperance, who was making little headway with her halfhearted interjections.

      \n

      "It seems like you have an interesting collection...Tropic of Cancer..."

      \n

      "I only keep that out for the zeitgeist. Miller is a pig," said Michelle.

      \n

      "Is that a copy of The King in Yellow?"

      \n

      "Oh, that. Not a good play. But it's really about the replacement of the patriarchy with a matriarchal culture. Let me explain..."

      \n

      "Time for my medicine," coughed Jimmy.

      \n

      "Right. The sun is going down. My father was the same way..." said Michelle.

      \n

      "Martha, is that you?" said Jimmy.

      \n

      "Uncle Jimmy, we've been through this," said Temperance, pushing them toward the door. "That's not Martha."
