      \nEpisode VI: Broken Night (Part 7)\n

      Candace tapped on Roger Carun's door. He proved to be a dapper, neatly dressed in slacks and a shirt and tie. He had fine features and delicate hands, and an accent from somewhere south of the Mason-Dixon line. "Should I know you?"

      \n

      "Perhaps. My name is Candace. I wanted to inquire about a friend of mine, Millicent."

      \n

      "Was she that dumpy little thing who lived down on the first floor? I knew her a little bit. We had a New Year's Eve party here, I got to talk to her a little bit. Where are my manners? Come on in."

      \n

      His apartment was rather, well, prissy: tastefully decorated, with elegant throw rugs and a couch in an understated modern style. On a large desk desperately trying to look like a French Empire piece was an expensive electric typewriter. He had a few bookcases; the one closest to the door had several science fiction novels displayed prominently, with one tilted so that guests could see that the author picture was of him.

      \n

      "Are you a new resident in the building?" said Carun.

      \n

      "No, but we're staying in Millicent's place until we can figure out where she went. I'm a writer."

      \n

      "Oh, I'm a writer too. I write science fiction. I wrote a series called Nightsea. I think that science fiction can be more than just about little green men with ray guns. What do you write, dear?"

      \n

      "Well...my style has changed a lot. I wrote a novel about my acceptance and growth after the death of my husband overseas," said Candace.

      \n

      "That was a terrible time. Were you a war widow? I was a war widower. My, uh, girlfriend died in the war. She was a very sweet, lady..."

      \n

      Candace tried to take it all in stride. "Lately I have let my writing be inspired by all sort of things. Have you ever been in San Francisco?"

      \n

      "Oh, I have spent quite a lot of time in San Francisco,\u201d said Roger. \u201cI really enjoyed the waterfront."

      \n

      "I made several friends out there, very inspiring."

      \n

      "It's about time that California made an impact on culture beyond those insipid movies. Whatever happened to Busby Berkeley? Now there was an artist."

      \n

      "That's an interesting thought."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Upstairs, Charleston and Sam knocked on Louise Post's door. "Who is it?" groaned a voice from inside.

      \n

      "We're friends of Millicent's," said Sam.

      \n

      "The door is open. You can come in if you want."

      \n

      The room was very dark. The lights were out, and the blinds were drawn. It was also filthy: empty boxes of Chinese food were scattered around, and papers were strewn everywhere.

      \n

      "Can we turn on the lights?" said Sam.

      \n

      "I'm afraid I'm rather light sensitive," said Louise. She was sitting far back in the room, in an armchair, shrouded in shadow. "I always was, but then I took some antibiotics and they made it much worse. I suppose you could sit near the door and use the reading lamp..."

      \n

      Charleston tapped his way inside, "blind" once again. "Reminds me of my place in New York. You aren't still sick? Is it contagious?"

      \n

      "No, not anymore," said Louise.

      \n

      "When was the last time you saw Millicent?" said Sam. In the dim light from the hall, he could see she was wearing dark glasses.

      \n

      Louise looked up at Charleston. "Oh, are you blind?" she said.

      \n

      "Yes, yes," said Charleston. Sam flicked on the reading lamp, and in the flare of light Charleston could see that Louise didn't have any eyes.

      \n

      [CP: That's all right, I'm not here to judge.]

      \n

      "I like your tie," she said to Charleston, who was wearing traditional Chinese clothing as usual.

      \n

      "Uh huh." Sam shook his head; he'd heard of something like this before, but it was pretty rare: a psychological disorder where despite organic blindness, the patient was convinced that they could actually see.

      \n

      "I'm working on several projects," said Louise. "They're not finished yet..."

      \n

      "How long have you been in this place?"

      \n

      "The sun is going down," said Louise, a bit strangely.

      \n

      "It has a tendency to do that," said Sam.

      \n

      "Then I can get to work." She pushed out of the chair and walked with determination over to her drafting desk. She took down a mirror and put it on the board next to her. "I hope you don't mind me working. Is that traditional Chinese clothes?" she said to Charleston.

      \n

      "I don't know," said Charleston. "I'm American."

      \n

      "What an interesting face. Do you mind if I use you as a reference?"

      \n

      "I'm flattered."

      \n

      She sketched him for a while, quite accurately. Then she looked up sharply. Her dark glasses slipped down her face, exposing her empty eyesockets. "Why did you do that?" she said to him sharply. "You could see before, but now you have eyes again. Why would you do that?"

      \n

      "I didn't do that," groused Charleston.

      \n

      "I didn't ask for this," muttered Sam. He watched Louise work. He could see her reflection in the mirror begin to change. It became indistinct but quite definitely not her reflection. Great, the LSD is coming back, he thought morosely.

      \n

      Whatever it was in the mirror tapped on the glass sharply.

      \n

      [And at this point everyone in the building lost a point of Stability as night fell.]

      \n

      "In a minute. I'm busy," said Louise grumpily. "Now about your eyes..."

      \n

      "It wasn't up to me!" said Charleston, loudly. "I didn't have a choice!"

      \n

      "Well. Maybe you should look in the Box. I keep it under the bed for safekeeping."

      \n

      "Don't let me interrupt your work," said Charleston.

      \n

      "You couldn't if you wanted to."

      \n

      "Wait," said Sam. "Yolanda? No? Okay, then how do you have the Box?"

      \n

      She had gone to Miskatonic, Louise explained, about six months ago. She had been searching in their occult section, looking for inspiration for a science fiction magazine cover she had been hired to paint. Instead, she found the Box; it had been misfiled. She hadn't wanted to steal it, but somehow she couldn't leave it...so she took it home, and began looking at what was in it. And then she had shown it to other people.

      \n

      "When did you show it to Millicent?" asked Sam.

      \n

      She had had to wait until Millicent got around to asking her; and she had to wait until night, of course. She hadn't waited for everyone to ask her directly, but Thomas had looked right away. Roger had taken a while\u2014he wasn't that interested. Michelle, on the other hand, had wanted to look immediately.

      \n

      Charleston meanwhile had slid the Box out from under the bed. It wasn't very big, but it was ornately carved in a language that wasn't Chinese or Hindi. While Charleston fiddled with it, Sam shot up some Yellow.

      \n

      [Sam's first experience with Yellow!]

      \n

      When the first shock of the hit subsided, he could see a staircase in the middle of the room that hadn't been there before. He also felt some change in the space, as if the apartment had suddenly sprouted several more rooms. As he blinked, deliriously, a shabby old basset hound came creeping down the stairs. It sat there, halfway up, and wagged its tail.

      \nEpisode VI: Broken Night (Part 8)\n

      Down in Michelle's room, as night fell she excused herself, saying she needed to change. Jimmy and Temperance waited a long, uncomfortable time. After a while they could hear music coming from far away...but inside the room. As if there was suddenly more space there.

      \n

      They decided to take the opportunity and fled downstairs. The door to Thomas' apartment was open, and they could see him lowering a microphone attached by a long cable to his reel-to-reel recorder through a hole in the floor. "Hi guys," he said when he noticed them. "You're the ones who were asking about Lily. Millicent. Yeah, I kind of envy her; she figured it out and found the way. Upstairs. With that guy on six, the book salesman. We had a going-away party for her, since she was going to go find her way..."

      \n

      Yes, she had gone up the stairs to the sixth floor, he answered in reply to Jimmy's question. Past the green room. In the night floors.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      "Oh, the sun has gone down," said Roger Carun, taking Candace's empty teacup. "I'm going to go dress for dinner. Would you like to come with me? Yes? Good, I'll be just a moment." He padded off to his bedroom.

      \n

      When he came back he was wearing nothing but suspenders, dance tights, and nipple clips. "Oh, I'm only half-dressed," he clucked to himself, picking up a bowler hat and placing it on his head at a jaunty angle.

      \n

      "Is there a party?" said Candace with aplomb.

      \n

      "There's always a party up on seven," said Roger.

      \n

      "I'm up for a party."

      \n

      She followed him up to the third floor, and then to the fourth floor...which hadn't been there before. "This building has more floors than I can count," he replied to her question. "Come with me to the Green Room."

      \n

      They emerged into what she was surprised to see looked like a green room, for a television show or a theater\u2014a waiting place where actors or guests could relax before going onstage. There was a table laden with food, much of it strange to her eyes. In one corner was a cabinet filled with bottles of what she guessed was alcohol\u2014there weren't any labels on most of them. The other corner had a walk-in humidor, which was definitely unusual.

      \n

      The lighting fixtures were gas, not electric, and there were buggy whips hung by the door. The magazines scattered around the tables were all from the end of the nineteenth century. On the walls were pictures, as most places like this had\u2014usually they were pictures of past productions, or celebrity actors. But as she looked closer, she saw that most of these pictures were pornographic, and many featured people with disabilities or deformities in them.

      \n

      [Me: Basically, it's Tod Browning's Freaks meets Eyes Wide Shut, that should get you there.]

      \n

      "This is a bit intense," she said.

      \n

      "Honey, this is just the green room,\u201d said Carun. \u201cWait til you get on stage...well, I assume there's a stage somewhere."

      \n

      "I'm not a performer, I'm a writer."

      \n

      "So am I, but trust me, I perform. Tell me, do you like getting whipped?"

      \n

      "No."

      \n

      "Quelle dommage. We had a spot for a girl in tonight's festivities. No matter. To be honest, I didn't really need a girl in it."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      "I'm interested in the King in Yellow," said Sam to Louise.

      \n

      "The play?"

      \n

      "The person."

      \n

      "I only know the play. I don't know any person."

      \n

      "Where's Millicent?"

      \n

      "She's gone. She found the Way. The Way forward...I guess. I don't know where it goes, I haven't found it yet. It's somewhere up on the Night Floors."

      \n

      "Why don't you go up there?" asked Charleston.

      \n

      "I do. But I'm just busy," she said, frowning. She tapped hard on the mirror.

      \n

      Charleston flipped through her portfolio. All the sketches were of a horrific nuclear holocaust. They had been commissioned by her client, she said. She didn\u2019t want to talk about them. Not in front of him.

      \n

      Charleston was still holding the box. Louise yelled at him as he began to walk toward the stairs. That was her Box. He couldn't take it outside her room! It was hers! She wasn't going to be fooled by people like him. No, he wasn't her comrade. He might get lost\u2014of course people got lost up there! Yes, Millicent had found the way. It was the way she said it, there was no doubt.

      \n

      Sam was practically pawing at the Box. With a sigh, Charleston opened it up.

      Inside was a sculpture, of rods and hemispheres. It was about the size of the inside of the box. It almost seemed to be breathing, somehow. Charleston tried to follow the pattern with his eyes, but he got lost in the myriad connections of it. Perspective seemed to be just wrong, like it was suspended. But then it was filling most of the area around him.

      \n

      \n

"I've been trying to get back into that fake reality for decades." He looked up and saw the dog sitting on the staircase. He ambled over and patted it on the head. It barked.

      [1 point Stability loss to Jimmy here.]

      \n

      "Jimmy, you need a distraction," said Charleston. "Maybe you could go fetch me something." He described the Box and told Jimmy where to find it under her bed.

      \n

      Jimmy dashed down the stairs and back into Louise's room. She was engrossed in her work, bent over her mirror. "Tell me again how beautiful I am," she said. Jimmy slipped past her, reached under the bed, and came up with the Box. He was back upstairs before she had time to look up.

      \n

      [Infiltration test here; JP scored an extra success and went with "Quick".]

      \xa0

      \n

      Temperance studied the map. "We need to get out of here. These people scare the hell out of me.

      \n

      "Temperance, you should be more open," said Candace.

      \n

      "That man has clamps on his nipples!"

      \n

      "You'd like some?" said Roger, holding out a pair.

      \n

      "Nope nope nope!" said Temperance, trying to shrink into herself. There was a way through. There had to be! Millicent found it...and she began to see a way, to move through this strange half-world, somewhere on the fringes of Carcosa. But she knew enough to realize that there was no leaving this building by the front door anymore.

      \n

      It was difficult. She was beginning to suspect that Millicent somehow didn't think like normal people...or maybe people in general. A check mark in the margins might mean something to her, but was opaque to her. But gradually she seemed to be able to find a route: landmarks, turnings, sometimes just an attitude. The Way.

      \n

      [Cthulhu Mythos spend here by TP; 3 Stability and 1 Sanity.]

      \n

      "Follow me, everyone," she said, striding forward with her best imitation of confidence.

      \nEpisode VI: Broken Night (Part 10)\n

      The Night Floors. They seemed endless, miles of corridors decorated in 1890s style, all threadbare silk wallpaper and sconces for gas lamps, faded photographs of men and women in old-fashioned clothes dotting the walls. They walked on and on, over staircases that they climbed and past ones they avoided, depending on Temperance's advice, but gradually they climbed higher and higher.

      \n

      They passed doors, locked, and doors, open. Some doors had been broken in, and some rooms didn't have doors at all; the rooms beyond were yawning abscesses in the building, full of dust and bricks and broken furniture.

      \n

      But other rooms were handsomely done in an elegant Art Deco style. When they were near those, they sometimes saw people dressed in evening clothes, quickly walking far down the corridors from them. Some wore masks as well.

      \n

      Now and again they would hear the sound of parties, or snatches of music. Once they heard the sound of gunfire. Temperance found a goldfish carved out of marble, with fantastically well done detail. She put it in her purse.

      \n

      Candace wandered into a beautifully decorated salon, full of books with bindings that looked at least 60 years old. They were all by her, all books she had never written. She found a faded, sepia-toned photograph of herself, dressed in turn of the century clothes. "The Authoress." said the caption.

      \n

      [2 points of Stability here.

      \n

      HP: Are we in Carcosa again?

      \n

      Me: Let's just say that you could take suburban rail to there from here. (In conductor's voice) "Change at Jamaica for Babylon, Carcosa, Huntington Station, and Ronkonkoma."

      \n

      TP: Wait...]

      \n

      Charleston stumbled upon a little girl. She was dancing around alone in a ballroom. She was wearing a white gauze mask and whirling around, singing:

      \n

      Strange is the night when the black stars rise

      \n

      And strange moons circle in the skies

      \n

      But stranger still is

      \n

      Lost Carcosa

      \n

      Charleston backed away and closed the door behind him.

      \n

      Temperance felt something move in her purse. She opened it and a goldfish, a living...well, dying goldfish flopped out.

      \n

      [Aaaand 2 points of Stability.]

      \n

      Sam heard the sound of lovemaking from behind a door, quite vigorous as it seemed. He shrugged; it didn't have anything to do with his mission. So he ignored it, just like he ignored the shrieks of terror that suddenly burst out.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Jimmy was paying attention to the people they would sometimes see at a distance. He noticed that they kept running into one person in particular: he was dressed in a business suit of 1920s vintage, with a camelhair overcoat draped over his shoulders. He wore a mean looking fedora and was carrying a beat-up leather book bag. He noticed Jimmy staring at him and lit up a cigar, grinning in a malicious way. Then he strode off.

      \n

      [Sense Trouble test here.]

      \n

      His attention was drawn by the figure, which is why he didn't see the door open next to Temperance and a skeletal figure tumble into the hallway. He grabbed Temperance. "No, no, don't hurt me!" he shrieked.

      \n

      "It's all right, we're not here to hurt you," she said in her most soothing voice. Still, it had an effect. He calmed down slightly and begged her for food.

      \n

      She shook out the last of the paper bag of trail mix she had been munching on (her father taught her long ago to never leave the house without iron rations, as he called them.) The man quickly ate up every crumb. Then he looked up. "You're not wearing masks," he said. "Oh my God. Are you real?"

      \n

      "Yes. What's your name?"

      \n

      "I'm Josh. I'm a TV repairman. I came to repair a TV and things got weird. I just stayed a little late and then I couldn't find my way out! What year is it?"

      \n

      "1956."

      \n

      "Oh no! I came here in 1955!"

      \n

      "It's just January," said Temperance. She took his hand. "Come with us. We're getting out of here."

      \n

      Josh explained that the only food he could find was stale champagne and leftover food from the parties that he heard from time to time. He had tried but he could never find a way out.

      \n

      "We will find it together," said Temperance. "God will provide!"

      \n

      "There is no God here!" wailed Josh.

      \n

      Jimmy smacked him. "Calm down," he growled, and slowly lowered his fist, shaking. Don't give in, he thought.

      \n

      [2 points of Stability lost, but there was a benefit...]

      \n

      He felt a dog licking his hand. He slowly lowered his gaze. "Betty?" he whispered. The dog howled, and he hugged it.

      \n

      "The dog is back," said Temperance. "Didn't the dog die? The dog died. I have a fish in my purse and a TV repairman, and now the dog is back. How can I see it?"

      \n

      Betty was howling and yelping joyfully. "I think I'm just going a little crazy," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "But how would that make me see the dog?" said Temperance. Jimmy ignored her and hugged Betty again. "I'm so sorry for what happened to you," he said to her.

      \n

      "That's all right, Jimmy," said Betty.

      \n

      Jimmy paused, straightened up, and walked down the hallway.

      \n

      [JP: I'm not waiting for you to ask, taking away 1-point of Stability.]

      \n

      "Candace, the dog is talking," said Temperance.

      \n

      "We've seen some strange things," replied Candace placidly.

      \n

      "We have to leave here. We have to go through. Though I think that will bring us back to Carcosa."

      \n

      "Are we going to Carcosa, girl?" said Jimmy to Betty.

      \n

      "Woof."

      \n

      "Are you stuck there."

      \n

      "Woof? Woof."

      \n

      "Betty, can you talk?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "Woof."

      \n

      "We heard you use English!"

      \n

      "Woof."

      \n

      "One woof for yes, two woofs for no," tried Jimmy.

      \n

      "Woof?"

      \n

      "Is Jimmy your owner?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "Woof? Woof. Woof."

      \n

      "You're a sassy-pants," said Jimmy. "All the women in my life are sassy-pants."

      \n

      "I'm not sassy," said Temperance. "Why would you say I'm sassy? You take that back."

      \n

      "Not bossy either," said Jimmy.

      \nEpisode VI: Broken Night (Part 11)\n

      They kept walking. After a long time, Jimmy realized that the man with the book bag was following them. He glanced back, and saw the man scurry away. This time he gave into temptation and pursued him, followed by Charleston.

      \n

      They followed him past several turnings of the corridors until they came face to face with the man. They recognized him: N. Quincy Lund. As they approached, the vicious wounds on his face and chest opened up. Jimmy recognized his handiwork from when he had met Lund in Carcosa.

      \n

      "Don't go to pieces on me," said Charleston.

      \n

      "You're looking for the girl?\u201d said Quincy. \u201cYou won't find her. But I wish you luck."

      \n

      "Woof," barked Betty angrily.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Candace hadn't followed them. As she walked along the corridors, she heard the sound of furious typing. Curious, she followed it to its source: a narrow, overheated room like all the bad hotel rooms she had ever slept in, with peeling yellow wallpaper and a hissing radiator. Beyond the window was a vista of more rooms, more or less identical to this one.

      \n

      Seated at the typewriter was Amadou Lalin.

      \n

      "Amadou!" said Candace.

      \n

      "Who?"

      \n

      "Amadou?"

      \n

      "Amadou...Amadou...wait. I do know you..."

      \n

      "Candace."

      \n

      "Yes, we met at the conservatory. I have so much work to do on the screenplay. I'm the author...aren't I?"

      \n

      "I was wondering if you could maybe help me," she said. "As a friend."

      \n

      "Yes...we're friends...aren't we..."

      \n

      "I'm looking for a young woman named Millicent."

      \n

      "Oh," he said. "She's not really in the building anymore. She went through. All the way. But not to where you think she went...somewhere else...I have trouble remembering. You have the same problem."

      \n

      "Which problem?" she said.

      \n

      "Remembering things."

      \n

      "I remember things. I remember leaving you in Carcosa. You were finally home."

      \n

      "So you don't remember everything from the night at the theater."

      \n

      "I remember everything from that night.'

      \n

      "I don't think you do," he said. She noticed that blood was soaking his clothes, covering his face. "That was my vision of Carcosa. You don't think you left of your own will, do you? Let me show you what I had to do so you could leave."

      \n

      He pulled open a desk drawer and took a pistol out of it, placed it to his temple, and blew his brains out. Blood splattered all over Candace; bits of flesh and bone struck against the wall paper. She felt sick and shocked.

      \n

      [3 points of Stability lost.]

      \n

      Amadou put the pistol down on the desk. "That refresh your memory, Candace?" he said in a hectoring tone. "You sure you remember everything that's been going on? You don't even remember...well. After all, you're His favorite now, aren't you?"

      \n

      [TP & JP: Oooooooooooo...]

      \n

      "Excuse me?" she said.

      \n

      "You're his golden girl. He doesn't need me anymore. He wants you. He already has me."

      \n

      "I'm really not sure what you're talking about..."

      \n

      "You know EXACTLY what I'm talking about! You feel it every time you're writing now. It's getting stronger and stronger every time. You can feel Him in the room with you. You know who it is. You know what He wants. You know that he can give it to you. Typing away at your little book. The real Art? You know he can give you the real Art. I had it once. And look where that got me!"

      \n

      He picked up the pistol again, pushed it against his temple, and pulled the trigger again.

      \n

      Candace lurched back in her chair, chalk-white.

      \n

      "I guess now you'll finally start using your head," he leered. "Or just give Him what He wants. Just give in. It's so much better when you're through. Maybe YOU'RE the one who is going to do it right."

      \n

      "Just point me in her direction," she cried.

      \n

      "If you follow your heart you'll find it, I guess. After all. He likes you. He's not going to hurt you."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Temperance and Jimmy looked up as a figure covered in blood lurched down the hallway toward them. "What happened?" said Temperance when she saw it was Candace.

      \n

      "He shot himself. Twice," Candace said faintly.

      \n

      "Wait a minute..." said Jimmy.

      \n

      "What happened?" repeated Temperance.

      \n

      "Amadou. I found him. He was talking about...not remembering things...not knowing what was going on...then he shot himself. In the head. But he was still alive...and then he shot himself again..."

      \n

      Betty the dog walked up, put her paw on Candace's leg, and gave a reassuring woof.

      \n

      "I've been dealing with that," said Temperance.

      \n

      "Thank you!\u201d said Candace, stroking Betty\u2019s head. \u201cSomeone who understands."

      \n

      "Woof," said Betty.

      \n

      "This is what Alice felt like," said Temperance. "Where's the rabbit?"

      \n

      A white rabbit came bounding down the hallway. "Time to follow the rabbit!" she said in a strained voice, and pursued it, followed by the rest of them.

      \n

      \nEpisode VI: Broken Night (Part 12)\n

      As Temperance rounded a corner, she came upon a rather startling tableau, even for this place. A couple of men in tuxes were struggling with a man in an overcoat; behind them, a pretty blonde with a flapper's hairdo and a champagne colored evening gown cowered against the wall. But most surprising was that the man in the overcoat was wearing a weird mask: somewhat like a samurai mask, perhaps, except for the heavy filter equipment she saw around the mouth and nose\u2014Colonel Murphy had sold war surplus for a while, and she knew a gas mask when she saw it. The "eyes" of the mask were mirrored and glittered in the light from a nearby gas lamp. She raised her pistol at him.

      \n

      He looked up at her. "Guns can't stop me," he said in a voice that reverberated strangely from behind his mask.

      \n

      "Make me find out if that is true or not!" she said.

      \n

      "You will feel the wrath of the Penitent if you do not step back," the masked man said. "None can affect the Penitent. I inhabit your dreams." He took a few steps toward them. Until he saw Jimmy.

      \n

      "No! NO! You can't be!\u201d the 'Penitent' screamed. \u201cThe OTHER! No!" And unceremoniously he turned on one heel and ran.

      \n

      Jimmy shrugged. He walked over to the petrified woman in the evening gown. "I knew this place was strange but that was too much," she wailed.

      \n

      "What's your name?" he said.

      \n

      "Nellie. I'm here with my friends. We thought we would celebrate the first night of Prohibition by getting really tight."

      \n

      Temperance exchanged a glance with Jimmy. They retreated to the rest of the group and huddled up. "We need to take her with us," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "Woof," said Betty. Temperance scowled. "No! You have to talk to be part of the huddle! Where's that rabbit anyway?"

      \n

      "We've been dragging around the TV repairman," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "He's only been gone a year," said Sam. "She's been gone too long."

      \n

      "She'll come back and be...what, fifty-six?" said Temperance. "Or twenty. Even better!" Sam shrugged, making a mental note to contact some of his friends in the government when they got back. She would be very interesting.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      They kept walking, working their way upward and upward. Each floor had a variety of rooms and people, but there was a sameness to them. Even Temperance's screaming match with a man who might have been Socrates had a certain ennui.

      \n

      They didn't know how long they had been there; their watches had stopped as soon as they entered the Green Room.

      \n

      Eventually they came to a floor that was a little different: it wasn't as nice. The wallpaper was duller, the lightbulbs dimmer, the decor of the rooms more obviously tawdry. They were passing down another endless corridor when a door opened at the end of the hall. A man stepped out, wearing a sleeveless white undershirt, suspenders hanging around. He walked over to a water cooler and poured himself a glass of water, then turned around and re-entered his room. The door slammed behind him. He hadn't seemed to notice them at all.

      \n

      As they approached his door, they could see a sign next to it:

      \n
      \n

      CASTAIGNE

      \nNight Manager
      \n

      Temperance rapped on the door. "Hold on, hold on," came a voice from inside. He had a rather Yiddish accent. No, she reconsidered: it sounded something like that, but at the same time there was some alien quality to it.

      \n

      The door was pulled open from the inside. "Whaddaya want?" said the old man. "It's the middle of the night."

      \n

      "We need to get out."

      \n

      "Vat? Don't you have a lease? Come in, siddown. You want some tea?"

      \n

      "Yes," said Temperance. The room inside looked like any ordinary single-room occupancy in a big city: a cast iron bed frame with a sagging mattress, a rather worse-for-wear dresser with a shaving mirror propped up on it, a hot plate and a tarnished and blackened kettle. Nothing looked like it had been made after the 1930s.

      \n

      Mr. Castaigne put the kettle on the hotplate. "Ach, you can't get the good tea here," he said. "Not like it was in the old country, am I right? Whaddaya you know, you're not from the old country. Why am I talking to people like you for? Annoying! S'all right. You're a nice girl. Hey," he said, leveling a teaspoon in Betty's direction. "Who said you could bring that dog in here? It's a pest. I've been trying to get rid of it for years."

      \n

      "It's attached herself to him," said Temperance. "We'll take it with us when we leave."

      \n

      "It's my dog," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "Your dog has been a nuisance. Chewing on things, leaving messes on the carpet. This is a nice hotel! You should do something with her. I had a dog that couldn't be trained, I put him down."

      \n

      "In the basement?" said Sam.

      \n

      "No. I put it down. You don't speak English? Always the same since I come to this country. Just sit down, sit down. You're not even tenants. You have an agreement to come in?" He poured them all a cup of tea in some cracked teacups. Temperance noticed a thick scrapbook on the nightstand next to his bed.

      \n

      "If nobody minds, I'm going to take a little pear brandy," said Mr. Castaigne. Temperance reached from the scrapbook and flipped through the pages.

      \n

      "Ach, that's from so long ago," said Mr. Castaigne. "Look, there's Momma." The pictures looked old fashioned: sepia-toned, and showing people wearing stiff celluloid collars or Edwardian ruffles and hats. There were also newspaper clippings.

      \n

      Those disturbed her. The headlines were from New York papers in the 1920s and said things like, "Russo-Germanic Pact Crumbles! Prague Liberated!"

      \n

      "Did you fight in the war?" she said as calmly as she could.

      \n

      "Oh, the war, that was terrible. Things were so bad. Now, I'm here, so things could be worse. I could be homeless. I spent a year working for the Superintendent, what a meshugge he is..."

      \n

      "He was polite to us."

      \n

      "If you met the Super, he would not have been so polite," Castaigne began, but then he caught Candace's eye. "Oh. I see. I understand. I like it here. I like my job. Tell him that."

      \n

      "Did a girl named Millicent come through here?"

      \n

      "Milly, ah, she was so nice," said Castaigne. "She went up to the roof. Not far from here, you take the stairs. But you need the key."

      \n

      "Who has the keys?" said Candace.

      \n

      "I do. But how do I know I'll get them back from you?"

      \n

      "If you're so worried, you could come with us," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "Oh, no. I don't like to go out on the roof. And if the Super finds out that people are going on the roof, without a lease..."

      \n

      "I paid for Millicent's lease," said Candace. "So it's mine now."

      \n

      "Did they give you a receipt?" said Castaigne. "Let me see it." He slipped on a pair of half-spectacles and read over the papers Candace handed him. Then he took out a pad of yellow paper and wrote out a receipt. He stamped it, and handed it with the other papers back to Candace. She looked at the seal he had put on the receipt: it writhed strangely in the dim light.

      \n

      The Yellow Sign.

      \n

      "I'm glad we took care of all that," said Castaigne. "I'll open the door for you. I didn't mean to cast no aspersions. If you vouch for these gonifs, I'll take you there. Are you...are you sure you want to go out there?"

      \n

      "We have no choice," said Candace coldly.

      \n

      "You know you can see the stars out there."

      \n

      "That would be lovely."

      \n

      "Lovely, she says. Well, your funeral. I'll always have to deal with people like you. But then I'm the Night Manager. I'll always be the Night Manager."

      \n

      \nEpisode VI: Broken Night (Part 13)\n

      Castaigne took them up a long, long spiral staircase. After a while they seemed to ascend outside, somehow, with a vast darkling plain of thousands of rooms many hundreds of feet below them, all without ceilings, all spreading off into infinity, it seemed. Finally, they reached a door that blocked the staircase.

      \n

      "Well, I'm not one for ceremony," said Castaigne, unlocking the door and then backing down below them on the staircase. "It's been nice knowing all of you."

      \n

      "When did you come here?" asked Sam.

      \n

      "A long time ago. To be honest...it feels like I've always been here. Many years ago, I read a book. Called The King in Yellow. Caused me to end up in a mental institution. Had a little trouble with my cousin. There was a death involved. Fortunately, the Superintendent was willing to give me a job here. If you want, I could see if he had a place for you."

      \n

      "I think he knows me."

      \n

      "Yes. Yes, he does, Dr. Acererak. As for you, Mr. Chiu, you're no worse than waitlisted for this place."

      \n

      Jimmy pulled open the door. "Come on, girl," he said.

      \n

      Betty cowered at the threshold, whining. "You afraid to go out?" he said. She whimpered.

      \n

      He thought about picking her up. He gazed into her eyes, and noticed for the first time they were no longer the deep mahogany brown he had known for a decade. They had turned yellow.

      \n

      "Woof," said Betty, knowing that he understood.

      \n

      "It was good seeing you again," he said.

      \n

      "Woof. See you around, Jimmy," she said, and padded back down the stairs.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Temperance stepped out onto the roof and stopped dead. "The...the...the stars..." she said. She felt her knees turning to water.

      \n

      All around her the cosmos was arrayed.

      \n

      Galaxies lazily unwound, trailing tendrils of stars; she could see the flashes of supernovae in their cores. Dust clouds blurred past, planets congealing out of them. It was impossible to take in at once. Her mind quailed. She was in awe.

      \n

      [And down 2 points of Stability.]

      \n

      The roof was made of obsidian, it seemed: perfectly reflective, glossy black, and smooth as glass. It gave all of them vertigo as they huddled together: they couldn't see where the roof ended but they knew the edge was out there somewhere, and beyond it that terrible void.

      \n

      As their eyes adjusted to the light, they saw doorways. They looked perfectly ordinary, if made of stone. Yellow light radiated dimly from them, but they couldn't see what was beyond the threshold.

      \n

      Sam handed Charleston his flask of "reality enhancer." Jimmy whistled slowly. "Amazing," he said softly.

      \n

      [Anyone with Astronomy only lost 1 point of Stability, because the sight was so cool. Sam and Charleston only saw the stars of an incredibly dark and clear night, but I ruled they were ineligible for making the Sense Trouble roll I called for at this point.]

      \n

      Temperance felt the hairs on the back of her neck stand up. She caught a glimpse of something\u2014a figure\u2014darting past one of the doorways. "There's something out there," she said. "Living. Sentient. The Night Manager was afraid of the Super..."

      \n

      [Sense Trouble; TP scored an additional benefit, which was "Safe".]

      \n

      "We need to find the right door," said Jimmy.

      \n

      "What doors?" said Charleston. "The doors are a lie! Wait! I sound like one of them now!"

      \n

      Jimmy peered into the darkness. He saw a double-star system flash briefly behind one of the doorways. It seemed strangely familiar. "That one!" he said, and lurched toward it, sliding and slipping across the slick floor. He held fast to Temperance's hand, and out of the corner of his eye he saw her forming a human chain with the rest of them. Something was moving toward them, he could feel it. The ground became covered with frost, which let him slip into an awkward but rapid bellyslide through the lintel...

      \n

      [Athletics test here, with everyone piggybacking and the NPCs not being very helpful. But they got a 16, which was actually enough to claim a benefit: JP went with "Fast".]

      \n

      ...and he fell.

      \n

      He fell and fell, tumbling through empty space, shrieking as he hit terminal velocity. The last thing he saw was Temperance shoot away at a right angle as suddenly he felt a vast constriction...

      \n

      \nEpisode VI: Broken Night (Part 14)\n

      Temperance slowly returned to consciousness, but she kept her eyes tightly closed. There was a loud knocking somewhere nearby but she was ignoring it.

      \n

      The knocking became more insistent.

      \n

      She sat up and looked around in confusion. She was wearing a nightgown and sitting up in a small bed. There was a window nearby; the grey light of early morning was coming in around the edges of the windowshades. In the dimness she saw the vague outlines of what looked like a typical, if unfamiliar, studio apartment.

      \n

      The knocking was coming from the door. "Come on, little miss," said a voice behind the door. "Open up."

      \n

      She got up and opened the door a crack. Through it she saw a face that she recognized, although it was changed: twenty years older than she had ever seen it, for one thing, and not covered with the fine tracery of tattoos. But without a doubt, it was Charlie, the man from her dreams, her spirit guide. A man who had been dead for going on twenty years.

      \n

      He was wearing a uniform that was so dark a blue it looked black. She wasn't familiar with the cut or the insignia; they looked vaguely military, but civilianized somehow. A policeman's uniform, perhaps.

      \n

      "Aren't you ready? Didn't you get my call?" he said.

      \n

      "Charlie?" she said in a low voice.

      \n

      "Yes, it's Charlie, Detective. Aren't you going to get dressed? Get your uniform on!"

      \n

      "Charlie, what are you doing here?"

      \n

      He sighed, a familiar sound but one that send shocks down her spine, because she was hearing it, not with her mind's ear but in waking, living life. "I told you. We have a case."

      \n

      "I'll...be down in a minute?"

      \n

      "Please. Just get your uniform on, I'll be just outside. Oh, here." He passed her a paper cup of coffee. It looked startlingly familiar, the blue and white Grecian pattern of any New York City coffeeshop. Down to the cheery "New York's Best Coffee!" printed on one side.

      \n

      "Right. I'll get dressed and then we'll work the case...partner..." she said.

      \n

      "That's very nice, little miss, but I'm not your partner," he said through the door.

      \n

      "I always saw you that way."

      \n

      "Yeah, yeah. Come on, Major, let's go."

      \n

      She turned on the lights. On a chair, neatly folded, she saw a black uniform. It had a double-breasted tunic and jodhpurs. A pair of knee-high patent leather boots went with it, along with a peaked cap. She put them all on and then opened the door.

      \n

      "Hey, where's your armband?" said Charlie.

      \n

      She went back to the chair. There was a blue armband there, with a stylized eagle picked out in yellow in the center. Next to it were the initials RSA.

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n

      \n\nSeptember 2017 \n

      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode VI: Broken Night (Part 15)\n

      Charleston came to naked in a room. Early morning light shone in from a hole in the ceiling. What he could see of the room was a perfect match for the impromptu skylight: fallen plaster, dust, a mildewed couch: some abandoned building, then.

      \n

      Helen hove into view next to him, also naked. She looked around. "Did we...fall?"

      \n

      "I'm pretty sure we did," he said, standing up. He found a grey suit in a heap nearby. It seemed to be his size, so and he slid into it. Helen blinked and looked around. "Oh no," she said softly, and then much louder. "No!" She ran out the room and he could hear her descending a flight of stairs. From below, he heard her scream out "NO!" again. He gathered up her clothes and followed her.

      \n

      At the bottom of the stairs he emerged into a vast ruined space that looked a little like a hotel lobby. "What's with all the noise?" he said. He tossed Helen's dress at her. She caught it and pulled it on, face red with anger and frustration. And fear.

      \n

      Outside he could see a public square with broad avenues radiating away from it; for a moment it reminded him of Paris, but the buildings nearby were skyscrapers that had never graced a Parisian roofline.

      \n

      And then he saw the arch. And he knew where he was, but he didn't know how.

      \n

      It was the arch in Washington Square. In New York City. He turned away from the entrance and looked above the ruins of what seemed to be a reception desk of some kind. Written in faded gilt letters was the legend, "SUICIDE CENTER."

      \n

      "Why are we back? Why are we back?" shouted Helen. "You're just a figment of my imagination! You're a drug hallucination! I feel sober! How is this possible?"

      \n

      "I don't know. Am I your conscience, like Jimminy Cricket? Because if I am, then you're screwed." He threw an arm over her and led her outside.

      \n

      Parked nearby was an enormous car that could only be a limousine, although he couldn't place the make of the car at all; it seemed to resemble cars from the 1930s or 40s, all chrome fairing and bulbous hood. A man in a uniform stood nearby. He coughed politely.

      \n

      "Party leader?" he said.

      \n

      "Just a moment," said Charleston. He pulled Helen aside. "What the hell is a suicide center?" he said, looking at the building. It looked like some kind of cross between a hotel and a theater.

      \n

      "People would go in there. There were machines up there. But it closed in 1923, and this feels like 1955. Or 1956, I guess." It certainly was cold enough to be New York in winter.

      \n

      There was a pin with a symbol he didn't recognize stamped on it in the lapel of his suit. The man in the uniform strode over to him, holding a warm wool overcoat out. He helped Charleston into it, and as he slipped his arms through the sleeves he noticed an armband tied around one of them; on it was a stylized eagle.

      \n

      "Symbol of America," he said in a low voice to Helen.

      \n

      "Of course!" she hissed back. "This is the USA."

      \n

      "What are we doing down here?"

      \n

      "I told you when I met you, I used to like to come down here and take pictures! Figment of my imagination, from a drug hallucination of some other Earth." She turned around in agitation, and then froze, staring through the gaping door of the Suicide Center at something on the ground inside.

      \n

      On the floor of the lobby was a beat up old Brownie camera.

      \n

      "Calm down, we were down here taking pictures. You passed out and had some weird dream. In the dream I wasn't a very stand-up guy but here I seem to have more...stature, right?"

      \n

      "You have a limo waiting for you," she sniffed.

      \n

      "Waiting for us, babe. You want to go get something to eat? What's wrong?"

      \n

      "You're wearing the armband of someone in the Inner Party. I didn't know you were so high up."

      \n

      "Me neither!"

      \n

      "I didn't know you were in the Party!"

      \n

      "Me neither!"

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Candace awoke with a start. Her head was resting on a desk. Stacks of papers covered everything her head didn't. She sat up. She was sitting in a very nice leather armchair. She picked up one of the sheets of paper. "Request for Information Cancellation," it said.

      \n

      She picked up another. "Speech outline to be given by Party Secretary," this one read. There was a tap at the door and a woman in a business suit stuck her head in. "Oh! Mrs. Heartbrooke! Did you sleep at your desk again?"

      \n

      "I must have," said Candace.

      \n

      "We seem to have a situation," said the woman. "We need you to come handle something, that's all they told me. Somebody from the government. But hush-hush. There's not going to be a 37-6 on this or anything. There's a car waiting downstairs."

      \n

      "What is it about?" said Candace, getting up and shrugging into a suit jacket she found hanging from a coat rack in one corner of the room.

      \n

      "I think it's about some muckity-muck who died," said the woman as they walked out of the office.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Temperance sat in the back seat of a black car. She had tried to get into the front seat, next to Charlie, but he angrily forced her out of it. "Major, what's wrong with you?" he said. "Were you out drinking? You don't drink!"

      \n

      "No, I was just thinking about a case," she deflected.

      \n

      "If your father thought you were drinking, I'd really be in dutch," said Charlie. "The Admiral is an important man."

      \n

      "Of course, of course."

      \n

      "So the story is some bigwig got himself killed last night. Case looks really weird. We're supposed to go over there and cover everything up. Or find out who did it, I mean. At least, somebody who did it. His personal secretary is going to meet us at his place." Charlie flipped through his notebook, keeping considerably less than one eye on the road as they sailed through traffic lights, siren blaring. "Here it is. Some dame named Millicent Lowell. The Wright Foundation has always been a bit in skew with the party, but what they're going to say when they find out Jimmy Wright got killed, I don't know."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      \n
      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 1)\n

      \xa0

      \n
      \n

      That's a funeral in the mirror

      \nAnd it's stopping at your face.
      That's right, it's come to this,
      Yes it's come to this,
      And wasn't it a long way down,
      Ah wasn't it a strange way down?
      \u2014Leonard Cohen
      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Charlie stopped in front of an apartment building and Candace slid into the backseat next to Temperance.

      \n

      "How are you this morning?" said Temperance. She eyed Candace warily; she wasn't sure if this was her Candace, or some doppelganger.

      \n

      "You two know each other?" said Charlie. "From the admiral's dinners or something, right?"

      \n

      "Visit any new places lately?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "Just here," said Candace evenly.

      \n

      "Say, what do you think of the Van Carlyle Trio?" said Temperance. "Think they've gotten better?"

      \n

      "I think they were good to begin with," said Candace.

      \n

      "True," said Temperance slowly. "Charlie, what do you think of them?"

      \n

      "The who?" said Charlie, making a sudden left turn. Against the light.

      \n

      "Not the Who, the Van Carlyle Trio," said Temperance

      \n

      "Roger Carlyle's got a band now?"

      \n

      [Shout out to Masks of Nyarlathotep, of course.]

      \n

      "What genre would you say they are?" said Temperance to Candace.

      \n

      "Jazz," said Candace.

      \n

      "You like jazz, Charlie?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "I dunno. It's hard to find nowadays," said Charlie.

      \n

      "Do me a favor," said Temperance. "There's a diner up ahead that I like. Pull up there."

      \n

      "I thought you said that place wasn't any good?" said Charlie.

      \n

      "I want comfort food, all right!"

      \n

      "Sure thing, Major," said Charlie. "Just remember we're supposed to be\u2014"

      \n

      "Guy's not going to get any deader," said Temperance. They screeched to a halt and she jumped out of the car, followed by Candace. They swept into the diner. It was a respectable enough New York coffee shop, padded swivel stools along a counter, wooden booths along the walls, the smell of burnt coffee and bacon frying.

      \n

      "Gimme a bagel," said Temperance to the counter guy.

      \n

      "Bagels?" he said. "We haven't had those in years. They only started letting, you know, those people back in a few years ago. I gotta buttered roll, Major."

      \n

      "Yeah, fine," said Temperance. "Candace, I have to powder my nose. Care to join me?"

      \n

      "What the heck is going on?" hissed Temperance once they were safely inside the Ladies'.

      \n

      "I don't know," said Candace, "but I think we're back in Carcosa."

      \n

      "Is this what drugs is like?" said Temperance wildly.

      \n

      "Only with certain kinds," said Candace.

      \n

      "Who are you in this world?" said Temperance. "I seem to be a Major, people salute me..."

      \n

      "Something in the propaganda office, I think," said Candace. "Have you seen any of the others?"

      \n

      "Just Charlie," said Temperance.

      \n

      "Who's Charlie?" said Candace.

      \n

      "Oh, he was my mother's Dreamtime mentor. He's been mine ever since he died," said Temperance, unhelpfully. "It's all real, all on the up and up, but he doesn't remember anything. I have a theory..."

      \n

      "We're in Carcosa," said Candace.

      \n

      "Nobody's wearing masks! I think we altered the timeline," said Temperance. "Superman #25. He fell through a time portal that was made by Dr. T. O. Morrow. He caught the criminal, but it changed time."

      \n

      "All we were doing was following Millicent's trail," said Candace.

      \n

      "Maybe Millicent's the one who changed time!" said Temperance.

      \n

      "Who cares!" said Candace. "Right now, the only thing that matters is finding everyone and finishing the mission."

      \n

      [Of course it was Jimmy who changed the timeline...]

      \n

      As she walked out of the restroom, the counterman passed her a roll wrapped in tinfoil. There was a radio on in the kitchen, and she could hear a newsreader droning "...the Premier of the USSR will be arriving in New York City to meet with the President in this historic first 'Summit Talks'..."

      \n

      "I can't believe they're letting those commies here," said the counterman.

      \n

      "Wasn't up to me to let 'em in," said Temperance.

      \n

      "You're probably gonna be super busy, Major, with all them frogs running around," said the counterman.

      \n

      "You know it!" said Temperance. Silently she mouthed help me at Candace. Candace glanced at the calendar behind the cash register. It was open to February, 1956.

      \n

      "What the heck, Major!" said Charlie as they sat back down in the backseat. "You dames, always powdering your nose! My people had the right idea\u2014separate huts!"

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n
      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 2)\n

      James Wright turned out to live on a large mansion on what used to be Fifth Avenue. It was called the Avenue of the Heroes now. As they drove there, Temperance noted that huge boulevards had been cut diagonally through Manhattan, making large public squares. Most of the buildings had a sort of Georgian revival look to them, although the street plan was clearly meant to evoke Haussmanian Paris. Her familiar New York had been transformed into a gleaming city of marble and glass.

      \n

      [My extrapolation of what the world of "The Repairer of Reputations" would have looked like thirty years on.]

      \n

      They screeched to a stop in front of the mansion. "You're supposed to meet with his assistant, some gal named Millicent Lowell," said Charlie as they were shown inside by a clearly distraught maid.

      \n

      "Never heard of her," said Temperance, and they were let into the room that was the murder scene.

      \n

      It was a particularly macabre setting. Jimmy Wright\u2014looking somewhat younger and fitter\u2014was pinned to a mahogany column by a three foot long metal javelin. Standing next to him was a blonde woman in her thirties, looking completely unperturbed.

      \n

      "Well, it wasn't a suicide booth, I can tell you that," said Millicent Lowell.

      \n

      "Yeah, they been closed for like twenty years now," said Charlie. "Just those beatniks hanging out down in the one at Washington Square."

      \n

      "Miss Millicent, please come with us," said Temperance. "You'll be assisting with the investigation."

      \n

      "What can I do?" said Millicent.

      \n

      Temperance waited until Charlie had stepped out of the room. "What do you know about the Van Carlyles, and tell me the truth?"

      \n

      "The Van Carlyes? Like Carlyle Industries? Are they making cars now?" said Millicent.

      \n

      "You sure he's not related to the governor of California?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "I don't know any Carlyle governors," said Millicent. "Roger, you could call the paterfamilias. If he had a familias, that is."

      \n

      "Where did you meet Mr. Wright?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "He was a friend of my mother's, so all my life," said Millicent.

      \n

      "Did you ever go on any adventures?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "We had to file some papers at City Hall, that was adventurous," said Millicent.

      \n

      "Have you ever met a woman named Ruby Fitzgibbons?" asked Temperance.

      \n

      "You mean Mrs. Admiral Murphy? Yes. Aren't you related?" said Millicent. "She's kind of the hands behind the throne. Both of them."

      \n

      "How long have you worked for Mr. Wright?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "One way or another since about 1937," said Millicent. "He'd been acting a bit erratic...I mean, more than usual. Not the kind that would get a javelin in the chest. I mean, he was a wonderful man and philanthropist but he had his eccentricities. Nothing treasonous, of course. Just...eccentric."

      \n

      "He seemed to be a man of large personality," said Temperance.

      \n

      "He did try to do the right thing," said Millicent. "I didn't intend the pun."

      \n

      "We haven't arrested people for puns since the 1940s," improvised Temperance. "Were you aware of Mr. Wright's recent trip to a city called...Carcosa?"

      \n

      "When did Mr. Wright go to this Carcosa?" said Millicent. "I could check his schedule..."

      \n

      "We have intel. We're not at liberty to say," began Temperance.

      \n

      "A few weeks ago," said Candace.

      \n

      "Have you ever been there?" said Temperance. "Are you familiar with a play called The King in Yellow?"

      \n

      "Yes. It's pretty big here, you know," said Millicent. "Doing a musical revival on Broadway. Clark Gable is starring."

      \n

      "Second act is a doozy, comes out of nowhere," said Temperance. Without a word, Millicent went to the bar and poured Temperance a double.

      \n

      "Have you been a Major long, Major?" she asked.

      \n

      "As long as I can remember. I woke up this day and felt like a new person. A real brightening dawn."

      \n

      [The name of Ruby's plane.]

      \n

      "What were you before this morning?" said Millicent.

      \n

      "I was a member of an investigation into an individual that resides within Carcosa who has been deemed a threat. And a person from there that we're trying to find. She's gone missing, and we're worried about her safety," said Temperance.

      \n

      "I think I heard of something about that," said Millicent. "Does she also go by Cassandra, or Cassie? I think she's used a lot of names."

      \n

      "Yes, people have secrets. Secrets within secrets...within secrets. She went missing after her performance in the King in Yellow."

      \n

      "I know an expert, a Mr. de Marigny," said Millicent.

      \n

      "We met him in New Orleans," said Temperance. "He was helpful. We were hoping to find another person who had experience with these things. We were on her trail, actually." Temperance glanced at Jimmy's desk. He saw a picture of Beth Queen on it. "You know this woman?" she said, pointing.

      \n

      "Miss Auckland? She's an ace reporter. A friend of Mr. Wright's," said Millicent.

      \n

      "I have one other question," said Temperance. "Are you aware of any projects related to time travel?"

      \n

      Millicent blanched faintly. "I know of some incidents a while back...but nothing recently, no."

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n

      \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n

      \n\nMarch 2018 \n

      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 3)\n

      At that moment a man in a bad government suit strode into the room. He flipped out a very official looking ID card. "Captain Kroeger, CSA," he said to Candace. "You the one they sent from the Department of Information? Right. Whatever happened to Mr. Wright we just gotta..." For the first time he saw Jimmy's body.

      \n

      "What the..." Kroeger \xa0swore. "So he dies in a car accident? How you gonna make something like that go away?"

      \n

      "Architectural accident," said Temperance.

      \n

      "Building was unstable," said Millicent.

      \n

      "Shoddy workmanship," continued Temperance.

      \n

      Kroeger shook his head. "I mean, we can get a guy in a car no problem, we'll identify him for you. I agreed to work with you Regionals, all right? But this is a matter of state security. I mean, the President and the Premier are going to meet at the Wright Foundation in a couple of days and now Jimmy Wright's dead? This could be the Froggies! I wouldn't put anything past those freaks."

      \n

      "I think for right now we'll just investigate. No one needs to know what happened," said Candace.

      \n

      "The Central Security Administration stands behind your investigation 100%," said Kroeger. "We will run whatever cover you need. Talk to my boss, Colonel Ballantine, he'll take care of you."

      \n

      Candace suggested that Millicent check Jimmy's appointment book. Strangely enough, he had cleared his entire week. Candace decided that the cover story would be that he was out of town.

      \n

      "All right," said Kroeger, "but we'll need a good excuse. The Premier of France is arriving and now Wright's not gonna be there to shake his hand! We don't need this, with the British situation spinning out of control, and the Chinese..."

      \n

      For the first time, Temperance noticed a political map hanging from the wall. She stared at it, fascinated. It looked very much like a map of Earth\u2014her Earth\u2014around the year 1900, before the wars and the breakups of the colonial empires. She noticed quite a bit of what had been French Africa was listed as "constituent republics" of the USSR\u2014the Union of Socialist Syndicalist Republics.

      \n

      Communist France.

      \n

      [I made a map for the game. The basics are just as described: the major European powers never broke up, and there was no World War I. The German-American war happened, of course, and in the course of the Revolution France fought and defeated a German-Russian coalition, leaving Germany and Central Europe contested between the rival blocs. So eerie echoes of our own Earth...]

      \n

      Kroeger broke her reverie in his snide way. "You know where to find me, Major. We think you Regies are fine. You do good work. Not everybody can do the glorious work of counterterrorism and subversive suppression. We need you doing the rest. Gotta have a Cripo in order to have a Stapo, right?"

      \n

      After Kroeger left they discussed what to do. Millicent sadly punctured Temperance's theory.

      \n

      "Are you familiar with the theory that the universe is just a simulation?" she asked Temperance.

      \n

      "Yes," she said. Very quickly.

      \n

      [Presumably she got that from her mother; in my Eternal Lies run the simulation hypothesis was a major plot point.]

      \n

      "Let's assume it's not for the moment. And assume that the universe casts shadows ... echoes ... that are real."

      \n

      "Ah, parallel dimensions," said Temperance. "Superman #37."

      \n

      "We need to find out what happened to Mr. Wright," said Candace. "What was he doing before this?"

      \n

      "Well, what killed him was this statue of an American Indian," said Temperance, standing next to it. "It's made of lead, like the javelin, and I think the arm can move."

      \n

      Under an area rug they found a floorplate like a pedal or switch. When they cocked the statue's arm back and then pressed the plate, the arm shot forward\u2014it seemed to have some kind of clockwork on the inside. If the spear had been its hand, it would have hurled it, probably quite hard. Millicent ran through Jimmy's date books. A Meldrick Farnum was listed a few days prior; he worked for some kind of metal casting company.

      \n

      "What do we do with the body?" said Candace.

      \n

      "I can have the boys come by and take care of it, I guess..." said Temperance.

      \n

      "I can handle that," said Millicent, too deadpan to be mysterious.

      \n

      Candace knelt down beside Jimmy's body. "Sorry, Mr. Wright," she said, and went through his pockets. The only thing out of the ordinary was a tarot card, the Knight of Wands.

      \n

      "I have a tarot card too," said Temperance a little guiltily. "I found it in my wallet."

      \n

      "I do too," said Candace.

      \n

      "But why? Everyone knows that they're the devil's playground, but that's neither here nor there," said Temperance. "Millicent, what do you know about them?"

      \n

      "They eventually become the playing cards we know today. The major aracana got removed except for the Fool, which becomes the Joker. Why?" said Millicent, sweating a little. "Though I heard that there was somebody who gave out cards..."

      \n

      "Who?" said Candace.

      \n

      "Have you heard of the Penitent?" said Millicent. "All right. You might want to sit down. This room should be soundproofed, and I don't think we're being bugged by anyone. Except Mr. Wright. Who's dead. Which reality did you come from?"

      \n

      "You're our Millicent! From Earth One!" said Temperance. "JSA and JLA! She's from the JSA, but we're on the JLA world!"

      \n

      [Me: Points to Gryffindor.]

      \n
      \n

      \n
      \n Hrm:

      Jimmy: thinks like Hufflepuff, acts like Gryffindor
      Temperance: Gryffindor
      Charleston: Slytherin
      Millicent: Created to be Slytherin, ended up iconically Ravenclaw
      Candace: Maybe started out Hufflepuff, ended up by burning the Sorting Hat and pissing off to whatever the Wizarding School equivalent of USC* is.
      Dr. Orange: Slytherin
      Ruby: Gryffindor
      Geronimo: Iconically Gryffindor

      * I sure hope in the new series we find out that American wizarding schools don't bother with the pointless elite tribalism of Hogwarts

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 4)\n

      "But which world is that?" said Millicent.

      \n

      "The real world?" said Candace.

      \n

      "Let's not make any assumptions!" said Millicent.

      \n

      "The one where Ruby has only one arm and Bradley Grey is governor of California," said Temperance.

      \n

      "Did you come from the McAllister Building?" said Candace. "Then we were following you."

      \n

      Millicent explained, in her usual breathless style, that in this world there was a...vigilante named the Penitent. He used to give out tarot cards to people\u2014a Knight meant you were under his protection, an Ace meant you were a target, and a card from the major arcana meant you were an ally.

      \n

      "I have a tarot card," said Candace, pulling it out. "The Tower. Major arcana."

      \n

      "Me too," said Temperance, displaying The Magician.

      \n

      "The only other thing you need to know is that the Penitent was...Mr. Wright," said Millicent.

      \n

      "He was a vigilante on this world?" said Temperance. "As well, I mean."

      \n

      "Was he murdered, or was this a plan?" wondered Candace.

      \n

      "We sometimes talked about his business," admitted Millicent. "I was thinking we could hide his body in his secret lair."

      \n

      "Did you go on any adventures with him?" said Temperance. "Did you have an alias?"

      \n

      "Yes. No. The idea was nobody would ever see me," said Millicent.

      \n

      "Did you tell him where you were from?" said Candace.

      \n

      "No. But he could have found out that there wasn't a Millicent Lowell in this world," said Millicent. "Roger Carlyle is in this world, so I can't be."

      \n

      [See The Post-Modern Masks of Nyarlathotep for the origin story of Vanessa and Mirabelle/Millicent.]

      \n

      "How are we here?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "Well, there is a Major Murphy here," said Millicent. "But whether or not you swapped places or you're overriding her, I don't know..."

      \n

      "Now about this lair you spoke of," said Temperance, eyes gleaming.

      \n

      "It's just your average...vigilante...masked fighter for justice...lair," said Millicent.

      \n

      "He is a millionaire here," said Candace.

      \n

      "You're right. Let's move the body to the lair," said Temperance, jumping up. "And talk to leads. This Betty Auckland. Does she know about Mr. Wright being the Penitent?"

      \n

      "I haven't told her," said Millicent. "But here she's pretty sharp. I guess on Earth One she wasn't always, but her she is."

      \n

      "On Earth One she is pretty sharp," said Temperance distractedly.

      \n

      "Oh right," said Millicent. "On Earth Zero, I meant." Temperance didn't seem to notice.

      \n

      "Candace, you talk to Betty," said Temperance. "You're good. Very good at talking. Very charismatic and wise. And I really, really think I would be better suited going to superhero lair. And taking care of things. I have more upper body strength."

      \n

      "You know, I thought you were scared, but now I think you're enjoying this," said Candace.

      \n

      "No, I am scared! Just yesterday I was in a very strange building, and now I'm in a comic book."

      \n

      "Temperance, listen. We need to find Jimmy. We need to find out what happened. Then we need to get home. This isn't play time," said Candace.

      \n

      "Yes, but we all came through. Where's the real Jimmy? Maybe he's wandering around!"

      \n

      Millicent rang Betty up on the phone. "Hiya Millicent!" said Betty when she picked up in her familiar, brassy, New Yorker accent.

      \n

      "Listen, I got a propaganda specialist and a major here, so giving you a heads up..." began Millicent.

      \n

      "Oh, I thought you was calling about tonight," said Betty.

      \n

      "I hope tonight is still on, but I'm sending the propaganda lady to you. All I know is that Mr. Wright trusted them?"

      \n

      "Am I in trouble? This major with the RSA or CSA?"

      \n

      "RSA," said Millicent.

      \n

      "Oh, cops. No worries. Lissen, I'll see ya tonight," said Betty, and hung up.

      \n

      Earth-Zero Betty Auckland: Gryffindor
      Earth-One Beth Queen: So Raven...claw.

      \n
      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 5)\n

      Candace took a cab down to the offices of the New York Mirror, one of the city's most important dailies. She flipped through a copy of the morning's paper as she whisked through the unfamiliar yet all too familiar streets: the headlines were about the summit with the French, of course. She read over the masthead. Unusually, the paper's chief editor was a woman named Elisa Olney.

      \n

      "Call me Jax," said Olney when Candace arrived at her office. She was an older woman in a menswear suit that would have looked good on Marlene Dietrich, complete with a cigarette in a long black holder. "Everyone does. My girl says you want to talk to Betty Auckland. This an official matter?"

      \n

      "Not at all," said Candace.

      \n

      "This isn't about the Penitent, is it? We've been getting a lot of heat on that, but it's a significant story and we're going to keep on it, and Betty's my ace. I don't get you government types, you were high on the vigilante before but now you're down on him. Anyway, she's in the bullpen."

      \n

      Candace followed Olney's secretary out into an open space clotted with a thick fug of cigarette smoke and raucous with the sound of rapid typing. From a desk near a window she heard a piercing, nasal cry of "Copy!" She followed the sound to its source, a brassy blonde woman lighting a cigarette and flipping through some notes on her desk.

      \n

      "Miss Auckland? Hi," said Candace. She noticed that there were pictures of both Millicent and Jimmy on her desk. "I came to ask some questions\u2014"

      \n

      "This on the record?" said Betty.

      \n

      "No, not at all. I want to talk about Mr. Wright's assistant."

      \n

      "Millicent? She's a good kid."

      \n

      "Indeed," said Candace. "Let's go into the conference room."

      \n

      "Sure," said Betty. A look of confusion crossed her face. "I thought you said it wasn't official."

      \n

      "It isn't," said Candace as she guided her gently into the small, stuffy conference room. She hoped it wasn't bugged. "I have sad news for you. We really need you for your information and connection with Mr. Wright. I'm sorry to tell you that he's dead\u2014"

      \n

      "What?" said Betty. She collapsed into a chair and began to weep.

      \n

      "I'm sorry," said Candace. "I know it must be a shock\u2014"

      \n

      "I know, I know," sniffed Betty. "I mean, you can only carry a torch for a guy for so long, you know."

      \n

      "Since you were so close to him we figured you'd be an excellent resource to learn about him, who his friends were..." said Candace calmly.

      \n

      "He was a special guy," said Betty, wiping her eyes. "But he didn't have a lot of friends. I saw him the last time a couple of weeks ago. It said only open it in the event of his death, but I didn't think\u2014he had a lot of dangerous interests..."

      \n

      "Right now we can't tell anyone that he died, or how he died," continued Candace. "We were told by his assistant that we could trust you."

      \n

      "Millicent? Did she say how much I could trust you?" said Betty, said. Candace noticed that Betty was nonchalantly playing with something in her hand. A Tarot card. One of the Arcana.

      \n

      Cards on the table, thought Candace, and took out her own card.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      The Penitent's Sanctuary was underneath the Pitcairn House on the East Side, behind a door with a complex lock that Millicent expertly disarmed. "It shoots out poison gas if you do it wrong," she told Temperance.

      \n

      Beyond the door was a chilly chamber, about forty feet long. At one end was a metal grate; beyond it was a collapsed subway tunnel. There were bookshelves filled with reference books and directories. Hanging from wires on the ceiling were some trophies: a fake serpent, a paste replica of the Hope Diamond, a fortune telling machine with a mechanical swami, and several pieces of exotic weaponry.

      \n

      There were file cabinets in a line stretching down the center of the room. Most were blackened and warped by heat, and there was a distinct odor of smoke in the air.

      \n

      "This is new. This wasn't like this before," said Millicent.

      \n

      "What happened? We have to investigate!" said Temperance with a mad gleam in her eye and a smile on her lips. "Could he have destroyed it? Was he expecting it? Could his nemeses done this?"

      \n

      "They would have to have found this place," said Millicent. "But there weren't any signs that anyone broke in, and he had a special way of doing the locks."

      \n

      "He must have destroyed them himself," said Temperance. "But why? Did he have an arch-rival?"

      \n

      "He usually made sure that his rivals didn't stay around long enough to become arch," said Millicent. "He did start changing his targets recently."

      \n

      "What did he start going after? Mobsters? Mutated Men from Mars?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "I don't know about Men from Mars, but he stopped chasing gangsters and petty criminals and started going after the government. Working with subversive elements," said Millicent.

      \n

      "Perhaps someone was on his trail," mused Temperance. "Someone who figured out who he was. Maybe they rigged his booby trap." She paced a little, and suddenly stopped. In one corner of the room there was a freestanding wardrobe, with a combination lock on it. Temperance stared hungrily at it until Millicent sighed and opened the lock.

      \n

      Inside were a trenchcoat, a slouch hat, dark slacks, a light chainmail vest, a glowering metal mask, and a pair of boots with three inch lifts.

      \n

      "The mask is really a gas mask," said Millicent. "And down the sleeves of the coat are these tubes, see? You press this button and it would blow this powder out. The drug had some kind of psychological effect on people..."

      \n

      "How do I look?" said Temperance, her voice muffled by the mask.

      \n

      "You couldn't pass for Mr. Wright," said Millicent.

      \n

      "Mummmmmble mmummmble the Pemmitntt," said Temperance.

      \n

      "I'm not sure I follow," said Millicent. "Mr. Wright had to practice speaking clearly too."

      \n

      "Immf faard mu vreeethe im vis fimg," said Temperance. She pulled off the mask. "I'm going to keep this for safekeeping." She poked at the files. "I think he definitely destroyed these on his own."

      \n

      [Notice use by TP, who was enjoying this immensely.]

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
