      \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nApril 2018 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 6)\n

      The limousine whisked Charleston and Helen through downtown Manhattan. Charleston noticed that Chinatown seemed larger than he remembered it being. "Why do we need ethnic districts? We're all one people," he mused.

      \n

      "Yes, Party Leader," said the chauffeur. "But when we had that refugee crisis twenty years ago, a lot of people came here. You know, when they closed the Chinese border\u2014"

      \n

      "The past is the past," said Charleston.

      \n

      "\u2014and detonated that atomic device over Hong Kong," continued the chauffeur.

      \n

      "...who could forget that?" said Charleston. He hoped he said it smoothly. "You make some excellent points. I should make sure the history curriculum is teaching things appropriately. If you could get me a third-grade history book..."

      \n

      "Sure, Party Leader, I'll pick up a copy of My First Party Primer when we get to the office," said the chauffeur.

      \n

      Not my first parallel world, Charleston thought smugly, and settled back in his seat. Helen was quietly freaking out in the corner.

      \n

      "How are you in the real world?" she muttered.

      \n

      "You keep saying that, but the entire world interacts with me."

      \n

      "You're a big shot!" said Helen.

      \n

      "And you're with me, so that makes you a big shot too!"

      \n

      "I've been in your dream too long," she moaned. "I must be hallucinating. I've got it! I'm hallucinating being back in the real world!"

      \n

      "Whatever gets you through the day," said Charleston. He examined his surroundings closely. The windows of his car were made of bulletproof glass. Perhaps my popularity isn't absolute, he thought. He glanced back at the guys on motorcycles following him. But I rate a security detail. He looked at his reflection, and then looked at it again sharply.

      \n

      "My dear, do you have any tinted spectacles?" he said to Helen.

      \n

      "No, why should I?" she muttered.

      \n

      "Because if anyone notices these\u2014" he pointed at his eyes, which were still green\u2014"they might ask questions."

      \n

      "Just pull your hat down," she said.

      \n

      "At least I'll be fashionable," he groused.

      \n

      "Yeah, you make an excellent fascist. Look at your armband! You really think anyone is going to look you in the eyes?" She noticed his confusion and sighed. "It means you're a District Leader. You're in charge of the Party in a given region."

      \n

      "That doesn't sound impressive," he said. "Sounds like a store manager. How big is this district?"

      \n

      "Chinatown, I guess, so most of lower Manhattan. In New York City, which is practically the capital," she said.

      \n

      "Keep telling me how powerful I am," he leered.

      \n

      "I am not feeding this," she said. "This is my trip and I want it to be a good one. Allen taught me that."

      \n

      "I probably have important enemies," he said. "I'm not used to not knowing who my enemies are."

      \n

      "It's all intra-party politics," said Helen wearily. "I don't know your relationship with the Upper Party. I don't know your relationship with the President."

      \n

      "Wait, important people care about me here?"

      \n

      "There ain't but a couple of hundred District Leaders!"

      \n

      "A couple of hundred now," said Charleston.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      The District Headquarters had once been the Customs House, a grandiose mock-classical building that had heralded the new look of New York City.

      \n

      [It does kind of look like that. A lot of turn of the century NYC architecture makes this easier to extrapolate.]

      \n

      Inside was a bustling crowd of bureaucrats and functionaries, many of them young people. They greeted him respectfully as they walked by. "Good morning, Mr. Chiu."

      \n

      "Accompany me to my office," he told someone, who shrugged and led him to his elegantly appointed mahogany office. There was a large window where he could glare ominously down at the street below, and a large globe showing the empires of the world.

      \n

      He had barely settled down before the double doors opened and an efficient looking young woman bustled in, carrying a slender book and a sheaf of carbon paper. "Here's the book your driver asked us to get, and your messages. Party Leader Brophy wants to talk to you today. Here's your invitation to the Summit Dinner at the Wright Foundation in a couple of days..."

      \n

      Charleston spun the globe idly. "Ottoman Empire is still a thing, eh?" He noticed that there were markings on the globe in what should be colonies of the British Empire. On top of his desk was a memo concerning the status of the Dominion Wars.

      \n

      It seemed that a rebellion by the Indians and the Boers had led to an Empire-wide civil war. The memo noted that Great Britain was exerting tremendous pressure on the United States to intervene on their side, but that so far the US had not wanted to risk the possibility of conflict with the USSR...the French, he noted incredulously.

      \n

      Everything was complicated by the possession of nuclear weapons by all the great powers.

      \n

      He glanced up at the wall, where a picture of the President was hung. "Quincy Lund," he moaned. "The fun just drained out of this."

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      • \n
    • \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n\nAviatrix \n\n\n
      \n
      \n\nApril 2018 \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 7)\n

      He dismissed his secretary and sat down to read his papers. It seemed, unsurprisingly, that the Party was deep into graft and corruption. He himself seemed to own a significant amount of property in Chinatown, including a nightclub.

      \n

      There was an angry memo from the local office of the CSA\u2014the Central Security Administration, according to his primer; they seemed to be in charge of counterterrorism and the suppression of communists, anarchists, and other threats to "democracy"\u2014to the effect that the vigilante called the Penitent was working with subversive elements instead of taking on the local gangsters, which had been approved of as a way of keeping up the pressure on them.

      \n

      "Says he can cloud the minds of men," muttered Charleston. "What a knock-off." He found a memo that said to destroy after reading. "The meeting with Mr. Han is set," was all it said.

      \n

      He chewed the paper meditatively. "I love this place," he said aloud.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Candace had convinced Betty to come with her to the Lair, following Millicent's instructions. "I only been here once," said Betty. "And he blindfolded me when I came. And then didn't even do nothing!"

      \n

      "Sorry," said Candace, waving at the place Millicent had said had an electric eye.

      \n

      "Me too." The door buzzed and rolled back, and they followed the stairs into the Lair. Betty gave Millicent a kiss on the cheek. "Well, we all knew this day might come someday," she said morosely. "I guess we gotta look at the letter he gave me." She pulled it out of her purse:

      \n
      \n

      "Soon I will know if I am successful or lost but then again I will know. It is a paradox not unlike the looping swirl I now see before my eyes all the time. It is geometric, and yet it is not\u2026K would have known. Why does he no longer contact me? I can feel the wind now but it is on the other side of the earth and scorching\u2014

      \n"If I could have foreseen in advance what all this meant; if I could have turned aside from that first vision, when he spoke to me out of the eddies of time of other worlds, of other places\u2026if I had only turned aside, how many could I have spared? How many of those dear to me will suffer? I have seen their pain in so many places. And I was the cause of it all\u2014
      "I have burned all my case files.\u2014
      \n

      Hey, that's why it smells like smoke

      \n
      "\u2014 If I succeed, then I will destroy the machine, no matter what the Professor says. Accursed condition that I can no longer distinguish between the thoughts I utter aloud and those that silently stalk my mind\u2026
      "No one will understand what I did. Since I first saw him, the Other\u2014it's capitalized, dat's strange\u2014\u2026telling me my destiny, to find the paths to other worlds. Oh, the agony of knowing he was out there, the Other! Then I met Millicent, child of another world\u2014"
      \n

      "He knew!" said Millicent. "How did he know\u2014"

      \n

      "Know what?" said Betty. She resumed:

      \n
      \n

      "\u2014 a gentler one I think, one I longed to journey to. She made me understand that my fears were only madness, and for a while I was content. But K, always returning, always telling me that I had to push past this paltry world\u2026and I tried to find Millicent\u2019s home.       \n"They will never know. The other lair is safe even from Millicent. Only you, Betty, do I trust even with the knowledge that it exists\u2014"
      \n

      "Should I put my hands over my ears, Betty?" said Millicent.

      \n

      "Enh, he's dead, don't matter no more..."

      "You must never go there. What I have done, what you would see there\u2026it would destroy you.
      "I want to blame K. I want to say he tricked me into this, that I was a disposable tool of his. But I know. I wanted this. I wanted this vengeance, this bloody act of penance and self-destruction.
      "And now he approaches. I know he will be here soon. I have laid the trap. The Other will stalk me, but I have killed many times over and know his ways. I hope that I will live to burn this file. Or that you and I, Betty, can escape this world. Before the shadow over it consumes us forever.
      "Yours,

      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 8)\n

      "I guess the Other must have been his other him," said Millicent.

      \n

      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 9)\n

      Thomas Two-Tone Brophy was the Party Leader for the West Side of Manhattan. According to Charleston's notes, he was one of the Old Comrades, from the first days of the Party, after the Chinese detonated their first atomic weapon and then closed their borders. It didn't really surprise him that he seemed to be one of the Old Comrades as well.

      \n

      "Five nuclear detonations in combat," said Charleston to Helen, as he waited for Brophy to be shown into his office. "And yet we're still here. Good thing you guys haven't invented jet power yet. I do like the four prongs on the plugs, though."

      \n

      [I had to improvise here as CP asked which detonations had happened. They were: the Hong Kong attack; a US detonation during one of the more despicable wars in South America (which is why Argentina was now two countries); a British demonstration in Africa during the Dominion Wars; a Japanese attack on the Dutch colonies; and a French attack on Dresden, which had been in rebellion.]

      \n

      "Charleston, you old bastard," said Brophy, striding into the room and seizing Charleston's hand. He was a shortish man in his 50s, with a pronounced Irish brogue.

      \n

      "Old and bastardy, that's me," said Charleston.

      \n

      "You got your invite from our blessed Party Leader, N. Q. Lund," said Brophy.

      \n

      "Blessed indeed," said Charleston, fishing out a bottle of whisky from his desk. Wow, I can afford this stuff? he thought. He poured them each a shot and they tossed them off.

      \n

      "So I'm here to talk about our problem," said Brophy. "With all your boys comin' up from Mott Street and messin' with my territory. Gotta be yer boys, they're all Chinese fellas."

      \n

      "I'm telling you, it's a false flag," said Charleston.

      \n

      "You keep sayin\u2019 that, but who else has Chinese people."

      \n

      "They might not be Chinese," said Charleston. "Could you tell? They might be Mongolian!"

      \n

      "I might," said Brophy, scowling.

      \n

      "Really? Because I couldn't," said Charleston. "We go way back. We didn't come this far to have petty squabbles."

      \n

      "Well, it's messing with me business, and we can't have that. Bad enough that we have that masked fella runnin' around. Seems drawn to those Chinese people."

      \n

      "Doesn't sound like a coincidence to me," said Charleston.

      \n

      "Ah, who knows what the Penitent wants," said Brophy. "It was better when he was taking out the mobsters. You saw the memo from the CSA?"

      \n

      "They have their ways of dealing with things, and we have ours," said Charleston.

      \n

      "He'd probably be happier if we caught him," said Brophy. "We'd be gentler than them."

      \n

      "Would we, now?" said Charleston, flashing the grin that usually made people flee in terror.

      \n

      "That was a long time ago," said Brophy darkly. "We have our reputation to consider now."

      \n

      "I'll level with you. Them boys, if they're mine, I disown them. Do what you have to," said Charleston.

      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 10)\n

      Brophy gestured frantically for a moment. Charleston gradually realized that he was being asked to turn off the recording devices. He frantically looked around his desk. Finally he opened up a drawer that had switches with locations marked on them: Front hall, back hall, liquor cabinet, desk...he flipped the one marked Desk and a flashing light came on: probably to remind him that the people who were bugging him might notice eventually that he was jamming their signal.

      \n

      [Surveillance test by CP.]

      \n

      "Who's this Mr. Han," said Brophy. "We caught one of these fellas and that was the only name we got. Whoever he is, he's got them more afraid of them than normal. Usually they give it up right away."

      \n

      \n

      \n

      \n

      \n

      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 12)\n

      Candace returned to her\u2014"her"\u2014office downtown. She knew that she must have access to extensive archives that she might be able to use to research Jimmy and the Penitent and maybe figure out exactly how this world worked.

      \n

      She was buried in a ledger when her secretary buzzed the intercom. "Mrs. Heartbrooke, your husband is here to see you."

      \n

      "My...husband. Yes. Send him in..."

      \n

      Andy strode in. He was...he was...

      \n

      Handsome as she remembered him, yes: even here, even as a result of parallel evolution or whatever it was that guided these two worlds to be so close to each other, he had that twinkle in his pale blue eyes. His hair was longer than she'd ever seen it; when they had dated in high school he'd worn it short, and then kept it in a Marine buzz cut during the war. He was wearing a tweed jacket and carrying a leather book bag. A pair of reading glasses peeped out from his breast pocket.

      \n

      She watched him in silence, feeling the blood slowly drain from her face. Andy. Andy. Dead for more than a decade now, but here, living, breathing again. After the years of trying to move past his death, to put that pain and shock behind her, it took her breath away to see him now. It was beyond shock. It felt like a physical blow.

      \n

      "Hi, honey," he said distractedly, and slouched into a chair. "They cancelled classes for the rest of the day with all the political stuff going on. So I came down to see you."

      \n

      "Andrew," she said slowly. "Classes. Of course..."

      \n

      "You all right? You look like you've seen a ghost."

      \n

      "It's been a very strange day," she said.

      \n

      "You're telling me," he said, taking out a pipe. "What with the French in town."

      \n

      "Did we agree to meet?" she said. Something was bothering her; there was something wrong with Andy. She frowned slightly.

      \n

      "No, no, I called down before but they said you were doing something with the RSA. You in trouble?" he said.

      \n

      "No, no. You know my job," she said.

      \n

      "No I don't. We agreed on that."

      \n

      "It's just...government things...the summit...how are you doing?" she said, trailing off.

      \n

      "Fine. These kids, they have a lot of good ideas. I'm hoping we can get some of them into Jet Propulsion, and I want to make some recommendations to the grad school program."

      \n

      She nodded. Physicist? He did want to study that, before the war. She suddenly realized what it was about him that seemed wrong: he was older.

      \n

      She'd never gotten a chance to see him this age.

      \n

      Andy lit his pipe. "Read an interesting paper by some German refugee, Julius something."

      \n

      [Shout out to Dr. Orange, from the last campaign.]

      \n

      "Was there...did we plan..." she stuttered.

      \n

      "No, I wanted to surprise you," said Andy. "Was hoping to take you to lunch, but I guess it's too late now. You going to be home for dinner tonight, or are you working?"

      \n

      "I can try to," she said. "I have a few more things to work on...I should be home by seven. I'll head back then."

      \n

      Andy got up. "Oh, they arrested another bunch of kids at one of those crazy poetry readings. Some kid named Kerouac got thrown in jail. Real troublemaker. See you at home. I'll feed the dog, don't worry."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Temperance had Charlie drive her up to the Metropolitan Museum, which seemed to be in the same place in this world as in hers. Small favors. She clutched her satchel, now stuffed with Jimmy's trenchcoat and iron mask to her chest, and kept clutching it as she was shown into Professor Homans' small office deep in the archives of the Museum.

      \n

      "Well, Major, I wasn't aware of any reason for such a charming representative of the RSA would come to meet me." He was sweating slightly. Her uniform seemed to have that effect on people.

      \n

      "I know," she said, ominously. "I'm not going to take you away. But I know."

      \n

      "Know what?" said Homans, hyperventilating. "It was just one time! I broke it off with the boy right away!" He stopped and looked at her quizzical expression. "You're not here about me and my graduate student?"

      \n

      "Every world I go to," muttered Temperance. "No. I know about the Penitent."

      \n

      "Yes, everybody knows about the Penitent..."

      \n

      "He died last night. Killed by a mechanical Indian with a lead spear."

      \n

      "What?" Homans paused. "Actually, that is sort of the thing I would have pictured him going out on."

      \n

      "Yes, it makes so much sense when you know Jimmy Wright," said Temperance quickly.

      \n

      "Jimmy Wright was the Penitent? Jimmy Wright's dead?"

      \n

      "Yes, and it's terrible and the city needs a new protector but that's not important right now," said Temperance. "I need to know where the Other Lair is. The second lair! The one he talked about in his letter to Betty! The reporter! What did you do for him?"

      \n

      "I used to run down things for him. Artifacts. He had...deals to get things," said Homans.

      \n

      "Are we talking about items of religious or occult significance?"

      \n

      "Well, I don't believe in such things. But he did. He...used to call me about ancient cultures. The last few times, he didn't sound well. Something about Pitcairn House was permeated by some force...I thought it was a tropical disease. And about Euclidean loopholes. The crazy thing is, when he was talking, it was like he was talking to himself, you understand? But one time...I thought I heard...I thought I heard his voice coming from somewhere else on the line, like somewhere else in the room."

      \n

      "When was this?"

      \n

      "Several weeks ago. He said he was working on something at the Watershed. I don't know what that meant. Look. Go talk to his pilot, Summers."

      \n

      "First name Joyce?"

      \n

      "Yes, actually."

      \n

      "Another doppelganger," said Temperance.

      \n

      "Another what?" said Homans.

      \n

      "Doppelganger."

      \n

      "What does ancient German legends have to do with this?"

      \n

      "I don't have time to explain. Where can I find this pilot?"

      \n

      "She has a helicopter down at the waterfront. Frankly, I'm surprised he was working with you. I thought all you cops wanted to arrest him." He slapped his hand over his mouth, suddenly conscious of saying too much. "I mean, I'm not political," he said weakly. "I took a trip to France in 1918. Before the Revolution."

      \n

      "There's more going on in the world than you realize," said Temperance, distracted.

      \n

      "'There's more under heaven than in all your philosophy'" quoted Homans.

      \n

      "You have Shakespeare here, then."

      \n

      "I'm going to pretend you didn't say that," said Homans. "After all, there's nothing either good or bad but thinking makes it so." He poured Temperance a glass of water. She noticed that it had a faint yellow tinge.

      \n

      "Did you ever make anything for him? Or get him a machine?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "No. I do remember...he fought a man with a bit of a flair for the occult. Called himself the Blue Mist. He was making some kind of machine, and the Penitent captured it. Some kind of deadfall...no. It threw a javelin, I think," said Homans.

      \n

      "Its location probably remains unknown to this day," said Temperance quickly.

      \n

      "Well, the Penitent did always keep his cards close to his vest," said Homans. He casually flashed a Tarot card. Temperance flashed her back.

      \n

      "Is the Blue Mist around?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "No. He's dead."

      \n

      "Was there a body?"

      \n

      "Well, pieces of one. The Penitent pushed him off a building."

      \n

      "Sounds like Jimmy Wright."

      \n

      "Clearly you knew him better than I did," said Homans.

      \n

      "We have a complicated and interesting history," said Temperance, standing up.

      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 13)

      Charleston spent the early evening making a series of creepily cheerful requests to his staff, which had the desired intimidating effect: they quickly assembled a list of the off-book personnel he used in his\u2014well, the other Charleston's\u2014various graft and legbreaking operations.\n

      [Intimidate spend by CP to find the people who would know if Brophy actually had any of his men.]

      \n

      He took a video call as the sun was setting from Colonel Ballantine of the CSA. \xa0He was a fiftyish man with the steely-eyed glare of secret policemen all around the world. "Chiu! what the hell are you doing?"

      \n

      "I was trying to decide if I was going to have scrambled or poached eggs..."

      \n

      "Why are you trying to track down these people?" said Ballantine. "I thought we all agreed there was going to be a complete separation. That we wouldn't talk about what's going on! So why are talking about it?"

      \n

      "Talking about what?"

      \n

      "Too late. Look, we're at a very vulnerable stage of this. You've been a good ally so far. And when we come into our own, you WILL be rewarded. We all know this. But what am I going to say to Mr. Han when he asks why you're FUCKING IT ALL UP?"

      \n

      "Tell him everything is fine. Say, 'Mr. Han, everything is going according to plan.' This what we all want."

      \n

      "Don't think I'll hesitate to take out Brophy. I don't care how old a Comrade he is. And if I gotta go that far...well, let's just say we'll have to cut our losses in certain areas."

      \n

      "Let's not make any hasty decisions," said Charleston.

      \n

      "Yeah, let's not," said Ballantine. "Clamp this down. Also, what the hell is with that RSA major you were talking to? Keep out of this case! Central Security is handling it. I'm doing my job. Your job is to make sure everything goes right at the Foundation when the President is there."

      \n

      "That's my job, all right," said Charleston, verbally tap-dancing. "They said we need somebody who specializes in things not going wrong and they said Charleston is the man for this kind of responsibility...thank you very much for the call, it's been educational." He hung up quickly.

      \n

      "Where's Temperance," he muttered to himself. "I think she's right. Time to go. Power isn't what it's cracked up to be. I'm a simple, real American."

      \n

      He pulled one of the asset books his staff had left for him. It showed he was a millionaire several times over. Most of it was sunk into apartment buildings. He noted he was collecting protection money from lots of nightclubs, many of them gay. Who am I here? he wondered. He got up and went into his executive bathroom.

      \n

      It wasn't what he was used to; for one thing, it lacked the shattered mirrors, blood in the sink, and general air of disrepair and slovenliness that was typical of the places he lived. The bright chrome furnishings were annoyingly cheery. He yanked open the medicine cabinet and found several shelves full of happy times stuff. That much hasn't changed, he thought, and grinned.

      \n

      When he closed the cabinet, his reflection caught his eye. Mostly because it wasn't reflecting what he was doing. Instead, his face glared out of the mirror full of malevolence. It raised a fist and began banging on the glass. He staggered back from the thudding sound it made.

      \n

      [2 point Stability loss.]

      \n

      His face began to scream, soundlessly, at him.

      \n

      He pointed one at the mirror, and laughed. He could just make out an obscured figure walking up behind his reflection. There was a flash of yellow from its cloak...

      \n

      He slipped out of the bathroom, slammed the door, and slumped against it, wiping away his tears. He grabbed a bottle from the bar and slammed down a shot. Then he called for his driver. He owned a club downtown. According to his notes, it was arranged around some fantasy theme.

      \n

      But when arrived, he recognized the theme immediately: what on his world would be called Roaring Twenties style. This didn't surprise him; the Roaring Twenties, the decade of his youth, was his favorite period.

      \n

      But on this Earth\u2014Tellus, he had taken to calling it\u2014the Roaring Twenties had never happened. (Their Twenties was the decade of a European war and the Second French Revolution.) So...just how the hell had his doppelganger come up with the idea?

      \n

      He shrugged as an obsequious ma\xeetre d' ran up to him. "Mr. Chiu! How wonderful to have you back!"

      \n

      "Yes it is," he snapped. "Get me something to eat. A nice hot cup of coffee. And I want to see every reflective surface in this club."

      \n

      "There are a lot of things like that in the club," stammered the ma\xeetre d'.

      \n

      "Why do you think I need a Sherpa?" he growled. They began a slow tour of every mirror in the building. He spent time looking in each, tapping on the glass. "You! What do you see in there?"

      \n

      "A very handsome man?" said the ma\xeetre d'.

      \n

      "Why, thank you." He stepped away. "Now look. What do you see?"

      \n

      "Me?"

      \n

      "Good. Let's keep it that way. Now, go check anything that reflects that isn't a mirror. Then give me a report, good and bad, before the evening is over." Charleston stalked into his private room and slumped into a banquette. They brought him a hot sandwich and some strong coffee.

      \n

      [MP, as a waiter: He's practicing his etiquette, for when he meets the Premier!

      \n

      CP: We better be out of here long before that or this thing is going to really blow up.

      \n

      TP: You don't say.]

      \n

      After he was done eating, he walked into the main ballroom and watched the band rehearsing, idly sipping his coffee. He looked down for a second and saw his reflection in the coffee.

      \n

      He slammed the cup against the wall. Everyone stopped what they were doing.

      \n

      "Oh that was hot," he muttered. "Carry on." He walked into the bathroom, hung his coat over the mirror, and washed his hands.

      \n

      [CP was on fire, again.]

      \n

      "This Charleston's gotta have sorcery books. Maybe at home! Wait, where do I live?" he said to himself. "I can't wander around talking to myself, people will think I'm crazy! I guess I can just ask my driver."

      \n

      He walked out and summoned the ma\xeetre d'. "I need you guys to get the spotlight on the marquee pointed up at the sky and make a Mobius Strip."

      \n

      "A figure eight? Sure, Mr. Chiu. Good advertising...I guess..."

      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 14)\n

      Uptown, Temperance saw the figure eight traced against the clouds as her car whisked through the streets. She sat up and pressed her face against the glass.

      \n

      "Anything wrong, Little Miss?" said Charlie from the driver's seat.

      \n

      "No. Wait. How long have you called me Little Miss?" she said.

      \n

      "All your life, Little Miss. Ever since your father rescued me from that attack by the Japanese."

      \n

      "Quick question. I've been having strange dreams. What do you think?"

      \n

      "It's been so long," said Charlie. "My people, we knew how to interpret dreams...but I've been here for a long time."

      \n

      "Kind of atrophied, eh?"

      \n

      "That, and all the matriarchs of my people were killed by the Japanese."

      \n

      Still a smart ass in this world, thought Temperance. They pulled up to a heliport on the Hudson River. She stepped outside and walked down to a helipad.

      \n

      A short, wiry, middle-aged woman was working on the engine of a helicopter. "You sonofgun...goddamnit!" said the woman as Temperance approached. "Move, goddamn you!" The woman began smacking something with a wrench.

      \n

      "You Joyce Summers?" said Temperance.

      \n

      Joyce turned, and then staggered back.

      \n

      "You're not in trouble," said Temperance.

      \n

      "I'm paid up, you know," said Joyce. "How can I help you, Major?"

      \n

      "A mutual friend of ours is in a bit of trouble," said Temperance. She flashed her Tarot card.

      \n

      "Jesus Christ," sighed Joyce.

      \n

      "I need to know if you know where the water shed is," said Temperance.

      \n

      "Been a while since I saw the Penitent," said Joyce, putting away her tools. "Last time, all we did was fly out to Long Island. Didn't land anywhere, just kept circling in the air." She reached into the cockpit of the helicopter and pulled out a map. "Brookhaven, mostly. I think there was a laboratory out there. That's where the Mandarin Project was researched. Guess it was contaminated, at least since 1937."

      \n

      "That would be the perfect place," said Temperance excitedly. "It was all underground, wasn't it?"

      \n

      "I don't know anything about that," said Joyce. "Nobody knows anything about that."

      \n

      "But the Manhattan Project\u2014"

      \n

      "\u2014the what?"

      \n

      "\u2014don't ask. Government secret. But they built the Manhattan Project underground in subway tunnels. So they did the same here. What did he say?"

      \n

      [Growing up on Long Island, we knew there was a lot of secret and maybe unsavory things going on at Brookhaven\u2014they had their own nuclear reactor (which leaked) and of course there was also Plum Island for germ warfare research. So it seemed natural to use it for this scenario.]

      \n

      "All kinds of crazy stuff. You know the Penitent! He was saying things like, the thing that was attacking him was attacking more often. And that he thought it was a ghost at first but now he realized it wasn't."

      \n

      "Could it be the Blue Mist?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "Wow, that takes me back," said Joyce. "Funny story. I flew him up on top of that building. He rappelled out of my helicopter."

      \n

      "How far is out to Brookhaven? About sixty miles, right? Good. Where's the closest costume shop?"

      \n

      "The only one I know is frequented by, uh, female illusionists, and I don't think they'd have what you want," said Joyce.

      \n

      "What...magicians?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "Of a kind. They are good at making some things disappear."

      \n

      "Like buildings?"

      \n

      "Depends on the person."

      \n

      "Not important. You never saw me."

      \n

      "I wish," said Joyce.

      \n

      "Thank you Joyce. You've been very helpful. I'll tell your doppelganger if I see her."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      On her car phone, Temperance called the precinct and had them connect her to Candace's house.

      \n

      "Good evening," said a pleasant baritone voice. "Dr. Andrew Heartbrooke speaking."

      \n

      "Andrew? Good to hear you're in good health. This is Major Murphy. I need to speak to your wife on a matter of national security."

      \n

      "Honey?" said Andy, cupping his hand over the phone, "The police are calling?"

      \n

      Candace took the phone. "Temperance?"

      \n

      "I need you to do something for me," said Temperance. "Listen. Follow the Mobius Strip. Don't tell anyone else." She hung up before Candace could say anything then she had the precinct ring Millicent's apartment.

      \n

      Betty answered, in her familiar brassy accent. "Major Murphy? Just a second."

      \n

      "What can I do for you," said Millicent.

      \n

      "Follow the Mobius Strip. Go straight there. Don't tell anyone," said Temperance, and hung up.

      \n

      Millicent sighed. "She's being weird," she said sadly to Betty. She gave her a deep, long kiss on the mouth. "This may take a while." Then she kissed her again, because it might take a while.

      \n

      Millicent... fit in oddly well to that world. Just, you know, kind of accepting all the horrible stuff in a fatalistic sort of way, because why would the world be different anyway? That probably doesn't say anything good about her state of mind, does it?

      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 15)\n

      Millicent wasn't surprised, when she arrived, that the lemniscuses was hovering over Charleston's bar. It was one of her regular haunts; not that she had ever met the owner. When Temperance arrived she wasn't surprised that the two of them were sitting next to each other at the bar, blissfully unaware of each other.

      \n

      "I found it," said Temperance. "The way home."

      \n

      "You sure?" said Millicent.

      \n

      "Hey," said Charleston. "Private conversation."

      \n

      "That's Millicent," said Temperance. "Millicent, this is Charleston."

      \n

      "Ah, the subject of our great pursuit," said Charleston, laying it on thick. He ordered a private table for themselves.

      \n

      "This place bugged?" asked Temperance as she sat down.

      \n

      "Of course," said Charleston. "And not just by me. Why do you think I have an eight piece band in this room? Okay, boys, let 'em hear you in heaven."

      \n

      The bandleader nodded. "Sweet Georgia Brown on four. A-one, a-two, one, two, three..."

      \n

      "I like this place," said Millicent. "It reminds me of home."

      \n

      "Brookhaven," said Temperance. "Site of the Mandarin Project. The same as the Manhattan Project back home. It's all underground."

      \n

      "I have the correspondences," said Millicent, pulling a large sheaf of notes out of her purse. "See, here's where the first bomb was dropped in our world, and here in this world..."

      \n

      "I could have made use of that technique over the last several years," said Charleston.

      \n

      "Jimmy went out to Brookhaven with the Aviatrix a while ago. His sidekick," said Temperance.

      \n

      "Miss Summers," said Millicent.

      \n

      "We don't have to fly, though," said Charleston. "We can drive."

      \n

      "Sure, we're government," said Temperance. "But we need to get everyone back together. Where's Helen? She said she was going to a horse."

      \n

      "I think I know where to find her," sighed Millicent.

      \n

      [It was a Streetwise spend before her next scene.]

      \n

      "And where's Candace?" said Temperance.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Candace was at home. Whatever the hell it was that Temperance wanted her to do, it wasn't as important as having dinner with her husband.

      \n

      It was bittersweet, she thought, taking the last swallow of a glass of white wine. He was very different than the man she remembered. Beyond being older...it was seeing his potential realized. And of course it was different than what she had imagined; after all, she was different than anything they had imagined together.

      \n

      But he was still Andy. She still could nestle in his arms and feel safe the way she hadn't in years.

      \n

      They tried to make love after dinner. It was...awkward. Had it always been so awkward? They had just been kids when they got married, after all. And now she was far, far more experienced and confident.

      \n

      But, too, he wasn't as awkward either; it made things uncomfortable, like being with a stranger that one knew too well for the comfort of anonymity but not well enough for the comfort of intimacy. It wasn't until she drank some water that she felt a change. As she rolled over Andy, she felt a pair of hands on her shoulders, warm against her naked flesh. This was stronger than she had ever felt the presence before; it seemed all around her, like something invisible yet immanent.

      \n

      "Is everything all right?" asked Andy afterwards.

      \n

      "It's just...all this...it's work," said Candace. "I've just been exposed to so many things. I feel disconnected from reality."

      \n

      "Could we talk...about having children again?" said Andy.

      \n

      "Well..." she trailed off. She couldn't think of anything to say.

      \n

      "We agreed that we wouldn't have children but things are different now."

      \n

      "I'm...not sure that the time is right. Everything is so crazy now...I should probably head back to the office," said Candace.

      \n

      "I won't wait up for you," Andy said.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Millicent found Helen down in Washington Square, slumped next to the abandoned Suicide Center. Millicent sat next to her. "Mr. Chiu says he has a way to get us all home. Want to come?"

      \n

      "I thought I was home," said Helen bitterly.

      \n

      "If you want to stay, I won't force you, but if you want to come back with us, we'll take you."

      \n

      "All right, I'll come," said Helen. "This world seems just as crazy as yours. Although four prongs on plugs, that just makes more sense."

      \n

      "I agree," said Millicent. "That's one of the things I like about here."

      \n

      She helped Helen over to Charleston's limo. Candace was in the back, having been picked up just outside her apartment. She wasn't crying. No, not at all.

      \n

      "This car is a Tucker!" said Temperance from behind the wheel. "Look, it has three headlights! Seems that Tucker is a huge company here!"

      \n

      "He did better before starting Tuckerland," muttered Charleston. "On the other hand, Howard Hughes actually made the Spruce Goose work here. I think it's why they don't have jets yet."

      \n

      "Brookhaven?" said Candace. She flipped through her notes. "The Wright Foundation owns it. Bought it from the government, although they haven't finished decommissioning it yet. Seems he wants to build some kind of education center there, maybe a facility for rehabilitating prisoners."

      \n

      [HP made a Research spend earlier, and here is where it paid off.]

      \n

      "So this Jimmy believes in second chances," said Charleston.

      \n

      "It's still technically off limits to the public," said Candace. "Of course, we're not the public."

      \n

      The drive took about ninety minutes, much of it spent navigating the dark farmlands of Long Island. Eventually they found the road to the main gate. There was a guard post.

      \n

      A tired looking guard staggered over to the car. "This is a secure facility," he began in a bored voice. He noticed Temperance's uniform. "Good morning, Major. We...weren't told you were coming..." He shuffled through some papers on his clipboard.

      \n

      "You're fine. We're here to look for some old records at the facility," said Temperance.

      \n

      "Thought they moved all that," said the guard. "But I don't know what they keep up there."

      \n

      "Mr. Wright's secretary said they were here, and it's all part of the deal he has with the government."

      \n

      "You'll need to fill out a RU-286 form," said the guard. "C'mon, I'll give you a cup of coffee."

      \n

      A little rain fell while the rest of them waited in the car. Candace noticed again how responsive people in this world were to authority. She suspected they could have so few guards here because most people would have turned around as soon as they saw the No Trespassing signs.

      \n

      [Psychology nabbed this clue. As a planet under the shadow of Hastur, the Tellurians indeed are cowed by authority. It also helps that most national insignia are forms of the Yellow Sign, of course.]

      \n
      \n

      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 16)\n

      Eventually they drove through the gate and onto the abandoned campus of the laboratory. They got out to search on foot with flashlights, looking for anything that made sense as a "water shed."

      \n

      It was Millicent who found it: a little shed near one of the Quonset huts (well, they looked like Quonset huts at least) with a faded sign hanging from the door: Danger\u2014Heavy Water Storage.

      \n

      [Notice spend.]

      \n

      "The water shed," cooed Temperance. "We found it. Kind of small, isn't it?" She smashed the lock off with a crowbar and they shuffled inside. The walls were covered with various tools\u2014pliers and tongs, mostly; there were some rusted cans or barrels stacked in a corner. Temperance frowned, and turned around slowly, "Aha!" She reached behind a workbench and threw a switch.

      \n

      The entire floor began to sink.

      \n

      "This is Mr. Wright's kind of thing, yes," said Millicent.

      \n

      "This is what I wanted," groused Charleston. "What kind of Party Leader am I if I don't even have a decent hidden lair?"

      \n

      They descended perhaps fifty feet. Temperance slid back a grating. Beyond was a fairly large chamber, dimly illuminated by sickly fluorescent lights. All along one wall was machinery and electronics of some kind.

      \n

      "There's a lot of power running through here," said Millicent. "A lot of juice."

      \n

      [Physics got this clue.]

      \n

      Somebody moved out in the dim space of the chamber. A figure turned around and stepped forward a bit into the light. He was wearing a lab coat, a sickly looking man who might have been handsome once.

      \n

      "Dr. Schicksal?" whispered Candace.

      \n

      "Did the Penitent send you?" asked Percival Schicksal. "Good. I saw your uniform...thought the game was up."

      \n

      "Don't worry, I shouldn't need it much longer," said Temperance. "We're here about your machine. Does it work?"

      \n

      "Of course it works," said Percival. "At least that's what the Penitent told me. It was supposed to send him to other worlds. Obviously it only works for him. He was a little strange. His psychic frequencies vibrated in a way that the machine could use. It wouldn't work for me."

      \n

      "Baby, don't bring up the past\u2014wait a second..." Charleston stared through the gloom. As he feared, the man's face was identical to his own. "You! The usurper!" he said.

      \n

      [Back in the Post-Modern Masks of Nyarlathotep, Charleston's sanity dropped down to 0 during the Africa section. A few weeks later CP told me that his idea was for him to play a preacher named James Jones from West Virginia...except that it was actually Charleston, manifesting a new personality. As it turned out, the climactic struggle of the campaign was between Charleston and the Rev.

      \n

      That game got weird.]

      \n

      "Me! You're the usurper," said the man. "You're the pretender."

      \n

      "I was born in this body! I raised it from a baby!"

      \n

      "And you did such a great job of it, too."

      \n

      "Hey, I won! You should be grateful you're even here!"

      \n

      "Look, I figured this all out," said the Reverend James Jones. "Between you and me, that is. We always had the wrong half. You have the Will, but you lack Conviction. I had Conviction, but I lacked Will. But don't worry, baby. Things change. We'll be seeing each other again soon. And then you won't be laughing."

      \n

      "That was your problem!" shouted Charleston as the phantom began to fade. "You lacked a sense of humor! You're not real. You're paper-thin. You're just an aspect of me."

      \n

      "You're like a hollowed out sea shell. I hold you up and I can see...right...through you..."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 21)
      \n

      Temperance met herself. "You're not Major Murphy," her doppelganger said. To herself.

      \n

      Temperance replied, "No."

      \n

      "I think I'm Major Murphy."

      \n

      "You are Major Murphy."

      \n

      "I don't think I'm going home, am I?"

      \n

      "You're not going anywhere pleasant."

      \n

      "Where you're from, are you a good person?"

      \n

      "I strive to be."

      \n

      "Have you ever been in love?"

      \n

      "No."

      \n

      "Neither was I. Seems kind of a waste, doesn't it?"

      \n

      "Yes. But I plan on rectifying that."

      \n

      "Is there a home for me to go to?"

      \n

      "Go to Brookhaven. There's a very nice man fifty feet underground there."

      \n

      "Typical. Finally on the trail of a man and he's underground."

      \n

      "He's a very nice man. And probably the only man left. He's Adam. You could be Eve."

      \n

      "I was holding out for Mary Magdalene."

      \n

      "Everybody wants to be her."

      \n

      "Temperance," said Major Murphy, "Don't make the same mistakes. I was a fascist and never fell in love."

      \n

      "I promise I'm going to do nothing but good..."

      \n

      "That's a lie and we both know it."

      \n

      "No! I have conviction now. I've learned things. I'm going to keep the world safe. My good friend Charleston showed me the way."

      \n

      "You listen to him?"

      \n

      "In our world he's a flawed man. But even a broken clock..."

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      They woke up to a crushing pressure on their bodies. Millicent blinked through the dust. They were in a room that looked like the basement of the MacAllister building. It looked like most of the building had joined them in it.

      \n

      Temperance began screaming for help. Her father had trained her well; she had a voice that could make an Admiral jump to attention when she used it. A fireman poked his head down into the hole.

      \n

      "I thought we checked dis area," he said in a broad Boston accent. "Whaddya, appear outta nowhere?"

      \n

      After a while they were dug out and rushed to the hospital. "You guys didn't come out so bad," an orderly told Temperance. "Not like that old codger who got a rebar through his chest. Some old derelict, grey hair, messed up face. Some loopy blonde dame with him, says she's been looking for him for months."

      \n

      "What month is it?" said Millicent groggily.

      \n

      "Whaddya talking about? It's May first. Happy May Day, ya goddamned Reds."

      \n

      "We went into the building in February," said Temperance. She grabbed the orderly's arm. "What year is it!"

      \n

      "What's wrong wit you! It's 1956! Brooklyn won the World Series last yeah!"

      \n

      "I had money on the Yankees," muttered Temperance.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      A few days later Millicent wheeled herself into Charleston's room. Her leg was setting nicely; the doctors were impressed with how quickly the bone was knitting. "Mr. Chiu? I have a message for you."

      \n

      "These are never good," said Charleston in his plummiest tones. The free morphine was a definite perk of his stay.

      \n

      "No, no they're not," said Millicent glumly. "He's not looking for you anymore. He says He's pretty sure you'll take care of the problem yourself."

      \n

      "I'm not good at taking care of problems," said Charleston. "Who sent the message?"

      \n

      "He's...maybe a god?"

      \n

      "Oh, that asshole?"

      \n

      "I think he meant not that you were going to solve any problem," said Millicent. "I think he means that whatever He was going to do to you, you'd do it to yourself worse."

      \n

      "Did I ask for the Cliff's Notes? On bright side, that insipid loser is off my back. Worst ex I ever had. Obsessive\u2014"

      \n

      The radio next to the bed suddenly exploded.

      \n

      Charleston looked up. "Still listening, huh? You're not going to get over me that easy!"

      \n

      Millicent was boggling. "He's your ex? Because that's a kind of thing in my family\u2014"

      \n

      "No, no, not that I'm aware of. My life has some blank spots. I apparently found religion at one point. But I'm telling you I'm not finding it again!"

      \n

      "That's okay you can lose it that's fine with me," Millicent babbled.

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      That afternoon, safely back in her room, Millicent was visited by a rather serious looking blonde woman. She wore a plain sweater set and horn-rimmed glasses, and she looked over them at Millicent. "Are you...Millicent Lowell? I think we were looking for you. Beth Queen."

      \n

      Millicent shook her hand. "Miss...Mrs..."

      \n

      "Doctor, I guess," said Beth. "I'm an anthropologist by trade. My published work is under my married name, Schicksal."

      \n

      "I'm so sorry," Millicent blurted.

      \n

      "No cause for alarm," said Beth a little quizzically. "How are you?"

      \n

      "I was lost for a while. Really lost. But now I guess...I don't know."

      \n

      "My friend Mr. Wright nearly died looking for you. Was it...worth it?"

      \n

      "I'm not even quite sure what I was looking for anymore. Or if I found it. But I didn't mean to draw anyone after me. I didn't want to cause trouble."

      \n

      "All this for...a high school English teacher? I don't understand." Beth fingered a folded up piece of paper in her hand; she'd been doing this nervously ever since she came in. "I have so many questions that I think I should ask you," she said to Millicent after a moment. "But I'm afraid of the answers I might get, so I don't think I'm going to ask them. Miss Lowell...just do me one favor\u2014"

      \n

      "Stay away from Mr. Wright?"

      \n

      "Please?"

      \n

      "I'll try! I really will!"

      \n

      "Miss Lowell...I don't know exactly what you are. But I know there are a lot more unusual things in this world than I thought. Maybe you should be doing more of what Mr. Wright is doing. So that Mr. Wright can stop doing it."

      \n

      "I'll have to talk to my sister about that," said Millicent after a pause. "She'll probably think it's amusing. And amused...is not a bad way for my sister to be."

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \n

      \n
      \n
      \n
      \nEpisode VII: A Funeral in the Mirror (Part 22)\n

      "Gospazha, how wonderful to see you awake," said Vladimir Nabokov as he came into Candace's room. His wife Vera came in behind him, carrying a vase of flowers. "I tried reaching you for months, you took a leave from your university, then I heard you were in a collapsed building? Very unprofessional."

      \n

      Candace smiled back. "It's wonderful to see you."

      \n

      "We were on Cape Cod," continued Nabokov, pulling up a seat. "On an expedition if you will. Look here." He fished out a jar. Inside was a perfectly preserved butterfly, with brilliant yellow colors on its wings. "I was thinking of naming it after myself. But...I think naming it after you, would be appropriate in this instance. It's a new species, I'm almost sure. Of course I need a microscope."

      \n

      "It's an honor," said Candace.

      \n

      "You look terrible, if you don't mind me being frank," said Nabokov in his strangely-accented English. "I am a little worried about you, my dear. I know it has been very difficult to adjust. But it's eleven years now since Andy died. Haven't you found anyone new?"

      \n

      "Not any one in particular," said Candace.

      \n

      "Modern Western women," said Nabokov, throwing up his arms. "Even in Berlin it was more demure. Now. The doctors have told me that you are frail, and the psychiatrists\u2014those quacks\u2014tell me you require many weeks of therapy. But I know exactly what therapy you need."

      \n

      He took out a bottle of excellent vodka.

      \n

      [Nabokov was actually a quite impressive amateur lepidopterist. And famously dismissive of psychiatrists.]

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Temperance woke up to see Colonel Murphy sitting next to the bed, holding her hand. "I thought I lost you there, baby doll," he said, choking up.

      \n

      "Father...what are you doing here?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "A building dropped on you! What do you think I'm doing here? The first thing I thought was 'Jimmy Wright must be involved!' And I was right!"

      \n

      "We saved him this time," said Temperance with a weak grin.

      \n

      "You saved his life?"

      \n

      Temperance winced the memory of Other Jimmy's autoabbatoir out of her mind. "Events happened," she said.

      \n

      "When I write my autobiography, the part about Jimmy is going to be called Events Happened," said the Colonel. "Actually, that's a good name for it...the Ashley Murphy story. Maybe get Audie Murphy to play me..."

      \n

      "We still in Arkham?" said Temperance.

      \n

      "They transferred you to Boston. What were you doing at Miskatonic any way? Look, the best decision you ever made was to drop out of that dump."

      \n

      "We were looking for a woman. We found her. Millicent Lowell."

      \n

      "Millicent? I thought I told you to stay away from that crazy dame."

      \n

      "We had to find her. And we found her," said Temperance with fervor. "I feel so alive and awake and...aware of everything."

      \n

      "That's probably because of the collapsed lung," said Murphy.

      \n

      "I only need one! Isn't that what you always said!"

      \n

      "There is a lot of redundancy, yes..."

      \n

      "One lung, one kidney, and half a liver! The Murphy way!"

      \n

      They laughed. "When you feel a little bit better," started the Colonel. "I know I gave you that RV...but that wasn't really a present, just what you need to continue in the Murphy way. So I didn't so much buy you a present as...well...one day it will be yours. I bought a boat."

      \n

      "It's been twenty years, pop," said Temperance slowly. "Since you burned the last one."

      \n

      "I was hoping maybe we could take it out to the Vineyard."

      \n

      "Perhaps. But I have a mission now. I was too passive before. Not making a stand for what I knew was right. I see the truth. I know what I need to be doing. Maybe one day, father\u2014"

      \n

      "Darling, I just have one question," said the Colonel. "What the hell is this mask doing in your bag?"

      \n

      \xa0

      \n

      Helen was sitting vigil over Charleston from her wheelchair.

      \n

      "Hey babe, you made it back," he said, stretching his arms.

      \n

      She took a long time to respond. "This world's real, isn't it?" she said at last.

      \n

      "Sweetie, I don't know what to tell you. I don't really know. I'm beginning to suspect that they're all real enough."

      \n

      "There. You did it again. You are always doing it. Where you say something that's supposed to sound like it's comforting but all it does is make me feel all weird inside. Also the morphine is not enough," she said hysterically.

      \n

      "I finally get you to a place where you can have all the morphine you want and it's not enough?"

      \n

      "What can I do now? I saw what happened there."

      \n

      "Back there is gone now," said Charleston.

      \n

      "I ain't got a home anymore," she wailed.

      \n

      "Of course you do," he said.

      \n

      "Am I real?"

      \n

      "Of course!"

      \n

      "How would you know?"

      \n

      "Listen. I think you're real...I don't know how to comfort you in your time of misgiving. But would you rather be in a place that you thought was real but was not that great a place to be and got leveled in a flash of sunlike temperature? Or would you rather be in a place that you're not so sure is real, but good things happen? Good things are good things. Accept them when they come," said Charleston.

      \n

      "I can't decide if it's better to be with you, since you're the only one who even remotely understands what I'm going through, or if I should just run away from you and try to live out whatever weirdo delusional life I got left," said Helen. "Or if I should just finish the job I started."

      \n

      "You run, I'll follow," said Charleston. "It will be fun. We'll go wherever you want. Once our legs work."

      \n

      "See, there you go again. You say something that sounds terrible, but is actually comforting." She smiled.

      \n
      \n

      Aviatrix said:


      "I'm not going to miss you," said Percy. "Just tell me one thing: in your world was I a good man?"

      \n

      "Yes," lied Charleston. "The best. He achieved something absolutely amazing. Your genius will live on."

      \n
      \nIf I recall correctly, everyone said "Yes" in unison, even Millicent, who really had no idea either way.
